2401 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Sassano v. Lennox


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


32 Misc. 2d 222; 223 N.Y.S.2d 830; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1882



December 19, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the reasons stated, the motion to dismiss is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In petitioner taxpayers' proceeding for a review of real property tax assessments under N.Y. Real Prop. Law art. 7, respondent tax officer filed a motion to dismiss the petition on the ground that the court did not have jurisdiction of the proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers did not fully answer the questions in the application they filed for the reduction of the assessment. Thus, the tax officer contended that the application was vitiated under City of Yonkers, N.Y., Local Law No. 8 of 1961, which provided that failure to fully answer the questions rendered the application null and void. The court disagreed. N.Y. Const. art. IX, § 12 provided that no local law could be adopted which repealed or superseded any law enacted by the legislature relating to the making and review of assessments, unless authorized by the legislature. N.Y. City Home Rule Law § 11(1), as amended by 1960 N.Y. Laws ch. 260, 1961 N.Y. Laws ch. 684, allowed the adoption of local laws concerning the correction of local tax assessments. The court held that N.Y. City Home Rule Law § 11(1), as amended by 1960 N.Y. Laws ch. 260, 1961 N.Y. Laws ch. 684, and N.Y. Const. art. IX, § 12, did not empower the city to affect the jurisdiction of the court to entertain a proceeding to review an assessment. Thus, City of Yonkers, N.Y., Local Law No. 8 of 1961, did not divest the court of its jurisdiction on the ground that the taxpayers failed to fill out the application properly.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- assessments -- court not deprived of jurisdiction to review assessment by failure of petitioner to answer questions on application for reduction of assessments despite provision in Local Law that application for reduction was void if not filled out.

The court was not deprived of jurisdiction of a proceeding under article 7 of the Real Property Tax Law to review an assessment by the failure of petitioner to answer questions on the application filed with a city for a reduction of the assessment, despite a provision in a Local Law of said city that failure to complete the application should render the application for correction of the assessment null and void.

 

2402 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


County of Orange v. Newburgh


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Orange County


30 Misc. 2d 898; 222 N.Y.S.2d 283; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1892



December 18, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings in its action against defendant city seeking a declaratory judgment establishing the unconstitutionality of 1959 N.Y. Laws ch. 657, which set forth procedures for the dissolution of the city's welfare district and the takeover by the county of all public assistance and welfare programs. Intervenor attorney general joined with the city in seeking to uphold the validity of the law.


OVERVIEW: The Legislature of the State of New York enacted 1959 N.Y. Laws ch. 657 (welfare law), which authorized both the city and county to dissolve the city's welfare district and to authorize the county to take over all public assistance and welfare programs. Although the city council passed a resolution urging the county's board of supervisors to accept the transfer of its public welfare programs, the county neither accepted nor rejected the proposal. The county created a special committee to study and report the feasibility and advisability of the proposal, and it filed an action against the city challenging the constitutionality of the welfare law. The county filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings. The court denied the motion and dismissed the county's complaint without prejudice. The court held that declaratory relief was not appropriate under N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act § 473 and N.Y. R. Civ. Prac. 212 because the welfare law was not set in motion by resolutions of both the city and the county, and there was no bona fide justiciable controversy between the parties. The court held that it would not render an advisory opinion in advance of the happening of an event.


OUTCOME: The court denied the county's motion for judgment on the pleadings, and it dismissed the county's complaint without prejudice.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Declaratory judgments -- jurisdiction refused -- court refuses to render merely advisory opinion of constitutionality (Rules Civ. Prac., rule 212; N. Y. Const., art. IX, § 1; L. 1959, ch. 657).

The court declines to take jurisdiction of an action by a county against a city for a judgment declaring the unconstitutionality of a statute authorizing the county and the city to adopt resolutions dissolving and reorganizing the city's public welfare district, since only the city but not the county has adopted such a resolution, and since the county now seeks a merely advisory opinion which will settle nothing. (Civ. Prac. Act, § 473; Rules Civ. Prac., rule 212; L. 1959, ch. 657; N. Y. Const., art. IX, § 1.)

 

2403 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


West Bronx Auto Paint Shop, Inc. v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


33 Misc. 2d 29; 223 N.Y.S.2d 984; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1907



December 13, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motions are disposed of accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the City of New York Department of Air Pollution and others, sought judgment on the pleadings dismissing the complaint for insufficiency, in an action presenting a question of whether plaintiff automobile painting business was subject to regulation by the City. The automobile painting business sought judgment on the pleadings on the ground that the denials raised by the answer and amended answer were insufficient.


OVERVIEW: The court held that definitions of dust, fumes, odor and vapor as set out in the New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code were sufficiently clear and definite to give notice thereof and constituted adequate guides and standards for the Department of Air Pollution. The court also held that the auto painting business from which vapors escaped into the outer air was within the province and jurisdiction of the City of New York Department of Air Pollution. The court further held that provisions of the city charter and administrative code and rules and regulations concerning air pollution were not unconstitutional and invalid as applied to the paint spraying operation. Moreover, the court held that a failure to provide any administrative review did not render a legislative scheme of air pollution control and its implementation unconstitutional. The court reasoned that no review by proceeding under N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act art. 78 need be provided in order to enable an aggrieved party to take advantage thereof, but no such proceeding could have been maintained in the absence of exhaustion of an administrative remedy.


OUTCOME: The court granted the city's motion for an order for judgment on the pleadings and denied the motion of the automobile painting business.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- air pollution control -- in action to declare city's air pollution legislation unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff's automobile body paint-spraying operations, city was granted judgment declaring such legislation constitutional -- jurisdiction of Department of Air Pollution Control, as defined, included spray from paint-spraying operations -- legislation supplied adequate safeguards and standards -- rules of department were not shown to conflict with those of other agencies -- failure to provide proceeding for review did not prevent aggrieved party from seeking one.

1. In an action to declare that paint spray and vapors emanating into the outer air from plaintiff's automobile body painting business were not within the jurisdiction of the Department of Air Pollution Control established by section 1071 et seq. of the New York City Charter and section 1072-1.0 et seq. of the Administrative Code, and to declare chapter 47 of the New York City Charter (in which § 1071 et seq. were contained) and the sections of the Administrative Code unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff's paint-spraying [***2] operation, defendants were granted judgment on the pleadings declaring the sections valid and applicable to plaintiff's business.

2. The Department of Air Pollution Control was given "jurisdiction to regulate and control the emission into the open air of harmful or objectionable substances, including but not limited to smoke, soot, fly ash, dust, fumes, gas, vapors, odors and any products of combustion or incomplete combustion resulting from the use of fuel burning equipment or from the heating of fuels or refuse." Jurisdiction was not limited to emissions resulting from the use of fuel-burning equipment or from the heating of fuels or refuse, but included all substances of a harmful nature and with respect to any equipment producing such emissions, including spray and fumes from plaintiff's paint-spraying operations.

3. The charter and code supplied safeguards, standards and definitions, as a matter of law, to give notice of the particular act or action made subject of punishment in the event of violation. While paint-spraying operations were not mentioned in the charter and code, such operations were a proper subject for continuing supervision and control.

4. The rules and regulations [***3] of the department were not shown to conflict with those of other agencies.

5. No review by a proceeding under article 78 of the Civil Practice Act need be provided to enable an aggrieved party to take advantage thereof, and no review by way of administrative remedy need be supplied. The failure to provide any administrative review did not render the legislative scheme and its implementation unconstitutional.

 

2404 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Long Beach v. Sealtest Foods Div.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, Long Beach, Nassau County


32 Misc. 2d 432; 222 N.Y.S.2d 607; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1913



December 13, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Defendants' challenge to the statute is sustained and the several informations dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant milk delivery companies challenged the constitutionality of Long Beach, N.Y., Code, ch. 5, art. 2, § 5-113, after they were charged with having carried on the business of milk deliveries at various locations within the city without having obtained a mercantile license or permit.


OVERVIEW: The companies were charged with having carried on the business of milk deliveries at various locations within the city without having obtained a mercantile license or permit therefor, all in violation of Long Beach, N.Y., Code, ch. 5, art. 2, § 5-113. The companies contended that § 5-113 was unreasonable, arbitrary, and excessive in its imposition of a $ 100 annual tax on milk dealers. The companies argued that when a municipal corporation was given the power to license useful trades or occupations, it could not use the license as a tax to raise revenue. The court sustained the companies' challenge and dismissed the informations. It was not apparent what relation existed, or could have existed, between a license fee of $ 100 and the companies' sales of their milk products. A license fee should be sufficient merely to compensate for the expense of issuing and recording the license, and by inspecting and regulating the particular business, and to secure police control of the matter licensed.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the companies' challenge and dismissed the informations against them.


HEADNOTES

Licenses -- milk distributors -- license fee of $ 100 imposed by city ordinance on milk distributors was unreasonable, amounting to tax -- informations charging violation of ordinance were dismissed.

An ordinance of a city imposing a $ 100 fee for a mercantile license to carry on a milk distribution business in the city was unreasonable and informations charging defendants with violation of the ordinance were dismissed. The grant of power to license useful trades did not authorize plaintiff to use such power as a tax to raise revenue. No relationship existed between the license fee of $ 100 and defendants' sales of their milk products.

 

2405 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Mann v. Compania Petrolera Trans-Cuba, S. A.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


32 Misc. 2d 790; 223 N.Y.S.2d 900; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1914



December 13, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the foregoing reasons, the Referee's report is confirmed and the motion for substitution is granted, without prejudice to an application by the substituted attorneys for leave to intervene.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff shareholder filed an action against defendant foreign corporation for the appointment of a permanent receiver of the foreign corporation's assets in New York. Movant attorney, representing the foreign corporation's president, filed a motion to be substituted as attorney for the foreign corporation.


OVERVIEW: The foreign corporation was a Cuban corporation and first appeared by attorneys designated by an interventor appointed for the foreign corporation under Cuban law. The attorney sought to be substituted as counsel for the foreign corporation. A referee appointed to consider the matter recommended that the motion for substitution be granted. The court confirmed the report of the referee and granted the motion. The court found that the interventor's attempt to control the litigation deprived the shareholders and the directors of the foreign corporation the right to manage the corporate affairs in this country. The shareholder had a right to expect that New York courts would apply the public policy of the state in litigation affecting assets in the district. Where the appointment of the interventor violated the public policy of this country, the court was not required to recognize the appointment.


OUTCOME: The court granted the attorney's motion to be substituted as counsel for the foreign corporation in an action by a shareholder for appointment of a permanent receiver of the foreign corporation's assets in New York.


HEADNOTES

Attorney and client -- right to represent Cuban corporation -- in action to liquidate assets of Cuban corporation, attorney designated by corporation's president was substituted for attorneys designated by interventor of corporation appointed under Cuban law -- order of intervention not entitled to extra-territorial effect -- Cuban order contrary to public policy -- corporation's president had right to support relief requested by plaintiff.

1. In an action by a stockholder of a Cuban corporation for the appointment of a receiver pursuant to section 977-b of the Civil Practice Act to liquidate and distribute the New York assets of defendant, a motion by an attorney designated by the corporation's president to be substituted for the attorneys designated by an interventor of the corporation appointed under Cuban law was granted.

2. The order of intervention was not entitled to extra-territorial recognition in this State with respect to assets located in this State. By the corporation's [***2] listing of itself on the American Stock Exchange, soliciting subscriptions from American investors and leaving money on deposit in a New York bank, American stockholders had a right to expect American courts to apply American public policy in respect to litigation affecting that deposit.

3. The Cuban order and the procedure involved was contrary to our public policy since the intervention was effectuated without notice to the corporation or an opportunity for it to be heard.

4. Defendant's president had the right to support the relief requested by plaintiff if he deemed it to be in the corporate interest.

 

2406 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Politano


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Montgomery County


32 Misc. 2d 526; 224 N.Y.S.2d 401; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1928



December 10, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment on the ground that section 975 is unconstitutional is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The matter was before the court upon defendant's oral motions to suppress evidence seized under a search warrant and to dismiss the indictment. The prosecutor stipulated that the court could hear these motions without the necessity of the usual formal written motions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's oral pretrial motion to suppress evidence was based on the contention that the search warrant was defective and null and void. Defendant had filed a motion before the issuing court to have the warrant declared null and void and the issuing court held that the question of its validity should be raised upon the trial. After an examination of the search warrant and the affidavit upon which it was granted, the court was of the opinion that the search warrant was issued on probable cause supported by a sworn affidavit describing the person, and particularly the property, and the place to be searched and the property to be seized. The property to be seized was contraband. The return indicated that the property actually seized was contraband connected with the crime for which defendant was arrested. The search warrant was legal. Defendant also sought to dismiss the indictment accusing defendant of violating N.Y. Penal Law § 975 as unconstitutional. The court held that § 975 did not violate defendant's rights to due process of the law under the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to suppress and motion to dismiss the indictment.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- search and seizure -- statutory presumption that possession of "policy" slips is knowing (Penal Law, § 975) is constitutional -- such contraband may be seized under search warrant -- affidavit in support of search warrant showed probable cause by wire tapping; motion to suppress such seized evidence, policy slips, is denied.

1. Possession of "policy" slips is presumptive evidence of the crime of possession with knowledge (Penal Law, § 975). The statutory presumption is constitutional.

2. "Policy" slips and other book-making records are contraband, like weapons or narcotics or counterfeit money. They are not merely evidence. A search warrant may legally issue for their seizure.

3. The affidavit in support of a search warrant showed probable cause, based on an investigation made by the affiant by eavesdropping and recording of telephone calls to and from the defendant's premises during which he overheard conversations that persons in the residence of the defendant were keeping a place for transferring money in a game of policy. The property and [***2] place to be searched were described as the residence of this defendant, by street and house number. The person operating the place was described as "John Doe", his true name being unknown. The property sought to be seized was equipment and paraphernalia used in playing the game of policy. The property subsequently seized was, among other things, policy slips. This was contraband, and it was connected with the crime for which defendant was arrested. The search and seizure were legal (U. S. Const., 4th Amdt.) and complied with the ruling in Mapp v. Ohio (367 U.S. 643); accordingly, motion to suppress the seized evidence is denied.

 

2407 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Shpritzer v. Lang


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


32 Misc. 2d 693; 224 N.Y.S.2d 105; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1934



December 8, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner policewoman initiated a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding to review a decision of respondents, a city department of personnel, its personnel director, a city civil service commission, and its chairman, denying petitioner's application to take an examination to qualify for appointment as a sergeant.


OVERVIEW: The controlling question posed by the controversy was whether New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § 434a-2.0(d) was an unconstitutional abridgment of the rights of women. Petitioner, after competitive examination, was appointed as a policewoman in the city police department, and after some 18 years of exemplary service, made application to take an examination to qualify for appointment as a sergeant. In denying her application, the commission informed petitioner that she was ineligible to take the examination because she was not permanently employed in an eligible title, because, in other words, there was no authority to promote policewomen to the rank of sergeant. The court ruled that there could be no doubt that § 434a-2.0(d), as opposed to other sections of the code cited by petitioner, made policewomen ineligible for promotion as sergeants. The court ordered a hearing on the issue of whether it reasonably might be concluded that policewomen could properly perform such a number of the assignments in the police department which were currently performed by male sergeants as to warrant the promotion of at least some policewomen to the position of sergeant.


OUTCOME: The court ordered a hearing to determine the reasonableness of the legislature's judgment in regards to the constitutionality of the city administrative code at issue.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- police -- Administrative Code of City of New York (§ 434a-2.0) which provided that there should be only one rank of policewoman within Police Department made women ineligible for promotion to sergeant -- determination of whether statute was unconstitutional was deferred until after hearing on issues.

Subdivision d of section 434a-2.0 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York, which provided that there should only be one rank of policewoman within the Police Department, made policewomen ineligible for promotion to sergeants. On its face such statute, in an organization containing approximately 25,000 policemen and 300 policewomen, wherein some positions of authority must exist where women could perform at the same level of competence as men, may be arbitrary and violate the equal protection clauses of the Federal and State Constitutions. Before determining its constitutionality, a hearing was ordered on the issue of whether or not it reasonably may be concluded that policewomen can properly perform such a number of the assignments in the Police Department which were currently performed by male sergeants as to warrant the promotion of at [***2] least some policewomen to the position of sergeant. At such hearing, the parties should be prepared to offer evidence as to the administrative procedures of the Police Department, in particular the nature of the duty assignments of male sergeants, as well as to any other matters pertinent to the determination at issue.

 

2408 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Chiropractic Asso. of New York, Inc. v. Hilleboe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Albany County


31 Misc. 2d 554; 227 N.Y.S.2d 309; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2068



November 15, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Complaint dismissed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a chiropractic association (association), on behalf of itself and its individual members and by an individual, brought an action against defendant, Commissioner of Health of the State of New York (Commissioner), seeking to enjoin the Commissioner and all persons acting under him or by his authority from preventing the members of the association and the individual from operating X-ray equipment in their profession.


OVERVIEW: The court sufficiently quoted the individual's testimony to indicate why the court thought the individual was and had been unlawfully practicing medicine. One of the witnesses who testified on behalf of the association stated that there were fewer than 1,000 members of the association and that all of the members either used their own X-ray equipment or sent their patients out to a laboratory to have X-ray radiation applied. The court held that the members of the association and the individual were holding themselves out as competent to cure disease within the meaning of N.Y. Educ. Law § 6501(4). In addition, the members of the association and the individual violated the first and second paragraphs of regulation 19 of Chapter XVI of the New York State Sanitary Code, which precluded the application of radiation to the human body unless the radiation was applied by a licensed person. The court determined that the chiropractors had never been licensed under the laws of New York to diagnose and treat disease either in New York City or New York State.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the complaint and vacated the attempted stipulation, stayed the enforcement of the sanitary code regulation, and denied the motion to dismiss the separate defenses of the Commissioner.


HEADNOTES

Physicians and surgeons -- chiropractors -- X rays -- as chiropractors are not licensed to practice medicine or any other healing art in New York State, they are prohibited from applying radiation to persons who seek chiropractic treatment (N. Y. State Sanitary Code, ch. XVI, reg. 19).

1. The individual plaintiff and witnesses for the corporate plaintiff testified that they use in their "practice" as chiropractors such instruments as the stethoscope, the otoscope, the ophthalmoscope and the sphygmomanometer, and that they take or prescribe X rays of nearly all persons who come to them for therapy, such X rays, in most instances, being of the entire spinal column. The stethoscope, the otoscope, the ophthalmoscope and the sphygmomanometer are all medical instruments. Moreover, the X-ray machine, which produces radiation described by an expert witness for defendant as having an effect upon the human body similar to that produced by the explosion of an atom bomb, is an instrumentality of medical practice. These facts, as well as other testimony given on behalf of plaintiffs, establish that the individual plaintiff and the members of the [***2] corporate plaintiff were holding themselves out as competent to cure disease. Therefore, they were practicing medicine within the meaning of the Education Law ( § 6501, subd. 4) which states that a person is practicing medicine "* * * who holds himself out as being able to diagnose, treat, operate or prescribe for any human disease, pain, injury, deformity or physical condition * * *". However, as chiropractors are not licensed in this State to practice medicine or any of the other healing arts, they were practicing medicine illegally (Education Law, § 6502).

2. The individual plaintiff and the members of the corporate plaintiff also violated regulation 19 of chapter XVI of the New York State Sanitary Code which, inter alia, prohibits the application of radiation to human beings except by, or by order of, a person licensed or otherwise authorized to practice medicine, dentistry, podiatry, or osteopathy under the provisions of the Education Law.

3. Sausser v. Department of Health (242 N. Y. 66), wherein the Court of Appeals directed the issuance of a permit to operate an X-ray laboratory to a chiropractor, is obsolete.

4. Accordingly, the complaint in an action to [***3] enjoin defendant, the Commissioner of Health of the State of New York, and all persons acting under him, from preventing the members of plaintiff association and the individual plaintiff from operating "in the practice of their profession as chiropractors [certain] X-ray equipment * * *" and generally to restrain defendant from carrying out the provisions of regulation 19 of chapter XVI of the New York State Sanitary Code against plaintiffs and other chiropractors, is dismissed.

 

2409 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hill


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Onondaga County


31 Misc. 2d 985; 221 N.Y.S.2d 875; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2092



November 10, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the reasons above stated, the defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment is hereby granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for an order permitting him to inspect the Grand Jury minutes, or, in the alternative, that the court inspect the minutes, and upon such inspection by the court, that an order be granted dismissing his indictment on gambling charges under N.Y. Penal Law § 975.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted by a grand jury and charged with violating N.Y. Penal Code § 975 after he was arrested while in possession of more than 10 chances, bets, or wagers upon numbers sold in a "policy" or "numbers" game. Defendant had been stopped by police, who had no warrant but asked to see his license and registration. When defendant produced his wallet, one of the officers grabbed it and began to go through its contents, whereupon he discovered the slips. Defendant filed a motion for an order permitting him to inspect the grand jury minutes or, in the alternative, that the court inspect the minutes and that an order be thereafter granted dismissing the indictment. The court granted the motion to dismiss, holding that (1) the alleged policy slips found in the possession of defendant could not be used because they were obtained as a result of an illegal search and seizure; and (2) defendant's confession was not sufficient to warrant his conviction under N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 395 without the policy slips, which were additional proof that the crime charged had been committed.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion and dismissed his indictment on gambling charges.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- indictment -- unreasonable search and seizure -- alleged policy slips in possession of defendant were seized by police officers after defendant's arrest without warrant, under circumstances insufficient to engender reasonable belief that misdemeanor was being attempted or committed -- evidence obtained during illegal arrest not admissible -- uncorroborated confession not sufficient to sustain indictment.

Defendant was arrested by police officers who halted defendant's automobile, requested to see his license and registration, and then grabbed his wallet and searched its contents, taking from it papers alleged to be policy slips. He was then taken to his home and accompanied inside by the officers. No warrant was ever exhibited to defendant, who was later indicted by a Grand Jury for possessing policy slips in violation of section 975 of the Penal Law. As the facts known to the police officers at the time of defendant's arrest were insufficient to engender reasonable belief that a misdemeanor was being attempted or committed in their presence, defendant's arrest [***2] was illegal, and consequently the alleged policy slips were obtained by unreasonable search and seizure and cannot be used as evidence ( Mapp v. Ohio, 367 U.S. 643). Since there remains no evidence of the commission of the crime other than defendant's confession, the indictment must be dismissed.

 

2410 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gonzales


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of General Sessions of the County of New York


31 Misc. 2d 486; 221 N.Y.S.2d 846; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2097



November 9, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental opinion November 20, 1961.



DISPOSITION: Since, upon suppression of the evidence obtained by search and seizure in this case, there would be no legal evidence to support the indictment, it is ordered dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following defendant's indictment for the crime of feloniously possessing a narcotic drug, defendant moved for an order to inspect the grand jury's minutes, for dismissal of the indictment, and for the suppression of certain evidence. Defendant claimed that certain evidence against him was procured by means of an unreasonable search and seizure.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for a drug-related crime. Defendant moved for an order to inspect the grand jury minutes, for dismissal of the indictment, and for the suppression of certain evidence. The court noted that the exclusionary rule that applied in federal courts that barred the use of evidence procured by means of unreasonable searches and seizures was made applicable to the states by a United States Supreme Court decision. The court found that there was a preliminary hearing before a magistrate that occurred after the Supreme Court's decision was made, and because evidence was adduced that showed the illegality of a search of defendant that resulted in the seizure of three paper bags containing a narcotic drug, the magistrate should have granted defendant's motion to suppress the evidence. The court noted that the police officer who seized the evidence had no search or arrest warrant, did not know defendant, had no confidential information regarding him, and for some undisclosed reason, followed defendant for several blocks and then forcibly searched him. The court found that the district attorney did not submit further evidence that showed probable cause.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence and dismissed the indictment.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- motion to suppress illegally seized evidence -- search and seizure can be made without warrant, on probable cause, which may consist of hearsay -- such issue is for court, not jury -- defendant's motion to suppress illegally seized evidence and dismiss indictment is granted.

1. A search and seizure can be made on probable cause, without a warrant. Such probable cause can be proved by less than "legal evidence", such as hearsay, knowledge of prior criminal activities, reasonable grounds for suspicion, or information from a reliable source. The issues of law and of fact as to such probable cause are for the court, not the jury.

2. A policeman saw defendant on the street and became suspicious of him, and accosted him and seized three paper bags containing narcotics, and arrested him. Such search and seizure and arrest were apparently made without probable cause. Defendant's motion to suppress the evidence and to dismiss the indictment of feloniously [***2] possessing a narcotic drug is granted by the Motion Part of the Court of General Sessions of the County of New York, since the District Attorney submits an affidavit which does not sufficiently raise a factual issue of probable cause, and since the suppression of the illegally seized evidence leaves no legal evidence to support the indictment.

 

2411 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Blumfield v. Ramapo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Rockland County


30 Misc. 2d 678; 222 N.Y.S.2d 939; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2157



October 30, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Defendants' request for summary judgment dismissing the complaint is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff licensee brought an action against defendants, a town and a state liquor authority, seeking a permanent injunction and a declaration that a town ordinance was unconstitutional. The licensee and the town moved for summary judgment or, in the alternative, for judgment on the pleadings.


OVERVIEW: The licensee was authorized to sell beer, wine, and liquor on-premises in his restaurant and beer for off-premises consumption. The town's ordinance, which was adopted pursuant to N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 86, restricted and prohibited the sale of alcoholic beverages on Memorial Day until 1:00 p.m. In his motion for summary judgment, the licensee contended that, among other things, that the state expressly enacted the New York Alcoholic Beverage Control Law (Law) to regulate the sale of alcoholic beverages and that the power to further restrict the hours during which alcoholic beverages could be sold was delegated only to local boards outside of the city pursuant to N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law § 43. The town contended, among other things, that nothing in the Law preempted further regulation of the sale of alcoholic beverages. In granting the licensee's summary judgment motion, the court held that the provisions of the Law were exclusive and state-wide in scope and that the state legislature had the sole province to regulate the sale of alcoholic beverages. The legislative history did not indicate an intent to allow municipalities to further regulate such sales.


OUTCOME: The court granted the licensee's summary judgment motion and denied the town's request for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Intoxicating liquors -- sale on Memorial Day -- municipality cannot regulate hours of sale on Memorial Day (cf. General Municipal Law, § 86; Alcoholic Beverage Control Law, §§ 43, 106, subd. 5).

The hours and days on which alcoholic beverages may be sold for on-premises or off-premises consumption are regulated by the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law ( §§ 43, 106, subd. 5). The General Municipal Law ( § 86, enacted by L. 1957, ch. 387) does not empower a municipality to adopt an ordinance restricting those hours on Memorial Day.

 

2412 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Du Bois


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Queens County


31 Misc. 2d 157; 221 N.Y.S.2d 21; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2191



October 24, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a husband and wife, were indicted for criminally receiving and criminally concealing stolen property. They filed a motion for an order to suppress evidence and to strike from the record and from the minutes of the grand jury evidence seized in violation of their constitutional rights and for an order dismissing the indictment. Defendants claimed that the police entered their home without a warrant and without their permission.


OVERVIEW: The State denied the factual basis of defendants' motion. The court noted that the factual issues of violation of the Fourth Amendment applicable to the State through the Fourteenth Amendment raised by the conflicting versions contained in affidavits could not be summarily determined. Taking testimony was required. Noting that whether the evidence should be suppressed was regarded as not immediately relevant to the question of guilt, the court said that a jury should not be called upon to focus its attention upon such a purely collateral issue and chance being diverted from its purpose for being: the determination of the guilt of defendants. The court concluded that it could both try and decide the issues of fact. The court added that the absence of any procedural statutory authorization as to how and in what manner evidence illegally obtained should be suppressed did not affect the obligation of the court to safeguard the constitutional rights of those accused through the use of such evidence. The court decided that it would therefore seem to be better to assimilate New York practice to that employed in the federal courts and determine the question in advance of trial.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion to the extent of ordering a hearing at which it would receive evidence of the parties on the questions of fact involved. In the interim the court held in abeyance the determination of the balance of the motion.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- motion to suppress illegally seized evidence -- court will hear evidence as to forcible entry and seizure, and will determine motion, in advance of jury trial of main case (U. S. Const., 4th and 14th Amdts.).

1. Defendants, who were indicted for criminally receiving and concealing stolen property, move to suppress evidence allegedly forcibly seized at their home and to dismiss the indictment as wholly based on such illegal evidence. A sharp issue of fact is presented by the police officers' affidavits that the defendant who was at home consented to their entry and search. The court, without a jury, will hear the evidence and determine this issue and this motion, in advance of a jury trial of the main case. ( Mapp v. Ohio, 367 U.S. 643, followed; U. S. Const., 4th and 14th Amdts.; N. Y. Const., art. I, §§ 2, 12.)

2. In the Federal courts, (1) such issues are thus tried by the court without a jury, in advance of the main trial (Federal Rules of Criminal Procedure, rule 41, subd. [e]), and (2) the arresting officers are presumed to have acted lawfully. Our Code of Criminal Procedure is silent as to the procedure to be followed under the recent decision [***2] of Mapp v. Ohio (367 U.S. 643). The court suggests that the Legislature fill in this procedural void; otherwise, different Judges may adopt different procedures.

 

2413 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Lyden v. Katz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Putnam County


29 Misc. 2d 1072; 221 N.Y.S.2d 445; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2198



October 24, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The relief sought in the petitions is granted. The respondents' motions for an order amending the certificates of nominations nunc pro tunc are denied. Submit order on notice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner voters applied for an order restraining respondent Board of Elections of Putnam County from placing on the ballot for the county general election the names of candidates purported to be nominated by the Liberal party in nomination certificates filed with the Board.


OVERVIEW: The Liberal party submitted five nomination certificates with the Board, which purported to nominate candidates for offices in the county. The voters objected to the placing of the candidates on the ballot, arguing that the certificates failed to comply with the requirements of N.Y. Elec. Law § 131 by failing to name the offices for which each candidate would be eligible for election. The Board moved to offer outside evidence of the offices intended to be sought by the candidates, and the voters objected to the motion. The court held that the Board was entitled to offer the extrinsic evidence to clarify the offices sought. However, the court found that even in considering the outside evidence, the defects in the nomination certificates could not be cured and the evidence was insufficient to justify amending the certificates. Because the certificates were inadequate, the court ruled that the nominees could not be placed on the ballot by the Board.


OUTCOME: The court granted the voters' petition, denied the Board's motion to amend the nomination certificates, and determined that the members of the Liberal party could not be placed on the ballot.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- certificates of party nominations for town offices -- five certificates which fail on their face to state for which of six towns candidates are nominated are jurisdictionally defective and cannot be corrected nunc pro tunc (Election Law, § 131, subd. 9) -- candidates were properly served by mail (Election Law, §§ 330, 335).

1. In these review proceedings (Election Law, § 330, subd. 2) instituted by Republican party candidates and by the Republican County Committee chairman, against the Board of Elections and the respective chairmen of the Liberal and Democratic County Committees, the court directed that the Liberal party candidates and the committee on vacancies named in the nomination certificates under review for the general election to be held on November 7, be joined as necessary parties respondent and that they be served in person or by mail on or before October 14 for a hearing to be held on October 18; and such service was then properly and timelily made by mail (Election [***2] Law, § 335; Civ. Prac. Act, §§ 1, 5, 192, 193). Rule 21 of the Rules of Civil Practice, to the extent that it is inconsistent with sections 330 and 335 of the Election Law, does not apply.

2. Putnam County has 6 towns. The Liberal party filed 5 separate certificates of nomination of candidates for offices which the court judicially notices are town offices: namely, Supervisor, Town Clerk, Justice of the Peace, Councilman, Assessor, Tax Collector, and Superintendent of Highways. However, none of the 5 certificates states the name of any town for whose public office any candidate is named (Election Law, § 131, subd. 9); the certificates merely state that the above-mentioned offices are "to be filled by the voters of Putnam County at the general election". Each certificate gives each candidate's town of residence, but in some instances the same town thus appears on different certificates. Their registration cards merely indicate in which town they resided at the time of registration, and not at time of nomination (Town Law, § 23). Their authorizations and acceptances (Election Law, § 137, subd. 4) similarly state towns of residence, but not the particular town for whose office [***3] the nomination was made. Most, but not all, of the Liberal party candidates were also nominated by the Democratic party, by certificates which properly stated the town of that candidacy; but the certificates of one political party should not be open to correction by the certificates of another political party, since such practice would open the door to frauds. Thus, these 5 Liberal party certificates of nomination are jurisdictionally defective, and cannot be corrected by a nunc pro tunc order. The motion to amend the certificates nunc pro tunc is denied, and the Board of Elections is directed not to place the names of those Liberal party candidates on the ballot.

 

2414 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Application of Tani


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


32 Misc. 2d 53; 221 N.Y.S.2d 314; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2244



October 13, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The application of the petitioner is denied, and the petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was an application filed by petitioner under N.Y. Elec. Law § 330(1) to have it determine that a petition that nominated respondent, as a candidate for the same office as petitioner had been nominated for, was insufficient, invalid, and illegal.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was nominated as the candidate for supervisor of the of the city by the democratic party. Petitioner alleged that the petition that nominated respondent as a candidate for the same position was insufficient, invalid, and illegal. The challenged petition consisted of 568 signatures. Respondent Board of Elections sustained petitioner's objections to 139 signatures, which left 429 signatures. The remaining signatures were sufficient to support the nomination of respondent. The court denied petitioner's application. The court found that the signatures using initials, or abbreviations, or the title "Mrs." were valid under N.Y. Elec. Law § 138-a. The court found that six signatures were invalid because they were not signed in the presence of the subscribing witness. The court determined that one signature was forged. In all the court concluded that an additional 23 signatures were invalid. The court concluded that the irregular signatures did not render the entire petition invalid. The court found that petitioner failed to prove that the irregularities and fraud were so ample that the validity of the entire petition was in doubt.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petitioner's application and dismissed his petition.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- independent nominating petitions -- petition in proceeding to annul independent nominating petition was dismissed where, after eliminating invalid signatures found by Board of Elections and by court, more than required number of valid signatures remained -- section 138-a of Election Law was constitutional -- forgery and fraud permeating entire nominating petition was not shown.

1. A petition in a proceeding to annul an independent nominating petition for the office of supervisor was dismissed. The nominating petition contained 568 signatures although only 273 were required. The Board of Elections invalidated 139 signatures, leaving 429 signatures. The court in this proceeding invalidated 24 more signatures, leaving 405 valid signatures.

2. Section 138-a of the Election Law provided that the use of titles, initials or abbreviations by the signers of independent nominating petitions should not invalidate the signatures provided that the identity of the signer could be established by the use of the register of voters. Such section was constitutional. The direction for the use of registers [***2] of voters to identify signatures was reasonable.

3. The signatures of eight persons who did not sign their names in the immediate presence of the subscribing witness were invalid.

4. The signatures of 15 persons, who also signed the nominating petition of petitioner, a Democratic party candidate for the same office, were invalid.

5. The signature of one person, which was written by his wife, was invalid.

6. Forgery as to 45 signatures was not shown. Fraud was not established by petitioner by clear and convincing evidence.

7. The evidence did not justify an inference that the whole nominating petition was permeated with fraud and deception.

Long Island Racing Publications, Inc. v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


31 Misc. 2d 286; 220 N.Y.S.2d 907; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2313



October 3, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motions are granted to the extent of directing the entry of judgment declaring the tax in issue is properly and constitutionally imposed and is applicable to the plaintiff. Settle order and judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff racing publication and defendant city moved for summary judgment in an action brought by the publication for a declaration that the city sales tax did not apply to the publication's "tip sheet."


OVERVIEW: The racing publication brought an action for a declaration that the city sales tax did not apply to the publication's "tip sheet" because it was not tangible property but embodied services and was not an information service. Upon review, the court found that the "tip sheet" was tangible personal property and an information service made taxable following the adoption of New York City, N.Y. Admin. Code § N41-2.0, para. 5-a. The court held that no unconstitutional classification was involved. The court stated that the right of freedom of the press or the right to equal protection of the law was not invaded or denied unconstitutionally by the imposition of the tax. The court granted the motions to the extent of directing the entry of judgment declaring the tax in issue was properly and constitutionally imposed and was applicable to the publication.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motions to the extent of directing the entry of judgment declaring the tax in issue was properly and constitutionally imposed and was applicable to the publication.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- New York City sales tax -- racing "tip sheet" was subject to New York City sales tax; no unconstitutional discrimination involved in excluding newspapers and periodicals from tax.

1. Section N41-2.0 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York imposed a sales tax upon every sale of tangible personal property and "upon the receipts from every sale of information services involving the furnishing of printed" matter, "information services" including the service of analyzing information. Newspapers and periodicals were excluded from the tax. Judgment declaring that plaintiff's racing "tip sheet" was subject to such tax was directed. The "tip sheet" showed on its face that it was an analysis.

2. No unconstitutional discrimination was involved in imposing the tax on plaintiff's "tip sheet" but not on newspapers and periodicals.

Bradley v. Waterfront Com. of New York Harbor


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


30 Misc. 2d 518; 220 N.Y.S.2d 681; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2327; 43 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P50,340



September 29, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion to dismiss is granted and the cross motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Waterfront Commission and the District Attorney, motioned for summary judgment to dismiss the complaint of plaintiffs, longshoreman's association and four employees. Plaintiffs cross-motioned for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought a declaration that Section 8 of the Waterfront Commission Act, 1953 N.Y. Laws 882, as amended in 1961 N.Y. Laws 211, was unconstitutional and that it had no application to the receipt in New York of dues collected from persons working outside the State or of dues from persons engaged in operations not subject to the Act. The court first held that the amendments to the Act were constitutional. The Act's original form forbade the solicitation of dues from any employees that had been convicted of a felony. The legislature sought to eliminate the criminal influence in the association and to clean up corrupt conditions on the waterfront. The amendments provided exemptions in cases where the Commission determined that an exemption would not be contrary to the objectives of the Act. The fact that the amendments extended to collections from persons not subject to the Act did not render them violative of due process. The court also held that the amendments to the Act applied to receipts in this State from persons outside the State and to receipts in this State from persons not subject to regulation under the Act. Further, the court found no federal preemption.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment and denied plaintiffs' cross-motion for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Labor unions -- Waterfront Commission Act -- 1961 amendment (L. 1961, ch. 211) valid.

Sections 8 and 8-a of the New York Harbor Waterfront Commission Act (L. 1961, ch. 211, amdg. L. 1957, ch. 188 and L. 1953, ch. 882) are constitutional and valid (cf. U. S. Const., 14th Amdt.; U. S. Code, tit. 29, §§ 151, 157, 504, subd. [a]) and constitutionally and validly apply to the receipt "within the state" of dues, assessments, levies, fines, and contributions from persons outside the State and from persons who are not subject to regulation under said Waterfront Commission Act.

Lanza v. Wagner


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


30 Misc. 2d 212; 220 N.Y.S.2d 477; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2356



September 25, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] In view of the findings herein, I must of necessity hold that the action for a declaratory judgment is itself without merit and the complaint is consequently dismissed. An order having already been entered denying the motion, settle a further order on notice to dismiss the complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff members filed a motion for an injunction pendente lite to restrain defendant mayor from nominating and appointing new members of the Board of Education of the City School District of the City of New York.


OVERVIEW: The members likened the emergency legislation to that of a bill of attainder because they were thereby summarily discharged without opportunity to defend their reputations and records and without proof of personal wrongdoing. The court dismissed the complaint. The court found that while the legislative findings specifically cited improper and deleterious conditions as prevailing in the school system, no blame for those conditions was directed to the members, either as individuals or to the Board as a unit. Nor was any crime cited against, property taken from, or punishment meted out to the members. The court determined that if the members had been removed for cause under existing provisions of law, which required officials to prefer charges and conduct hearings prior to removal, the failure to provide them would have entitled the members to relief. The court found, however, that where the legislature chose to take the matter of removal into its own hand by abolishing the old Board, those provisions could not possibly bind the governing body itself.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the complaint.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- schools -- at Extraordinary Session, Legislature validly ended terms of all members of New York City Board of Education and provided new method for Mayor to choose new Board of Education (L. 1961, ch. 971).

On legislative findings based on a report of the State Commissioner of Education, the Legislature, at an Extraordinary Session called by the Governor, validly and without a hearing (1) terminated the terms of office of the persons who comprised the New York City Board of Education, (2) provided a new method for the Mayor to choose a new Board of Education from a group of persons to be chosen by a special board which is constituted for that purpose, and (3) repealed provisions of the Education Law which had provided the manner of choosing the Board of Education of the city. (L. 1961, ch. 971.) This was not a bill of attainder (U. S. Const., art. I, § 10) or a violation [***2] of home rule (N. Y. Const., art. IX, §§ 8, 9; cf. New York City Charter, § 523, and Education Law, § 306) or a violation of the due process (N. Y. Const., art. I, § 6). Action by two members of the terminated board, for a judgment declaring the legislation unconstitutional, is dismissed.

Application of Shafer


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Erie County


31 Misc. 2d 859; 226 N.Y.S.2d 727; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2418



September 6, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [**1] For the reasons stated the present motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner brought a motion to inspect any and all ex parte orders for eavesdropping granted with respect to him following his indictment by an Erie County Grand Jury in which he was charged with the crimes of book-making and conspiring to engage in the crime of book-making in violations of N.Y. Penal Law §§ 580, 986.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner's application was based upon statements, allegedly made by an assistant district attorney and a state police officer that telephones used by petitioner had been tapped. Although the motion referred to no particular case, petitioner sought an examination to determine whether the requirements of N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. §§ 813-a, 813-b were fulfilled in order to lay the foundation for a timely motion to suppress evidence illegally obtained, if such could be maintained, before trial. In denying the motion, the court held that any order would lack certainty because petitioner asked to inspect orders, believed to exist, copies of which may have been in the possession of the several judges and the originals, if any, of which may have been in the possession of the district attorney and other law enforcement officers. Further, it was not certain whether evidence obtained in violation of Federal law and not directly unconstitutional conduct was inadmissible in a State court.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion.

1. Petitioner, who was indicted on charges of book-making and conspiracy, seeks to inspect any and all ex parte orders for eavesdropping granted with respect to him, with a view to making a motion to suppress evidence illegally obtained. However, it may be that evidence obtained in violation of Federal law, and not directly unconstitutional conduct, is admissible in a State court.

2. Moreover, New York State decisions are not uniform as to whether a motion to suppress must be made prior to trial.

3. In any event, an order granting the relief sought would lack certainty.

4. The motion is denied without prejudice to the making of a similar application at the time of trial.

Franklin v. Lynne


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


31 Misc. 2d 343; 219 N.Y.S.2d 822; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2422



September 5, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff residential property owners sought a declaratory judgment that the zoning classification of nearby business property was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The residential property owners asked that construction be enjoined and frankly stated their fear that defendant property owners would obtain vested rights in the existing classification before passage of an ordinance on which the town board had previously held hearings, which would upzone the property. The court denied the application. The court held that the exercise of a legal right could not be enjoined on the possibility that legislation to change the right could, or even probably would, be enacted. Further, the court held that having made their application for injunction, the residential property owners, even though the application was being denied, had put the property owners on notice. According to the court, they would not, therefore, be barred from obtaining an injunction that required the removal of any buildings that were placed upon the property while the action was pending.


OUTCOME: The court denied the application for the injunction.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Injunctions -- temporary injunction -- temporary injunction to bar construction on land zoned for business was denied despite claim that upzoning by legislation was being contemplated.

In an action for judgment declaring that the zoning classification of business property near the residences of plaintiffs was unconstitutional, plaintiffs were denied a temporary injunction to enjoin construction. The exercise of a legal right could not be enjoined on the possibility that the Town Board might enact legislation zoning the property into a higher classification. The denial was without prejudice to a subsequent application should upzoning be enacted.

Supreme Industrial Catering Corp. v. Fuerst


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County

CASE SUMMARY:

OVERVIEW: The Board denied the merchant's application for a peddler's license without holding a hearing on the application. In its denial, the Board stated that granting the license would not be in the best interests of the village. The merchant brought an action for an order pursuant to N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act art. 78 to direct the Board and mayor to issue him a peddler's license. The merchant also requested a declaration that his business did not require a peddler's license and that New Hyde Park, New York, Ordinance No. 1 was unconstitutional. The court did not grant the declaratory relief requested by the merchant, holding that such relief was unavailable in a proceeding under N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act art. 78. The court ruled that the Board's denial of the license application was arbitrary and capricious and ordered the Board and mayor to issue the merchant a license. The court held that N.Y. Village Law § 89(48), (52) did not allow the Board to prohibit peddling by a particular individual or by peddlers generally and that the village ordinance was invalid insofar as it attempted to enlarge the authority conferred on the Board by N.Y. Village Law § 89(48), (52).

HEADNOTES

 [***1] Licenses -- peddler's license -- in answering petition which seeks order directing respondents to issue peddler's license, respondents do not allege sufficient facts to justify their denial of petitioner's application for such license as will entitle them to trial (Civ. Prac. Act, § 1291) -- justification for denial cannot be found in statute on which they rely (Village Law, § 89, subds. 48, 52) nor in ordinance which invalidly enlarges upon their statutory authority -- petitioner was not given opportunity to be heard.

1. Petitioner seeks an order directing respondents to issue a peddler's license to it. Respondents' answer, in which they admit denial of petitioner's application for such a license, does not allege sufficient facts justifying such denial as will entitle them to a trial (Civ. Prac. Act, § 1291). The statute on which they rely for justification of the denial (Village Law, § 89, subds. 48, 52) does not empower respondent board to prohibit the business of peddling in general, but rather to regulate it. An attempt to enlarge the authority of the board in this regard by enactment of a village ordinance is invalid.

2. Moreover, the decision of respondent board [***2] was made without affording petitioner an opportunity to be heard.

3. Respondents are directed to issue the license to petitioner.

People v. Bellfield


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


33 Misc. 2d 712; 230 N.Y.S.2d 79; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2468



August 22, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the City Court of Buffalo (New York), which dismissed the information that charged defendant with violating N.Y. Penal Law § 1747-d(3). The trial court entered the order after the jury found defendant guilty as charged after the trial, but before the sentence was announced.


OVERVIEW: The State alleged that § 1747-d(3) was constitutional and that defendant's conviction should have been upheld. On review, the court found that § 1747-d(3) was constitutional and was a valid exercise of the State's police power. The court noted that § 1747-d(3), which prohibited the possession of material that could have been used to manufacture illegal drugs, did not violate defendant's due process rights. The court concluded that unless a statute appeared to have no substantial relation to a proper purpose, the legislature did not exceed its authority when it attempted to limit the type of paraphernalia that was allowed to be possessed by persons who were not in the medical field. The legislature was intending to help the drug crisis in the State.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's order, reinstated the information, and ordered defendant sentenced upon the verdict of the jury.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- possession of hypodermic needle -- Penal Law ( § 1747-d, subd. 3), rendering unlawful possession of hypodermic needle except when obtained by valid prescription, was constitutional.

Subdivision 3 of section 1747-d of the Penal Law, which rendered unlawful the possession, except by certain persons, of a hypodermic syringe or hypodermic needle, or any other instrument adapted for the administering of narcotic drugs, unless such possession be obtained upon a valid written prescription from, and such use be authorized by a duly licensed physician or veterinarian, was a valid exercise of the police power of the State and was constitutional.

Gaynor v. New York State Harness Racing Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


32 Misc. 2d 484; 222 N.Y.S.2d 859; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2489



August 16, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner government employee sought review of a determination of respondent New York State Harness Commission, which denied the employee's application for a license as a mutuel clerk.


OVERVIEW: The employee claimed that the Commission illegally, capriciously, arbitrarily, and unreasonably construed N.Y. Pari-Mutuel Revenue Law § 63 by construing the section to mean that a gross salary of $ 7,500 disqualified him from being licensed as a mutuel clerk. The employee took the position that the restriction imposed on public employees referred to "take home pay". The court disagreed. The reasoning behind the restriction was that the number of licenses for race tracks and the share of pari-mutuel revenues available to those tracks were prescribed by law. Government created the monopoly and controlled its income. Section 63 was therefore designed to meet a unique situation which did not exist elsewhere in government. It was originally proposed to bar all municipal employees from employment at race tracks. When the salary cap was included to soften the restriction for those government employees that needed second jobs to survive, the salary amount specified was arbitrarily selected and reflected a gross, not a net, amount.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Horse racing -- employment of public employees at race tracks -- public employee, with annual gross salary of $ 7,500 or more, not eligible for employment as mutuel clerk at race track (Pari-Mutuel Revenue Law, § 63).

1. A motion by the Attorney-General to have referred back to New York County the place and hearing of a proceeding for orders annulling a denial by the New York State Harness Racing Commission of petitioner's application for a license as a mutuel clerk, directing issuance of such license, and determining the constitutionality of such employment, is denied. No reason is shown for changing the place of the hearing.

2. The Pari-Mutuel Revenue Law (§ 63) permitting public officers and employees to be employed at race tracks if their annual governmental salary does not exceed $ 7,500 refers to gross salary, not to take home pay. Therefore, as petitioner, a special deputy clerk of the Supreme Court, earns $ 7,500 or more a year, the petition is dismissed.

 

2423 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Bradley v. Waterfront Com. of New York Harbor


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


30 Misc. 2d 516; 219 N.Y.S.2d 137; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2501; 48 L.R.R.M. 2846; 43 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P50,375



August 11, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff longshoremen's union filed a motion for an injunction pendente lite in its declaratory judgment action against defendants, the waterfront commission and the district attorney, seeking an interpretation of certain statutory changes made in § 8 of the Waterfront Commission Act, 1961 N.Y. Laws ch. 211, § 8, and an order to restrain them from enforcing the statute.


OVERVIEW: Section 8 in its original form prohibited the collection of dues for any waterfront union that had a convicted felon as an officer or an agent. It had been held constitutional. The waterfront commission argued that the amendments to § 8 did not detract from the constitutionality of the section. The union argued that serious issues of constitutionality were presented and that a temporary injunction was necessary to prevent the section's enforcement until the issues had been adjudicated. The court held that the union had failed to demonstrate either of the indispensable preconditions to the issuance of a preliminary injunction. No imminent threat or irreparable injury was shown because no one was prosecuting the union for violations of the law. The practice of the district attorney's office was to give notice of its intent to prosecute for a violation of § 8 before actually doing so. The court also ruled that the union had failed to show a probability of ultimate success. While it refused to prejudge the ultimate issues, the court pointed out that it appeared that there was no justiciable controversy since there was no threat of imminent prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion.


HEADNOTES

Injunctions -- pendente lite -- pendente lite injunction denied, for lack of imminent danger of irreparable injury and for lack of probability of ultimate success.

An injunction pendente lite against the prospective enforcement by a State commission and by a county District Attorney of new legislation (L. 1961, ch. 211, amdg. Waterfront Commission Act) will not be granted for plaintiffs who do not show (1) a probability of ultimate success and (2) an imminent danger of irreparable injury.

 

2424 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Kurlander v. Hempstead


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


31 Misc. 2d 121; 224 N.Y.S.2d 461; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2503



August 10, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner filed a declaratory judgment action against defendant village regarding a zoning ordinance that required a building used for a professional use in a residential area also be used as a dwelling.


OVERVIEW: The landowner owned a property that he used as a business and as his home. The property was located in a Residence B zone and the village ordinance provided that the area could be used for a professional use as long as it was also used as a dwelling. The landowner later moved his residence out of the building and maintained his business while renting the living quarters to a third party. The landowner then filed a declaratory judgment action against the village to determine that he could maintain the professional use without living on the premises. The court found that the ordinance's provision for a business was an accessory use. The court found that the ordinance was amended after the landowner began his practice in the building. The court construed the old ordinance and concluded that the ordinance was clear in that it did not require that the practitioner reside in the building that was being used in a profession. Therefore, the court found in favor of the landowner.


OUTCOME: The court found in favor of the landowner.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- statutory construction -- in zone for multiple dwellings and uses permitted in more restricted zones, professional persons could maintain offices without being subject to proviso, applicable to more restricted zones, that they live in such dwelling -- doctor who rented out his dwelling to tenant but kept his office there, before zoning ordinance was recently amended to add such proviso to his zone, has prior nonconforming use.

1. The Zoning Ordinance of the Village of Hempstead (as enacted in 1955 and prior to amdt. in 1960) permits the following buildings: (1) in Residence A and BB districts, one-family and two-family dwellings, and accessory uses by professional persons of such dwellings "in which practitioner resides"; and (2) in Residence B districts, buildings for multiple dwellings and "for any purpose permitted in a more restricted district". This meant that, in a building in a Residence B district, the office of the doctor or dentist or other professional person need not be merely accessory to his residence there.

2. The 1960 amendment to the zoning ordinance supplied the missing proviso as to Residence B districts; but the doctor [***2] and the dentist in this case had each rented out the dwelling portion of his home to a tenant, prior to the 1960 amendment; hence the doctor and the dentist each has a valid prior nonconforming use and may continue to maintain his office in his said former dwelling, though he now lives elsewhere.

 

2425 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Finkelstein


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Special Sessions of the City of New York, New York County


28 Misc. 2d 771; 218 N.Y.S.2d 341; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2558



July 25, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motions made by each of the defendants at the conclusion of the entire case and in their briefs to dismiss the information on the grounds that the defendants' guilt has not been established beyond a reasonable doubt, are denied, and each defendant is found guilty as charged in the information.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed motions to dismiss the informations against them, which charged them with selling, or have in their possession with the intent to sell, obscene books in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 1141.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged in separate informations of violating § 1141. On retrial, the court denied defendants' motions for dismissal of the informations on the ground that § 1141 was unconstitutional in that it violated the Fourteenth Amendment of the Constitution of the United States and § 6 of article I of the New York State Constitution, and on the ground that the informations were insufficient as a matter of law in that each count failed to allege that defendants sold, offered to sell, or possessed with intent to sell books mentioned in each such count knowing that the said books were obscene. The court denied the motions, holding that the issues had already been ruled upon and determined by the appellate court. The court also found that the State was not required to prove under § 1141 that defendants read the obscene materials and knew they were legally obscene because that was not the legislative intent behind the statute.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motions to dismiss the informations against them and entered judgments convicting defendants.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- obscene books -- booksellers found guilty (Penal Law, § 1141).

Defendants are found guilty of possessing and intending to sell books which they knew were obscene (Penal Law, § 1141).

 

2426 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Larchmont v. Sutton


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Westchester County


30 Misc. 2d 245; 217 N.Y.S.2d 929; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2808



June 2, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the court grants judgment in favor of the plaintiff, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff village brought an action to secure an injunction restraining defendant businesses from maintaining a sign in violation of Larchmont, N.Y., Sign Ordinance (January 4, 1954).


OVERVIEW: The village brought an action to enjoin the businesses from maintaining a sign in violation of the ordinance. The businesses argued: (1) that the ordinance was not properly noticed for public hearing, or its enactment properly published; (2) that the village lacked power to adopt the ordinance; (3) that the defendants had a vested right to maintain the sign; and (4) the ordinance was unconstitutional. The court held that the notice was sufficient because it described the subject of the hearing in general terms, as required, and that the description of the ordinance in the notice complied with the terms of the local law calling for "a brief description." The court further held that the legislature authorized the adoption of the ordinance and found that the village was empowered to determine that signs such as that maintained by the businesses had a distracting influence on motorists. The court also found that the nature of the nonconforming use of the sign did not rise to the stature of a vested right because the sign not appear to be a substantial investment and the initial variance granted to the businesses was conditioned on the compliance of all signs with the building code.


OUTCOME: The court granted judgment in favor of the village to enjoin the businesses from maintaining a sign in violation of the ordinance.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- villages -- regulation of signs -- notice of public hearing for and adoption of ordinance requiring removal of existing nonconforming signs sufficient -- village is empowered to regulate signs -- maintenance of yard sign not vested right.

1. After defendants had maintained for several years a nonconforming business use under a variance, the village adopted an ordinance (Local Laws, 1952, No. 1 of Village of Larchmont) which limited sign display in residential districts and provided for the removal of existing nonconforming signs. A notice of the public hearing to be held describing the subject of the hearing generally was sufficient (Village Law, § 90), as was a notice of adoption of the ordinance which briefly described it.

2. The village was empowered to adopt an ordinance reasonably regulating signs, and defendants have no vested right to the maintenance of a yard sign.
