2428 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sabatino


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Queens County


29 Misc. 2d 886; 216 N.Y.S.2d 276; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2874



May 22, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The matter was before the court on the demurrer of defendant to the indictment charging him with the crimes of grand larceny and forgery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with multiple crimes. He filed a demurrer to the indictment on the ground that N.Y. Jud. Law § 609, which provided for the selection of grand jurors, was unconstitutional in that it was violative of N.Y. Const. art. III, § 17. Section 17 prohibited the enactment of local or private legislation dealing with the selecting, drawing, summoning, or impaneling of grand or petit jurors. The court held that a demurrer was not the proper vehicle to raise the constitutional issue of the valid existence of the grand jury because it served only to raise objections which appeared upon the face of the indictment. A defect in the composition of the grand jury did not appear on the face of the indictment. Defendant's challenge to the grand jury was prohibited by N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 231. The court held that, even if N.Y. Jud. Law § 609 was private or local legislation, the indictments returned against defendant were not null and void. Because the grand jury was acting under color of law, it was a de facto grand jury and its acts were valid. Therefore, it was not necessary for the court to pass upon the constitutionality of Section 609.


OUTCOME: The court disallowed defendant's demurrer.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Grand Jury -- constitutional law -- although Legislature cannot enact local grand jury law, defendant cannot demur to such Grand Jury's indictment valid on its face (N. Y. Const., art. III, § 17; Code Crim. Pro., §§ 231, 323).

An indictment which is valid on its face cannot be demurred to on the ground that the Grand Jury was impaneled and selected pursuant to a statute which, the demurrer asserts, is unconstitutionally local legislation (Judiciary Law, § 609; N. Y. Const., art. III, § 17; Code Crim. Pro., §§ 231, 323).

 

2429 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Hiscox v. Levine


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


31 Misc. 2d 151; 216 N.Y.S.2d 801; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2875



May 19, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated proceedings, petitioner neighbors sought judicial review under N.Y. Town Law § 282 of a zoning variance given by respondent, a town planning board, on the application of respondent developer to build 49 homes on approximately 33 acres in exchange for conveyance of approximately 30 acres to the town for a public park.


OVERVIEW: The town authorized the board to make "reasonable" changes in zoning regulations, but it required the maintenance of the average population density and strict conformance with § 281. The developer offered land for a park in exchange for a variance to develop the rest of the property. The board approval was annulled on judicial review. The board granted the reapplication. The neighbors sought judicial review. The delegation of power to the board was constitutional because the standards were capable of reasonable application and the board's powers were sufficiently limited and defined. The standards in § 281 were constitutional, and there was no conflict with N.Y. Town Law §§ 261-265. However, N.Y. Town Law § 281 had not given the board the power it had attempted to exercise because the variance given to the developer affected 63 acres out of a 100 acres and was so great a change as to be considered unreasonable. The board's action was prohibited under N.Y. Town Law § 265. In addition, the variance given to the developer increased the population density of the area, which exceeded the power given by the town's delegation. The board's alleged findings were unsupported conclusions.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the determination of the board.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- town planning board's approval of subdivision, permitting lots lying in zone which requires one acre per building to comply with other zone which requires only half acre per building, annulled (Town Law, §§ 281, 282).

Purportedly acting under a general resolution of the Town Board authorizing the town's Planning Board "to make any reasonable change" in the zoning regulation of platted lands, provided (1) that such change maintains the "average density of population" permitted in the zone and (2) that the appropriate use of adjoining land is reasonably safeguarded and (3) that such plan is "consistent with the public welfare" (Town Law, § 281), the Planning Board passed a resolution accepting an offer by the owner of a plat to dedicate 37.4 acres thereof to the town for park purposes, and modifying the zoning regulations so as to permit all lots in the subdivision's remaining acres, some of which lay in an "A" zone requiring one acre for each building, and some of which lay in a "B" zone requiring only half an acre for each building, to comply merely with the "B" zone requirement. The Planning Board's resolution is annulled (Town Law, § [***2] 282). Such a change in a large tract would in effect amend the zoning ordinance itself -- a power exercisable by the Town Board only (Town Law, §§ 261-265, 267, 277, subd. 1). Moreover, (1) the Planning Board's resolution necessarily increases the permitted "density of population"; and the Planning Board's findings under (2) and (3) above stated are mere conclusions unsupported by any facts.

 

2430 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Di Prima v. Wagner


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


27 Misc. 2d 380; 215 N.Y.S.2d 687; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2951



May 5, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Mayor of City of New York and intervenor-defendant Attorney General, sought dismissal or summary judgment in plaintiff taxpayer's action to declare unconstitutional 1961 N.Y. Laws 87, that amended N.Y. Mun. Home Rule Law § 20(3) and added a new subdivision § 20(4), authorizing a mayor to appoint a charter commission, and to enjoin defendants from spending city money to further the new law.


OVERVIEW: The gravamen of the suit was that the challenged statute was not a general law applying to all cities alike, but was designed solely for the mayor of New York City. The court denied the taxpayer's motion for a temporary injunction and held that the statute was valid insofar as it authorized the alternative method of naming a charter commission because there was no showing that the statute's application was not alike as to the charters of all cities in the state. The court also upheld the provisions granting mayors power to appropriate city funds for the use of the mayor's commission, after 30 days of inaction by the appropriate city officials. But the court denied defendants' motions for dismissal or summary judgment and held that the new restrictive provisions of §§ 20(3), (4)(e), which essentially choked off alternative action by the local legislature and people, were invalid as an improper delegation of legislative power, in violation of N.Y. Const. art. III, § 1, the home rule policy of the state reflected by N.Y. Const. Art. XI, §§ 11, 12, and N.Y. Mun. Home Rule Law § 33.


OUTCOME: The court denied the taxpayer's motion for a temporary injunction. The court also denied defendants' alternative cross-motions for dismissal or summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- new charter for city -- Mayor's appointment of charter revision commission declared not to exclude concurrent revision by local legislature (City Home Rule Law, § 20; N. Y. Const., art. III, § 1; art. IX, §§ 8, 11, 12).

Paragraph (e) of subdivision 4 of section 20 of the City Home Rule Law, and the newly added next-to-last sentence of subdivision 3 of said section 20 (both portions as added by L. 1961, ch. 87), are declared by Special Term of the Supreme Court to be invalid, as violative of constitutional and statutory principles governing home rule and delegation of legislative power and implied repeal of statutes (N. Y. Const., art. III, § 1; art. IX, §§ 8, 11, 12; City Home Rule Law, § 15, subd. 10; § 20, subd. 3; §§ 16, 19-a, 33; New York City Charter, § 40, subd. 10; § 44), insofar as the newly added provisions prohibit a city's legislature and people from acting upon any alternative plan of charter revision after the Mayor of the city has appointed a charter revision commission.

Savage v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


29 Misc. 2d 725; 215 N.Y.S.2d 682; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2983



May 2, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The application is in all respects denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidate filed an application before the Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County (New York), challenging respondent city board of education's denial of his request for absentee voting and designation of inspectors in a school district election.


OVERVIEW: After denying the candidate's request for absentee voting and designate inspectors, the board advised him that although the provisions of the election law that concerned election watchers did not apply to a school district election, he had the right to designate the presence of qualified voters at the various polling places. The candidate argued that N.Y. Elec. Law § 2607 was unconstitutional. The court denied the candidate's request insofar: (1) as it sought permission to designate inspectors of election because no basis was presented to declare § 2607 unconstitutional; (2) as the request for permission to designate watchers was concerned because the candidate had been afforded the rights that he requested by the board; and (3) as it sought to require the institution of absentee voting procedures because there existed no provision of law that authorized the procedures. School district elections were clearly excluded from the ballot provisions of the election law. Only the legislature, in the exercise of its constitutional authority, had the authority to grant the absentee voting rights that were requested by the candidate.


OUTCOME: The court denied a candidate's application which challenged a city board of education's decision to deny his request for absentee voting and to designate inspectors in a school district election.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- school district elections -- petition by candidates for permission to designate inspectors at school district election denied absent showing that section 2607 of Education Law is unconstitutional -- permission to designate watchers already has been granted -- application denied as to request to permit use of absentee ballots -- no statutory authority therefor exists.

1. An application by petitioner, who is a candidate in a Board of Education election, for permission to choose 20% of the total number of inspectors to be designated for the election is denied absent any basis for his contention that section 2607 of the Education Law, providing for designation of inspectors of election by the Board of Education, is unconstitutional.

2. Petitioner's request for permission to designate two watchers at each school election district already has been granted by the Board of Education.

3. The application is denied insofar as it seeks to require the institution of absentee voting procedures. Neither the Education Law ( § 2609, subds. 1, 4) nor the Election Law ( §§ 100, 117) makes any provision for, and portions of such statutes [***2] actually are inconsistent with, the use of absentee ballots in school district elections.

 

2432 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Le Bous


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, Binghamton


29 Misc. 2d 850; 215 N.Y.S.2d 829; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2984



May 2, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss before the City Court of New York, Binghamton County (New York), seeking the dismissal of the People's action against him for operating his motor vehicle at a speed greater than was reasonable and prudent under the conditions, in violation of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1180(1).


OVERVIEW: The People filed an action against defendant for violating § 1180(1). The case was tried without a jury. Defendant moved for dismissal of the information at the close of his case on the grounds the People failed in their proof because the information was sworn to on direct knowledge and not upon information and belief. Defendant objected to the part of the information that specifically stated 40 miles per hour. The court found defendant guilty of operating his motor vehicle at a speed greater than was reasonable and prudent under the conditions and denied his motion to dismiss the action because the information was sufficient in and of itself to establish prima facie the essential elements of the violation charged against defendant. The People met their burden of proof and established the three essential elements of § 1180 and that defendant operated his motor vehicle at a speed greater than was reasonable and prudent under the conditions.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the People's action and found him guilty of operating his motor vehicle at a speed greater than was reasonable and prudent under the conditions.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Motor vehicles -- speeding -- information of officer, based on personal knowledge from having witnessed accident, was sufficient to charge defendant with violation of subdivision 3 of section 1180 of Vehicle and Traffic Law; officer's evidence established essential elements of violation and defendant was found guilty.

1. An information, used as a pleading, charged that defendant violated subdivision 3 of section 1180 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law in that he operated his vehicle at a speed greater than was reasonably prudent, in excess of 30 miles per hour, "specifically 40 miles per hour, under the conditions existing, which was wet and slippery pavement resulting in his being unable to stop his vehicle without skidding and colliding with another vehicle". The information, based in part upon an officer's personal knowledge from witnessing the accident, was sufficient to establish the essential elements of the violation. The use of the phrase "specifically 40 miles per hour" was surplusage.

2. The officer witnessed the accident and gave his opinion of defendant's speed from the moment defendant came into view and until the collision, and also testified that, following the [***2] accident, defendant admitted that he was traveling at 40 miles per hour. This evidence was sufficient to show that defendant travelled (1) at a speed greater than was reasonable and prudent, (2) under the conditions existing and (3) having regard to actual and potential hazards then existing. Defendant was found guilty.

 

2433 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Apostle


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Rockland County


30 Misc. 2d 55; 214 N.Y.S.2d 101; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3005



April 27, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The judgment of the Court of Special Sessions is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Court of Special Sessions of the Town of Clarkstown (New York) of advertising without a permit in violation of N.Y. Comp. Code R. & Regs. tit. 6, § 261.10. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sitting behind the wheel of a car located on a bridge that ran over a parkway. The rear of the car contained a sign that advertised a business. A police officer noticed the car when he passed the bridge while travelling on the parkway and again on his return to the area a few minutes later. The officer cited defendant with advertising without a permit. On appeal, the court held that the evidence provided by the officer was sufficient to establish the State's case beyond a reasonable doubt. The court found that the vehicle was within the boundaries of the parkway when it parked on a bridge running over the parkway and was subject to the advertising restrictions in effect for the parkway, which prohibited the advertising without a permit, N.Y. Comp. Code R. & Regs. tit. 6, § 261.10.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's conviction of defendant for advertising without a permit.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- advertising on parkway -- rule against advertising on parkway applies to exit bridge above parkway and to car which stood on bridge and carried sign "Escort Car to [homes for sale]" -- attorney for park commission properly appeared for People.

1. Homes for sale in Rockland County were advertised in a New York City newspaper, with directions to reach the site through the Palisades Interstate Parkway and to "Look for Escort Cars at Pkwy. Exit 10." At exit 10 a road, which was formerly a county road, and which may perhaps still be a county road, is carried over and above the Palisades Interstate Parkway by a bridge which is owned and maintained by the Palisades Interstate Park Commission. On this bridge stood a motor vehicle bearing the sign "Escort Car to [the advertised homes for sale]". The driver of this car was properly convicted of advertising without permission (Rules and Regulations of Palisades Interstate Park Commission, rule 13 [6 NYCRR 261.10]; see, also, Conservation Law, §§ 675, 678, 748, 762; cf. Vehicle and Traffic Law, §§ 1600, 1604, 1630).

2. Defendant's assertion that the commission's [***2] rule is enforced in a discriminatory and hence unconstitutional manner was not sufficiently proved.

3. The attorney for the commission properly appeared for the People of the State of New York, with the District Attorney's permission.

Levin v. Haber


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


28 Misc. 2d 529; 215 N.Y.S.2d 274; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3007



April 27, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Therefore the application is denied, and the cross motion granted, but without prejudice to the institution of such plenary suit as petitioners may be advised.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, petitioner landowners sought an order directing respondents, members of a board of education, to discharge a notice of designation and notice of pendency of proceeding in connection with the condemnation of the landowners' property and to enjoin the members from filing any further designations affecting the property. The members filed a cross-motion to dismiss the petition as legally insufficient.


OVERVIEW: The members filed a notice and designation but an approving referendum, which was required by law because the indebtedness of the school district would exceed 10 percent of the value of its property, was defeated. The board filed a new designation, but the referendum was again defeated. The school board advised the court that it intended to file a new designation and put the same referendum up for vote a third time. The landowners contended that the Nassau County Civil Divisions Act, 1951 N.Y. Laws ch. 767, § 520.4(2)(b), in providing for the liening of property without compensation was unconstitutional. The court held that the landowners could not challenge the constitutionality of the act in a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, which was in the nature of a mandamus proceeding. Mandamus was not a substitute for an injunction in a plenary suit to prevent a violation of a law, nor was it to be used to direct nonenforcement of an law alleged to be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court denied the landowners' application without prejudice to file a plenary suit and granted the members' cross-motion to dismiss.


HEADNOTES

Proceeding against body or officer -- mandamus -- proceeding in nature of mandamus to test constitutionality of law or to prevent violation of law or to direct nonenforcement of law alleged to be unconstitutional was dismissed on ground that mandamus was not substitute for plenary action.

Respondent Board of Education filed, pursuant to paragraph (b) of subdivision 2 of section 520.4 of the Nassau County Civil Divisions Act (L. 1951, ch. 767), a notice of designation and notice of pendency in connection with the contemplated condemnation of 52.8 acres of land owned by petitioners for a school site. Thereafter, a referendum to approve the proposition for condemnation was defeated by the voters. Respondent board then cancelled the old designation and filed a new one again tying up petitioners' property. A new referendum was had and again the proposition was defeated. Petitioners alleged that, in providing for the liening of property without compensation, paragraph (b) of subdivision 2 of section 520.4 was unconstitutional.  [***2] A proceeding under article 78 of the Civil Practice Act in the nature of mandamus to direct respondent board to discharge a notice of designation and to enjoin it from filing any other further designations cannot be used to test the constitutionality of paragraph (b) of subdivision 2 of section 520.4 of the Nassau County Civil Divisions Act, nor may mandamus be used as a substitute for an injunction in a plenary suit to prevent violation of a law nor may it be used to direct nonenforcement of a law alleged to be unconstitutional. The petition was dismissed for legal insufficiency.

 

2435 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Kress


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


30 Misc. 2d 265; 214 N.Y.S.2d 555; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3134



March 30, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Settle order, which should provide for payment of guardians' fees and attorneys' allowances.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner trustee instituted an action to settle his account under an irrevocable trust indenture. The trustee also sought a determination as to whether the trustee had to contribute to the payment of estate and inheritance taxes or whether the burden fell upon the trust and respondent beneficiaries.


OVERVIEW: The settlor established an irrevocable trust consisting of stock and life insurance policies on the life of her father, the trustee. The settlor provided in her will that estate and inheritance taxes on the trust corpus were to be equitably prorated and paid from the trust. Because the settlor died a resident of Connecticut and because Connecticut had an apportionment statute, the court applied Connecticut law. Connecticut had a statute that provided that the trustee was to contribute to the payment of taxes. However, the statute was not enacted until 10 years after the creation of the trust. The court found that the apportionment statute was applicable to the trust; however, totally aside from any statute, where the will clearly directed apportionment, the will would be honored. The court found that the settlor clearly and unambiguously directed that the trust pay its fair share of the taxes. Thus, apportionment was applicable to the trust.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the trust would bear its portion of estate and inheritance taxes.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- estate tax -- apportionment -- inter vivos trust, located in New York and created prior to enactment of apportionment statute of Connecticut, domicile of settlor who died after passage of statute, is subject to proportionate share of estate taxes, pursuant to statute and under terms of settlor's will -- outstanding loan by trust to settlor may be continued under conditions specified.

1. A Connecticut resident created an irrevocable and unalterable inter vivos trust, the corpus of which is located and administered in New York State. The trust indenture is silent as to payment of estate taxes. However, the settlor's will directed that estate and inheritance taxes on property not passing under the will should be "equitably prorated and paid from the said property". Moreover, a Connecticut apportionment statute, which New York will apply, provides for inclusion of inter vivos transfers within a decedent's gross estate and applies to trusts created prior to its passage where the settlor died subsequent thereto. Accordingly the subject trust should bear its proportionate [***2] share of the estate taxes, which the trustee is authorized to advance directly to the taxing authorities, making proper safeguard for return of any refund to the trust corpus.

2. An outstanding loan of the settlor from the trust may be continued upon deposit by the executor of additional security as specified, with the written consent of all adult parties. The trustees are directed not to extend payment of the loan beyond maturity or otherwise modify the agreement without further court approval.

 

2436 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Thomas v. Bedford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


29 Misc. 2d 861; 214 N.Y.S.2d 145; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3154



March 28, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff neighbors filed an action against defendants, town, board members, owners, and vendee, seeking a judgment declaring that an ordinance was void and unreasonable, which reclassified the owners' property from a residential to a research office district.


OVERVIEW: A town board enacted an ordinance reclassifying the owners' parcels from residential to research office uses. Neighbors in the residential district filed an action against the town, its board members, the owners, and a contract vendee seeking a judgment declaring the ordinance unreasonable and void. The court dismissed the complaint, which came down to a difference of opinion between the neighbors and town as to the area's proper development. The court held that the town and planning boards were within their legislative judgment in weighing the usefulness of rezoning and considering that the use of the property for education and a pre-existing laboratory under special permit was closely allied to research purposes, that the prior estate quality of the surrounding land was disintegrating, that the tax rate had increased, and that the trend among municipalities in the county was to permit highly restricted business uses on acreage of a large size. The court held that the reclassification in response to changing patterns of living was not spot zoning because there was no evidence that the town was motivated by favoritism for the owners of the large area.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the neighbors' action against the town, board members, owners, and vendee for a declaratory judgment that the rezoning ordinance was void.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- complaint seeking declaration of invalidity of town ordinance reclassifying three parcels of real property from residence district to research office district dismissed -- plaintiffs failed to sustain burden of proving reclassification was spot zoning and constituted improper exercise of powers of Town Board -- board's determination, based on consideration of need, congruity of surrounding uses, physical, economic and social causes and effects, was not arbitrary or unconstitutional.

1. In view of the importance of the issues involved, an action for a judgment declaring unreasonable and void a town ordinance reclassifying three parcels of real property from a Residence 4-Acre ("4 A") district to a Research Office ("R O") district is considered on the merits, despite doubt as to plaintiffs' standing to contest the validity of said ordinance.

2. The burden was on plaintiffs to prove that the reclassification was invalid as "spot" zoning and was not a proper exercise of the powers of the Town Board, which has authority to make changes in zoning policy to adjust to changing patterns of living.

3. In forming the legislative judgment the town [***2] officials were justified in considering that (1) two of the subject parcels already were used for purposes similar to "R O" purposes; (2) the subject area bordered on a State highway, near a junction with a parkway; (3) the State had established a museum nearby; (4) the subject area was within a short distance of a settled community with railroad service; (5) there was evidence that the prior estate quality of the surrounding land was in the process of disintegration; (6) the quantity of residentially zoned land in the town far exceeded that zoned for commercial purposes; (7) the tax rates, especially for school needs, had increased sharply in recent years. A judgment based on such considerations may not be declared arbitrary or unreasonable.

4. The town authorities were not required to prove a change of condition to justify the reclassification.

5. Plaintiffs have not proved their charge of "spot" zoning. The subject parcel comprises 123 acres. Moreover, there is no evidence that the town authorities were motivated by favoritism for the owners of the subject area, without consideration of the welfare of the town at large.

6. At best, plaintiffs make debatable the reclassification [***3] of the subject area; and that is insufficient to overturn the legislative judgment.

7. The complaint is dismissed.

 

2437 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Benedict v. Roberts


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial and Special Term, Madison County


30 Misc. 2d 650; 221 N.Y.S.2d 192; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3186



March 21, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowners sought the annulment of a determination of respondent town highway superintendent closing a portion of a town road.


OVERVIEW: The portion of the road in question ran through the landowner's farm property. The town discontinued the road as useless. The landowners alleged that they had been unconstitutionally deprived of the use of their property without due process and that discontinuance of the portion of the road was illegal. They also claimed that the superintendent did not comply with the requirements of N.Y. High. Law § 171 because consent of adjoining landowners was not obtained before the discontinuance. The superintendent argued that the landowners' property did not immediately abut the discontinued portion of the road and, thus, they were not entitled to maintain the proceeding. The court found that because the property was not adjoining and a mere inconvenience to the general public was not actionable, the landowners were not entitled to a remedy. N.Y. High. Law § 186 was not applicable to the claim, as the landowners' argued, because it only applied where a road lied within two or more towns.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the landowners' claim as a matter of law.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Highways -- discontinuance by town of portion of town road -- owner of land on open portion of town road cannot object to discontinuance of other, useless portion (Highway Law, § 171, subd. 2).

A town road in Madison County runs from a State highway in the Town of Madison to a county highway in the Town of Eaton. The owners of a farm through which a portion of this town road ran, and a proposed purchaser of a portion of said farm for use as an airplane landing strip, petitioned the Town of Eaton's Highway Superintendent for an order discontinuing such portion of the town road, as useless. The Town of Madison's Highway Superintendent and Town Board also consented, perhaps gratuitously and unnecessarily. The Town of Eaton's Highway Superintendent found that this portion of the road was useless and he ordered it discontinued, and the Eaton Town Board so consented. Petitioners, who own property in the Town of Madison abutting a portion of this road which is still open, cannot object (Highway Law, § 171, subd. 2; cf. §§ 184, 186). Their review petition (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78) is dismissed.

 

2438 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gazulis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, City of Poughkeepsie, Dutchess County


29 Misc. 2d 939; 212 N.Y.S.2d 910; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3197



March 17, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to dismiss the information accusing him of violating N.Y. Penal Law § 986-b.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that § 986-b was unconstitutional because it was too vague and indefinite to prescribe a crime and the presumption created by the statute violated the constitutional requirement of due process of law. The law made a person who knowingly possessed a record of a bet made by a person engaged in book-making or pool-setting guilty of a misdemeanor. Defendant contended that the language in the statute was vague. Further, he alleged that the statute did not specify whether it applied to the occasional better or whether it applied only to the professional gambler. The court found the legislative intent of the statute was to make the occasional better guilty of the misdemeanor. The court found that the legislature's attempt to create a presumption in the last section of § 986-b was unconstitutional and the court declared it a nullity. However the rest of the statute was lawful and enforceable. Thus, the court directed that defendant be tried upon the information.


OUTCOME: The court directed that defendant be tried upon the information.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- book-making -- section 986-b of Penal Law, which provides that any person knowingly having possession of writing, paper or document which is record made by person engaged in book-making or pool selling of bet or wager shall be guilty of misdemeanor, not unconstitutional -- statute intended to cover occasional bettor -- part of statute providing that proof of possession of such document is presumptive evidence of possession thereof knowingly is unconstitutional -- defendant may be tried on valid part of statute.

1. Section 986-b of the Penal Law, which provides that any person who shall knowingly have possession of any writing, paper or document representing or being a record made by a person engaged in book-making or pool selling of a bet or wager shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, is not too vague and indefinite to prescribe a crime and is not unconstitutional.

2. The statute was intended to make the horse and number player guilty of a misdemeanor, even though they did not make their living by gambling and were an occasional bettor.

3. That part of the statute which provides that "Proof of the possession of any writing, paper or document of the kind mentioned herein [***2] is presumptive evidence of possession thereof knowingly" is unconstitutional in that it attempts to convict a citizen without due process of law. To hold the presumption valid would require an accused to establish his innocence instead of requiring the People to prove his guilt.

4. Defendant may be tried upon the information, but the part of the statute attempting to create the presumption must be treated as a nullity.

Kohilakis v. Harwood


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


29 Misc. 2d 800; 213 N.Y.S.2d 892; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3205



March 16, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Plaintiffs' cross motion for a temporary injunction is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed a complaint against defendant town board that asserted that the town board was unauthorized to expend any money in connection with the preparation of an incinerator site for construction. The town board sought a dismissal of the complaint on the ground that no bond or surety was served with the summons and complaint as provided by N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 51.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed a cross-motion for permission to file a bond nunc pro tunc and also for a temporary injunction enjoining the expenditure of funds by the town board. The taxpayers asserted that a bond was not necessary because the action was not filed under § 51 but was merely one for a declaratory judgment wherein a bond was not required. The court noted that the nature of the instant action must have been determined from the complaint and prayer for relief. The court held that the action was basically an action under § 51 and the filing of a bond was required. The court also concluded that the taxpayers had not shown a right to a temporary injunction. The resolution that was passed as well as a referendum authorized the issuance of bonds and capital notes. The taxpayers' allegations were merely conclusory and insufficient to authorize the granting of a temporary injunction. Finally, the court determined that the taxpayers' argument that until the prior litigation attacking the legality and constitutionality of the referendum and resolution was determined, any payments to have been made were unauthorized was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court granted the town board's motion to dismiss unless the taxpayers filed a bond within 10 days after service of the order. The taxpayers' cross-motion to file a bond nunc pro tunc was granted. However, the court denied the taxpayers' cross-motion for a temporary injunction.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- taxpayer's action -- bond -- action seeking declaration as to validity of payments made following resolution and referendum authorizing acquisition of certain property and erection of incinerator and issuance of bonds and capital notes, and seeking return of funds, limitations of payments and injunctive relief, considered as action brought under section 51 of General Municipal Law -- filing of bond was necessary -- no right to temporary injunction shown -- papers insufficient to determine whether prior action to declare resolution and referendum unconstitutional is finally determined.

1. Defendant Town Board adopted a resolution authorizing the acquisition of certain property, the erection thereon of an incinerator and the issuance of bonds and capital notes of the town to pay the cost thereof. Thereafter, at a referendum, the resolution was approved by the voters. Allegedly expenditures have been made for engineering services out of the town's surplus account. Plaintiffs seek judgment to declare invalid the payments already made, with a direction for the return thereof, a direction [***2] that any payments in connection with improvement of the incinerator site and construction thereof be limited to the funds authorized by the referendum and resolution, and to enjoin the Town Board from paying out any moneys for the purpose of the incinerator except out of the bonds and capital notes authorized by the referendum and resolution. The action is one brought under section 51 of the General Municipal Law. It is not an action only for declaratory judgment. Plaintiffs seek not only a declaration as to the validity of payments made, but also ask for other relief specified in section 51 of the General Municipal Law -- return of funds, limitations of payments and injunctive relief. A filing of a bond was, therefore, necessary and a motion to dismiss the complaint is granted unless the bond is filed.

2. Plaintiffs have not shown a right to a temporary injunction. Their claim that the expenditure of general or surplus town moneys for the purpose or object of the referendum and resolution is illegal and contrary to the intent of the Local Finance Law is not supported by statutory authority (cf. Local Finance Law, § 165.10).

3. The papers in support of the instant motion are [***3] insufficient for the court to determine whether or not a prior action to declare the resolution and referendum unconstitutional, null and void and contrary to law is finally determined or is still pending.

 

2440 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Franklin Nat'l Bank v. Clark


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, New York County


26 Misc. 2d 724; 212 N.Y.S.2d 942; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3221



March 14, 1961 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bank sought a declaratory judgment and incidental relief against defendants, the Superintendent of Banks of the State of New York and various commercial and savings banks, in its action claiming that the Omnibus Banking Bill, 1960 N.Y. Laws ch. 237, which was described as an act to amend the banking law, in relation to bank holding companies, was void and violated N.Y. Const. art. III, § 14, and N.Y. Legis. Law §§ 40, 41, 42, and 44.


OVERVIEW: The bank sought declaratory judgment and incidental relief against defendants, claiming that the Omnibus Banking Bill (Bill), 1960 N.Y. Laws ch. 237, was void and did not become a law because when it was called up for passage, it was not on the desks of the members of the legislature in its final form, in violation of the N.Y. Const. art. III, § 14, and because the existence of the original law in the archives and in the custody of the Secretary of State was in doubt and unexplained, contrary to N.Y. Legis. Law §§ 40, 41, 42, and 44. The court held that the Bill was invalidly passed and did not become law because according to documentary evidence and testimony from several senators, the final form of the Bill was not on the legislators' desks for three days before its passage and that despite the governor's call for an immediate vote, the Bill was required to be in its final form, even if it wasn't printed. The court found that discrepancies between the senate journal and copies of the final Bill and its certificate of the presiding officers at its passage, although presumed effective, still cast doubts on the legislative procedures followed, or not, in the Bill's enactment.


OUTCOME: The court granted judgment in favor of the bank, holding that the Omnibus Banking Bill was invalidly passed and that defendant banks were jointly and severally enjoined from opening, occupying, and operating any branch office in two specific counties. The court further held that defendant superintendent had no legal authority or powers to permit any banks to open, occupy, or operate branches in the said counties.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- judgment invalidating hastily passed law -- law (L. 1960, ch. 237) is adjudged void, since it was not on legislators' desks in final form when it was certified as passed (N. Y. Const., art. III, § 14) -- testimony and documents show that certificates by presiding officers are not "conclusive" (Legislative Law, § 40).

1. Chapter 237 of the Laws of 1960 (amending the provisions of the Banking Law as to bank holding companies) is, after a trial in this action instituted by a bank in the New York Supreme Court, at which trial testimony was adduced from two State Senators and the General Clerk and the Journal Clerk of the Senate and from the State Superintendent of Banks, and there were received in evidence the originals or photostats of legislative documents including legislative journals, a stenographic transcript of the Senate proceedings on the final consideration of the bill, a mimeographed version of the bill and a different printed version of the bill each certified a month apart by the Secretary of State as the original law, declared void. This judgment is based on the grounds that (1) in spite of a certificate from the Governor to the Legislature [***2] stating "the facts which in his opinion necessitate an immediate vote thereon", the bill was not "nevertheless * * * upon the desks of the members" of the Legislature "in final form * * * before its final passage" (N. Y. Const., art. III, § 14), and (2) the existence of the original law in the archives and in the custody of the Secretary of State is in doubt and unexplained, contrary to the Legislative Law ( §§ 40, 41, 42, 44). Accordingly, the defendant banks are enjoined from opening any branch offices in Nassau County and Westchester County, and the State Superintendent of Banks, codefendant, is declared to have no legal authority relating to any application of any bank for permission to open such a branch.

2. Certificates by legislative presiding officers that a bill has been passed are not "conclusive evidence thereof" (Legislative Law, § 40) when testimony and documents show that the certificates contravene the mandatory requirements of the State Constitution (art. III, § 14).

Simone v. Kennedy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


26 Misc. 2d 748; 212 N.Y.S.2d 838; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3336



February 24, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion for judgment in favor of plaintiffs is denied, and the cross motion for dismissal of the complaint is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff representative of all owners, operators, and employees of cabarets, artists performing in cabarets, and taxpayers of the City of New York and others, filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings or summary judgment in an action contesting certain regulations issued by defendant Police Commissioner of the City of New York. Defendants, the Commissioner and others, filed a cross-motion for judgment in their favor dismissing the complaint.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought an action contesting certain regulations issued by the Commissioner. The regulations required the fingerprinting of every cabaret employee who comes in contact or is likely to come in contact with patrons of the cabaret. The regulations also required all such employees to obtain identification cards. The court denied plaintiffs' motion for judgment on the pleadings or summary judgment and granted defendants' cross motion for judgment in their favor dismissing the complaint. The court found that the regulations had previously been held to be constitutional and valid. The court held that it could not rule on the legality of service charges for the identification cards because there had been no allegations that they exceeded the cost of rendering the services for which the fee was exacted. The court held that although there was no authority for the provision in the police regulations that the fees collected be deposited to the credit of the Police Pension Fund, there had been no showing that the City of New York had been financially damaged by the regulation, nor had there been a showing of a waste of municipal funds.


OUTCOME: The court denied the representative's motion for judgment on the pleadings or summary judgment in her action contesting certain regulations issued by the Commissioner. The court granted defendants' cross motion for dismissal of the complaint.


HEADNOTES

Licenses -- cabaret employees -- New York City Police Commissioner's regulations requiring cabaret employees to carry $ 2 fingerprinted identification cards are valid -- $ 2 may be turned over to Police Pension Fund.

1. The New York City Police Commissioner's regulations governing cabarets validly require every employee of a cabaret who is likely to come in contact with patrons to be fingerprinted and to obtain an identification card for $ 2. The $ 2 fee is not excessive. Section 67 of the Public Officers Law and sections 1826 and 1830 of the Penal Law are inapplicable.

2. The $ 2 fees are validly turned over to the New York City Police Pension Fund, pursuant to the aforesaid regulations. These fees merely have a small effect in reducing the Pension Fund's annual deficit which the City of New York annually makes good (Administrative Code of City of New York, § B18-3.0).

Bettman v. Michaelis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


27 Misc. 2d 1010; 212 N.Y.S.2d 339; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3369



February 17, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Settle one order on notice reciting the granting on consent of the motion for consolidation from the Bench, and dismissing both proceedings, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner homeowners and respondent permittee appealed a decision of respondent Board of Zoning Appeals of the Town of Hempstead (board) (New York), which granted a building permit to the permittee to build a bowling alley. Both parties brought proceedings under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 that were consolidated for review under Hempstead, N.Y., Town Law § 267(7).


OVERVIEW: The homeowners sought to annul the board's decision that affirmed the issuance of the permit. The permittee sought to annul the board's decision that reversed the building inspector's approval of a parking plan for 128 cars to only 125 cars, and modified the permit by reducing the number of alleys permitted from 32 to 31. The court dismissed both proceedings on the merits. The homeowners' contention that the existence of gasoline stations within 300 feet mandated denial of the permit was overruled. The ordinance only prohibited erection of a gasoline station within 300 feet of a place of amusement, but permitted a place of amusement to be erected within 300 feet of an existing service station. The board did not err when it visited the property though it would have been better practice for the board to make its survey in the presence of both parties. The court concluded that there was substantial evidence to support the board's conclusions, and the board's decision had a reasonable basis in law and was neither arbitrary nor capricious.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the board of zoning appeals that permitted a bowling alley over the objections of adjacent homeowners and dismissed the proceedings.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- bowling alley permit modification confirmed (Town Law, § 267).

1. A town building inspector's permit to erect a 32-alley bowling building, with a 10-foot setback, and with parking spaces for 128 cars between the columns on which the building rested, in a zone wherein such uses and setback are authorized by the zoning ordinance, was properly modified by the town's Board of Zoning Appeals (Town Law, § 267, subds. 2, 3, 7) so as to reduce the number of alleys to 31 and the number of cars to 125.

2. The board's members, after conclusion of hearings, drove their cars to the property and inspected it and spent about four hours maneuvering in and out of the parking spaces and measuring them for accuracy of dimension, all without notice to the parties, although a representative of the permittee was present. However, the objectants' counsel had suggested an inspection, and the board's decision set forth the facts it thus found. If this inspection was irregular, the irregularity was not [***2] substantial.

 

2443 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Curtis v. Hennequin


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


27 Misc. 2d 1042; 212 N.Y.S.2d 796; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3514



January 24, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] In the light of all the facts and circumstances judgment is granted defendant dismissing plaintiff's complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff daughter of decedent, as the third-party beneficiary of an alleged oral agreement between her mother and father, sought to impress a trust upon property left by her father upon his demise, against defendant executrix of her father's estate, who was his second wife.


OVERVIEW: The daughter claimed that prior to her parents' divorce, her mother and father entered into an agreement whereby the mother waived all right of support for herself and the daughter in consideration for which the father agreed that upon his death he would leave one half of his estate to the daughter. However, when he died, his will bequeathed all his property to his second wife. The daughter filed a complaint to impress the alleged trust. The court dismissed the complaint and held that the Statute of Frauds, N.Y. Real Prop. Law § 259-a barred any recovery insofar as her father's real property was concerned. The court held that the daughter failed to prove her interest in the father's personal property when her mother could not testify about the agreement because it was through her that the daughter derived her rights. The court held that any such oral agreement needed to rest upon the clearest and most convincing evidence, lest the wise and salutary purpose of N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act § 347 be frustrated. The court also held that there was proof that the second wife had worked hard to help the decedent acquire the property at issue and therefore, deserved to retain the property.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the daughter's complaint.


HEADNOTES

Witnesses -- personal transactions with decedent -- plaintiff's father's oral promise to leave half his estate to plaintiff cannot be proved by testimony of promisee, plaintiff's mother (Civ. Prac. Act, § 347); case dismissed.

Plaintiff alleges that her mother, before instituting a divorce action against plaintiff's father, orally waived all right of support for said mother and child, and that plaintiff's father thereupon orally agreed to devise and bequeath half his estate to plaintiff; and that, instead, he left all his estate to his second wife; wherefore plaintiff, as the alleged third-party beneficiary of such oral agreement, seeks to impress a trust on his estate. The alleged oral agreement was made before the enactment of subdivision 7 of section 31 of the Personal Property Law, hence that Statute of Frauds cannot constitutionally nullify this agreement. But the mother's testimony is barred by section 347 of the Civil Practice Act. Without the mother's testimony, plaintiff's case consists of two letters and the equivocal testimony of plaintiff's husband.  [***2] This is not clear and convincing evidence. The action is dimissed.

 

2444 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Application of Gaiser


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


30 Misc. 2d 619; 211 N.Y.S.2d 337; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3551



January 17, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition is dismissed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner police lieutenant filed a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, seeking to review the determination of respondents, an official and the Suffolk County Civil Service Commission, by which the Commission denied the lieutenant's request that he be granted the rank of captain in the police department.


OVERVIEW: The Commission approved a resolution purporting to cover-in certain persons and listing incumbents whose names were affected. The lieutenant claimed that the omission of his name from the resolution was improper. Under the court's reading of N.Y. Const. art. V, § 6 and the decisions construing it, a method of permanently creating status and tenure in the competitive class of the classified civil service of the State or any less municipal agency was specifically interdicted. The lieutenant's permanent status in the police department was that of lieutenant. His promotions thereafter were on a provisional basis only. He acquired no right of tenure either from the continuance of that provisional status beyond the statutory limit or from the failure to schedule or provide promotional examinations. Thus, the lieutenant never had claim to a permanent status beyond that of lieutenant and gained nothing by a report or any resolution implementing it. The lieutenant's transfer to the county police department as a lieutenant was in proper conformity with the provisions of the Suffolk County Charter and N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 70, and consequently could not have been arbitrary or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the lieutenant's petition.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- reclassification -- petitioner, whose permanent rank was that of lieutenant in Islip Town Police Department, but who had been appointed provisionally as captain, was not entitled to be "covered-in" at provisional title in reclassification of titles and positions of civil service employees of Suffolk County.

1. On January 7, 1960, the State Civil Service Commission approved a reclassification of titles and positions of civil service employees of Suffolk County whereby, with the exception of employees of the Probation Department and the County Court, all incumbents who had served in their respective positions for at least a year prior to July 1, 1956, were continued in such positions under their newly assigned titles without further examination. On July 1, 1955, petitioner was serving in a provisional appointment as a police captain in the Islip Town Police Department and later he was provisionally appointed chief of police. However, his permanent status was that of lieutenant. He acquired no right of tenure either from the continuance of his provisional status beyond the statutory limit or from the failure to [***2] hold promotional examinations for the higher positions. Accordingly, he was not entitled to be "covered-in" at the rank of captain.

2. Petitioner's transfer to the Suffolk County Police Department as a lieutenant on January 1, 1960, when the personnel and functions of the Islip Town Police Department were transferred to the County Police Department, was in proper conformity with the provisions of the Suffolk County Charter (§ 1207) and the Civil Service Law ( § 70) and was not arbitrary or unreasonable.

3. Therefore, a petition to review the determination of the Suffolk County Civil Service Commission denying petitioner's request that he be granted the rank of Captain in the County Police Department is dismissed.

 

2445 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Gross v. Cross


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


28 Misc. 2d 375; 211 N.Y.S.2d 279; 1961 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3581; 47 L.R.R.M. 2423



January 10, 1961 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion is granted only to the extent of dismissing the third cause of action, but without prejudice to any relief the plaintiff may pursue in any other forum, or in this forum if the facts and circumstances in the future warrant such relief.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff member filed an action to compel defendants, a union's president and treasurer, to process and pay the death benefits due under a sick and death benefit fund contract between the parties and to impress a trust on the union's assets equal to the amount credited to the fund. The president and treasurer filed a motion to set aside the alleged service of summons or, in the alternative, to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The union's main office was in Washington, D.C. Summonses were served personally upon the president and treasurer in the State. They sought to set aside the service of summons upon the ground that the court did not have personal jurisdiction over them. The also sought to dismiss the complaint on the ground that the court, in its discretion, could decline to exercise subject matter jurisdiction over the action. The court held that there was no requirement that an unincorporated association had to be doing business in the State in order to be sued there as long as the other requirements under N.Y. Gen. Ass'ns Law § 13 were met. The court did not decline jurisdiction of the first and second causes of action, which sought the process and payment of the death benefits. A resident was not denied the right to invoke the State's judicial tribunals to recover only damages in a transitory action predicated upon a breach of a contract. Under the allegations stated in the action seeking to impress a trust, the regulation and management of the internal affairs of the union could be involved. Therefore, the court could be unable to enforce its decree and could not retain jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court granted the president and treasurer's motion only to the extent of dismissing the action seeking to impress a trust on the union's assets. The court dismissed that action without prejudice to any relief the member could pursue in any other forum or in the same forum if the facts and circumstances in the future warranted such relief.


HEADNOTES

Associations -- jurisdiction -- personal service of summons on president and treasurer of union sufficient, whether or not union is doing business in this State (General Associations Law, § 13) -- court will not decline jurisdiction of two causes of action to compel payment of benefits claimed under contract between parties -- cause of action to impress trust, appoint trustee, and segregate certain assets dismissed -- if judgment were for plaintiff court might be unable to enforce decree.

1. Personal service in New York State of the summons herein upon the president and treasurer of defendant union, an unincorporated association, whether or not said association is doing business in this State, is sufficient (General Associations Law, § 13).

2. The court assumes jurisdiction of the first two causes of action, to compel defendants to pay certain benefits claimed under a Sick and Death Benefit Fund contract between [***2] the parties.

3. However, the third cause of action, to impress a trust on assets of the association equal to the amount credited to said Fund, segregation of such assets, and appointment of a "trustee", is dismissed, without prejudice to plaintiff's pursuing relief in any other forum. Under the facts presented, the regulation and management of the internal affairs of the unincorporated defendant which has its main office in Washington, D. C., may be involved, and were this court to find for plaintiff, it might not be able to enforce its decree or might create a condition over which it would not have full control.

 

2446 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Huber v. Huber


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


26 Misc. 2d 539; 209 N.Y.S.2d 637; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2006



December 19, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ex-wife filed a partition action seeking to divide the marital property that was located in New York after the wife obtained an ex parte divorce in Florida. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment. The wife held the marital property with defendant ex-husband as tenants by entirety.


OVERVIEW: After obtaining an ex parte divorce in Florida, the ex-wife initiated a partition action to divide the marital property located in New York. The ex-wife and the ex-husband filed motions for summary judgment. The court denied the ex-wife's motion and granted the ex-husband's motion for summary judgment. The court held that the full faith and credit clause, U. S. Const., art. IV, § 1, as implemented by 28 U.S.C.S. § 1738 required only that a state give to the judgment of another state such force and effect as it had in the state in which it was rendered. The court found that the ex-husband's affidavit stated that he did not appear in the Florida action, therefore, the Florida court had no jurisdiction over the ex-husband's person or over the property located in New York. The court held that it was the due process clause as applied to husband's property rights that governed rather than the full faith and credit clause. The court held that under the "divisible divorce" doctrine, giving effect to the decree as to the marital status but denying its effect as to property, was not violative of the full faith and credit clause.


OUTCOME: The court denied the ex-wife's motion for summary judgment and granted the ex-husband's motion for summary judgment. The court signed a short-form order dismissing the complaint on the merits.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Tenants by the entirety -- foreign divorce -- Florida divorce without defendant's appearance does not convert New York tenancy by entirety into tenancy in common; partition action dismissed (Civ. Prac. Act, § 1012).

An out-of-State divorce -- Florida, in this case -- rendered after service on the defendant, is presumptively valid, even without any appearance by the defendant; and the decree is entitled to full faith and credit in New York State (U. S. Const., art. IV; U. S. Code, tit. 28, § 1738); but, under the due process clause of the Federal Constitution, such foreign decree cannot be given the added effect of extinguishing the defendant's vested property right to succeed, on the plaintiff's death, to the New York real property to which they had taken title as tenants by the entirety. A tenancy by the entirety in New York realty, in which each owns the whole and each owns a right of survivorship, is not converted by such foreign decree into a tenancy in common in which each owns merely a half. Accordingly, a partition action by the wife against the husband is dismissed (Civ. Prac. Act, § 1012).

 

2447 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Pruzan v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


25 Misc. 2d 945; 209 N.Y.S.2d 966; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2042; 47 L.R.R.M. 2281; 41 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P50,131



December 12, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant board of education filed a motion to dismiss for insufficiency and for judgment a complaint filed by plaintiff teachers seeking an order declaring the Condon-Wadlin Act, N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 108, unconstitutional insofar as it applied to their proposed course of conduct. The teachers also filed a motion for judgment.


OVERVIEW: The teachers desired to absent themselves from their position so that they could, en masse, consult with and petition members of the legislature and executive departments as to various proposals aimed at improving their working conditions. They desired a declaratory judgment because if their absence were prohibited by the Condon-Wadlin Act, they would be subject, under the act, to immediate forfeiture of their positions. Noting that declaratory judgments were intended as a guide to future action, the court held that a proper case for declaratory judgment was presented. However, the Act was not unconstitutional. In so ruling, the court stated the definition of "strike" contained in subdivision 1 of the Act was as clear and definite as any definition could reasonably be. Further, the Act did not deprive the teachers of a full and fair hearing. Although subdivision 4 provided for automatic termination, subdivision 6 entitled a teacher to request a hearing. Although not expressly stated in the Act, a determination that the Act had not been violated would entitle a teacher to compensation retroactively to the date it ceased.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment for the board of education and dismissed the teacher's action on the merits.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Civil service -- anti-strike law -- Civil Service Law ( § 108) is constitutional -- judgment rendered declaring that schoolteachers cannot absent themselves en masse to petition Legislature.

1. The so-called Condon-Wadlin Act (Civil Service Law, § 108, entitled "Strikes by public employees prohibited; penalties") is valid and constitutional as applied to schoolteachers. However, its constitutionality would be doubtful without the provision in subdivision 1 thereof guaranteeing "the right of any public employee to the expression or communication of a view, grievance, complaint or opinion on any matter related to the conditions or compensation of public employment or their betterment, so long as the same is not designed to and does not interfere with the full, faithful and proper performance of the duties of employment." For constitutional reasons, this should be construed to permit the absence for a limited time of a limited number of employees -- not the employees en masse -- to represent and set forth the views of the greater number. The Legislature should clarify the act so as to permit reasonable, approved leaves of absence to representatives to petition the Legislature.

 [***2] 2. This action for a declaratory judgment, brought by 31 schoolteachers comprising the executive board of a teachers' association, suing individually and on behalf of all members of the association and for all others similarly situated, and by said association itself, is dismissed (Rules Civ. Prac., rules 112, 113), except that judgment will be rendered declaring that it would be a violation of the Civil Service Law ( § 108) for the employees to absent themselves en masse for an unlimited period of time in order to consult with and petition the members of the local and State Legislatures and executive departments of government as to 14 proposals set forth in this complaint as to working conditions and compensation.

 

2448 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Gulest Associates, Inc. v. Newburgh


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Orange County


25 Misc. 2d 1004; 209 N.Y.S.2d 729; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2043



December 12, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff real estate developer filed a motion to strike the answer of defendant town and for summary judgment in its action contending that N.Y. Town Law § 227 and regulations thereunder were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The developer acquired land for subdivision. However, as no suitable park or parks of adequate size could be located on the land, the town, under the authority of § 227 and regulations promulgated thereunder, required, as a condition to approval of the subdivision, that the developer make payment to the town, which payments the town could use for a neighborhood park, playground, or other recreational purposes. Payment in lieu of a reservation of land was not mandatory under § 227; rather, the statute vested in the town board absolute discretion to apply or not apply the condition of payment. The statute and the regulations promulgated thereunder were unconstitutional. In so ruling, the court stated that the statute compelled the developer to pay more than its proportionate share of the moneys to be spent on parks, playgrounds, and recreational facilities for the town as a whole. Further, because the statute failed to set out standards or tests to guide the holders of the delegated power, the statute was void. The court held that the statute and the regulations thereunder permitted a taking of property without due process of law and amounted to a denial of equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court granted the developer's motion for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- planning of realty subdivisions -- subdivider cannot be required by planning board to pay money in lieu of dedicating area for park (Town Law, § 277, subd. 1, as amd. by L. 1959, ch. 846); such statute and regulation unconstitutional.

The Town Law ( § 277, subd. 1) requires that the approval of a town's planning board be obtained for the filing of a realty subdivision plat or map, and empowers such planning board to require that the plat show a suitably located park or playground, and further provides that, if the planning board determines that a suitable park cannot be properly located in such subdivision, then (as amd. by L. 1959, ch. 846) "the board may require as a condition to approval of any such plat a payment to the town of an amount to be determined by the town board, which amount shall be available for use by the town for neighborhood park, playground or recreation purposes including the acquisition of property." The quoted portion, and regulations adopted thereunder by defendant town which required plaintiff subdivider to pay the town $ 50 for each lot on the plat or a total of $ 2,300, are declared unconstitutional and void, and the town [***2] is enjoined from requiring any payments in lieu of a reservation or dedication of land (N. Y. Const., art. I, §§ 6, 7; U. S. Const., 5th Amdt.).

 

2449 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sterling Optical Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


26 Misc. 2d 412; 209 N.Y.S.2d 953; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2058



December 8, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State of New York sought summary judgment and defendant optical company sought judgment on the pleadings and to strike out a reply; or, in the alternative, for summary judgment on the action and counterclaims, in the State's action commenced to annul the company's corporate charter on the grounds that it engaged in the unlawful practice of optometry and ophthalmic dispensing under N.Y. Educ. Law § 7109.


OVERVIEW: The company employed optometrists to examine customers to determine whether they needed eyeglasses, what type of lenses they needed, and to prescribe lenses. Opthalmic dispensers in the company's employ made and fit eyeglasses in another part of the store. The court held that (1) N.Y. Educ. Law § was aimed at regulating the sale of bargain counter reading glasses, but did not sanction the company's employment of optometrists to write prescriptions; (2) every citizen had the right to an occupation, subject however to government supervision in the interest of the public welfare; (3) seven bills that prohibited a corporation from practicing optometry directly or through a licensed optometrist failed to pass the legislature in the previous three sessions; (4) the law did not confine an optometrist employed by a corporation to the simple determination as to whether a customer should select readymade glasses because such a limitation had no relation to the protection of the health, welfare, or safety of the public; and (5) the State's allegation that the company represented to the public that it provided complete optical care raised issues of fact precluding complete summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court denied the State's motion for summary judgment, limited to the propriety of the company's employment of optometrists and opticians as a necessary incident to the sale of eyeglasses at retail. The court granted partial summary judgment to the company only to the extent of declaring that the employment of optometrists and opticians as a necessary incident to the sale of eyeglasses was not unlawful.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Corporations -- optometry -- corporation may employ licensed optometrists and opticians in connection with its sale of eyeglasses (Education Law, §§ 7109, 7120) -- but issues of fact exist as to defendant corporation.

1. Though a corporation is not a person who can be licensed to practice optometry (optometrist) or ophthalmic dispensing (optician), a corporation may employ licensed optometrists for the limited purpose of examining the eyes of its customers in connection with the sale of eyeglasses at retail, and for this purpose the corporation may utilize their skill to determine the need for eyeglasses and the prescription to meet such need; and similarly, as a necessary incident to the sale of eyeglasses, the corporation may employ licensed ophthalmic dispensers (opticians) who read the optometrist's prescription and select the lens to conform with such prescription and who adapt the eyeglasses to the customer's face. (Education Law, §§ 7109, 7120.)

2. Issues of fact exist, however, as to whether defendant corporation represents to the public that it provides complete optical care and as to whether its optometrists and opticians thus perform other functions which would [***2] constitute the unlawful practice of optometry and ophthalmic dispensing by a corporation.

 

2450 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Nangaparbet


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Erie County


29 Misc. 2d 984; 210 N.Y.S.2d 446; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2225



November 9, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] It is further ordered that the indictment be and it is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was accused of the unlawful possession of a hypodermic syringe and hypodermic needle, moved to dismiss the indictment at the conclusion of the People's case, arguing that under N.Y. Penal Law § 1747-d(3), the conclusive presumption of illegality of use deprived him of the right to challenge the premise, denied him a fair opportunity to have been heard, and was arbitrary, unreasonable, and violative of the Due Process Clause.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was arrested for possession of a hypodermic syringe and needle, asserted that § 1747-d(3) subjected him to penal consequences by the mere fact of possession without regard to criminal intent. The court dismissed the indictment, holding that the portion of § 1747-d(3) which imposed criminal liability through the creation of a conclusive and irrebutable presumption of guilt based on mere possession of an instrument used essentially for useful and necessary purposes was an unreasonable exercise of police power and was unconstitutional as violative of the Due Process Clause. To have presumed illegality of purpose by virtue of possession alone of an inherently innocuous instrument was to have sanctioned a proposition that was predicated upon a fact whose verity ran counter to universal experience. The object was not inherently dangerous or sinister wherein there was a sufficient relationship between the fact proved and the crime presumed. The statute, which sought, without more, to conclusively equate possession of an object not inherently dangerous, noxious, or harmful with illegality of purpose was unreasonable and therefore constitutionally infirm.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the indictment against defendant.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- narcotics -- Penal Law ( § 1747-d, subd. 3), making possession of hypodermic syringe or needle criminal, unconstitutional.

The portion of the Penal Law ( § 1747-d, subd. 3, as amd. by L. 1956, ch. 692) which makes it criminal for the average person, regardless of his purpose and lack of criminal intent, to possess a hypodermic syringe or a hypodermic needle, is an unreasonable exercise of the police power and hence is unconstitutional (U. S. Const., 14th Amdt.). At the conclusion of the People's case, such an indictment is dismissed.
