Gregory v. Ball


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


25 Misc. 2d 861; 207 N.Y.S.2d 52; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2255



November 2, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] There being no bona fide question of fact raised by these pleadings, plaintiffs' motion is denied and judgment is granted for the defendants dismissing the complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff booksellers moved for summary judgment in a suit against defendant officials for a declaration that N.Y. Penal Law § 1141(1), (2) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The law made distribution of obscenity a misdemeanor. The booksellers claimed that they had been or were about to be arrested or prosecuted under § 1141 by law enforcement agencies of Buffalo and Erie County for selling alleged obscene literature. The booksellers sued the officials, claiming that the law was unconstitutional. Denying the booksellers' and dismissing the suit, the court said that § 1141 was constitutional. There was no bona fide question of fact raised by the pleadings. Obscenity possessed was not criminal, but obscenity possessed with intent to disseminate was. Constitutional liberty ended where obscenity began. The intentional dissemination of obscenity was prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court denied the booksellers' motion and granted judgment for the officials dismissing the suit.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- obscenity -- Penal Law ( § 1141, subds. 1, 2) is constitutional.

Subdivisions 1 and 2 of section 1141 of the Penal Law ("Obscene prints and articles") are constitutional. This action by booksellers against law-enforcement officials of the State, county and city, for a declaratory judgment, is summarily dismissed.

 

2452 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Realty Equities Corp. v. Gerosa


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


30 Misc. 2d 481; 209 N.Y.S.2d 446; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2268



October 28, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is, accordingly, denied in all respects and the cross and other motions are also denied, as academic.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought an order decreeing a lien for the fair value of legal services rendered by their attorney in invalidating defendant city's real property transfer tax.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers brought an action against the city which sought to invalidate a real property transfer tax. After successfully invalidating the tax, the taxpayers' filed a motion to assess an attorney's lien for fees against a fund allegedly created for the refunding of the invalidated tax. The court noted that ordinarily, an attorney could not recover legal fees from persons other than his client, merely because such persons were benefited by his services. However, a ground for charging a legal fee to persons who did not retain the attorney claiming the fee existed where the efforts of the attorney resulted in the creation or the distribution of a fund for the benefit of the persons sought to be charged as well as for the benefit of the client who retained the attorney. Nevertheless, the judgment here had not created any fund in which others than the taxpayers had any interest, nor was such a fund created by operation of the doctrine of stare decisis. While the judgment had established the rights of other taxpayers who paid under protest to recover the amounts of their payments as general creditors of the defendants, no fund whatsoever had resulted.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion of the taxpayers where no fund resulted for the payment of the attorney's fees.


HEADNOTES

Actions -- representative action -- expenses and legal fees -- judgment in action brought by individuals for return of tax payments not subject to amendment to transform it to determination of rights of all persons similarly situated -- motion for reimbursement of expenses and legal fees denied since action was not representative nor did it create fund in which others could share -- theory that recovery of expenses is justified because others will benefit under stare decisis not applicable in this case.

1. After successful prosecution of an action against the City of New York for the return to plaintiffs of certain Real Property Transfer Tax payments made by them, plaintiffs and their attorney applied for an order decreeing that the judgment be modified to provide that it constituted a determination of the rights of all persons who made tax payments under similar circumstances and that plaintiffs and their attorney were entitled to reimbursement for expenses and legal fees from the "fund" thus created by them for the benefit of persons similarly situated. Since [***2] the first action was not brought as a class or representative suit, nor did it directly or indirectly create a fund in which others could share, the motion must be denied and the injunction against defendants' payment of refunds and against prosecution of suits by other taxpayers must be dismissed.

2. Mere mention in the complaint that others were affected by the tax did not transform the action into a class or representative suit, where neither the title of the action nor any of the pleadings contained a statement indicating that plaintiffs purported to sue on behalf of anyone but themselves.

3. Plaintiffs are not entitled to an amendment of the judgment so as to provide that it is a determination of the rights of all persons similarly situated, since such an amendment would be a change of substance.

4. Plaintiffs are not entitled to recover expenses on the doctrine that others will benefit under stare decisis, since allowances under that theory "are appropriate only in exceptional cases and for dominating reasons of justice" ( Spague v. Ticonic Bank, 307 U.S. 161).

 

2453 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Chelcy v. Buffalo Municipal Housing Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


24 Misc. 2d 598; 206 N.Y.S.2d 158; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2300



October 18, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Plaintiff's motion for injunction denied; defendant's motion for summary judgment granted, dismissing the complaint. No motion costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff public housing tenant filed a motion for an injunction against defendant public housing authority, as well as its employees and agents, from taking any action in furtherance of a housing conversion plan pending final determination of the public housing tenant's declaratory judgment action. The public housing authority filed a cross-motion for an order denying the request for temporary injunction and for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The public housing tenant filed an action for a declaratory judgment against the public housing authority challenging the constitutionality of its plan to convert a low-income housing project into a private co-operative apartment operation, claiming that the plan violated N.Y. Const. art. XVIII and the N.Y. Pub. Hous. Law §§ 3, 17, 132, 156, 302, 318. He filed a motion for a temporary injunction seeking to restrain the public housing authority from taking any action in furtherance of its plan, and the public housing authority filed a cross-motion for summary judgment. The court granted the public housing authority's motion, dismissing the complaint. The court refused to pass judgment upon the legislative policy or administrative discretion, holding that the public housing tenant had shown no illegality or fraud. The court further held that the public housing tenant had not suffered and would not suffer any irreparable injury, the harm to his children from having to change schools and injury to his furniture in transit being incident to any moving of a home from one school district to another and thus incidents of living in a populous community.


OUTCOME: The court denied the public housing tenant's motion for a preliminary injunction and granted the public housing authority's motion for summary judgment, dismissing the complaint.


HEADNOTES

Public housing -- limited profit housing companies -- proposed leasing of low income public housing project to limited dividend housing company for operation as co-operative with occupancy by middle income tenants did not violate New York Constitution (art. XVIII, § 6) or Mitchell-Lama Limited-Profit Housing Companies Law (Public Housing Law, art. 12); court will not interfere with Housing Authority's determination of what constitutes "low income" within statutory definition; tenant in project was not irreparably injured by relocation to another project at Authority's expense and had no cause of action to restrain and annul proposed leasing.

1. The proposal that a State-aided public housing project constructed in Buffalo for, and restricted to occupancy by, "Persons of low income" (N. Y. Const., art. XVIII, § 6; Public Housing Law, § 17), be converted to occupancy by middle income tenants at substantially higher rentals by the defendant Housing Authority's leasing the project to a limited dividend housing company for operation as a [***2] co-operative was not unconstitutional or contrary to the Mitchell-Lama Limited-Profit Housing Companies Law (Public Housing Law, art. 12, added by L. 1955, ch. 407, as amd.), and was a scheme not to evade the law but rather to comply therewith. The State Constitution and Public Housing Law refer to "low income" as distinguished from the Federal statute's reference to "lowest income" (U. S. Code, tit. 42, § 1402), and inasmuch as standards of income and rent vary in different communities and times, the general definitions of the Legislature (Public Housing Law, § 3, subds. 18, 23), leaving their application to the local authority, are constitutional. Accordingly, the application of the Mitchell-Lama Law to a plan for public housing that appears to benefit a "middle income group" was not unconstitutional if their income was insufficient to pay rentals high enough to attract private industry to build adequate, safe and sanitary housing for them. The court, which takes judicial notice of the great increase in income and building costs since World War II, will not, in the absence of fraud or illegality, judge legislative policy or administrative discretion or take from the local authority [***3] the power to determine what constitutes "low income" or "low rent" at a given time and place.

2. A tenant in the low income housing project in question has not suffered, and will not suffer, irreparable injury by the proposed conversion. As a tenant on a month-to-month term, he had no vested rights affected by the proposed lease of the project to the limited dividend housing company. Moreover, the defendant Municipal Housing Authority will comply with the tenants' preferences for relocation at other public housing projects and will provide for such moving at its expense. Such inconveniences to the tenant as changing his children's schools or injury to his furniture in transit are incident to any such moving and to living in a populous community. Accordingly, the tenant was not entitled to an order enjoining acts in furtherance of the conversion plan, and his complaint stated no cause of action for a declaratory judgment against the Authority, which was entitled to summary judgment.

 

2454 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Davlee Constr. Corp. v. Brooks


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


26 Misc. 2d 240; 213 N.Y.S.2d 593; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2319



October 13, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner construction company sued respondent Zoning Board of Appeals for a declaratory judgment that an ordinance invalid insofar as it classified real property. The company also challenged the Board's procedure.


OVERVIEW: The property and the land adjacent to it had been in a Residence E zone (5,000 feet), changed to a Residence C zone (10,000 feet), and then placed in a Residence B zone (one acre) by an amendment of the building zone ordinance. The area was about 12,000 square feet. After a building inspector refused to issue a building permit, the company appealed. Invalidating the ordinance as to the property, the court said that the effect of the declaration of invalidity of the amendment was to restore the zoning applicable prior to that amendment to Residence C (10,000 sq. ft.) zoning. The enactment of a new amendment substantially the same as the nullified amendment was not effective to avoid the consequences of the judgment. Overruling the company's challenge to the procedure, the court said that the Board had jurisdiction to make the determination complained of under N.Y. Town Law, § 267(2). The Board neither granted nor denied the appeal to it from the refusal to issue the permit. On a stipulation between counsel for the parties, an order directed the Board to review the inspector's order and decision.


OUTCOME: The court said that the company was entitled to the declaration that the ordinance was invalid insofar as it classified the real property. The court overruled the company's challenge to the Board's procedure.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- confiscatory minimum area amendment, invalidated, re-enacted, and re-invalidated, leaves former area requirement in force; Zoning Board of Appeals must direct Building Inspector to issue permit (Town Law, § 267, subd. 2).

1. A zoning ordinance amendment which was invalidated as confiscatory cannot be enacted a short time later with substantially the same invalid provisions.

2. The prior judgment was based on confiscation and unconstitutionality, and only incidentally on the amendment's failure to prescribe the boundaries of the zone as required by the Town Law; and the material circumstances have not significantly changed since then; so the re-enactment with properly described boundaries is still invalid.

3. The zoning ordinance as it read prior to said invalid amendments is thus still in force.

4. Accordingly, the Zoning Board of Appeals must direct the Building Inspector to issue a permit to petitioner (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78; Town Law, § 267, subd. 2) to construct a dwelling on petitioner's plot, which plot contains not less than 10,000 square feet (the valid minimum requirement), the amended requirement of one acre (43,560 square [***2] feet) being invalid.

People v. Wagonseller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, Plattsburgh, Clinton County


25 Misc. 2d 217; 205 N.Y.S.2d 933; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2367



October 6, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the information is dismissed, the bail posted ordered remitted, and the operator's license and registration, suspended pending the instant hearing, returned.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with a violation of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1192(1), in unlawfully and knowingly operating a motor vehicle while his ability to operate such motor vehicle was impaired by the consumption of alcohol. Defendant moved that the information be dismissed.


OVERVIEW: The arrest was made right after N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1192(1) went into effect. Defendant refused to take a blood test. Defendant argued that N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1192 required that he could not be convicted after pleading not guilty unless it was shown by means of a chemical test that there was at least a minimum percentage by weight of alcohol in his blood. Defendant argued that because no chemical test was available to establish the minimum percentage of alcohol required, a dismissal had to follow. The court held that it had to dismiss the information in view of the specific language of the statute. The court stated that violators of this new section did not have a means of escaping a penalty by refusing to take a blood test. Under N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1194, the Commissioner of Motor Vehicles was empowered to revoke an operator's license after a hearing, and temporarily suspend it without notice pending a determination. Defendant also moved that the information be dismissed arguing that the section was unconstitutional. Because defendant's motion to dismiss was granted on other grounds, it was unnecessary for the court to pass upon the section's constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the information be dismissed, that the bail posted be remitted, and that the operator's license and registration, which were suspended pending the hearing, be returned.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- operating vehicle under influence of alcohol -- defendant improperly convicted of operating motor vehicle while ability was impaired by alcohol (Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 1192, subd. 1) where, since defendant refused to take blood test, alcoholic content of blood was not shown "by means of a chemical test".

Defendant was improperly convicted of a violation of subdivision 1 of section 1192 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law for allegedly unlawfully and knowingly operating a motor vehicle while his ability to operate the vehicle was impaired by the consumption of alcohol. The statute provides that no conviction shall be had after an entry of a plea of not guilty unless it is shown "by means of a chemical test" that there was ten-hundredths of one per centum or more by weight of alcohol in defendant's blood. Defendant refused to take a blood test, and accordingly no blood test was ever made.

 

2456 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dybak


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Ulster County


24 Misc. 2d 1023; 205 N.Y.S.2d 454; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2383



October 3, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Therefore, for the reasons stated, the judgment of conviction appealed from is reversed and the information dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction by a Justice of the Peace of the Town of Esopus, New York, for defendant's violation of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1143. Defendant argued that § 1143 was unconstitutional because it was vague and indefinite.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating § 1143. On appeal, he attacked the constitutionality of § 1143. The court held that § 1143 was unconstitutional, so it reversed the judgment of conviction and dismissed the information. Section 1143 was too vague and indefinite to afford a comprehensible guide as to what a driver had to do and what had to be avoided, so that an ordinary member of society could not comply with its requirements. Section 1143(a) required vehicles about to enter or cross a highway from a private road or driveway to yield the right of way to all vehicles approaching on the highway. The use of the word "all" was confusing, especially because of the use of the word "any" in § 1143(b), and § 1143 did not establish a comprehensible standard of the rule to be obeyed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction and dismissed the information.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- yielding right of way -- section 1143 of Vehicle and Traffic Law, which provides that driver about to enter or cross highway from private road or driveway shall yield right of way, unconstitutional as vague and indefinite.

 Section 1143 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, which provides: "The driver of a vehicle about to enter or cross a highway from a private road or driveway shall yield the right of way to all vehicles approaching on said highway", is unconstitutional. The statute is vague and indefinite.

People v. Kassover


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Special Sessions of the City of New York, Appellate Part, First Department


24 Misc. 2d 1080; 205 N.Y.S.2d 428; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2384



October 3, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment rendered by the magistrate's court (New York), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint and found that the New York City, N.Y., Traffic Regulation § 51(a) was vague, indefinite, imprecise, and unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant made a U-turn and was charged with violation of § 51(a), which prohibited turning the vehicle "so as to proceed" in the opposite direction upon any street in a "business district." The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss, and found that the regulation was vague and unconstitutional. The trial court found that "business district" was not defined, and "so as to proceed" denoted purpose. It was possible, the trial court found, that defendant turned to park or for some purpose other than to proceed. The court dismissed the appeal and found that anybody would have been aware that the area where the turn was made was a business district. The court also held that it did not matter what the purpose of the turn was. The court dismissed the appeal because the motion to dismiss filed in the trial court was on the merits, and contended that the state failed to prove its case. The state did not have a right of appeal from that judgment. The court found that subjecting defendant to a new trial would have placed him in double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the state's appeal of the dismissal of the charges against defendant for making a U-turn because the state had no right of appeal.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- appeal -- all U-turns in New York City business districts are validly prohibited (N. Y. City Traffic Reg., § 51, subd. [a]) -- but People cannot appeal from judgment of acquittal made on erroneous legal ground (Code Crim. Pro., §§ 9, 326, 518, subd. 3); appeal dismissed.

1. Subdivision (a) of section 51 of the New York City Traffic Regulations, which provides that "the driver of any vehicle shall not turn such vehicle so as to proceed in the opposite direction upon any street in a business district", is valid and constitutional in an area which is visibly a business district (Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 105; cf. §§ 1640, 1642), even in the absence of any sign prohibiting U-turns, and even if the driver's object were merely to park and not to proceed in the opposite direction.

2. In this case, after a full trial, the Magistrates' Court of the City of New York granted a motion which defendant had made for a dismissal on the ground that guilt had not been proved beyond a reasonable doubt, and acquitted the defendant, with an opinion which erroneously held that subdivision (a) of section 51 of the New York City Traffic Regulations is so vague [***2] as to be unconstitutional. Since this ruling was made at the end of the entire case, with an acquittal, this appellate court -- the Appellate Part of the Court of Special Sessions of the City of New York -- cannot grant a new trial (Code Crim. Pro., § 9) and cannot entertain this appeal by the People from the judgment of acquittal (Code Crim. Pro., §§ 326, 518, subd. 3). Therefore, in spite of the erroneous ruling of law below, this appeal by the People is dismissed.

3. For the above reason (headnote par. 2), a trial court in a criminal case should give the People the benefit of any reasonable doubt on the law.

 

2458 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Lafayette Hotel Co. v. County of Erie


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


26 Misc. 2d 755; 205 N.Y.S.2d 626; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2395



September 30, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hotel owner sought a preliminary injunction pending the determination of the action enjoining defendant county from taking immediate possession of certain premises owned in fee by the hotel owner. The county board of supervisors authorized the taking under 1937 N.Y. Laws 758 in order to build a free public library.


OVERVIEW: The county wanted to demolish the hotel owner's parking garage to build a free public library. The loss of those parking facilities would destroy a large segment of its hotel business and its public parking business, No compensation had yet been to the hotel owner for the proposed taking. The hotel owner contended that 1937 N.Y. Laws 758 was unconstitutional because at any time prior to the granting of the final decree and the vesting of title to the lands in the county, the county board of supervisors could, by unilateral resolution, order the discontinuance or abandonment of the proceeding, leaving the hotel without power to collect any "damages" as a result of the temporary taking; in other words, the hotel owner contended that the expression used in 1937 N.Y. Laws 758 § 9, namely, "reasonable and necessary expenses and disbursements incurred by each person who has appeared in the proceeding," did not include or cover the "damages" sustained by such person. The court held that as used in 1937 N.Y. Laws 758, "compensation" was synonymous to "damages." When read together, the sections of the act adequately and justly protected injured owners under each possible contingency.


OUTCOME: The court denied the hotel owner's motion for a preliminary injunction.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Eminent domain -- constitutionality of condemnation statute -- statute under which real property preliminarily condemned for library in City of Buffalo adequately protects property owner whether property ultimately returned to owner or not and is not unconstitutional.

Plaintiff's property was condemned by defendant county by a resolution which authorized the taking in order to build a free public library. Plaintiff's contention that the act, Erie County's Special Condemnation Act (L. 1937, ch. 758, as amd.) is unconstitutional, because at any time prior to the granting of the final decree the County Board of Supervisors may unilaterally order discontinuance of the proceeding leaving the plaintiff without power to collect any damages as a result of the temporary taking, is not well taken since the act provides for payment of "compensation or damages" (Erie County's Special Condemnation Act [L. 1937, ch. 758, as amd.], §§ 2, 3, 6, 13), "expenses and disbursements", "costs and expenses" (§ 9), and "interest" (§ 13) and when read together the sections of the act adequately protect injured owners under each possible contingency.

 

2459 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bunis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Erie County


24 Misc. 2d 561; 205 N.Y.S.2d 517; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2432



September 26, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the decision of the City Court of Buffalo is reversed, and the information reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the order of the City Court of Buffalo (New York), which dismissed an information against defendant that charged him with a violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 436-d on the grounds that the statute was unconstitutional as an invalid exercise of the State's police power and on the principle of stare decisis.


OVERVIEW: The publishers credited dealers who returned the covers of recalled magazines and agreed to destroy the magazines. Defendant was arrested and an information filed for the illegal selling of coverless magazines in violation of § 436-d. Defendant moved to dismiss the information on the basis that § 436-d was unconstitutional and was an invalid exercise of police powers because it protected a special trade interest in violation of the case law. The trial court granted the motion and dismissed the information. The State appealed. The court reversed. The case law decisions were distinguishable because in those cases the statute had completely prohibited or destroyed an otherwise lawful business, whereas N.Y. Penal Law § 436-d was a reasonable regulation that prevented fraud on the public. Section 436-d contained no restriction on the publishing, distribution, or sale of any magazine, but reasonably restricted the sale of published and distributed magazines without covers in order to combat an evil found to exist in the fraudulent sale of magazines owned by publishers following a recall. The evil combated was the defrauding of the public, which was a permissible use of the police power.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which had dismissed the information against defendant. The court reinstated the information.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- constitutional law -- section 436-d of Penal Law, prohibiting sale of periodicals from which cover has been removed, is constitutional.

Section 436-d of the Penal Law, providing that "Any person who knowingly sells, offers or exposes for sale, (except in bulk as waste paper) any newspaper, magazine, periodical or other publication, except a rare book, manuscript or educational text, from which the cover or title page has been removed, or from which the title, trade name, trade mark or other identification mark has been removed or obliterated, is guilty of a misdemeanor", is a reasonable regulation aimed at an existing evil and is, therefore, valid and constitutional.

 

2460 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Application of Excavating Machine Owners Asso., Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


25 Misc. 2d 419; 205 N.Y.S.2d 265; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2527



August 30, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicants, excavation business owners, appealed the refusal of respondent, the Attorney-General for the State of New York, to issue a certificate of incorporation to the applicants and refusal to inform them of the reasons their application was rejected.


OVERVIEW: The applicants formed an association and applied for incorporation. The Attorney-General examined one of the incorporators under oath and gave notice that he would oppose approval of the certificate, but refused to provide a copy of the examination transcript or provide the basis of his objection. The applicants tendered a revised certificate on judicial review. The Attorney-General opposed the application on the basis it violated the anti-trust provisions of N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 340 and agreed to provide the court, but not the applicants, a copy of his records on basis that N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 343 prevented disclosure to the applicants. Because the only persons involved in the hearing were the applicants, the policy of § 343 was not detrimentally affected by the disclosure to the applicants. Without the facts contained in the Attorney-General's records, the court was unable to exercise its semi-administrative discretion to arrive at its own conclusion. The offer to provide the court but not the applicants a copy of the record was unfair. The applicants were entitled to know the reasons for the denial and have an opportunity to test and convert those reasons.


OUTCOME: The court held the application in abeyance to permit the Attorney-General to serve a further affidavit and gave the applicants three days to reply to such affidavit. If the Attorney-General filed no further affidavit, then the certificate was to issue.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Corporations -- membership corporations -- trade association's certificate of incorporation will be approved, unless Attorney-General releases facts of his investigation and examination which he asserts show price-fixing (Membership Corporations Law, § 10, subd. 8; General Business Law, §§ 340, 343).

On this application to a Justice of the Supreme Court by a trade or business association for approval of its certificate of incorporation (Membership Corporations Law, § 10, subd. 8, as amd. by L. 1958, ch. 598 and L. 1960, ch. 985), which application is opposed by the Attorney-General, who offers to let the court alone see a transcript of an examination of the incorporators which the Attorney-General conducted under the General Business Law ( § 343) and which examination, he says, shows that the real purpose of the association is unlawfully to fix prices (General Business Law, § 340), the court will approve the certificate of incorporation, unless the Attorney-General is willing to release, not only to the court but to the applicants (General Business Law, § 343), the facts which show that the corporation's real purpose is unlawful, so that then the applicants may serve a [***2] reply, for the court's consideration.

 

2461 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Hofstra College v. Wilmerding


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


24 Misc. 2d 248; 204 N.Y.S.2d 476; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2592



August 10, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner nonprofit college sought reversal of an order of respondent Board of Zoning Appeals pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, which denied the college's application for a special exception, as provided by Village of Old Westbury, N.Y., Zoning Ordinance § 401(11), to alter a residence into student housing. Intervenors, neighborhood association and adjacent property owners, excepted to portions of the college's petition.


OVERVIEW: The college sought a license for the construction of student housing for an experimental college in a zoning district that normally allowed single family residences on two-acre parcels. The board denied the permit on the grounds that the parcel subject to the college itself could have accommodated up to 5,000 students and that population density was against the public health and welfare. On the college's petition for judicial review, the court refused to consider whether the college had been discriminated against by the board's denial. On the college's challenge to the constitutional validity of Zoning Ordinance § 401, the court held that the board had improperly construed certain ordinance subdivisions against the college. The existence of more suitable sites was irrelevant. The board's conclusion that the low local proportion of enrollment in the college would have been unaltered was without basis. The board improperly considered the maximum occupancy of the college as opposed to the college's asserted plan. Denial of the permit was arbitrary and unreasonable, but the board was entitled to assurances of as to the maximum student population allowed by the college.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the board's determination and held that the reasons given by the board were insufficient for the denial of the use permit to the college.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- determination of Board of Zoning Appeals denying special exception use permit to establish small experimental college reversed and matter remanded to board -- findings of board unauthorized -- only standards constitutionally applicable to petitioner are whether use will be hazardous to health or safety or detrimental to public welfare -- further application necessary before exceeding stated limits of use -- application subject to subsequent amendment to zoning ordinance.

1. Petitioner applied for a special exception use permit under the zoning ordinance of defendant village to establish in a Residence BB district of the village a small experimental college in connection with the parent institution. The Board of Zoning Appeals denied the application. The question whether petitioner is discriminated against by the requirement that it obtain a use permit is not one that may properly be presented for determination, since there is before the court no respondent who could be directed to issue a permit were the court to conclude that the ordinance is discriminatory.

2. In this proceeding the court may consider the constitutionality of the standards [***2] applied by the Board of Zoning Appeals.

3. The provisions of the zoning ordinance which require the zoning board to consider traffic problems and accessibility of fire and police protection to the property pertain to applications made under subdivisions 1, 4, 14, 17 and 18 of section 1002 of the ordinance. Since the application in question was made under subdivision 15, the board was not authorized to consider such factors in connection with its determination.

4. In denying the application, the board stated that there were other areas in the Residence BB district which might be suitable for college purposes. The ordinance, however, requires the board to find that the proposed use "will not be feasible or practical in a less restricted district".

5. The board's finding that only nine students residing in the village presently attend petitioner's classes is both unauthorized and a non sequitur, for this finding does not necessitate the conclusion that a similarly small proportion will be part of the 120 to 600 students attending the experimental college.

6. Notwithstanding that the plan of the village is for a low population density, the board improperly reasoned that the density [***3] concentrated on the property in question would be almost three times that of the population of the whole village, since the Village Board has legislatively determined that a density in excess of the present village norm is consistent with the general welfare.

7. In considering a college application, the only standards set forth in subdivision 24 of section 1002 of the ordinance that may constitutionally be applied are that the proposed use will not create a hazard to health or safety or otherwise be detrimental to public welfare.

8. Petitioner must make a further application before it can exceed the stated outside limits of the use presently proposed.

9. Petitioner's application was made prior to December, 1959. On December 14, 1959 the ordinance was amended to provide that uses under special exception permits are limited to those set forth in a statement accompanying the application. The application is subject to that amendment, for the court must decide the proceeding according to the law existing at the time of its decision.

10. The matter is remanded to the board with directions (1) to consider what, if any, modifications of the height restrictions and marginal roadway requirements [***4] need be granted, and then to issue a use permit valid for at least 10 years, or (2) if the board so sees fit, to require that the college file the additional data required to bring its application within subdivision 15 of section 1002 of the ordinance, as amended, in which event the board should consider the application anew.

 

2462 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Coish v. State


Claim Nos. 35926, 35927, 35928, 35929, 35930, 35931, 35932, 35933


Court of Claims of New York


23 Misc. 2d 117; 203 N.Y.S.2d 748; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2649



July 28, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant accident victims filed an action against defendant state to recover damages for wrongful death, personal injuries, medical expenses, and loss of services arising out of an automobile accident allegedly caused by the state's negligent maintenance of a stretch of highway. The court rendered its decision after trial of the issues.


OVERVIEW: The accident victims alleged that they were injured by the state's negligent maintenance of a stretch of highway upon which the accident occurred. The state argued that the claims were not filed within the statutory time limit, that an enabling act (act) conferring jurisdiction on the court to hear claimants' case violated N.Y. Const. art. III, § 19, and that claimants failed to establish the state's negligence, their freedom from contributory negligence, and the proximate cause of the accident. The court dismissed the wrongful death claim and rendered judgment for the accident victims on their personal injury and medical expense claims. The act was unconstitutional as to the wrongful death claim because its effect was to provide a period of two years and six months in which to file the action against the state whereas such an action between citizens of the state had to be filed within two years of the date of death. The act did not contravene the state constitution as to the other claims because its effect was to extend the period of time for filing the action to two years and six months whereas a three-year period was available for such actions between citizens.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the accident victims' wrongful death claim against the state as untimely filed and entered judgment for the accident victims on their claims for damages for personal injuries and medical expenses caused by the state's negligence in maintaining a highway.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] State -- claim against State -- enabling act (L. 1958, ch. 246) permitting claimants to sue State for damages resulting from motor vehicle accident unconstitutional as to claim for damages for wrongful death -- not unconstitutional as to claims for personal injury damages -- sole proximate cause of accident when automobile skidded at curve of road was negligence of State -- awards made to claimants.

1. Chapter 246 of the Laws of 1958, which was enacted to permit claimants to sue the State for damages resulting when a motor vehicle was involved in an accident, is unconstitutional as to the claim for damages for wrongful death. Section 19 of article III of the New York State Constitution provides that: "No claim against the state shall be audited, allowed or paid which, as between citizens of the state, could be barred by lapse of time." The enabling act, in providing for an additional six months in which to file a claim to recover for the wrongful death after claimant had already had available to it a tribunal for the enforcement of the right for a period of two years ( Court of Claims Act, § 10), provides a period of two years and six months for the bringing of this claim,  [***2] whereas such an action as between citizens of the State must be filed within two years of the date of death (Decedent Estate Law, § 130). The claim for wrongful death is dismissed.

2. The statute is not unconstitutional as to the claims for personal injuries since the applicable Statute of Limitations as between citizens of the State is three years (Civ. Prac. Act, § 49), and the effect of the enabling act was to extend the period for filing the claims to two years and six months.

3. As an automobile driven by decedent and owned by her husband, and in which the other claimants were passengers, rounded a left curve on a highway, it skidded out of control on the wet, slippery pavement and struck some trees on the shoulder of the road. Concededly, the District Safety Engineer had recommended that the curve have a warning sign of 35 miles per hour as a safe speed, but there was no such warning sign and no sign of a curve. The road was not only slippery but it was rough. The sole proximate cause of the accident was the negligence of the State in the failure to adequately place signs at a known dangerous condition and to use ordinary care in the maintenance of the highway.

4. Awards [***3] are made to claimants.

 

2463 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Somers v. Camarco Contractors, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


24 Misc. 2d 673; 205 N.Y.S.2d 724; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2681



July 19, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Plaintiff's motion for summary judgment is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town sought an injunction preventing defendant business, a sand and gravel pit, from continuing unless it complied with a new zoning ordinance regarding nonconforming uses. The town moved for summary judgment. The sand and gravel business sought to have the zoning ordinance declared unconstitutional as applied to its property.


OVERVIEW: The sand and gravel business had operated for years before any zoning. The business had invested substantial value in lands, plant, and structures. In 1945 the town adopted its first zoning ordinance, placing the property in a residential zone but containing a provision for nonconforming uses. The ordinance was amended several times. Amendments discontinued nonconforming use for "natural products uses," meaning sand and gravel pits. At the expiration of a short period, the nonconforming use must be discontinued. In a prior suit, this amendment was held unconstitutional as applied to the subject property. In 1959, the town enacted an entire new zoning ordinance. Again, the right to absolute continuance of nonconforming uses was preserved except for the sand and gravel pit, which was given five years upon application before it would be forced to relocate. The business ignored the ordinance. The town sued and sought summary judgment. The motion was denied. The ancient rule in New York was that nonconforming uses could not be terminated if there was a substantial investment in them. Whether that rule still applied was an issue needing clarification and precluding summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The town's motion for summary judgment was denied. There were both vital questions of law and questions of fact which must be determined before the rights of the parties could be ultimately settled and the law as to nonconforming uses clarified.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- town cannot have summary judgment against vested nonconforming user, by enacting zoning ordinance requiring such user to file bond and obtain five-year permit which can be renewed only in board's discretion.

A town cannot have summary judgment enjoining a sand-and-gravel mining corporation, which has a vested right to continue such nonconforming use, from doing business unless the corporation complies with a newly enacted zoning ordinance which (1) requires such nonconforming user to furnish a bond guaranteeing that, at the end of five years, it will restore the premises to their original condition as nearly as may be practicable and will remove all structures and machinery, (2) requires that such bond be in an amount to be fixed by the town's Zoning Board of Appeals, (3) provides that, on approval of such bond's form and sufficiency by the Town Board, the Town Clerk shall issue to such user a permit for five years, and (4) provides that such user may thereafter apply to said Zoning Board of Appeals for a discretionary extension of such five-year period.

Zucker v. Bloch


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


24 Misc. 2d 1008; 204 N.Y.S.2d 1018; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2704



July 13, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a motion as an application for an order of prohibition to prevent the further prosecution of a charge against him for possessing obscene books with the intent to sell on the basis that the statute that he allegedly violated, N.Y. Penal Law § 1141 was unconstitutional. Respondents, magistrate and others, filed a motion to dismiss petitioner's application.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with possessing obscene books with intent to sell. Petitioner subsequently filed a motion as an application for an order of prohibition to prevent the further prosecution of the charge against him on the basis that the statute that he allegedly violated, N.Y. Penal Law § 1141, was unconstitutional. Respondents filed a motion to dismiss petitioner's application. The court denied petitioner's application and granted respondents' motion to dismiss petitioner's application. The court found that other courts had generally upheld the constitutionality of § 1141. The court held that a constitutionally valid prosecution for keeping an obscene book in stock to be sold was conceivable despite the lack of expression in the statute of scienter as an element of the crime, providing knowledge was included as an element of the proof at the trial. The court determined that the statute was valid even though it did not contain the mens rea required to obtain a conviction where it was necessary to prove mens rea at trial.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's motion for an application for an order of prohibition in which he sought to prevent the further prosecution of a charge against him for possessing obscene books with the intent to sell of prohibition. The court granted respondents' cross motion to dismiss petitioner's application.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- possession of obscene books with intent to sell -- United States Supreme Court has not invalidated section 1141 of Penal Law under which petitioner is charged with possessing obscene books with intent to sell.

An application for an order of prohibition against prosecution of petitioner, who is charged with possessing obscene books with intent to sell them, on the ground that the statute which he allegedly violated (Penal Law, § 1141) has been declared unconstitutional by the Supreme Court of the United States in Smith v. California (361 U.S. 147), is denied. The Supreme Court has not invalidated the statute.

Cannata v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


24 Misc. 2d 694; 204 N.Y.S.2d 982; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2764



June 28, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion for judgment on the pleadings is in all respects granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners filed an action for a declaration that N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 72-n was unconstitutional both on its face and as applied to the project area involved. The landowners also asked that § 72-n be declared null and void, that the designation of the area as blighted be cancelled, and that defendant city be restrained from proceeding further. The city filed a motion to dismiss, for judgment on the pleadings, and for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The landowners were owner occupants of certain residential properties located in an area known as the Flatlands area of Brooklyn, which was designated by the city planning commission as a predominantly vacant area characterized by certain of the blighting conditions specified in § 72-n. Such a designation was a requisite preliminary step to the city's condemnation of the area for clearance and redevelopment purposes. The landowners filed their action, and the court granted the city's motion for judgment on the pleadings. Section 72-n provided for taking of private property for public use. Eminent domain was one of the powers inherent in the state. A purpose for the acquisition of land, designated to facilitate other projects such as slum clearance, was in the public interest even though the property taken might ultimately be sold to private interests. The landowners did not meet their onerous burden of overcoming the presumption that the legislative enactment was presumed to be constitutional and supported by facts known to the legislative body.


OUTCOME: The court granted the city's motion for judgment on the pleadings in all respects.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- condemnation and redevelopment of predominantly vacant area -- municipality may condemn area which retards city's development and may sell such area to grantee who agrees to city's plan for area's redevelopment ( General Municipal Law, § 72-n: N. Y. Const., art. XVIII).

Under article XVIII of the State Constitution and section 72-n of the General Municipal Law, a city validly designated a predominantly vacant but partially improved area, which was not a slum and which was "without tangible physical blight", as "blighted", in that the area had such irregular subdivisions and such poorly designed street patterns and such scattered improvements as to render the area incapable of effective development ( General Municipal Law, § 72-n, subd. 1, par. a, cls. [1], [2], [7]); and the city thereupon validly determined that this area should be condemned by the city and should be redeveloped by private industry for light manufacturing uses primarily, in order to provide space for industries displaced by the city's urban renewal developments and by other public improvements [***2] and in order to stem the tide of industries moving out of the city (§ 72-n, subd. 7); and the city thereupon validly adopted a plan for clearing and developing the area, which plan must be agreed to by any purchaser from the city (§ 72-n, subd. 8). This does not put the city into "private business" (N. Y. Const., art. XVIII, § 10). Plaintiff property owners have not demonstrated that the statute is unconstitutional, either on its face or as applied to this area; and their suit for such an adjudication is dismissed.

 

2466 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


New York Post Corp. v. Moses


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


23 Misc. 2d 826; 204 N.Y.S.2d 44; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2765



June 28, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner newspaper sought an order directing respondent Triborough Bridge and Tunnel Authority (authority) to allow the newspaper to inspect certain of the authority's records and files.


OVERVIEW: A newspaper sought court approval to inspect certain file and records of the authority. The court denied the newspaper's request and held that the authority was well within its legal rights in refusing to grant the inspection and the court was powerless to interfere. The court found that the action of the authority in denying the inspection of its records was not arbitrary, unreasonable, or capricious and there was no statutory right of inspection. The authority was not found to be conducting its affairs in secrecy because under the law the authority was subject to the investigative and auditing processes of certain state and city public officials. The court held that the fact that the newspaper was in the business of disseminating news gave them no special right or privilege not possessed by other members of the public to the information. The court held that no newspaper could claim the right of access to sources of information not available to others and the denial of such alleged right was not a violation of the newspaper's rights, constitutional, statutory, or otherwise.


OUTCOME: The court denied the newspaper's request.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Proceeding against body or officer -- inspection of contract files of Triborough Bridge and Tunnel Authority -- petition in proceeding brought by newspaper corporation for order directing Triborough Bridge and Tunnel Authority to permit petitioner to inspect contract files of Authority for 10 years and minutes of meetings of Authority for 10-year period, dismissed -- Authority under no legal duty to grant inspection sought -- newspaper has no such personal interest as would require granting of inspection -- petitioner has no constitutional right to inspection.

1. A petition in a proceeding brought by a newspaper corporation for an order directing the Triborough Bridge and Tunnel Authority to permit petitioner to inspect the contract files of the Authority for the past 10 years and the minutes of meetings of the Authority for the 10-year period is dismissed.

2. The Authority is under no legal duty to grant the inspection sought. Section 66 of the Public Officers Law and section 51 of the General Municipal Law do not provide a statutory duty since the records of the Authority are not "public records", and those statutes do not apply to this Authority.

3. In certain situations [***2] where a member of the public is shown to have a personal interest in a situation, he may be allowed an inspection of records which are not within the strict definition of public records, but the fact that petitioner is engaged in publishing a newspaper does not give it such an interest.

4. Petitioner has no constitutional right to an inspection of the records.

 

2467 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Crispell


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Ulster County


23 Misc. 2d 173; 202 N.Y.S.2d 822; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2767



June 27, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an application for a writ of error coram nobis after his original sentence was reimposed for the crime of grand larceny.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arraigned on a charge of grand larceny in the second degree, waived examination, and was held to await the action of the grand jury. Pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 222, defendant undertook to waive his right to have the grand jury inquire into the pending charge. The district attorney filed an information charging him with grand larceny in the second degree. Defendant pleaded guilty to the crime of grand larceny, as charged in such information, and his following sentence was suspended during good behavior. The suspension was thereafter revoked and the original sentence imposed. Defendant then filed an application for a writ of error coram nobis after his original sentence was reimposed. Upon review, the court vacated his conviction. The court held that coram nobis was an appropriate remedy in view of defendant's present incarceration on another commitment and in view of the fact that the case involved the abrogation, without adequate remedy, of fundamental precepts going to the jurisdiction of the court.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the conviction.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- coram nobis -- defendant's conviction in 1926 upon plea of guilty was nullity and vacated where he waived his right to have Grand Jury inquire into charge pursuant to section 222 of Code of Criminal Procedure and that statute was subsequently declared unconstitutional -- charge may be presented before another Grand Jury -- coram nobis is appropriate remedy.

1. In 1926 defendant was arraigned on a charge of grand larceny in the second degree. He waived examination and was held to await the action of the Grand Jury. Pursuant to section 222 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, as it then existed, he undertook to waive his right to have the Grand Jury inquire into the pending charge. Section 222 of the Code of Criminal Procedure was subsequently declared unconstitutional by the Court of Appeals. Defendant's conviction, therefore, in 1926 upon his plea of guilty to the crime of grand larceny was a nullity, and is vacated.

2. Since defendant is presently incarcerated on another commitment, the District Attorney may present the charge before the present County Court Grand Jury and in the event of an indictment return the defendant to this jurisdiction for due processing.

 [***2] 3. Coram nobis is an appropriate remedy.

Hotel Armstrong, Inc. v. Temporary State Housing Rent Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


25 Misc. 2d 89; 204 N.Y.S.2d 226; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2792



June 21, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion of the plaintiff is granted and the motions of the defendants are denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hotel owner brought a declaratory judgment action against defendant administrator of the State Housing Rent Commission regarding the administrator's imposition of rent control under an amendment to the State Residential Rent Law, L. 1946, ch. 274. Both parties motioned for judgment pursuant to N.Y. R. Civ. Prac. 112, 113. Intervenor State Attorney General also motioned for judgment under N.Y. R. Civ. Prac. 113.


OVERVIEW: The hotel owner's premises had not been subject to rent control because it had been operated as a hotel. A proceeding was instituted by the administrator, which resulted in an order determining that the premises was no longer a hotel. The administrator exercised control over those tenants whose occupancy was continuous. The administrator fixed a maximum rent on the basis of comparable accommodations and reduced the rents by approximately fifty percent. The court held that hotels were excepted from rent control by Section 2 of the State Residential Rent Law, but not "pseudo hotels" that were in reality rooming houses with hotel names. The court held that the "pseudo hotel" situation might require correction and regulation by the administrator. However, the hotel owner's premises had never been under rent control and there was no evidence that it was a "pseudo hotel." The language of the State Residential Rent Law provided only for the "recontrol" of premises that at some earlier time had already been under rent control.


OUTCOME: The court granted the hotel owner's motion for judgment and denied the administrator's motion for judgment.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and tenant -- rent regulation -- hotels which are really rooming houses.

An amendment (L. 1959, ch. 695) to the State Residential Rent Law (§ 2, subd. 2, par. [b]; § 4, subd. 2-b), pursuant to which stringent rent controls are imposed on hotels which are really rooming houses, was declared by Special Term to be not applicable to a building which had always previously been exempted, as a hotel, from rent control.

Nelson v. Camillus


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Onondaga County


28 Misc. 2d 52; 210 N.Y.S.2d 907; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2874



June 3, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a town board and a theatre, filed a motion for summary judgment in the action by plaintiff property owners. The property owners requested a general injunction and a declaration that Camillus, N.Y., Zoning Ordinance (October 14, 1959) was illegal and void and that the rights of the parties be determined.


OVERVIEW: The property owners alleged that the zoning ordinance was unconstitutional, illegal, and invalid as not being passed for the purpose of public, health, safety, and morals as required by Camillus, N.Y. Town Law § 263. They also alleged that it constituted a violation of Camillus, N.Y. Town Laws § 261-263. The property owners alleged that it granted a zoning change upon conditions or agreements, which was an unauthorized delegation of legislative power. There was some doubt as to whether the zoning ordinance was enacted pursuant to any comprehensive plan. The court did not pass on the legality or illegality of a covenant to run with the land. The court felt that sufficient issues of fact had been raised regarding the alleged illegality of the proceeding under Camillus, N.Y. Town Law art. 16 that to grant summary judgment on affidavits would be an abuse of discretion. The property owners alleged that the theatre's application, the notice of public hearing, and the notice of the amendment of the zoning ordinance were all defective. The court felt that questions of fact were raised regarding all three of the items, which could not be resolved on affidavits.


OUTCOME: The court denied the summary judgment motion by the theatre and the town board.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- motion for summary judgment denied -- it is doubtful whether challenged zoning ordinance was enacted pursuant to comprehensive plan -- issues of fact exist regarding legality of proceeding under article 16 of Town Law -- rezoned property inaccurately described in said proceeding.

1. In an action for a general injunction, a declaration that an ordinance rezoning certain real property owned by defendant corporation from "Residential" to "Local Business A" is illegal and void, and that the rights of the parties be determined, a motion for summary judgment is denied.

2. There is doubt as to whether the subject ordinance was enacted pursuant to any comprehensive plan.

3. Issues of fact exist regarding the alleged illegality of the proceeding under article 16 of the Town Law insofar as procedures are concerned. Furthermore, the rezoned property was inaccurately described in said proceeding.

4. The legality of imposing a covenant to run with the land in connection with the change of zoning is not passed upon in view of a pending appeal to the Court of Appeals on a similar question ( Church v. Town of Islip, 8 A D 2d 962).

 

2470 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Devine v. Hults


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


25 Misc. 2d 59; 202 N.Y.S.2d 886; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2896



June 1, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner bus driver applied for an order under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 directing respondent Commissioner of Motor Vehicles to cancel and annul the revocation of the bus driver's license to operate a motor vehicle. The bus driver was required to submit to a re-examination after being involved in three accidents in 18 months. The bus driver passed the written test, English test, and eye test, but failed the road test.


OVERVIEW: The examiner that failed the bus driver stated that the bus driver failed to keep to the right, used poor judgment in traffic and in approaching intersections, and swung wide on right turns and short on left turns. The bus driver denied that he made the mistakes charged to him and asserted that the Commissioner's action in revoking his license was arbitrary and unreasonable, that N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 20(8) was unconstitutional in that there was no clear and reasonable norms established for the guidance of the Commissioner, and that § 20(8) denied the bus driver the equal protection of the laws because it deprived him of the means of earning a livelihood. The court found that there was no need to decide the constitutionality question raised by the bus driver because the court held that the action of the Commissioner was arbitrary and unreasonable. The court found that the bus driver was a member in good standing of a bus driver association and had not been involved in any accident in which he was at fault. The court further found that the bus driver's employer had never charged him with negligence and that even the most inconsequential accidents required reporting.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the order of the Commissioner revoking the bus driver's motor vehicle operator's license and directed the Commissioner to re-examine the bus driver within 30 days.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Motor vehicles -- revocation of operator's license -- on basis of facts surrounding petitioner's re-examination, and testimony of president of bus drivers' union, revocation of operator's license of petitioner, bus driver, who was involved in three accidents within 18 months and failed to pass re-examination, is held to be arbitrary and unreasonable -- constitutionality of Vehicle and Traffic Law ( § 20, subd. 8) not decided.

1. Petitioner, a bus driver, was involved in three accidents within 18 months and was ordered to submit to a re-examination. He did not pass the road test and his license was revoked. At a subsequent hearing held to determine whether such revocation was arbitrary, capricious and unreasonable, the president of the bus drivers' union of which petitioner is a member testified that petitioner is a "very good operator", that he has not been involved in any accident in which he was at fault and that he has not been charged with negligence by his employer. The facts also developed, inter alia, that when petitioner appeared for re-examination the license examiner refused to permit the use of the automobile in which he planned to take the test, for failure [***2] to display an inspection stamp, although his friend, who had just purchased the car, displayed the registration certificate stamped with a motor vehicle stamp that it was registered and inspected. Petitioner was forced to procure another car immediately, was re-examined, and of the nine persons re-examined that day, he was the only one failed. On the basis of the facts, respondent's action is held to be arbitrary and unreasonable, the order of revocation is annulled, and respondent is directed to re-examine petitioner within 30 days.

2. In view of the above determination, the question of constitutionality of the statute (Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 20, subd. 8) [providing in respect to the "reexamination of licensees in certain cases and action thereon"], if it is applied to an operator who became involved in three accidents within 18 months without any fault on his part, is not passed upon.

Atlantic Beach Hotel v. Larkin


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


25 Misc. 2d 511; 202 N.Y.S.2d 769; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2905



June 1, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] This branch of the motion is likewise denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, various property and business owners, brought suit and a motion for a temporary injunction against defendant incorporators seeking a decree which restrained the filing or prosecution of the proceedings for incorporation of a village and stay compliance of the order directing incorporation, which had been affirmed by the appellate court in another lawsuit.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff complained that the statutory provisions regarding incorporating a village afforded them no method of challenge or right to vote in the incorporation proceedings. The court held that it lacked power to impose new requirements or change requirements already imposed by the legislature in the discharge of its legislative functions and that the legislature had not in its enactment of the Village Law given persons in the position of plaintiffs a right to stay incorporation. The court further held that failure of the legislature to give persons such as plaintiffs such a right did not render the law unconstitutional. The court further found that no meritorious cause of action was stated to warrant the issuance of a temporary injunction as well as that plaintiffs failed to show any irreparable harm. Rather, the court found that plaintiffs' greatest fears and objections were that the disputed area was, as part of an incorporated village, subject to undue, disproportionate, and burdensome taxation and regulation. There was no evidentiary showing that the village authorities would engage in unlawful acts.


OUTCOME: The court denied plaintiffs' motion for a temporary injunction.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- incorporation of village -- residential and business areas may be incorporated without separate vote by business area; temporary injunction denied (Village Law, art. 2; N. Y. Const., art. IX, § 9).

1. A proposition for the incorporation, as a village, of a residential area with a commercial and business area, must be acted upon by the Town Board, by publication and posting and hearing, even though the proposition is submitted by persons in the residential area only, and even though the statute does not give a separate vote to the property owners in the commercial and business area, who fear disproportionate taxation (Village Law, art. 2; N. Y. Const., art. IX, § 9).

2. A temporary injunction will not be granted against the Town Board's taking further steps and proceeding according to law (i.e., Village Law, art. 2).

 

2472 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Munoz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Special Sessions of City of New York, Appellate Part, First Department


22 Misc. 2d 1078; 200 N.Y.S.2d 957; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2950



May 25, 1960 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Bronx Adolescent Court, Borough of The Bronx (New York), which convicted him of violating New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § 436-5.2 for having in his possession a two-bladed knife.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a high school student, was stopped by police while walking through his neighborhood and arrested for carrying a two-bladed knife in violation of § 436-5.2, which applied only to persons under 21 years of age. Defendant challenged his conviction on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional, and the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that the statute was not vague or uncertain because its language was sufficiently definite to apprise the persons to whom it was addressed of the nature of the acts that were prohibited. There was no arbitrary discrimination that rendered the statute unconstitutional because the age provision was based on differences that were reasonably related to the purposes of the statute. As the statute was a reasonable and valid exercise of police power, defendant's conviction was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- possession of knife by person under 21 years of age -- judgment of conviction of possession of two-bladed knife by 16-year-old defendant, affirmed -- section 436-5.2 of Administrative Code of City of New York, under which defendant was convicted, does not violate due process and equal protection clauses of Fourteenth Amendment of Federal Constitution and sections 6 and 11 of State Constitution.

1. The 16-year-old defendant appeals from a judgment of the Bronx Adolescent Court convicting him, on undisputed facts, of violating section 436-5.2 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York, by having a two-bladed knife in his possession. The statute is sufficiently definite to apprise persons to whom it is addressed of the nature of the proscribed acts, and the language thereof is clearly understandable when given its ordinary and usual [***2] meaning.

2. Application of the statute to persons under 21 years of age is not an arbitrary discrimination against such persons, as the age discrimination is based on differences reasonably related to the purposes of the legislation.

3. Enactment of the legislation was not an arbitrary exercise of police power but was the result of legislative determination that criminal use of knives and sharp pointed instruments by persons under 21 years of age constituted a menace to the public safety and welfare.

4. As the statute does not violate the due process and equal protection clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment of the Federal Constitution and sections 6 and 11 of article I of the State Constitution, the judgment of conviction is affirmed.

Hotel Armstrong, Inc. v. Temporary State Housing Rent Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


25 Misc. 2d 87; 202 N.Y.S.2d 596; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3117



April 21, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, this motion is in all respects denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hotel owner filed an action seeking a declaratory judgment that §§ 2(2)(b), 4(2)(b) of the State Residential Rent Law, 1946 N.Y. Laws ch. 274, as amended by 1959 N.Y. Laws ch. 695, were inapplicable to its premises and were unconstitutional. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: Defendants established control of the hotel owner's premises in an administrative proceeding. The hotel owner claimed that its premises had never been subject to rent control and that its status as a hotel free of rent control could not be changed. The hotel owner filed a protest to the control of its premises by defendants, and then filed suit for a declaratory judgment. In its lawsuit, the hotel owner directly challenged the constitutionality of §§ 2(b)(2), 4(b)(2). Defendants consented to the hotel owner's application for a temporary injunction. The court denied defendants' ensuing motion to dismiss the complaint. Because the hotel owner challenged the constitutionality and construction of §§ 2(b)(2), 4(b)(2), administrative review and judicial review under N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act art. 78 was inadequate. Further, defendants' attempt to challenge the sufficiency of the complaint after consenting to a temporary injunction was inconsistent.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motion to dismiss the hotel owner's complaint was denied.
