Actions -- constitutionality of statute -- plenary suit, rather than review proceeding, proper.

The constitutionality of a statute -- in this case, the State Residential Rent Law (§ 2, subd. 2, par. [b], and § 4, subd. 2-b, both as amd. by L. 1959, ch. 695) -- is properly attacked by a plenary suit, rather than by a proceeding (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78) to review an administrative decision made under the statute.

 

2474 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Benzow v. Cooley


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


22 Misc. 2d 208; 199 N.Y.S.2d 22; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3183



April 13, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petitioner's application for an order is denied and the proceeding dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner councilman filed an application for a proceeding under N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act art. 78 seeking a writ of mandamus to compel respondents, city and officials, to comply with the provisions of § 18 of the City Home Rule Law by preparing an abstract of the Local Law No. 1 (1960) adopted by the Common Council of the City of Buffalo and approved by the mayor amending § 62 of the Charter of the City of Buffalo.


OVERVIEW: The councilman sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondents to comply with the provisions of § 18 of the City Home Rule Law by preparing an abstract of the Local Law No. 1 (1960) adopted by the Common Council of the City of Buffalo and approved by the mayor amending § 62 of the Charter of the City of Buffalo. The councilman contended that such amendment was to be submitted to a referendum of the voters of the city at the next general election and was not to become effective unless and until approved by the general voters. The court denied the councilman's application and dismissed the proceeding. The court concluded that the disqualification of ineligibility contained in § 62 when it was first enacted related to no lack of personal qualifications such as age, ability, experience, and integrity of a mayor. The court found that it was predicated upon the assumption that the mayor might have, through his appointive power, built up political "rings" and "blocs" and perpetuated himself in office. The court concluded that such conditions no longer existed, and the provision making a mayor ineligible to succeed himself was arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court denied the councilman's application for a writ of mandamus compelling respondents to prepare an abstract of a local law amending a provision of the city charter.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- change in law as to succession of Mayor -- Local Law of City of Buffalo removing disqualification of Mayor to succeed himself need not be submitted to referendum of voters -- prohibition against succeeding one's self in office is arbitrary disqualification for holding office (N. Y. Const., art. I, § 1; art. XIII, § 1).

1. Section 62 of the Charter of the City of Buffalo formerly provided that: "Any mayor elected as such under this act for a full term of four years shall be ineligible for the next term after the termination of his office." Local Law No. 1 (1960), adopted by the Common Council of the City of Buffalo and approved by the Mayor, amended that section to provide: "Any mayor heretofore or hereafter elected as such under this act shall be eligible for re-election." Said Local Law need not be submitted to a referendum of the voters of the City of Buffalo.

2. Section 15 (subds. 3, 4) of the City Home Rule Law provides in part that a local law shall be subject to mandatory referendum if it changes the law of succession to the mayoralty if the office of Mayor is an elective [***2] office. The Local Law changes the law of succession to the office.

3. However, section 1 of article I of the State Constitution provides that: "No member of this state shall be disfranchised, or deprived of any of the rights or privileges secured to any citizen thereof, unless by the law of the land, or the judgment of his peers". Section 1 of article XIII, after providing for the form of the oath of office to be taken by State officers, provides: "and no other oath, declaration or test shall be required as a qualification for any office or public trust". Under the Constitution, a statute may not be validly enacted containing arbitrary and unreasonable grounds of disqualification to hold office. The disqualification of ineligibility contained in the prior section 62 relates to no lack of personal qualification such as age, ability, experience and integrity of a Mayor, but is predicated upon the assumption that he might through his appointive power build up political "rings" or "blocs" and perpetuate himself in office. While this assumption was no doubt the basis of the original section 62, it has been shown that these conditions no longer exist. The provision making a Mayor [***3] ineligible to succeed himself, under the present conditions, is arbitrary.

4. It is unnecessary to decide whether section 62 was or was not constitutional when it was adopted in 1927. An act constitutional when adopted may become invalid by a change in the conditions to which it applies. Conditions surrounding the office of Mayor have substantially changed since 1927.

 

2475 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Wiltwyck School for Boys, Inc. v. Perry


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


24 Misc. 2d 281; 199 N.Y.S.2d 909; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3192



April 12, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The action of respondent Building Inspector in refusing to issue the requested permit is, therefore, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Building Inspector denied petitioner school's request for a permit to erect a school and residential treatment center. The school appealed to the Zoning Board of Appeals. The board affirmed the decision. The court upheld the board's decision. The school filed a direct appeal from the determination that denied the permit. The school contended that Town of Yorktown, N.Y., Ordinance art. IV, § 423(7), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance provided for certain uses as of right, including religious, charitable, and eleemosynary institutions other than for the insane. The Building Inspector denied the school's permit, holding that the proposed use was not a permitted main use in the residential area under the town ordinance. The court affirmed the determination. A substantial percentage of the children accepted for treatment had been characterized as "psychotic" or having such tendencies. The school was not a "school" in the accepted sense of that term; it was basically corrective in nature. It had been established and maintained for the care, custody, and treatment of children who were psychotic and the conduct of classes, while probably required by law and certainly beneficial to the welfare of the children, was, nevertheless, incidental to the basic purposes of the school. The municipality could have controlled the type of institution that sought to make its home in the community if the legislation did not violate state or federal constitutional provisions. The school had not sustained the burden of proving the invalidity of the ordinance under attack, or its interpretation by the Building Inspector.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the refusal of the requested permit.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- determination of Town Building Inspector denying application of petitioner, private corporation caring for boys who are, or are in danger of becoming, neglected or delinquent, for permit to erect school on its property in residential area, affirmed -- petitioner failed to establish that its institution meets requirements of charitable or eleemosynary institutions as defined in town ordinance, or that said ordinance is unconstitutional -- petitioner's property is both suitable and usable for purpose for which zoned.

1. Petitioner, a private corporation established to care for boys who are, or are in danger of becoming, neglected or delinquent, appeals from a determination of respondent Town Building Inspector, denying petitioner's application for a permit to erect a school on property owned by it in a residential area. The permit was refused on the ground that the proposed use did not meet the requirements of permitted charitable or eleemosynary institutions as defined in the Ordinance of the Town of Yorktown (art. IV, § 423,  [***2] subd. 7). Petitioner has failed to prove that its institution, which is basically corrective in nature, meets the requirements of a permitted use, as defined in said ordinance.

2. The municipality had authority to adopt an ordinance controlling the type of institution seeking to make its home in the community. The burden of proving the ordinance unconstitutional was upon the petitioner, and petitioner has failed to sustain that burden.

3. The legislation does not so restrict the use of the subject property that it cannot be used for any reasonable purpose. The land is both suitable and usable for the purpose for which it is zoned.

4. Petitioner is not being unlawfully discriminated against because orphan asylums "operated as an accessory use to a religious institution" are permitted. A zoning ordinance may permit one type of use to the exclusion of another if that use bears a reasonable relation to the public health, safety, morals and welfare.

5. The action of respondent Building Inspector in refusing to issue the requested permit is affirmed.

 

2476 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Felberbaum


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Special Sessions of the City of New York, Appellate Part, First Department


22 Misc. 2d 695; 199 N.Y.S.2d 326; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3277



April 4, 1960 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, etc.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was charged with two speeding violations under N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 155, pled guilty to both charges. The Magistrate's Court of the City of New York (New York) rendered judgment. Because it appeared that he had had a previous speeding conviction within 18 months, defendant's license to operate a motor vehicle was revoked. Defendant filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he had not been warned under N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 335-a and that he had not been advised of his rights under N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 699 and, therefore, that the judgment entered on his guilty plea should be reversed. The court reversed the judgment. Defendant had been properly warned pursuant to N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 335-a, but the trial court had not advised defendant of his rights as required by N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 699. Before adoption of 1957 N.Y. Laws ch. 698, N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 2(29) had applied the procedural rules for the trial of misdemeanors to traffic infractions. Under N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 699, at every arraignment, whether on indictment or information, defendant had to be told of his right to counsel and of his right to an adjournment for the purpose of getting counsel and had to be given a reasonable opportunity to ask for counsel and ask for an adjournment, all before being forced to plead. Because the magistrate had not given the warning, defendant's conviction had to be reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, granted a new trial, and remitted the fines.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- speeding -- failure of court to advise defendant of his rights under section 699 of Code of Criminal Procedure nullified proceedings wherein defendant was charged with speeding -- judgment reversed -- to construe section 155 of Vehicle and Traffic Law as entitling defendant to warning under section 699 of Code of Criminal Procedure if he were speeding in city having population under million but not entitled to such warning where city had more than million, would render statute unconstitutional.

Defendant was charged with two speeding violations and pleaded guilty. Failure of the court to advise him of his rights under section 699 of the Code of Criminal Procedure nullified the proceedings and requires a reversal of the judgment. Under section 155 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, as enacted by chapter 698 of the Laws of 1957, a defendant would be entitled to the warning under section 699 of the Code of Criminal Procedure if he were speeding in [***2] a city having a population under a million but would not be entitled to the warning if the same offense were committed in a city having more than a million. If the statute be so construed, it is discriminatory and unconstitutional.

Connecticut General Life Ins. Co. v. Superintendent of Ins.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


24 Misc. 2d 927; 200 N.Y.S.2d 909; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3287



April 1, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion is denied and cross motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff foreign insurer filed a motion for a declaratory judgment under N.Y. Ins. Law § 42(3). Both defendant commissioner and the insurer filed motions for summary judgment to determine whether operation of a subsidiary that offered fire insurance was permitted.


OVERVIEW: The insurer was a Connecticut insurance company in the business of life insurance, annuities, and accident and health insurance. In 1956, the insurer sought to acquire the stock of another Connecticut insurance company, which was engaged in the business of fire insurance. The insurer planned to operate the acquisition as a subsidiary. The commissioner advised the insurer that to do so would have resulted in revocation of its license to do business in New York. The court held that the legislature had not intended to permit a foreign insurer to conduct any other kind of insurance business through a subsidiary. The court noted that the legislature had liberalized N.Y. Ins. Law § 90, which dealt with the type of investment a life insurance company could have made. By that time, the issue between the parties was well known to those interested. Nevertheless, the legislature had not changed or clarified N.Y. Ins. Law § 42. In fact the legislature, in enacting the revised N.Y. Ins. Law § 90, had added "Nothing in this section shall be construed to relieve any foreign or alien insurer from compliance with any other provision of this chapter."


OUTCOME: The court denied the insurer's motion for summary judgment and granted the commissioner's cross motion.


HEADNOTES

Insurance -- foreign insurers -- foreign life insurance company, licensed in New York, cannot be permitted to acquire control of foreign fire insurance company (Insurance Law, § 42, subd. 3).

A foreign (Connecticut, in this case) life insurance company, licensed to do business in New York, cannot be permitted -- on pain of revocation of its New York license -- to acquire control of and operate a Connecticut fire insurance company (Insurance Law, § 42, subd. 3; § 90).

Association for Preservation of Freedom of Choice, Inc. v. Simon

Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County

The Secretary filed a cross motion to dismiss the corporation's petition on the grounds of insufficiency.

The Secretary of State cannot be compelled to accept a proposed certificate of incorporation of a membership corporation which has been disapproved by a Supreme Court Justice. The governing statutes (Membership Corporations Law, § 10; General Corporation Law, § 211, subd. 2) are constitutional.

 

2479 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


22 Misc. 2d 389; 201 N.Y.S.2d 111; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3297



March 31, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlord filed a declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of New York City, N.Y., Local Laws No. 80 (1957), which prohibited property owners from denying accommodations on the basis of race, color or religion. The landlord asserted he had an inviolable right to rent his property to whomever he chose. The landlord and defendant New York City (New York) both filed summary judgment motions.


OVERVIEW: On principle, the landlord objected to the anti-discrimination ordinance. He argued that if he only wished to rent to redheaded women, he had the inalienable right to do so. In granting the City's summary judgment motion, the court noted that it was unchallenged that governments had the power to enact regulations with regard to rental housing. Restrictions imposed with regard to the size, area, type of construction, window space, and sanitary facilities required for rental properties had all been unsuccessfully challenged in the past. Similarly, laws prohibiting racial discrimination with regard to employment were also found not to be constitutionally objectionable. The legislature had the power to decide what was in the public good of the community and to enact ordinances to promote that public good. The landlord had to yield to the legislative authority's determination that discrimination by landlords was not in the community's best interest.


OUTCOME: The court denied the landlord's motion for summary judgment. It granted the City's cross-motion for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- discrimination in housing -- Local Law of City of New York (Local Laws, 1957, No. 80 of City of New York) designed to prevent discrimination in housing not unconstitutional.

A motion by defendants for summary judgment in an action for judgment declaring that a local law of the City of New York (Local Laws, 1957, No. 80 of City of New York) which is designed to prevent discrimination in housing and forbids owners of multiple dwellings to deny accommodations on account of race, color or religion, is granted. The law is not unconstitutional.

 

2480 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Point Lookout Civic Asso., Inc. v. Hempstead


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


22 Misc. 2d 757; 200 N.Y.S.2d 925; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3332



March 28, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff residents and plaintiff association brought an actio against defendant town and defendant beach club, seeking a judgment declaring certain zoning ordinance amendments, enacted by the town's board, unconstitutional and invalid.


OVERVIEW: In 1953, the town rezoned an area from residential and business to business only. Under this amendment, beside other business uses, multiple dwellings were also permitted. Approximately four years later, the town at the request of the beach club amended the building zone ordinance again to allow multi-family dwellings. In response, the residents and the association brought their action, claiming the latter amendment was illegal spot zoning, both the 1953 and the latter amendments were zoning by contract and, therefore, void, and they were adversely affected. The court dismissed the complaint because the residents and the association failed to prove any damage or detriment to them, and thus, they were not aggrieved parties. In addition, the court found the association and residents failed to establish unconstitutionality beyond fair debate or beyond reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the complaint filed by the association and the residents against the beach club and the town.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- rezoning according to plan and restrictive covenants is not spot zoning or zoning by contract; besides, plaintiffs are not damaged; action to invalidate rezoning dismissed.

1. A rezoning amendment which is part of a comprehensive plan cannot be deemed illegal "spot zoning". Possible depreciation in the value of the plaintiffs' properties near the subject property is not of great significance, since the pecuniary profits of an individual are secondary to the public welfare.

2. Rezoning amendments which were unconditional cannot be deemed illegal "zoning by contract". The Town Board's requirement that the petitioning landowners execute and record a declaration of restrictions was within the board's governmental powers and in the town's best interests.

3. Furthermore, an amendment to a zoning ordinance is a legislative act. Therefore, this act by the Town Board, as recorded in its journal, may not be attacked collaterally, and the courts may not inquire into the motives of the board or go behind the duly enacted legislation of the board in an attempt to seek its motive.

4. Besides, in this action to declare the rezoning illegal and void,  [***2] the plaintiffs have failed to prove any damage or detriment to them, and hence they are not "aggrieved" parties. Most of them are so far from the subject premises that they fail to show how they are affected by the rezoning; and the evidence offered to establish a lessening of their residence values is innocuous. The civic association plaintiffs have no standing to maintain this action; they own no property which could be affected adversely by the zoning amendments. The action is dismissed.

 

2481 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Callaghan v. Bunis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, Buffalo


23 Misc. 2d 156; 198 N.Y.S.2d 568; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3352



March 23, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Defendant is discharged and the charge against him dismissed. It is further ordered that the 12 magazines be confiscated and destroyed because of their obscene nature.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with a violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 1141 on allegations that he did display and he did offer for sale several obscene magazines at his bookstore.


OVERVIEW: Several hundred magazines were confiscated from defendant's store, 12 of which formed the basis of the allegations against defendant. In dismissing the charges against defendant, the court first ruled that, despite defendant's exhibits in which he sought to establish that the magazines were not obscene based upon his proof of contemporary accepted standards in the community, the 12 magazines were obscene. The average person, applying contemporary community standards, would find that the dominant theme of the magazines taken as a whole appealed to prurient interest. The court ruled, however, that the record did not indicate that defendant had knowledge that the magazines were obscene. Under § 1141, knowledge or scienter war required on the part of defendant as to the obscene material and content of the material in his possession for sale or distribution. Without a finding of knowledge on defendant's part, there could be no finding of guilty. Because the magazines were obscene, the court ordered that they be confiscated and destroyed.


OUTCOME: The court discharged defendant, dismissed the charge against him, and ordered the magazines to be destroyed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- obscene books -- materials which form subject of charge of violation of section 1141 of Penal Law are obscene -- however, absent finding of knowledge by defendant of their obscene character, he is found not guilty.

1. Defendant is charged with violation of section 1141 of the Penal Law, in that he displayed and offered for sale copies of obscene magazines. Employing, as the test of obscenity, whether to the average person, applying contemporary community standards, the dominant theme of the material taken as a whole appeals to prurient interests, and taking into consideration the exhibits produced on defendant's behalf as evidence of contemporary community standards, there is no doubt but that the materials which are the subject of this action are obscene.

2. However, although subdivision 4 of section 1141 raises a presumption upon proof of possession of six books or magazines, obscene in nature, that the possession is presumptive evidence of intent to sell, lend, distribute or give away, that [***2] subdivision was not intended to raise a presumption of guilty without a finding of knowledge. As there is no mention in the record herein of defendant's knowledge of the obscene nature of the magazines upon which the charge is based, he is found not guilty.

3. Because of their obscene nature, the said magazines are to be confiscated and destroyed.

 

2482 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Russell Sage College v. Troy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Rensselaer County


24 Misc. 2d 344; 198 N.Y.S.2d 391; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3362



March 22, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff interested parties brought an action against defendant, a property owner, the City of Troy, and others, seeking a permanent injunction and a judgment to declare void a resolution of the City Common Council that granted the owner permission to erect a slaughterhouse and to also declare void a building permit issued to the owner. Pending before the court was plaintiffs' motion for a temporary injunction.


OVERVIEW: The City had an ordinance that prohibited slaughterhouses within certain wards without first receiving permission from the City's Common Council. The proposed slaughterhouse was within one of the protected wards, and the City authorized the building by resolution. Plaintiffs contended that the granting of permission was a legislative act requiring an ordinance, rather than a resolution, and that the City failed to comply with N.Y. Second Class Cities Law § 35. The court found that the granting of permission was an administrative act requiring only a resolution. Further, the permit was not void because the owner's property was never classified under the zoning ordinance and zoning laws could not be extended by implication. An affidavit of the City stated that all proceedings taken by the Council were in accordance with the rules of the Council. Therefore, plaintiffs failed to establish by clear and convincing evidence that the official action was illegal, that plaintiffs' rights were certain as to the law and the facts, and that there was a clear violation of law.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion for a temporary injunction.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Injunctions -- temporary injunction -- plaintiffs not entitled to temporary injunction against operation of slaughterhouse by defendant -- clear violation of law not established -- resolution of Common Council granting permission to erect slaughterhouse not subject to requirements of section 35 of Second Class Cities Law.

1. By resolution of the Common Council, defendant was granted permission to erect a slaughterhouse in the City of Troy. The plaintiffs are not entitled to a temporary injunction pending determination of the rights of the parties since they have not established a clear violation of the law which would authorize such action.

2. The resolution of the council was an administrative act and therefore not subject to the requirements of section 35 of the Second Class Cities Law, which regulates legislative acts.

 

2483 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Kass v. Schneiderman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Municipal Court of the City of New York, Borough of Manhattan


21 Misc. 2d 518; 197 N.Y.S.2d 979; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3380



March 21, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Both motions are therefore denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff car owner filed suit against defendant another car owner for damages sustained to plaintiff's automobile. Plaintiff alleged that defendant was negligent for having left his car unattended with the motor running in violation of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1210(a). The matter was before the court upon the parties' cross-motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: After midnight, in the early morning hours of a winter day, defendant, who had attended a function, left to get he car which he had parked about a block and a half from the building in which the function was held. He drove his automobile back to the building intending to pick up his friend who was waiting for him. The building fronted on a boulevard, which had a vehicular service lane immediately adjacent to the sidewalk curb. Defendant got out of the passenger side door, leaving it open, in order to get his friend's attention. An unknown assailant then knocked down defendant. The assailant then jumped into defendant's car and drove it down the service road, running into and damaging several parked automobiles, one of which was plaintiff's. Defendant contended that the enactment of § 1210(a) could not be so distorted in meaning as plaintiff suggested. The court concluded that, based upon the record before it, it could not, as a matter of law, grant a summary judgment to either party. The court determined that a material issue of fact existed as to whether defendant allowed the automobile to stand "unattended" as that term was used in the statute.


OUTCOME: The court denied both parties' motions for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- negligence -- leaving automobile unattended -- section 1210 (subd. [a]) of Vehicle and Traffic Law provides that motor vehicle shall not be left unattended without stopping engine, locking ignition, removing key and setting brake -- when defendant stepped out of automobile he was struck by assailant, who then drove automobile and damaged parked automobiles, one of which was plaintiff's -- motions for summary judgment denied -- questions of fact presented including whether automobile was left "unattended" and whether defendant was required to foresee what happened.

Section 1210 (subd. [a]) of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, effective July 1, 1958, provided that "No person driving or in charge of a motor vehicle shall permit it to stand unattended without first stopping the engine, locking the ignition, removing the key, and effectively setting the brake thereon and, when standing upon any grade, turning the front wheels to the curb or side of the highway." Defendant had double parked his automobile and remained inside awaiting a friend. When the friend came out of the building and did not see defendant, defendant got [***2] out on the right-hand side of his automobile and motioned to his friend, leaving the right-hand door of the car open. He was standing between the car and the car next to which he had double parked. At that time he was knocked forward by a stranger and, by the time he had recovered, his automobile was in motion going down the street. The unknown assailant jumped into the automobile and drove it down the road, running into and damaging several parked automobiles, one of which was plaintiff's. Plaintiff alleges defendant was negligent for having left his automobile unattended with the motor running in violation of the Vehicle and Traffic Law. A motion by plaintiff for summary judgment and a cross motion by defendant for a summary judgment are denied. The statute was enacted both as a safety measure and to prevent theft. A question is presented as to whether the automobile was allowed to stand "unattended". If it were so unattended, a finding might be made of negligence. On the other hand, if the presence of defendant under the circumstances did not deteriorate into lack of care or attention to the automobile, then the automobile stood "attended" within the meaning of the statute.  [***3] Questions of fact are presented, including the question whether defendant was required to foresee the possibility of what happened.

 

2484 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Cheektowaga v. Levitt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


22 Misc. 2d 163; 198 N.Y.S.2d 155; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3394



March 16, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner town board instituted a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act art. 78 to challenge respondent comptroller's denial of the board's request for an extension of a particular fire district. The comptroller filed a motion to dismiss the board's petition.


OVERVIEW: The town board initiated on its own motion a proceeding under N.Y. Town Law § 173 to extend a fire district. Pursuant to the authority vested in the comptroller by § 173, he denied permission for the proposed extension. The board thereafter commenced an action in the court to challenge such denial; however, the court dismissed the board's petition. It held that the proceeding was premature because there was no final order for the court to review until the board made and recorded an order required by § 173(4), which the board had failed to do.


OUTCOME: The court granted the comptroller's motion to dismiss the town board's petition.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- fire districts -- State Comptroller may refuse to allow extension of fire district (Town Law, § 173, subd. 4; N. Y. Const., art. V, § 1).

1. Subdivision 4 of section 173 of the Town Law, pursuant to which the State Comptroller may deny permission to a town board to extend a fire district, is constitutional (N. Y. Const., art. V, § 1).

2. A proceeding (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78) by a town board to review the Comptroller's denial cannot be commenced until the town board enters an order on such denial (Town Law, § 173, subd. 4); and this is so even where the town board originally resolved on its own initiative that the fire district should be extended (Town Law, § 173, subd. 2, par. [a], cls. [1], [3]).

3. Since section 173 of the Town Law does not require the Comptroller to hold a hearing, the proceeding to review his determination is not transferable to the Appellate Division (cf. Civ. Prac. Act, § 1296).

 

2485 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cohen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Queens County


22 Misc. 2d 722; 205 N.Y.S.2d 481; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3402



March 16, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the reasons stated, the defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment on all the grounds urged is in all respects denied. Order entered accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss his indictment for the crime of violating N.Y. Penal Law § 1141 in relation to his distribution of a magazine entitled "1958 Annual Sunshine and Health etc."


OVERVIEW: After defendant was arrested for a violation of § 1141, he sought a full preliminary hearing in the court of special sessions. Subsequently an information was filed, defendant's motion to dismiss was denied, and defendant obtained a certificate pursuant to N.Y. City Crim. Ct. Act § 31. When defendant was directed be prosecuted by indictment, the grand jury found the indictment, and defendant filed a motion to dismiss. The court denied the motion, holding that by applying for a jury trial pursuant to § 31, defendant subjected himself to whatever charges the grand jury found to be established by the proof. Moreover, the district attorney had the discretion in proceeding under either N.Y. Crim. Proc. Code § 22-a or under N.Y. Penal Law § 1141. Defendant's prosecution under § 1141 did not violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV on its face, as construed, or as applied. Although freedom of the press was a cherished constitutional guarantee, obscenity was not within the area of constitutionally protected speech. Further, prior decisions that found the magazine in issue not to be obscene did not apply to defendant's indictment because each issue was regarded as a separate publication.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- obscene periodical -- section 1141 of Penal Law is not unconstitutional restraint on publication of periodicals -- Post Office approval of publication does not bind District Attorney or Grand Jury -- United States Supreme Court's approval of 1955 issue of periodical does not adjudge purity of much more lascivious 1958 issue.

1. An information in the New York City Court of Special Sessions charged that defendant possessed an obscene magazine with intent to sell it (Penal Law, § 1141). He obtained a certificate and an order that the charge be prosecuted by indictment ( N. Y. City Crim. Cts. Act, § 31) and thus be tried by jury. A Grand Jury then handed up an indictment which properly charged more acts (under Penal Law, § 1141) than were originally charged in the information.

2. The indictment was properly signed by the assistant foreman of the Grand Jury (Code Crim. Pro., § 268).

3. A District Attorney need not first apply for an injunction (Code Crim. Pro., § 22-a) before prosecuting by action (Penal Law,  [***2] § 1141).

4. Section 1141 of the Penal Law, when applied to periodicals, does not in effect constitute a prior restraint on publication, in violation of the United States Constitution (14th Amdt.).

5. A letter from the United States Post Office Department stating that this 1958 issue of this magazine -- the issue for which this indictment was handed up -- is not obscene, does not bind this court; nor does a similar opinion, if any, of the District Attorney of a nearby county.

6. A decision of the United States Supreme Court that a 1955 issue of this magazine was not obscene is not res judicata or carte blanche for all subsequent issues of the magazine.

7. Moreover, this 1958 issue contains many more possibly obscene pictures than did the 1955 issue, and 10 of them are full-page in color. The dominant theme of this 1958 issue is such that a petit jury could legally find defendant guilty under section 1141 of the Penal Law.

8. The Grand Jury minutes show that the Grand Jury had sufficient legal evidence before it.

9. Accordingly, defendant's motion for an inspection of the Grand Jury minutes and a dismissal of the indictment is denied.

 

2486 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Loblaw, Inc. v. New York State Board of Pharmacy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


22 Misc. 2d 131; 202 N.Y.S.2d 711; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3462



March 7, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retailer and defendant state agencies moved for summary judgment in the retailer's declaratory judgment action to determine whether it had the right to sell aspirin tablets without first obtaining registration certificates from the state agencies.


OVERVIEW: The retailer operated many grocery stores in the state. Aspirin tablets were sold at these stores along with other over the counter medicines. After the state agencies required the retailer to obtain registration certificates to sell aspirin tablets, the retailed filed a declaratory judgment action to determine whether such registration was required. Both sides moved for summary judgment, and the court granted the retailer's motion. The court first determined that the aspirin at issue was a proprietary medicine which was excepted from the statutory registration requirement. The court then held that regulation of the sale of aspirin tablets was not a proper exercise of the state's police power because such regulation was not necessary for the protection of public health or welfare. The state could not, under the guise of protecting the public, arbitrarily interfere with private business or prohibit lawful occupations or impose unreasonable and unnecessary restrictions upon them.


OUTCOME: The court granted the retailer's motion for summary judgment in its declaratory judgment action to determine whether it was required to obtain registration certificates from the state agencies before selling aspirin tablets.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Drugs and druggists -- proprietary medicine -- Bayer Aspirin Tablets are proprietary medicine ( Education Law, § 6816, subd. 2, par. c), and plaintiff may sell them in its chain of supermarkets without holding registration certificates issued by Board of Pharmacy and through its unlicensed employees.

1. Plaintiff has the right to sell prepackaged Bayer Aspirin Tablets in its chain of supermarkets in the State of New York without holding registration certificates issued by the Board of Pharmacy and through its unlicensed employees.

2. Subdivision 2 (par. c) of section 6816 of the Education Law provides that article 137 of the Education Law shall not apply, except as to the labeling of poison and to adulterating, misbranding and substituting, "To the sale of proprietary medicines except those proprietary medicines which are poisonous, deleterious and/or habit-forming." Bayer Aspirin Tablets are a proprietary medicine within the provisions of subdivision 2 (par. c) of section 6816 of the Education Law.

3. The facts failed to show any such relation in the sale of Bayer Aspirin Tablets to the public health or welfare as would justify the exercise of the police power of the State [***2] in prohibiting the sale of the tablets in plaintiff's supermarkets and similar outlets.

4. It has not been shown that Congress intended to pre-empt the field relating to the retail sale of drugs and proprietary medicines in the several States.

 

2487 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re City of New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


23 Misc. 2d 690; 199 N.Y.S.2d 225; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3508



February 27, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is denied in all respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant filed a motion for an order directing reconsideration and setting aside of the court's decision awarding an amount of damages to the claimant for respondent city's land taking; the taking of additional testimony; and the rendering of a new decision on the grounds that the said decision was contrary to the law and the evidence.


OVERVIEW: The claimant's land was taken by the city as part of a redevelopment program. As part of the redevelopment program, the city first took land adjacent to the land of the claimant and several months later took the claimant's land. The claimant's expert witness testified that the value of the property increased as a result of the taking of the adjacent property and the proposed redevelopment. The claimant contended that the court should have considered the impact of the first taking on the value of the claimant's property in awarding damages and sought for reconsideration of the court's decision. The claimant also requested that the court take additional testimony and that it render a new decision. The court denied the claimant's motion because the expert's testimony as to the impact of the first taking on the value of the claimant's property was speculative where there was no guarantee that his property would be taken or that the redevelopment program would be completed. The court also determined that the claimant was not entitled to have the court take additional testimony where claimant should have been aware of such evidence at the time of the original hearing.


OUTCOME: The court denied the claimant's motion to reconsider its judgment and set aside its previous award of damages to the claimant for the city's taking of his property for a redevelopment program. The court also denied the motion as to the taking of additional testimony and confirmed its decision based on the law and the evidence.


HEADNOTES

Trial -- new trial -- condemnation claimant cannot, after long trial, reopen case for evidence which will not change decision.

This condemnation proceeding, involving 532 damage parcels and innumerable fixture claims, has occupied the court for over a year. The trial of the instant claim, involving 7 of the damage parcels, took 6 days. Voluminous briefs were submitted. A careful and detailed opinion was handed down and decision rendered. This motion by the claimants for a reconsideration of the testimony and the law and for the taking of additional testimony is denied. The law was not misunderstood. As for the testimony, a defeated litigant cannot get a second trial in order to introduce testimony which could have been presented at the first trial and which, in any event, would not change the result.

 

2488 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Schultz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Kings County


23 Misc. 2d 620; 198 N.Y.S.2d 814; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3518



February 26, 1960 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury found defendant guilty of burglary in the second degree, he was sentenced as a 12th-felony offender based on prior convictions outside the state. Defendant petitioned for resentence on the ground that he was not a fourth felony offender under N.Y. Penal Law § 1942 and that the statute was unconstitutional when an adjudication under that section was based on "foreign" convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary and sentenced as a fourth felony offender. Defendant had been charged with 12 prior convictions outside of the state, and defendant was resentenced as a 12-felony offender. Defendant sought resentencing on the grounds that he was not a fourth-felony offender under N.Y. Penal Law § 1942 and that § 1942 was unconstitutional. The court reviewed 12 charges against defendant and determined that three of the crimes should not have been counted because they either would not have been felonies in New York or they had been withdrawn. The court found that nine of the foreign crimes would have counted as felonies, and the court ruled that defendant was sentenced as a ninth felony offender. The court rejected defendant's constitutional claim.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's petition for resentencing.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- sentence -- prior felony offender -- Penal Law ( § 1942) is constitutional -- prior convictions in Kansas, Texas and Massachusetts, for burglary, larceny, and breaking and entering with intent to commit felony, were for crimes which would be felonies if committed in New York.

1. Section 1942 of the Penal Law, requiring increased punishment of a defendant who is four times convicted, either in this State or in any other State or nation, of felonies in New York or of crimes in other States or nations which would be felonies if committed in New York, is constitutional.

2. Defendant was convicted in New York State of the felony of burglary, second degree, and was sentenced, as being at least a fourth felony offender, under section 1942 of the Penal Law. The court found that this defendant, who was charged with 12 prior out-of-State felony convictions, had been thus convicted previously, at least 8 times, in other States -- Kansas, Texas, and Massachusetts -- of crimes which, if committed in this State, would be felonies. In so finding, the court examined the statutes of those States defining the crimes for which defendant was convicted, and examined the operative allegations [***2] and findings of the indictments or informations and judgments under such of those statutes as disjunctively defined both a felony and a misdemeanor ( People v. Olah, 300 N. Y. 96, and People ex rel. Gold v. Jackson, 5 N Y 2d 243, followed). The court thus counted as prior felony convictions 1 burglary conviction in Kansas, 1 burglary conviction in Texas, 1 larceny conviction in Massachusetts, and 5 convictions in Massachusetts of breaking and entering in the daytime with intent to commit a felony. The court concluded that, even if the court were to count as only one conviction those of the out-of-State convictions which were rendered at the same time on defendant's pleas of guilty, there would still be 4 out-of-State felony convictions prior to defendant's fifth felony conviction, the one in New York State.

 

2489 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kenneweg


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


District Court of New York, Nassau County


28 Misc. 2d 999; 220 N.Y.S.2d 877; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3594



February 17, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Support Proceeding. (See, now, L. 1960, ch. 770, eff. April 21, 1960.)



DISPOSITION: The information is dismissed for lack of jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a proceeding under N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 899(1), against defendant for neglecting to provide for his wife and child according to his means. The court, on its own motion, took the question of jurisdiction under consideration.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a proceeding against defendant under § 899(1), alleging that defendant neglected to provide support for his wife and child. The proceeding came on for trial, and the court ordered defendant to pay a weekly sum. A bond was required and the matter adjourned to give defendant an opportunity to furnish the bond. The court, on its own motion, considered the question of jurisdiction. The court dismissed the proceeding for a lack of jurisdiction. The court held that pursuant to § 30 of the Children's Court Act, the Children's Court of Nassau County had exclusive jurisdiction of support proceedings. The court also pointed out that § 234 of the Nassau District Court Act expressly provided that nothing in that Act was to be construed to confer upon the court jurisdiction of proceedings of which the Children's Court had jurisdiction. In addition, the court held that exclusive jurisdiction of matters pertaining to spousal support was vested in the Domestic Relations Court.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the information for a lack of jurisdiction.


HEADNOTES

Nassau County District Court -- support proceedings -- court, when first established, did not have jurisdiction of support proceedings.

The Nassau County District Court Act, as first enacted (L. 1939, chs. 274, 718, 719, 720), did not give the court jurisdiction of support proceedings.

 

2490 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. East


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Wayne County


23 Misc. 2d 529; 206 N.Y.S.2d 963; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3611



February 15, 1960 



DISPOSITION: Therefore, the judgment of the Justice Court of the Town of Williamson as a Court of Special Sessions convicting the defendant, Donald East, is hereby reversed and the fine may be remitted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Court of Special Sessions of the Town of Williamson, Wayne County (New York), a judgment convicting defendant of a traffic infraction, N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law art. 14, § 1124, which covered driving over the center line.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that his conviction for improperly passing over the center line was in error because the statute was unconstitutional as being too vague and indefinite to constitute a sufficient definition of criminal conduct, and contained no sufficient standard whereby such conduct could be tested. Defendant also argued that the prosecution failed to prove his guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The court reversed defendant's conviction. Section 1124 was unconstitutional because it was not clear, concise, and positive enough to give a definite and unequivocal definition from which either a citizen or the police could have any criteria on which to base what the law required. As for the evidentiary challenge, the court held that the evidence adduced by the prosecution was insufficient under the vague wording of the statute to sustain a conviction. The testimony was conflicting and confusing as to distances and speed. There was insufficient evidence to show incomplete or complete passing; sufficiency or insufficiency of distance; clear visibility; and interference or noninterference with safe operation. Those were questions of fact, not conjecture or surmise.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and held that the fine could be remitted to him.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- overtaking or passing vehicle -- section 1124 of Vehicle and Traffic Law prohibiting overtaking or passing vehicle unless left side of road is clearly visible and free of oncoming traffic is unconstitutional since not clear, concise and positive enough to give unequivocal definition of act prohibited.

1. Section 1124 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law which provides that "No vehicle shall be driven to the left side of the center of the roadway in overtaking and passing another vehicle proceeding in the same direction unless such left side is clearly visible and is free of oncoming traffic for a sufficient distance ahead to permit such overtaking and passing to be completely made without interfering with the safe operation of any vehicle approaching from the opposite direction or any vehicle overtaken" is unconstitutional [***2] since it is not clear, concise and positive enough to give a definite and unequivocal definition of the act prohibited.

2. Moreover, the evidence was insufficient under the vague wording of the statute to sustain a conviction.

 

2491 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Roosevelt Raceway, Inc. v. Monaghan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


22 Misc. 2d 776; 199 N.Y.S.2d 195; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3613



February 15, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Application granted. Settle order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78, petitioner corporation sought to compel respondent New York Harness Racing Commission to reimburse federal income taxes as required by § 45-a(10) of the Pari-Mutuel Revenue Law (Revenue Law) (amend. 1959), notwithstanding ch. 8, § 7 of the Laws of 1959, which had deleted the federal income tax credit.


OVERVIEW: Upon finishing improvements to its horse racing track, the corporation sought reimbursement for federal income taxes, pursuant to § 45-a(10) of the Revenue Law (amend. 1959). After the Commission refused to reimburse the taxes, the corporation sought review. However, while the appeal was pending, the legislature passed ch. 8, § 7 of the Laws of 1959, which deleted the federal income tax credit. In reversing, the court held that the Revenue Law had been completely free from ambiguity and that the Commission had acted as if there was no reference in the Revenue Law to include taxes. Moreover, the court held that because the Revenue Law had been so clearly opposite of the 1959 amendment, the 1959 amendment could not be given effect retroactively. The court held that because the legislature had intended to give credit for federal income taxes under the Revenue Law, the 1959 amendment could not change the Revenue Law's intent. Finally, the court held that because the state had granted the corporation a statutory privilege and the corporation had relied on this privilege, a contract had been created, the obligation of which could not be impaired by subsequent legislation.


OUTCOME: The court ordered the Commission to reimburse the corporation for federal income taxes as required by the Revenue Law.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- impairment of statutory contract -- statute pursuant to which race track corporation spent large sum on capital improvement, from which State would derive revenues, cannot be amended so as to repeal statutory promise to permit corporation to reimburse itself, out of its income, not only for cost of improvement, but for Federal income taxes which corporation will pay on such part of income.

1. The Pari-Mutuel Revenue Law (L. 1940, ch. 254, as amd.) was further amended (L. 1956, ch. 837) so as to add a section 45-a whereby harness race track corporations would be induced to make large capital improvements which would increase attendance and thereby increase the State's revenues. The inducement offered to said corporations was that they could deposit income in special "construction accounts" and that the State Harness Racing Commission would authorize them to repay, out of such special accounts, not only the cost of such an improvement but to reimburse themselves for Federal income taxes which they had paid on such income (§ 45-a, subd. 10). These statutory provisions were clear and unambiguous; and when petitioner [***2] corporation, in reliance thereon, spent $ 19,517,469.92 for a capital improvement authorized by the commission, and then deposited income in such a special account, a contract was created with the State which the Legislature could not constitutionally, subsequently impair.

2. Accordingly, when the commission authorized petitioner to withdraw $ 2,858,495.38 from the special account towards repayment of petitioner's expenditure of $ 19,517,469.92, the commission became obligated further to authorize petitioner to reimburse itself out of said special account for $ 1,404,664.63 which petitioner paid to the United States as income tax on said $ 2,858,495.38.

3. When the commission refused, petitioner commenced this proceeding (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78). While this proceeding was pending, the Legislature (L. 1959, ch. 881) purported to amend said subdivision 10 of section 45-a, by stating its "intent * * * to clarify what was its intent" and so as to delete the provision for Federal income tax reimbursement and so as to state expressly that no such tax payments shall be reimbursed, "whether paid before or after the effective date of this section." Such a statute cannot constitutionally,  [***3] retroactively apply to this duly authorized and completed $ 19,517,469.92 capital improvement.

4. The commission is ordered (1) to correct its records and its reports to the Secretary of State so as to credit the balance due petitioner with said $ 1,404,664.63, and (2) in future to credit the balances due petitioner with any and all Federal income taxes paid or hereafter paid by petitioner on any sums which are hereafter transferred from petitioner's construction account to petitioner's general funds.

 

2492 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Lincoln Bldg. Associates v. Jame


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Municipal Court of the City of New York, Borough of Manhattan


21 Misc. 2d 500; 196 N.Y.S.2d 241; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3646



February 8, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Final order awarded in favor of the tenant dismissing the petition on the merits.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlord sued defendant tenant, alleging the tenant was holding over after the expiration of his term and seeking to recover possession of the office occupied by the tenant. The landlord did not allege any statutory grounds for the removal of the tenant. The tenant was protected by the Business Rent Law, 1945 N.Y. Laws ch. 314, as amended by 1959 N.Y. Laws ch. 809, § 4. The landlord challenged the constitutionality of this law.


OVERVIEW: In 1955, the court of appeals upheld the constitutionality of this law in a case involving the same parties. The landlord argued that conditions had changed since that date to such an extent that there was now a free market in office space. Thus, it argued there was no longer a rational basis for the law. The court held the landlord had failed to sustain its burden of showing that the law was unconstitutional. The evidence offered at trial did not establish the change in conditions claimed by the landlord. Further, the landlord ignored the fact that the statute under attack was not the same as the legislation in effect in 1955. In each year, commencing with the 1956 extension of the act, amendments were inserted permitting landlords to decontrol space by offering two-year leases to statutory tenants, upon the expiration of which time the space occupied by such tenants would be decontrolled. If the tenant refused or failed to sign such lease his space became decontrolled within six months. These amendments plainly indicated a desire to end this emergency legislation gradually and without disrupting the economy of the state.


OUTCOME: The court found in favor of the tenant and dismissed the petition on the merits.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and tenant -- rent regulation -- Business Rent Law (L. 1945, ch. 314, as amd.) not unconstitutional.

The Business Rent Law (L. 1945, ch. 314, as amd.) is not unconstitutional. Accordingly, the petition in a proceeding by landlord to recover possession of an office occupied by a tenant who is concededly protected by Business Rent Law is dismissed, where the landlord does not allege any statutory grounds for the removal, but challenges the constitutionality of the Business Rent Law.

 

2493 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Fopeano v. Murdock


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


22 Misc. 2d 426; 198 N.Y.S.2d 377; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3663



February 4, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Therefore the motion to vacate the order of certiorari and to dismiss the petition is granted. Settle order on notice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner abutting property owners filed a certiorari proceeding for review of a determination of respondent Board of Standards and Appeals of the City of New York (New York), which granted intervenor property owner a use variation of the zoning regulations permitting a gas station in a business area. The board and property owner filed motions to vacate the order of certiorari, to dismiss the petition, and to affirm the Board's determination.


OVERVIEW: The property owner filed an application for a variance in the zoning regulations for permission to erect a gas station in a business area. The abutting property owners filed objections. After public hearings and inspections by the Board's committees of the site and the neighborhood, the application was granted for a period of 15 years, subject to certain conditions and safeguards. The abutting property owners filed a certiorari proceeding for review of the Board's determination. The Board and the property owner filed motions to vacate the order of certiorari, to dismiss the petition, and to affirm the Board's determination, which were granted. The court held that although a similar application had been denied five years earlier, the progressive change in the business area towards industrial use constituted new facts that increased the need for additional gas stations due to the increased traffic. Such changed property conditions were sufficient and proper for the Board to reconsider and change its prior determination. The court held that the Board could act on its own knowledge of the area and properly rejected the abutting property owners' proof of depreciation of property values.


OUTCOME: The court granted the Board's and the property owner's motions to vacate the order of certiorari and to dismiss the abutting property owners' petition.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- proceeding to review action of New York City Board of Standards and Appeals in permitting erection of gasoline station in business use district is dismissed.

1. The Board of Standards and Appeals of the City of New York granted a use district variation of the city's zoning regulations to permit erection of a gasoline station in a "business" use district. A similar application had been denied over five years before. Meanwhile, the neighborhood has been undergoing a change from business use to industrial. Such changed property conditions formed a sufficient basis upon which the board could reconsider and, if satisfied, change its prior determination.

2. In view of their special training and experience, the members of the board were justified in rejecting proof as to depreciation of values of surrounding properties and deciding the matter on personal knowledge of the pertinent locale.

3. As the board acted upon a reasonable basis and on sufficient evidence to permit the exercise of its discretionary powers under section [***2] 7 of the zoning resolution, this review proceeding is dismissed and the board's determination is affirmed.

 

2494 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cecconi


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Justices' Court of New York, Town of Schuyler, Herkimer County


23 Misc. 2d 164; 206 N.Y.S.2d 931; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3661



February 4, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The defendant's motion is granted, the charge dismissed, and the bail heretofore posted is returned.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with a violation of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1129a, which provided that a driver of a motor vehicle was not to follow another vehicle more closely than was reasonable and prudent. Defendant renewed his motion to dismiss the charge on the ground that § 1129a was unconstitutionally vague and uncertain.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving behind a police officer's vehicle on an icy and snow-covered road when the officer was required to stop for a school bus. The officer observed that defendant's vehicle was coming up behind him at a rate of speed that would not permit a safe stop and pulled to the side of the road to give defendant additional braking distance. Defendant was charged with a violation of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1129a, which was not a criminal offense but to which the rules of criminal law applied pursuant to N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1800. The court held that the failure to observe ordinary care was too uncertain and indefinite to subject an offender to criminal liability as well as civil liability. The court held that, for N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1129a to create criminal liability, it should be possible to ascertain the standard of conduct required prior to any consequences. Because that was not possible, the statute did not give the requisite unequivocal warning of the rule to be obeyed.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion and dismissed the charge.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- following another vehicle too closely -- prohibition against following other vehicle more closely than is "reasonable and prudent," taking into consideration speed, traffic, and highway condition, is too uncertain and indefinite, and, therefore, unconstitutional (Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 1129, subd. [a]).

As violation of section 1129 (subd. [a]) of the Vehicle and Traffic Law is a traffic infraction, to which the rules of criminal law apply, the language of the statute should be sufficiently definite to give unequivocal warning of the rule which is to be obeyed. The provision that "The driver of a motor vehicle shall not follow another vehicle more closely than is reasonable and prudent, having due regard for the speed of such vehicles and the traffic upon and the condition of the highway", is too uncertain and indefinite to subject offenders to criminal liability. Consequently, defendant's motion for dismissal of a charge against him of violating said statute, on the ground that it is unconstitutional by reason of vagueness and uncertainty, is [***2] granted.

People v. Schenkman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Special Sessions of the City of New York, New York County


20 Misc. 2d 1093; 195 N.Y.S.2d 570; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3739



January 25, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motions made by each of the defendants at the conclusion of the entire case, to dismiss the informations on the ground that the defendants' guilt has not been established beyond a reasonable doubt, are denied, and each defendant is found guilty as charged in the informations.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, who were each charged with violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 1141, filed motions to dismiss the informations on the ground that their guilt was not established beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with a violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 1141, because one of them had in his possession certain books with intent to sell, and four of them did sell certain books that were alleged to be obscene. Defendants each rested at the end of the State's case. On their motions to dismiss the information, they urged that the books were not obscene under § 1141. In the alternative, they could not be convicted for the reason that the State failed to establish scienter on their part. The court denied defendants' motions and held that no other conclusion could be reached but that each of the books was obscene. The court stated that the books had no place in literature and were not entitled to the protection that the First Amendment of the United States Constitution afforded to works of literary distinction or to the classics. Judged by contemporary community standards, the court held that each of the books was obscene under § 1141. The court found that the testimony of the police officers as to the conversations they had with defendants, furnished proof of knowledge by defendants.The court concluded that the State proved beyond a reasonable doubt the guilt of defendants.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motions made by each defendant and each defendant was found guilty as charged in the informations.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- obscene books -- short, obscene, blurbed, paper-covered books at $ 5 each must have been known by booksellers to be obscene; booksellers convicted (Penal Law, § 1141).

Detectives purchased, at four bookstores owned or managed by the five defendants, six paper-covered books, one having only 60 pages, two having only 94 pages, and three having 176 pages, at $ 5 a book or two books for $ 9. On the back cover of each book was printed a blurb extolling its "orgy" or similar excitement. The books were obscene; and professional, experienced booksellers must have known that such lewdly blurbed, overpriced, paper-bound books were obscene; and the testimonies of the detectives as to their brief conversations with the defendants show defendants' scienter. Four of the defendants are convicted of selling obscene books; and the fifth defendant is convicted of possessing obscene [***2] books with intent to sell them (Penal Law, § 1141).

Glaser v. Larkin


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


21 Misc. 2d 379; 198 N.Y.S.2d 257; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3757



January 20, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition is dismissed. Submit order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant brought an action pursuant to N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act art. 78 against respondents, the Town Board of the Town of Hempstead and others, to review an adverse determination made by the board after he requested certain permits to install gasoline storage tanks and to use his premises as a gasoline filling station as a special exception under Hempstead, N.Y. Building Zone Ordinance §§ X-1.0 and 1.9.


OVERVIEW: The applicant's property was in a business district but in an area that was predominantly residential. He requested permits to install gasoline storage and waste oil tanks and to use his premises as a gasoline filling station as a special exception under §§ X-1.0 and 1.9. A public hearing was held, but the application for the permits was denied on the ground that the installation and maintenance of the tanks would cause too great a concentration of flammable materials in a small area surrounded by residential structures, and it would be too dangerous to the public safety. The applicant filed an Article 78 proceeding for review. The court dismissed the petition, holding that the burden was on the applicant to establish that the board's action was unconstitutional because it was not justified by any reasonable interpretation of fact, but he did not sustain that burden. The fact that the highest use to which the property could be put was a gasoline filling station was insufficient to overcome the presumption in favor of constitutionality of the action because due process did not require legislative bodies to permit the highest financial use of property.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the applicant's petition.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- petition for review of Town Board's denial of application to permit installation of gasoline storage tanks and use of premises in business district in predominantly residential area as gasoline filling station, denied -- refusal to make special exception on ground that granting application would be dangerous to public safety was legislative action -- burden of showing such action was not justified rested on petitioner, who has failed to sustain that burden.

A proceeding to review the Town Board's denial of an application to permit installation of gasoline storage tanks and use of premises in a business district located in a predominantly residential area as a gasoline filling station as a special exception under the town's Building Zone Ordinance, is dismissed. Despite testimony of a real estate and fire insurance expert to the contrary, the board determined that the granting of the application would be dangerous to the public safety. Refusal to make a special exception was legislative action and the burden of showing that such action was not justified by any reasonable interpretation of the [***2] facts rested upon the petitioner. He has not sustained that burden.

People ex rel. Rothblatt v. Kross


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Bronx County


21 Misc. 2d 941; 198 N.Y.S.2d 149; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3777



January 18, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The writ is therefore dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The relator sought a writ in his action challenging the jurisdiction of the Bronx County Court (New York) pursuant to N.Y. City Crim. Ct. Act § 31(1). He contended that he was illegally detained under a void judgment of conviction rendered by the county court. The relator plead guilty to the misdemeanor violation of knowingly possessing or having under his control any illicit alcoholic beverages under N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law § 151.


OVERVIEW: The relator was indicted for unlawfully manufacturing an illicit alcoholic beverage, defined in N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law § 153 as a felony and later was permitted to plead guilty to a violation of § 151, a misdemeanor. He later claimed that the court lacked jurisdiction since the crime, being a misdemeanor committed in the City of New York, had to be tried in the Court of Special Sessions pursuant to N.Y. City Crim. Ct. Act § 31(1). The court stated that N.Y. Crim. Proc. Code §§ 444, 445 provided that a defendant could be found guilty of a crime of any degree inferior to or necessarily included in the crime charged in the indictment. The court held that the misdemeanor charge of possession and control of illicit beverages was clearly embraced within the former felony charge of unlawful manufacture of an illicit alcoholic beverage.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the relator's writ.


HEADNOTES

Courts -- jurisdiction -- County Court -- relator, indicted for unlawfully manufacturing illicit alcoholic beverage (Alcoholic Beverage Control Law, § 153), was permitted to plead guilty in County Court to knowingly possessing illicit alcoholic beverages (Alcoholic Beverage Control Law, § 151) -- County Court had jurisdiction.

Relator was indicted for "unlawfully manufacturing an illicit alcoholic beverage * * * not being then a licensed distiller", and owning, operating and possessing a still and other distilling apparatus not lawfully registered pursuant to Federal law (Alcoholic Beverage Control Law, § 153). The crime charged was a felony. He was permitted to plead guilty in County Court to a violation of section 151 of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law, a misdemeanor -- "knowingly possess or have under his control any illicit alcoholic beverages". Relator argues that the court lacked jurisdiction since the crime, a misdemeanor committed in the City of New York, must be tried in the Court of Special Sessions ( New York City Crim. Cts. Act, § 31, subd. 1). In this present case two related offenses were set forth in the same act,  [***2] one denominated a felony and the other a misdemeanor. "Possession and control of illicit beverages" under the latter clearly are embraced within the former charging "unlawful manufacture of an illicit alcoholic beverage." The County Court was not without jurisdiction and the writ of habeas corpus is dismissed.

Minkin v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


24 Misc. 2d 818; 198 N.Y.S.2d 744; 1960 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3848



January 7, 1960 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The cross motions of all defendants are granted. Settle order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sought an injunction precluding defendants, corporation counsel, city, and corporation, from going forward with eminent domain proceedings. Defendants filed motions to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The landowners brought an action against defendants for an injunction precluding the latter from going forward with planned eminent domain proceedings. The landowners claimed that defendants sought to take their land for an unconstitutional use. Defendants filed motions to dismiss the action, which the court granted. The court held that the fact that the property to be taken would have been used by defendants to benefit a middle income group, rather than a low-income group, did not make the taking unconstitutional. The court found that the state constitution and the statutes authorized defendants to take property for the purpose of building affordable housing for groups that were found to be unable to afford existing or planned private housing. Those provisions, the court said, did not define the income levels of persons eligible for such housing and left the definition open. The court found that, in this instance, the project attacked by the landowners was designed for those who had been found by the appropriate public agency to be persons falling within the legislative definition of persons of low income. Therefore, the court said, the taking fell within constitutional mandates.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motions to dismiss the landowners' motion for an injunction precluding defendants from going forward with eminent domain proceedings.


HEADNOTES

Public housing -- middle-income housing -- action to enjoin proposed condemnation for purpose of housing for middle-income families, dismissed (N. Y. Const., art. XVIII; Public Housing Law, art. 12).

Complaint of owners of vacant land in an area which is not slum or substandard or insanitary, seeking to enjoin, as unconstitutional, a proposed condemnation of their land for the projected purpose of having a limited profit housing corporation erect thereon co-operative apartments of 2 1/2 rooms to 6 1/2 rooms to be occupied by middle-income families who earn approximately $ 7,000 a year and who are to pay approximately $ 500 a room plus a maintenance charge of approximately $ 21 a room, is dismissed. (N. Y. Const., art. XVIII, §§ 1, 2, 10; Public Housing Law, § 3, subds. 18, 23; §§ 302, 318, subd. 2.)
