Lipschitz v. Doe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


19 Misc. 2d 1093; 193 N.Y.S.2d 950; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2706



November 3, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner voter filed an action against respondent, a board of election inspectors, seeking an order permitting her to vote on election day.


OVERVIEW: The voter went to the same polling place where she had voted the previous year. The board told the voter that she was not permitted to vote because her name was not on the list and that she had to get a court order before it would permit her to vote. The court held that the voter was entitled to vote in the election because there were no valid objections to her request. The court also held that the voter was not required to pay the fees set forth in N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act § 1557-a(III). The court held that N.Y. Const. art. II, § 1 did not contemplate that the right to vote could be obstructed by any financial hurdles.


OUTCOME: The court signed the order allowing the voter to vote and waived the fees associated with her action.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Elections -- right to vote -- no valid objection shown to right of petitioner to vote in election -- not required to pay fee to initiate proceeding or obtain certified copy of order in attempting to exercise right to vote.

1. From the evidence adduced petitioner is entitled to vote at the election since no valid objections appear to deprive her of that right.

2. Where one applies to the court to be allowed to exercise his constitutional right to vote, there should be no fee charged in order to initiate the proceeding or to obtain a certified copy of an order. If section 1557-a of the Civil Practice Act were interpreted as requiring a fee, the statute would be unconstitutional.

 

2512 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Winter v. Guenther


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


24 Misc. 2d 537; 192 N.Y.S.2d 892; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2720



November 2, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Proceedings dismissed upon the merits, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowner sought review, by initiating a proceeding under N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act art. 78, of a decision by respondents, members of the Town Board of the Town of Eden, which denied the landowner's application to have his property rezoned and for permission to erect a business sign.


OVERVIEW: The landowner owned a farm where his son incidentally sold and repaired farm equipment for almost 20 years. The landowner applied to the town to have his property rezoned for business use and for permission to erect a business sign, and the town denied both of his applications on the basis that the landowner's property was in an agricultural district and his request was for spot zoning to business in an area that was destined to become residential pursuant to a master plan for future development. The landowner appealed and claimed that the zoning ordinance that prohibited non-conforming uses was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court dismissed the landowner's petition. The court found that the landowner improperly placed the burden on the town to prove that the zoning ordinance was published and posted in accordance with the law because the landowner, as the petitioner in a proceeding under article 78, had the burden of proving that the ordinance was not justified under the police power of the state. The court found that the landowner's incidental sale of used farm equipment did not justify spot zoning and the commercial sign was prohibited by the valid ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the landowner's petition, without costs, and found that the town's refusals to rezone and to issue a permit to the landowner were proper.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- as question of constitutionality of Town Zoning Ordinance could not be determined by Town Board, Supreme Court had jurisdiction of entire controversy -- refusals of Town Board to rezone petitioner's property from agricultural to business district, and issue permit for public sign thereon, were proper -- petitioner failed to prove that enforcement of ordinance would preclude him from using premises for any purpose to which reasonably adapted -- incidental sale of used farm equipment does not justify spot zoning from agricultural to business -- commercial sign in agricultural district prohibited by valid ordinance.

1. Petitioner seeks to rezone a portion of his property from an agricultural to a business district, and contends that the section of the Town Zoning Ordinance entitled "Farmland or Agricultural Districts" is unconstitutional. As the question of constitutionality cannot be determined by the Town Board, the Supreme Court has jurisdiction of the entire controversy, despite the fact that petitioner claims a valid, nonconforming use.

2. The town had the right to enact a zoning [***2] ordinance, which is presumed to be constitutional. Unless the petitioner is affected by the alleged unconstitutionality of the statute in a specific way, he cannot complain.

3. Petitioner has failed to sustain his burden of proof by showing that enforcement of the ordinance will preclude him from using his property for any purpose to which it is reasonably adapted. Farming is still conducted on his premises as a primary function. The incidental sale of used farm equipment does not justify spot zoning from agricultural to business so as to allow petitioner to conduct a new business selling new farm equipment after enactment of the ordinance.

4. The commercial sign for which petitioner seeks a permit is prohibited by the valid ordinance.

5. Respondents' refusals to rezone the property and issue a permit for the sign were proper.

6. Overlooking petitioner's omission to serve a reply, as in an action, the court's conclusion remains the same.

7. The proceedings are dismissed on the merits.

 

2513 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Douglas


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, St. Lawrence County


21 Misc. 2d 551; 202 N.Y.S.2d 160; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2723



November 2, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were indicted pursuant to N.Y. Penal Law § 1141, which accused that defendants sold and distributed obscene, lewd, lascivious, filthy, indecent and disgusting magazines, which magazines were designed, composed, written and illustrated as a whole to appeal to prurient interest and to exploit the same commercially.


OVERVIEW: Defendants demurred to the indictment on the ground that the facts stated did not constitute a crime. The court dismissed the indictment, holding that N.Y. Penal Law § 1141 was contrary to the letter and spirit of the Fourteenth Amendment and N.Y. Const. art. I, § 8. The court determined that any test for obscenity that turned on what was offensive to the community's standards was too loose, too capricious, too destructive of freedom of expression to be squared with the First Amendment, and that every utterance which did not infringe upon another's person or property was protected by the First Amendment. The court further held that the expression did not need to have the slightest redeeming social importance in order to be protected. The court concluded that the defendants' publication was not obscene and could not be the basis for a criminal indictment.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the indictment.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- obscenity -- subdivision 1 of section 1141 of Penal Law, under which defendants were indicted on charge that they sold obscene magazines, is unconstitutional -- indictment dismissed.

Subdivision 1 of section 1141 of the Penal Law, under which defendants were indicted on a charge that they "sold and distributed obscene, lewd, lascivious, filthy, indecent and disgusting magazines, which magazines were designed, composed, written and illustrated as a whole to appeal to prurient interest and to exploit the same commercially", is contrary to the letter and spirit of the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution and section 8 of article I of the New York State Constitution, and the indictment should be dismissed.

 

2514 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Saso v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Westchester County


20 Misc. 2d 826; 194 N.Y.S.2d 789; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2752



October 28, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state and state agency, filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff property owner's second amended complaint on various grounds. The property owner had filed an action for declaratory and injunctive relief against defendants, among others, that was related to the allegedly illegal appropriation of the property owner's lands pursuant to the exercise of defendants' eminent domain power.


OVERVIEW: The property owner filed an action against defendants, among others. The property owner had sought declaratory and injunctive relief related to the allegedly illegal appropriation of the property owner's lands pursuant to the exercise of defendants' eminent domain power. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss the property owner's second amended complaint. The court denied defendants' motion. The court held in part that: (1) defendants' motion to dismiss the property owner's complaint on the basis of legal insufficiency was without merit, as the ultimate facts alleged in the property owner's complaint presented a legally sufficient showing that the purported appropriation of the property owner's lands was for an unauthorized private use; and that (2) defendants' motion to dismiss the property owner's complaint on the basis of the court's lack of subject matter jurisdiction was without merit, as the court had subject matter jurisdiction over a claim of an alleged unauthorized and illegal appropriation of real property by defendants.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motion to dismiss the property owner's complaint seeking declaratory and injunctive relief related to the purportedly illegal appropriation of property.


HEADNOTES

Eminent domain -- action in Supreme Court to enjoin taking for private use -- property owner may sue in Supreme Court to enjoin State Thruway Authority from taking part of his land in order to provide private right of way for benefit of otherwise landlocked adjoining property owner and to accommodate defendant utility company's power lines for said defendant owner -- property owner's pending claim in Court of Claims is not another action pending for same cause; motion to dismiss this action denied.

1. An action for a declaratory judgment and injunction may be maintained in the Supreme Court by a property owner who alleges facts showing that defendant State of New York and defendant State Thruway Authority appropriated a strip of land which bisects plaintiff's property, not for any public or Thruway or Thruway access purpose, but only (1) to provide a means of access to and from another street, for the benefit of defendant owner of another adjoining property, which adjoining property would otherwise be landlocked by a prior Thruway appropriation, and (2) to [***2] accommodate electric power lines recently erected by defendant utility company to service said adjoining property owner. Motion to dismiss (Rules Civ. Prac., rule 106, subds. 1, 4) is denied.

2. Before commencing this action, plaintiff, in order to prevent the Statute of Limitations on an appropriation claim against the State from running out, filed a claim in the Court of Claims for damages for this appropriation; and he has prosecuted said claim to the point of submitting proposed findings of fact and conclusions of law to the Court of Claims. The Court of Claims would have no jurisdiction of an action such as this one in the Supreme Court for a declaratory judgment and injunction (Court of Claims Act, § 9); in any event, no such action is pending in that court. If defendants wish to assert that plaintiff has elected his remedy, that would constitute an affirmative defense, which cannot be the basis for this motion to dismiss on defendants' asserted ground that there is another action pending (Rules Civ. Prac., rule 107, subd. 3). Such motion to dismiss is denied.

3. This action is not barred by Statute of Limitations (Rules Civ. Prac., rule 107, subd. 5).

4. Said adjoining [***3] property owner and said utility company are proper or necessary or indispensable parties defendant to this action.

 

2515 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Application of Weinstein v. Burns


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


20 Misc. 2d 362; 198 N.Y.S.2d 76; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2845



October 15, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition is dismissed.

Submit order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner dentist, proceeding pursuant to N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act art. 78, requested review and annulment of a determination by respondent town board, which gave the dentist permission to use his former residential property as an office for the practice of dentistry but imposed certain conditions and limitations on his use.


OVERVIEW: The board granted the dentist's petition for a special exception and permitted him to use his former residence as a dentistry office on the condition that the premises could not be used for residential purposes by any persons other than the dentist himself together with his immediate family. The dentist contended that the board's condition, which prohibited him from renting the remaining portion of the premises to a tenant, was arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable. The court dismissed the dentist's petition upon finding that he failed to sustain his burden of proving that the zoning ordinance was unconstitutional. The town board had the right to deny the dentist's application, and, in having the right to deny, it also had the right to grant the application subject to reasonable conditions. The restriction regarding the limitation of the premises for use of office space only applied to areas of the office where patients would be interviewed or treated. Hence, the rest of the building could be used for other purposes, including purposes for the benefit, comfort, and convenience of the dentist and his staff.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the dentist's petition.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- petitioner was granted special exception to continue practice of dentistry at residence upon condition that premises be used for practice as dentist and not for residential purposes for any other person than applicant himself and immediate members of family -- no showing that Town Board was arbitrary, unreasonable or capricious -- having right to deny application, it had right to attach conditions.

The Town Board amended the zoning ordinance so as to permit a dentist who had resided at or conducted his practice from a residence for not less than two years to continue the practice of his profession therein, whether he continued to reside there or not, when permitted by the Town Board as a special exception after a public hearing and subject to such conditions as appeared appropriate. Petitioner applied for such special exception and was granted the request upon certain conditions, one of which was that the premises should be used for the practice as a dentist and not for residential purposes for any other person or persons than the applicant himself and the immediate members of his family. Petitioner [***2] has failed to sustain the burden of showing that the Town Board was arbitrary, unreasonable or capricious. It had the right to deny the application and, having that right, it had the right to grant the application subject to reasonable conditions.

 

2516 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re City of New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


22 Misc. 2d 609; 194 N.Y.S.2d 253; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2847



October 15, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the final decrees should recite claimants' application, as set forth in their moving papers, and provide that their application is denied, and that interest on the award is allowed at the rate of 4% per annum from February 28, 1958 to the date of payment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a condemnation proceeding, claimant property owners moved to incorporate in the final decree a provision for an allowance calculated on the basis of the court's finding of the respective annual net rental values of the several acquired premises prorated according to time, or, in the event such relief was denied, then interest at a rate of six percent.


OVERVIEW: The provision sought by the property owners was in lieu of interest on the awards at four percent annum from the date of taking to the date the awards were ready for payment, which was the usual provision in final decrees regarding condemnation proceedings. In determining that the property owners' request for relief should be rejected, the court noted that N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 3-a(2) required that interest on any accrued claim against a municipal corporation arising out of condemnation proceedings was not to exceed four percent per annum. There was no constitutional requirement that just compensation for delay in making payment had to be exactly equal to the fair rate of interest for the use of money in the open money market in New York City where money was borrowed without collateral and where the lender did not receive income tax benefit. Regardless of the fact that six percent was the "proper rate" of interest to be paid by a nonpublic debtor, the court held that the statutorily-mandated four percent rate was appropriate in the instant proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court directed that the final decree should recite claimants' application, as set forth in their moving papers, and provide that their application was denied, and that interest on the award was allowed at the rate of four percent per annum from the date of the taking to the date of payment.


HEADNOTES

Eminent domain -- compensation -- interest -- 4% interest rate on awards in condemnation proceedings, as provided in General Municipal Law, ( § 3-a, subd. 2), is not so unreasonably low as to deprive claimants of just compensation -- claimants' motion for allowance based on rental values of acquired premises, or 6% interest rate, denied -- Corporation Counsel's objection that motion is premature, overruled -- final decree should adjudicate on merits what proper interest rate is -- final decree should recite claimants' application, that it was denied, and that interest on awards is allowed at rate of 4% per annum from February 28, 1958 to date of payment.

1. Several claimants in this condemnation proceeding have moved to incorporate in the final decrees, in lieu of interest at 4% per annum from the date of taking to the date the awards are ready for payment, a provision for an allowance based on the court's [***2] finding of the respective annual net rental values of the acquired premises, or interest at the rate of 6% per annum. The rate of 4% provided for in the General Municipal Law ( § 3-a, subd. 2) is not so unreasonably low as to deprive the claimants of just compensation, although the General Business Law ( § 370) prescribes 6% as the maximum general rate, and even though 6% may be the fair rate for use of money in the open market in New York City. There is no constitutional requirement that just compensation for delay in making payment in condemnation proceedings must be exactly equal to such rate. The motion is, therefore, denied.

2. The Corporation Counsel's objection that the motion is premature and that after the final decree fixes the interest at 4% claimants may attempt to enforce payment of the higher rate by ways of a motion to compel the Comptroller to pay such higher rate, or by way of appeal from the final decree is overruled. Interest at a proper rate is an integral part of the compensation to which claimants are entitled and the final decree should adjudicate on the merits what such proper rate is. Claimants would then have an adjudication of unquestioned finality [***3] which they can carry to the Court of Appeals, if so advised, and if appeal is taken from the principal amount of any award, the proper rate of interest can be disposed of on the same appeal.

3. The final decree should recite claimants' application, that it was denied, and that interest on the award is allowed at the rate of 4% per annum from February 28, 1958 to the date of payment.

 

2517 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Application of Lome


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


19 Misc. 2d 803; 192 N.Y.S.2d 787; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2892



October 8, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the respondent's motion to dismiss the petition is granted, but without costs.

Submit order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent city tax commission filed an omnibus motion to dismiss a petition before answer. Petitioners, 53 presidents of various civic associations in Queens County, New York, sought to reduce certain real estate assessments for a certain year to the level of the prior year.


OVERVIEW: The relief sought by petitioners was to reduce to the 1958-1959 level the real estate assessments for the year 1959-1960 of the individual petitioners, of all those 32,000 property owners who filed protests against the current increase, and the 250,000 home owners and taxpayers of the Borough of Queens that were similarly situated. The ground for such relief was that the increase was erroneous, illegal, excessive, and unconstitutional. The court found that the named petitioners refered to nothing but a section, block, and lot number. Each appeared to be in widely separated, divergent, and various areas, streets, and locations. The court found that the averment as to inequality was a mere unsupported conclusion. No comparative properties or figures were set forth. The petitioners seemed to claim that increasing the assessment over the prior year was evidence of overvaluation. The court held that each year was separate and distinct from every other year. In no sense could the value fixed by the assessors for one year, or by a court on review, have any application to the issue of value in recurring assessments or proceedings to review them.


OUTCOME: The court granted the commission's motion to dismiss the petition, without costs.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- real estate assessments -- tax review proceeding by 53 presidents of civic associations in borough of Queens, on behalf of themselves and 32,000 protestees and 250,000 owners of one-family and two-family homes in Queens, alleging inequality of their current assessments as compared with homes in Manhattan and Brooklyn, is dismissed as legally insufficient.

A tax review proceeding (Tax Law, art. 13; New York City Charter, §§ 163-166; Administrative Code of City of New York, § 166-1.0) by 53 individuals, each "individually and as president of" as many civic associations in Queens County, "on behalf of themselves and on behalf of the 32,000 protestees who have filed their applications for the correction of the assessed valuations for the fiscal year 1959-1960" and whose applications have been denied, "and on behalf of the 250,000 owners of one and two family homes in * * * Queens * * * similarly situated", which proceeding is based on allegations (1) that it is physically impossible for the tax assessors to examine personally every house and lot in the borough [***2] and city, as required by the Administrative Code of the City of New York, and (2) that the tax assessors simply decided to increase the previous year's assessments of all one-family and two-family houses in the borough of Queens by $ 500,000,000, and (3) that one-family and two-family houses in the boroughs of Manhattan and Brooklyn are now thus assessed at an average of less than 50% of full value whereas those in Queens are assessed at more than 60% of full value, and (4) that Queens does not receive services from the city corresponding to its increased share of taxes, is dismissed by Special Term, on the ground that the allegations are merely general and are legally insufficient not only as to the "250,000 owners" and the "32,000 protestees" but also as to the 53 individuals.

 

2518 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Grossman v. Wagner


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


20 Misc. 2d 707; 192 N.Y.S.2d 557; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2902



October 7, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the reasons indicated, the cross motion to dismiss is denied, with leave to answer within 10 days from the service of a copy of this order, with notice of entry. The application made in the petition may not be disposed of until after the joinder of issue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent city officials filed a motion to dismiss a complaint brought by petitioner building owners in an action in which the building owners challenged a determination made by a city tax commission that denied their application for tax exemption and abatement.


OVERVIEW: The building owners filed an action pursuant to N.Y. Civ. Practice Act. art. 78, seeking to set aside a determination made by a city tax commission, which denied their application for tax exemption and abatement. Respondents filed a motion seeking dismissal of the petition. The court denied the motion to dismiss. The court properly brought the proceeding under Article 78 insofar as it sought tax abatement because there was no other statutory provision that afforded a remedy for a denial of tax abatement. The court held that an amendment to the tax laws, N.Y. Admin. Code § J41-2.4, was not unconstitutional where the prior tax exemption that had been accorded to the building owners was revocable because there was no evidence the city had entered into a irrevocable contract with the building owners. The court noted that statutes granting tax exemptions were revocable at the will of the legislature in the absence of a contract. The court determined the city could not be held to have contracted with those who altered and approved their dwellings in reliance upon the tax exemption because the exemption was not a private one, but instead was available to the general public.


OUTCOME: The court denied respondents' motion to dismiss, and granted leave to answer within 10 days from the service of a copy of the order.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- local laws -- requirement that "No local law shall be passed until it shall have been in its final form and upon the desks of the councilmen at least seven calendar days, exclusive of Sundays, prior to its final passage" (New York City Charter, § 37) was allegedly violated by passing on December 23 bill which was not in final form until December 17 -- but local law granting tax exemption and tax abatement (Administrative Code of City of New York, § J41-2.4) may be repealed or modified (Local Law No. 14 of 1959 of City of New York) even as to those who have spent money in reliance on it -- proceeding under article 78 of Civil Practice Act proper; landlords not relegated to remedies for reviewing assessments (Tax Law, § 290 et seq.; New York City Charter, §§ 163-166; Administrative Code of City of New York, § 166-1.0).

1. The New York City Charter (§ 37) provides, in part, that "No local [***2] law shall be passed until it shall have been in its final form and upon the desks of the councilmen at least seven calendar days, exclusive of Sundays, prior to its final passage". In this proceeding under article 78 of the Civil Practice Act, the petition sufficiently alleges that a local law bill was "for the first time" placed "in its final form" on the desks of the city councilmen on December 17, 1958 and was passed on December 23, 1958, and was therefore void. Even if both December 17 and December 23 are both included in the count to make seven days -- such a count seems to be contrary to section 20 of the General Construction Law -- one of the seven days would still be a Sunday. There is nothing in the petition to show that the bill was on the councilmen's desks in unprinted but final form before December 17. On this motion to dismiss the petition as legally insufficient, the petition must be deemed true and must be liberally construed. The motion is denied.

2. The petition of landlords alleges that they spent large sums to renovate their unsanitary and hazardous dwellings, in reliance on the local law provision for tax abatements and tax exemptions for such renovation [***3] (Administrative Code of City of New York, § J41-2.4), and that the city thereafter amended said local law (by Local Law No. 14 of 1959 of City of New York) so as to withdraw its benefits from rent-decontrolled or uncontrolled dwellings, and that the city's Tax Commission therefore refused to grant them a tax abatement or tax exemption. That part of the petition which alleges that the amendment violated contract rights and was unconstitutional is legally insufficient. Statutes granting tax exemption and similar statutes are, in the absence of a contract to continue the exemptions or other privileges granted, revocable at the legislative will; and this is so notwithstanding the fact that persons may have performed acts or expended money in reliance upon such statutes.

3. Petition for tax abatement, involving a question of law rather than one of fact, is properly brought under article 78 of the Civil Practice Act; and it is unnecessary to determine whether the proceeding is also maintainable, concurrently with the remedy formerly denominated certiorari, in order to obtain tax exemption. Petitioners are not relegated to the remedy provided in section 290 et seq. of the Tax Law,  [***4] sections 163-166 of the New York City Charter, and section 166-1.0 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York.

 

2519 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Scudder


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Police Court of New York, Village of Lloyd Harbor


21 Misc. 2d 614; 191 N.Y.S.2d 511; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2922



October 3, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police sought a determination as to whether defendants, landowner and landowner's lessees, had violated Village of Lloyd Harbor, N.Y., Ordinance 2, § 1, regulating parking, by allowing the landowner's lessees to leave automobiles in the vicinity of the landowner's residence while mooring boats on the landowner's property.


OVERVIEW: The landowner owned property bordered by a public street on one side, and a harbor on the other. The landowner operated a business in which he leased mooring rights to individuals seeking to launch boats on the harbor. The landowner and his lessees parked automobiles on the public street in front of the landowner's property. The village in which the landowner resided had enacted an ordinance prohibiting all parking on public streets. The police sought convictions against the landowner and the landowner's lessees for violation of the ordinance. The court convicted all defendants except one, who was a guest of the landowner. The court held that N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Code § 1640(a)(6) permitted the village to regulate parking on its streets and that the village had clearly and suitably marked the restrictions by placing general signs in the town. The court finally held that the mere fact that the landowner owned property abutting the street did not entitle him to more parking privileges than any other member of the public.


OUTCOME: The court convicted all but one defendant of violation of a village ordinance for parking on a street where parking was prohibited.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Motor vehicles -- parking -- defendants convicted of violating ordinance of Village of Lloyd Harbor which prohibits parking of automobiles on public streets except for transaction of business or visits with residents of village -- one defendant, visiting lessee of another defendant, acquitted.

1. Section 1 of Ordinance No. 2 of the Village of Lloyd Harbor provides: "No person shall leave any vehicle standing or parked, nor shall any person picnic or trespass upon any portion of the public streets, highways, roads, lanes or other public places in the Village of Lloyd Harbor, except such as may be necessary or incidental to the transaction of business with or visits to residents of the Village or such as may be due to accidental or temporary disability." One of the defendants, developing a business consisting of leasing moorings, charges owners of pleasure boats rental for the moorings. His patrons have been parking in an area within the public right of way. Some of the customers have parked at a place where the village had erected a fence in 1954 to enforce the village ordinance. The automobiles were parked within a 50-foot right of way, on which the paved portion was 16 [***2] feet wide, leaving an area 17 feet wide on each side of the pavement. A defense, common to all defendants that they did not park their automobiles on any part of the road that is "intended for vehicular traffic", is without merit under the revision of the Vehicle and Traffic Law made by chapter 698 of the Laws of 1957. The village is authorized by the State to prohibit, restrict or limit parking on all roads of the village and the village ordinance validly extends not only to parking on the travelled portion of such roads but also to "the entire width between the boundary lines" ( Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 118) of every such road.

2. Section 1683 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law provides that no ordinance limiting or prohibiting the stopping, standing or parking of vehicles shall be effective until signs giving notice thereof are posted. Signs measuring four feet by one foot are conspicuously posted at the side of each four roads entering the village. Additional signs are posted at points along the village roads, all saying that no parking is permitted at any time. Five signs are posted in the vicinity of defendant's residence. The posted signs are more than sufficient to give [***3] notice of the ordinance as required by section 1683.

3. In the absence of any evidence tending to establish that the ordinance is an unreasonable, arbitrary, capricious or discriminatory exercise of the power granted the village by section 1640 (subd. [a], par. 6) of the Vehicle and Traffic Law to prohibit, restrict or limit the parking of vehicles within the village, it cannot be maintained that the ordinance offends the due process clause. On the contrary the ordinance could have been enacted in the reasonable belief that it was necessary for the preservation of good order and public morals. Defendants, as members of the public, have no just complaint against the terms of the ordinance, and the individual defendant who leases the moorings has no special ground for complaint.

4. Said latter defendant is not entitled to the exception made in the ordinance for parking that is "necessary or incidental to the transaction of business with or visits to residents of the village". The other defendants were not visiting with him in the sense intended by the statute. Moreover, the defendants had completed their "transaction of business" when they entered into leases of their moorings [***4] and when they went to the premises they did not do so for the purpose of transacting business but of exercising their rights as lessees.

5. One of the defendants parked her automobile as an incident to a visit to two people who had leased premises from the lessor. She could reasonably assume that they were rightfully enjoying a portion of his rights. As a guest she is entitled to the same privileges that the parking ordinance would accord a guest of the lessor. She is, accordingly, found not guilty.

 

2520 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Bookbinder v. Hults


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


19 Misc. 2d 1062; 192 N.Y.S.2d 331; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2941



October 1, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] No right to the relief sought having been shown, the motion is denied and the petition is, accordingly, dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner driver filed a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding asking the court to restore his right to operate and register a motor vehicle in the State of New York after respondent Commissioner of Motor Vehicles of the State of New York had revoked his rights.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner revoked the driver's right to operate and register a motor vehicle in New York after the driver was involved in an accident while he did not have proper insurance coverage. On the day of the accident in New York the driver was a resident of Florida, had a Florida driver's license, and had automobile insurance with a Florida company. The insurance company was not licensed to do business in New York, and did not file a statement with the Commissioner consenting to services of process and declaring that its polices met the requirements of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law art. 6-A. The court denied the driver's petition, holding that art. 6-A did not violate the driver's equal protection rights because the law was enacted pursuant to the police power of New York, and had a real and substantial relation to protecting the citizens of New York from financially irresponsible drivers. N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 93-a(4)(c) was applicable to nonresidents as well as residents; therefore there was no inequality.


OUTCOME: The court denied the driver's petition.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- liability insurance -- financial security -- petitioner carried auto liability insurance with company licensed to do business in Florida but not licensed to do business in this State and which did not file with Commissioner of Motor Vehicles statement consenting to service of process and declaring that its policies should be deemed to comply with article 6-A of Vehicle and Traffic Law (Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 93-a, subd. 4, par. [c]) -- statute is proper exercise of police power of State -- statute providing that Commissioner shall revoke privilege to operate and register motor vehicle in absence of proof of financial security (Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 93-h, subd. 4, par. [a]) is clear, reasonable and understandable -- motion for order restoring petitioner's right to operate and register motor vehicle denied.

1. The Commissioner of Motor Vehicles revoked petitioner's right to operate and register a motor vehicle in this State because of his involvement in an accident in the operation of his automobile while he did not have proper [***2] insurance coverage. Petitioner's automobile was also registered in Florida and he carried auto liability insurance with a company licensed to do business in the State of Florida but not licensed to do business in the State of New York. The company did not file, in accord with section 93-a (subd. 4, par. [c]), with the Commissioner of Motor Vehicles a statement consenting to service of process and declaring that its policies shall be deemed to be varied to comply with the requirements of article 6-A of the Vehicle and Traffic Law. The statute has a real and substantial relation to the protection of the public and is a proper exercise of the police powers of the State. There is no discrimination against nonresidents. The statute puts nonresident owners upon an equality with resident owners.

2. Section 93-h (subd. 4, par. [a]) of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, which provides that the Commissioner, upon receipt of evidence that the owner of a motor vehicle not registered in this State has operated or permitted the operation of a motor vehicle while proof of financial security was not in effect, shall revoke the person's privilege to operate a motor vehicle and the privilege of [***3] the operator within the State of any motor vehicle owned by him, is clear, reasonable and understandable. Although the extent of the evidence is not set forth in the act it is presumed that it must be of substantial character sufficient to justify his action. Once he has this evidence he has no duty to hold a hearing or make findings.

3. A motion for an order restoring petitioner's right to operate and register a motor vehicle is denied and the petition dismissed.

 

2521 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Peacock


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Yates County


19 Misc. 2d 1068; 191 N.Y.S.2d 296; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2985



September 24, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Court of Special Sessions of Yates County (New York), which convicted him of violating N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1173.


OVERVIEW: The patrolman who cited defendant stated that defendant committed the offense of emerging from a driveway and failing to yield the right of way, in violation of § 1173. He also stated that defendant's vehicle did not stop to yield the right of way upon entering the roadway, thus endangering said users of the roadway. He further stated that defendant swerved and skidded the tires of his vehicle on the dry pavement after turning off from the driveway onto the street in front of the patrolman's vehicle. At this time, there was no sidewalk along the relevant side of the street. Also, it was not alleged that any pedestrians were in the immediate vicinity of defendant's car as it was alleged to have been driven onto the highway without first stopping. Defendant was subsequently convicted of § 1173. He later sought review of his judgment of conviction. The court reversed the judgment, by holding that § 1173, was too vague and indefinite to be enforced and was unconstitutional because it did not set up a guide, rule, or standard for the operation of a motor vehicle when entering a roadway, a deviation from which could properly be made the basis for a criminal prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, which convicted defendant of violating the relevant statute.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- vehicle entering roadway -- section 1173 of Vehicle and Traffic Law, requiring driver of vehicle entering roadway to yield right of way to all vehicles approaching on said roadway, unconstitutional -- insufficient guide, rule or standard provided for operation of motor vehicle.

 Section 1173 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law provides that: "The driver of a vehicle within a business or residence district emerging from an alley, driveway, or building shall stop such vehicle immediately prior to driving onto a sidewalk or onto the sidewalk area extending across any alleyway or driveway, and shall yield the right of way to any pedestrian as may be necessary to avoid collision, and upon entering the roadway shall yield the right of way to all vehicles approaching on said roadway." Defendant is apparently charged with violating that part of the statute which reads "and upon entering the roadway shall yield the [***2] right of way to all vehicles approaching on said roadway." The statute does not set up such a guide, rule or standard for the operation of a motor vehicle when entering a roadway, a deviation from which can properly be made the basis for a criminal prosecution. The statute is unconstitutional and the information is dismissed.

 

2522 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Carollo v. Smithtown


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


20 Misc. 2d 435; 190 N.Y.S.2d 36; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3104



August 28, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion for a temporary injunction is denied.

Submit order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a peddler who was licensed by the county as a veteran, filed a motion for an injunction against the enforcement of an ordinance restricting the occupation of peddling during certain hours on certain highways in defendant town. The main action sought a declaration that the ordinance was unconstitutional and invalid and asked that its enforcement be perpetually enjoined.


OVERVIEW: By seeking a perpetual injunction on the motion, the court held that the peddler had mistaken his remedy. To grant a perpetual injunction would have given the peddler all the relief he sought in his main action; therefore, the court considered the motion as one seeking a temporary injunction. The ordinance's stated purpose was to avoid traffic hazards incident to the stopping of automobiles for trade during the hours of heavy traffic. The peddler argued that ordinances restricting peddling should not be favored by the courts. The ordinance aimed at the peddler who remained stationary at the side of the road attracting the travellers on the highway. The court found that such use was more in the class of a market use which use the town could prohibit on a public street in the exercise of its police power. The court also held that the peddler's claim that the ordinance was vague could not be determined preliminarily and had to await the trial.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- restrictions on peddling -- temporary injunction -- in action for injunction against enforcement of ordinance restricting occupation of peddling during certain hours on certain highways in defendant town, motion by plaintiff for temporary injunction denied -- if exercise of police power not unreasonable and not discriminatory, ordinance would be upheld -- claim that ordinance is vague not determined preliminarily.

1. In an action for an injunction against the enforcement of an ordinance restricting the occupation of peddling during certain hours on certain highways in defendant town, a motion by plaintiff for a temporary injunction is denied. The ordinance states that its purpose is to avoid traffic hazards incident to the stopping of automobiles for trade during the hours of heavy traffic. It aims not at the itinerant peddler but at the peddler who remains stationary at the side of the road attracting travellers on the highway. If the town's exercise of its police power is consistent with general law and is reasonable and not discriminatory, its action will be upheld.

2. The [***2] claim that the ordinance is vague will not be determined preliminarily.

3. Plaintiff mistakes his remedy when he asks for a permanent injunction at this time. The request is interpreted as asking for a temporary injunction.

 

2523 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kassover


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Magistrates' Traffic Court of New York, Borough of Manhattan


20 Misc. 2d 782; 191 N.Y.S.2d 54; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3116



August 25, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is now granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss a charge of making an illegal U-turn on several grounds, including that the traffic regulation, New York City, N.Y., Traf. Reg. § 51(a) (1958) was invalid because it was vague, indefinite, and imprecise; and that the People failed to prove a prima facie case. The court had previously reserved judgment on the issue.


OVERVIEW: Section 51(a) prohibited a driver from turning his vehicle so as to proceed in the opposite direction upon any street in a business district. The court held that (1) there was nothing in § 51 to apprise a driver that the term "business district" had the meaning ascribed in N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 105, as contended by the State, and there was no proof that the point at which the infraction allegedly occurred was within a business district as so defined; (2) there was no evidence that defendant made the U-turn in order to proceed in the other direction or, for example, to park; (3) the fact that the court was a magistrate's court did not lessen defendant's right not to be subjected to vague or unclear laws; and (4) although the court was required to interpret a statute that was reasonably susceptible of two constructions so as to preserve its constitutionality, § 51(a) was not so susceptible.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to dismiss.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- traffic infractions -- section 51 (subd. [a]) of New York City Traffic Regulations prohibiting turning vehicle to proceed in opposite direction in business district is unconstitutional because it is vague, indefinite and imprecise.

The defendant was charged with violating section 51 (subd. [a]) of the New York City Traffic Regulations which prohibits the driver of a vehicle from turning such vehicle "so as to proceed in the opposite direction upon any street in a business district." The record does not show that the U-turn complained of was made in a "business district", nor whether in was made "so as to proceed in the opposite direction" or for some other purpose, nor that the defendant "proceeded" after making the turn, nor does the complaint apprise the defendant that "business district" as used in the regulation is "defined" in section 105 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law. The regulation in question is penal in nature and should be informative on its face, but the definition of "business district" in section 105 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law is not referred to in section 51 (subd. [a]) of the Traffic Regulations. Moreover,  [***2] the fact that a definition of the term was necessary was proof that the words "business district" in the regulation are vague, indefinite, imprecise and equivocal. Furthermore, the "definition" itself, as found in the Vehicle and Traffic Law, lacks clarity. Section 51 (subd. [a]) of the New York City Traffic Regulations is unconstitutional because it is vague, indefinite and imprecise, and the complaint is dismissed.

 

2524 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Engel v. Vitale


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


18 Misc. 2d 659; 191 N.Y.S.2d 453; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3126



August 24, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner parents brought an action in New York against respondent school board (Board) seeking an order in the nature of mandamus, directing the board to discontinue use of a daily prayer in its school district. The board filed a motion to dismiss the action.


OVERVIEW: The parents alleged that the board by resolution directed that the prayer be said as a daily procedure and that it is being said aloud each day in the schools of the district, that the saying of the prayer and the manner and setting in which was said were contrary to the religious practices of the parents and their children who were believers and contrary to the beliefs concerning religion of those parents and their children who were nonbelievers, and that demand had been made for discontinuance of the prayer and refused by the board. The court held that while the board was entitled to authorize the daily prayer, it was not entitled to require the saying of the prayer in question. The court held that if the board did authorize the prayer, it had to bring the authorization to the attention of parents of children in the schools, establish a procedure for excusing non-participants not only from saying the prayer but from the room, if they so elected, and take affirmative steps to protect the religious freedom of both non-participants and participants.


OUTCOME: The petition as amended, was held legally sufficient, the board's defenses were held insufficient and were dismissed. The parents' demand for a jury trial was denied for the reason that there is no triable issue of material fact, and the request for mandamus was, as a matter of discretion, denied but the matter was remanded to the board for further proceedings not inconsistent with the court's order.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- prayer in public school -- Federal and State Constitutions do not prohibit noncompulsory saying of prayer in public school as part of daily procedure -- Board of Education may authorize, but not require, saying of prayer -- board must bring matter to attention of parents, establish procedure for excusing nonparticipants from prayer and from room, and take affirmative steps to protect religious freedom of both participants and nonparticipants.

1. A board of education directed that, as a daily procedure, following the salute to the flag, the following prayer should be said in its schools: "Almighty God, we acknowledge our dependence upon Thee, and we beg Thy blessings upon us, our parents, our teachers and our Country". The Federal and State Constitutions do not prohibit the noncompulsory saying of the prayer. However, the board must take affirmative steps to protect the rights of those who, for whatever reason, choose not to participate. While the board may authorize, it may not require, the saying of the prayer but, if it does, it must bring the authorization to the attention of the parents of children in the schools, establish a procedure for excusing [***2] nonparticipants not only from saying the prayer but from the room, if they so elect, and take affirmative steps to protect the religious freedom of both nonparticipants and participants. The resolution should be modified to establish a procedure whereby the parents of each child are advised of the adoption of the resolution calling for the saying of the prayer, of the wording of the prayer and of the procedure to be followed when it is said, and requested to indicate whether the child shall or shall not participate in the exercise.

2. The proceeding being in the nature of mandamus to compel performance of a duty specifically enjoined by law, it was not necessary to appeal to the Commissioner of Education.

3. Although the resolution of the Board of Education was adopted more than four months before the commencement of this proceeding, since what is charged is a continuing failure to obey the requirements of the Federal and State Constitutions, and the proceeding was commenced within four months after the demand for discontinuance, it was brought within the time allowed by section 1286 of the Civil Practice Act.

4. The application being one involving performance of constitutional [***3] duty, the question is properly raised in a proceeding under article 78 of the Civil Practice Act. The fact that relief might be granted in the nature of a mandatory injunction does not put the proceeding outside the scope of an article 78 proceeding.

5. The petition will be amended to include a statement that all of the schools referred to in the petition are within Union Free School District Number Nine and under the jurisdiction and control of respondents, although such fact would be judicially noticed.

6. The petition, which alleges violations of a constitutional duty in that the board has required, rather than authorized, the daily use of the prayer and the manner of its being said does not protect the rights of nonbelievers or the religious scruples of all of the believers, states a cause of action.

7. There are no factual questions requiring a jury trial.

8. Petitioners, parents of children who are currently attending the schools subject to the program, have standing to sue.

9. The board's resolution, though referring to and inspired by the Board of Regents' statements, was voluntary. The Regents' policy and program are involved in this decision only insofar as they form [***4] the background for and are referred to in the action of the board. The question is the power of the board, unsupported by any administrative, legislative or constitutional requirement that it adopt the resolution. The board was not merely carrying out a duty imposed upon it by the Regents.

10. The prayer is not sectarian or denominational.

11. The board's affirmative defense that petitioners, in seeking to interfere with the saying of the prayer by the children of others, are acting in violation of the Federal and State Constitutions is dismissed. The board may not be compelled to permit the saying of a prayer in the schools. The State may, in determining the curriculum of its schools, exclude any form of devotional exercise.

 

2525 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Pennsylvania R. Co. v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


17 Misc. 2d 1074; 192 N.Y.S.2d 298; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3127



August 22, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff railroad sought a declaration that 1958 N.Y. Laws ch. 358, which amended N.Y. R.R. Law § 307 to require a railroad seeking a passenger rate increase to apply to and get permission from the Public Service Commission of defendant State, was unconstitutional. The State sought judgment that the law was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: N.Y. R.R. Law § 307, as originally enacted, bestowed on certain railroads the power to increase passenger fares, which increases would not be subject to suspension by the Public Service Commission prior to a determination of unreasonableness. Then 1958 N.Y. Laws ch. 358 amended N.Y. R.R. Law § 307 to require prior application to and approval by the Commission before a fare increase could be effected. The railroad sought a declaratory judgment that the 1958 law was unconstitutional. The State moved for a judgment that the law was constitutional. The court entered judgment in favor of the State. The court held that the statute in question was a general incorporation act and not a private or local bill that would violate N.Y. Const. art. III, § 17 or N.Y. Const. art. XVI, § 1. The statute was not a contract between the State and the railroad and the State had the reserved power to amend or repeal it.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment in favor of the State.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Railroads -- railroad redevelopment corporations -- passenger rates -- constitutional law -- statute providing for incorporation of domestic railroad redevelopment corporations, and giving them power to increase passenger rates without first applying to Public Service Commission, was thereafter validly amended so as to require such application (Railroad Law, § 307; N. Y. Const., art. X, § 1).

Article 7 §§ 300-313) of the Railroad Law, enacted in 1954 and providing for the organization and incorporation of domestic railroad redevelopment corporations which should have power to increase passenger fares and which power should not be subject to suspension by the Public Service Commission prior to a determination of unreasonableness, was validly and constitutionally amended in 1958 (Railroad Law, § 307; L. 1958, ch. 386) so as to require prior application to and approval by the Public Service Commission before a fare increase can be effected. Even though plaintiff railroads had already spent large sums in reliance on the statute as originally enacted, the amendment is a valid exercise of the State's power to regulate rates and to amend general incorporation acts (N. Y. Const.,  [***2] art. X, § 1; art. III, § 17: art. XVI, § 1).

People v. Bogner


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, Rochester


20 Misc. 2d 465; 189 N.Y.S.2d 777; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3155



August 15, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion of defendant to dismiss the information is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the People's information. The People had charged defendant with operating a vessel in a city's navigable waters at such a rate of speed as to endanger the property of another or the life and limb of another, a violation of N.Y. Nav. Law § 45(1).


OVERVIEW: The People charged defendant with violating § 45(1). The People's information alleged that defendant had operated a vessel in a city's navigable waters at such a rate of speed as to endanger the property of another or the life and limb of another. Defendant responded by filing a motion to dismiss the information. The court granted the motion of defendant to dismiss the information. The court held that the provisions of § 45(1) were unconstitutional for lack of definiteness and certainty, as § 45(1) continued to utilize the terms "unnecessarily interferes" and "unnecessarily endangers" despite the fact that such terminology had been specifically condemned by the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion to dismiss the People's information that charged him with operating a vessel in a city's navigable waters at such a rate of speed as to endanger the property of another or the life and limb of another.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- violation of Navigation Law -- Navigation Law ( § 45, subd. 1) is unconstitutional -- motion of defendant to dismiss information charging violation of said subdivision was granted -- legislative review and action needed concerning complex laws applying to operation of boats on waters within State.

1. The provisions of subdivision 1 of section 45 of the Navigation Law requiring an operator of a vessel to navigate "in a careful and prudent manner and at such rate of speed as not to endanger the property of another or the life or limb of any person" and defining reckless navigation to include operating a vessel in a manner which "unnecessarily interferes with the free and proper use of the navigable waters of the state or unnecessarily endangers other vessels therein, or the life or limb of any person" is unconstitutional for lack of definiteness and certainty. Similar provisions in the Vehicle and Traffic Law have been declared unconstitutional by the Court of Appeals on the same ground.

2. A motion by defendant herein to dismiss the information charging him with violation of said subdivision is granted.

 [***2] 3. A review of the complex, inadequate and inconsistent laws, Federal, State and municipal, that apply to the operation of boats on waters within this State demonstrates the need for legislative action in view of the recent large increase of pleasure boating.
