Leeds v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


19 Misc. 2d 860; 190 N.Y.S.2d 127; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3205



July 31, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Therefore, the proceeding is dismissed on the merits.

Short-form order signed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer sought to annul the action of respondent school board in adopting an austerity budget. The taxpayer sought to direct the school board to resubmit a new budget to the voters in which optional items such as transportation, cafeteria service, adult education, etc., might be voted on separately.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer contended that N.Y. Educ. Law § 2023, the authority for adopting an austerity budget, was unconstitutional in that it provided for a delegation of the taxing power to the school board after an unfavorable vote, without providing any method for review of the board's actions. The court disagreed that this was the case, finding that the general review provision, N.Y. Educ. Law § 310(7), provided for grievances to be heard by the Commissioner of Education. The taxpayer then alleged that, assuming the law to be valid, the action of the board in submitting and then resubmitting the same budget without change, followed by the precipitate adoption of a stripped down budget of essentials only, was arbitrary and capricious. The court was sympathetic to the taxpayer but found that the school board had acted within its lawful capacity. Questions of good judgment were not for the court to decide. The court dismissed the action.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the taxpayer's petition on the merits.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- budget review -- austerity budget submitted to voters by school board, not reviewable by court.

A school board's budget was voted down. Subsequently, the board submitted the same budget to the voters, and again it was voted down. Thereafter, the board stripped the budget of all items such as cafeteria service, adult education, transportation, etc., and submitted it to the voters. Petitioner's proceeding (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78 ) for an order to annul this so-called "stripped-down, austerity budget" as petulant and capricious and to compel the board to resubmit a new budget with optional items such as cafeteria service, adult education, and transportation to be voted on separately, is dismissed. These are discretionary matters for the board and the voters, which are to some extent reviewable by the State Commissioner of Education, but not by the courts (N. Y. Const., art. XVI, § 1; Education Law, §§ 2023, 2024, 310, subd. 7).

 

2528 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Weber v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


18 Misc. 2d 543; 195 N.Y.S.2d 269; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3230



July 28, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion for an injunction pendente lite is accordingly denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxicab owners filed a motion for an injunction pendente lite to restrain the enforcement of New York City, N.Y., Local Law No. 343 (1959) and for the collection of the 10 cents per trip tax imposed by the Local Law. The owners sought a judgment declaring that the Local Law and the State Enabling Act, 1959 N.Y. Laws 359, § 5, pursuant to which the Local Law was adopted, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The owners claimed that the Enabling Act was enacted without a city home rule request. The court concluded that an enabling act that delegated to a city the power to impose a local tax did not relate to the "property, affairs, or government of a city" within the meaning of the home rule provisions in N.Y. Const. art. IX, § 12. The court held that a home rule request was not required before the enactment of an enabling act involving solely the delegation to a city of authority to impose local taxes for its general revenue purposes. According, the Enabling Act did not contravene the home rule provisions and the Local Law was validly adopted pursuant to the Enabling Act. The owners argued that the tax was discriminatory in taxing users of taxicabs while leaving untaxed the users of other means of public transportation. The court could not say that the legislature was wholly unjustified in making such a classification. The flat tax of 10 cents per trip was justified because the taximeter recorded the number of trips; further, the tax equally affected the riders. As a result, the tax did not violate the Equal Protection Clauses of the United States and New York Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court denied the owners' motion for an injunction pendente lite. .


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- taxicab tax -- temporary injunction -- motion for injunction pendente lite restraining enforcement of Local Law of City of New York imposing taxicab tax denied -- Enabling Act (L. 1959, ch. 369, § 5) not in conflict with home rule provisions of State Constitution -- no violation of equal protection clauses of Federal and State Constitutions.

1. A motion for an injunction pendente lite restraining the enforcement of Local Law No. 343 for 1959 of the City of New York and collection of the taxicab tax imposed thereby in an action for judgment declaring that the Local Law and State Enabling Act (L. 1959, ch. 369, § 5), pursuant to which it was adopted by the city, are unconstitutional is denied.

2. Where it is sought to enjoin the collection of a tax adjudged by the authorities to be necessary for the maintenance of the government, it must clearly and plainly appear that it conflicts with the fundamental law.

3. Enabling acts, authorizing the imposition of local taxes, do not relate to the property, affairs or government of a city within the meaning of the constitutional home rule provisions [***2] (N. Y. Const., art. IX, §§ 11, 12). The power to impose a local tax is excluded from the meaning and operation of the home rule provisions and no home rule request was required before the Legislature could pass enabling bills to grant such power. The Enabling Act does not contravene the home rule provisions of the Constitution.

4. The tax does not violate the equal protection clauses of the Federal and State Constitutions in taxing users of taxicabs while leaving untaxed users of other means of public transportation; and, as between the users of taxicabs themselves, in imposing a flat tax of 10 cents for each trip regardless of the length of the trip or the amount of the fare.

5. None of other incidental complaints or objections, even if sustained, could be the basis for enjoining collection of the tax in view of the separability clause in the law.

 

2529 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Opgal, Inc. v. Burns


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


20 Misc. 2d 803; 189 N.Y.S.2d 606; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3259



July 22, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a landowner and its mortgagees filed an action to declare the town's zoning ordinance to be invalid, void and unconstitutional on the grounds that it violated constitutional due process and the impairment of contract clauses. The ordinance under attack changed the zone classification on plaintiffs' property from residential to light industrial.


OVERVIEW: The landowner bought a large tract of land that was zoned for residential use. It sold part of the land, which was developed as residential property. Another part of the land was sold to the county for a storm drainage sump. In their action responding to the town's rezoning of their property, plaintiffs provided evidence that it was unnecessary for the property to be rezoned because there was sufficient land already zoned for industrial use and expert testimony that the land had little value as industrial property. The court found that plaintiffs had met their burden of proof by establishing that the property had no reasonable possibilities for industrial uses and that the ordinance precluded the use for which it was adapted. Under such circumstances, the ordinance as it related to the landowner's property was so unreasonable and arbitrary that it was an invasion of property rights contrary to the constitutional due process clause. Therefore, it was void. The ordinance did not unconstitutionally impair the mortgage because the ordinance did not act on that contract, did not affect its terms, and did not impair the obligation to perform or remedies available under the contract.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment for the landowner and its mortgagees on their complaint that the town's zoning ordinance violated their constitutional due process.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- rezoning of residentially zoned area so as to bar all residences and allow light industry only, for possible long-range economic benefit of town but at expense of precluding all uses for which properties in this area are now reasonably adapted, is unconstitutional and void.

A zoning amendment by which a portion of a residentially zoned area was rezoned as "light industry", and whereby residential and heavy industry uses were both excluded, is declared confiscatory, unreasonable, unconstitutional and void. Plaintiff property owners have sustained their burden of proving that their property was previously worth between $ 15,000 and $ 18,500 an acre and would now be worth no more than $ 7,000 an acre and that their property cannot profitably be developed industrially in the foreseeable future, and that the rezoning precludes all uses for which their property is reasonably adapted. The Town Board's purposes in rezoning this area appear to be (1) to set up a sort of reserve area for possible future industrial expansion of the town, and (2) to prevent an increase in the school population and (3) to increase the tax income of the school district.  [***2] These laudable, long-range, possible benefits to the whole town or to the school district cannot constitutionally be provided at the expense of plaintiff property owners.

 

2530 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Cedzich v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


19 Misc. 2d 572; 190 N.Y.S.2d 167; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3274



July 20, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion by defendants for judgment on the pleadings is granted and the complaint is dismissed.

Submit order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer brought an action for declaratory judgment against defendant city, alleging that the tax assessment on her property was illegal and void and that the taxpayer was not liable for the real estate taxes levied pursuant to the assessment. Specifically, the taxpayer argued that the city failed to personally inspect each property. The city sought a judgment on the pleadings for failure to state a cause of action.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer filed a complaint alleging that her property tax assessment was defective because the assessors failed to personally examine each property in the city as required by New York City, N.Y. Admin. Code § 155b-1.0. The taxpayer, who filed the action in an individual capacity, did not allege that the assessors' oath regarding their examination of the properties was deficient. The court took judicial notice of the fact that on its face the tax record complied with the statutory mandate for examination of properties. The court determined that the taxpayer could not collaterally attack the assessor's jurisdiction to assess the property, whether or not the property had been personally inspected. The court concluded that, because the taxpayer was in effect attacking the city's tax assessment of her property, she was restricted to the statutory remedies for contesting the levy of an "illegal" property tax provided in N.Y. Tax Law § 290 et seq., New York City, N.Y., Charter §§ 163-166, and New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § 166-1.0. The court noted that even when an actual view was required by statute, failure to do so was a mere irregularity and did not invalidate a tax.


OUTCOME: The court granted the city's motion for judgment on the pleadings and dismissed the taxpayer's complaint.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- real estate assessments -- plenary suit will not lie to adjudge illegality of assessed valuations because of inequality and because of assessors' alleged failure to examine all parcels personally; review proceeding is sole remedy.

A real estate taxpayer's sole remedy for asserted illegality of assessments because of (1) the alleged failure of the tax assessors to examine personally each and every house and parcel of taxable realty in the city (Administrative Code of City of New York, § 155b-1.0), despite the assessors' oath, which is attached to the assessment record, that they have indeed "personally examined each and every house, building, lot, pier and other taxable property", and (2) alleged inequality of assessed valuations, is a review proceeding (Tax Law, art. 13, § 290 et seq.; New York City Charter, §§ 163-166; Administrative Code of City of New York, § 166-1.0). A plenary suit for a declaratory judgment is dismissed, since the asserted illegalities are not jurisdictional.

 

2531 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Hempstead v. Goldblatt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


19 Misc. 2d 176; 189 N.Y.S.2d 577; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3310



July 13, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town filed an action to enjoin defendant landowners from mining and dredging a sand pit until the landowners obtained a permit required by Town of Hempstead, N.Y., Ordinance No. 16 (ordinance), and until violations of the ordinance were cured.


OVERVIEW: The sand pit had been used for commercial mining for almost 20 years when the ordinance was passed. The landowners claimed res judicata, due process, equal protection, and the motives of town officials as defenses. Finding for the town, the court held that the action was not subject to the doctrine of res judicata because a previous action against the landowners, in which a trial court found that the landowners were entitled to a nonconforming use, was brought under a zoning ordinance and, as such, involved different issues and rights. The court found that the prior nonconforming use did not make the landowners immune against the ordinance. The court held that the landowners failed to sustain their burden of proof that the ordinance was unconstitutional as applied to them as there was little evidence to show unreasonableness and the ordinance was within the town's police power. The court found that because the ordinance and its enforcement were lawful, the motives of the town officials in enforcing the ordinance were not relevant.


OUTCOME: The court found that the ordinance and its enforcement were valid exercises of the town's police power and gave judgment to the town against the landowners.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- ordinance regulating excavations -- town is granted judgment of injunction ( Town Law, § 135) against further dredging and excavating by sand and gravel mining corporation in 38-acre water-filled sand pit which said owner has been mining for 32 years, and which now constitutes hazard to children and to public of this now densely populated area, unless said owner complies with recently enacted town ordinance which requires fencing and regulates excavations below certain depths and prohibits pits within 20 feet of any property line -- town had previously sued defendant for injunction under zoning ordinance but had failed, because of defendant's prior nonconforming use; such judgment is not res judicata of present suit -- besides, motion by defendant, on ground of res judicata, to dismiss similar complaint filed by town three years ago, was denied -- present ordinance, unlike zoning ordinance, controls existing excavations -- ordinance not confiscatory -- ordinance validly excepts sumps owned by county -- there may be other noncomplying excavations besides defendant's, but town is not oppressing defendant or refusing defendant equal protection of laws --  [***2] town officials' motives in now suing defendant for benefit of public, after long inaction, are irrelevant.

1. A town which has grown in the past 32 years from a sparsely populated area to a densely populated area is granted judgment after trial enjoining ( Town Law, § 135) the owner and operator of a 38-acre sand pit which has been used for the past 32 years for the mining of sand and gravel, and in which pit there is now a 20-acre artificial lake 25 feet deep, from any further dredging or mining, until said defendants comply with a recently enacted town ordinance which (1) declares the town's policy "to prevent all manner of excavations which create pits, holes, or hollows in the earth, leaving it in a hazardous or dangerous state, or cause soil erosion * * * to remove the danger to health and life caused by deep excavations remaining in the ground * * * which ordinance will promote the safety, health and general welfare of the people of the Town", and (2) prohibits any pit excavation within 20 feet of any property line, or lower than 2 feet above the maximum ground water level at the site, or lower than 10 feet below the grade of the nearest street or highway unless the excavation [***3] has retaining walls or its sides are kept at less than a specified incline, and (3) prohibits removal of earth which weakens the support of, or interferes with the orderly development of, or depreciates the value of, other properties, and (4) requires, when earth has been removed from any part of the excavation to the maximum extent above allowable, that such part be refilled and the premises graded to the levels of the nearest streets or roads, and (5) requires the pit to be surrounded with a 6-foot-high chain link fence or its equivalent, set into 18 inches of concrete, so as to prevent access through or under the fence, and (6) requires an excavation permit from the Town Board, which shall refuse such permit if the proposed excavation will violate any of the above provisions.

2. About two years before the present suit, the town had sued these same defendants for an injunction under the town's zoning ordinance. Said suit had been dismissed on the ground that defendants had a prior nonconforming use. That judgment is not res judicata as to the present ordinance. The present ordinance is a proper exercise of the town's police power against the maintenance of nuisances and for [***4] the regulation of businesses. Against such an ordinance, a prior nonconforming use is no defense.

3. The present ordinance, unlike a zoning ordinance, is intended to and does control existing excavations.

4. Furthermore, a motion by these defendants to dismiss, on the ground of res judicata, a complaint filed by the town three years ago similar to the present complaint, was denied.

5. The ordinance is presumed to be constitutional and nonconfiscatory. It is obviously designed, among other things, to protect children and the public against the real and serious perils of falls, cave-ins and drownings. Defendants have not shown that any provisions of the ordinance are unreasonable or that they cannot conform to its provisions or what it would cost them to conform. It cannot be said that the ordinance unconstitutionally deprives them of property without due process of law.

6. The town's instituting this action against these defendants does not unconstitutionally deprive these defendants of the equal protection of the laws. Within the town there are other excavations, some dry and some water-filled, which do not comply with this ordinance; but defendants have not shown whether [***5] or not these are privately owned; one of them is an unfenced reservoir owned by the City of New York. Throughout the county there are about 300 water drain basins or sumps owned or operated by the county, many of which do not meet the standards of this town's ordinance; but the ordinance validly and constitutionally excepts excavations for public uses. There are perhaps another 100 privately owned sumps throughout the county; but defendants have not shown whether any of these are in operation and to what extent if any they fail to meet the standards of this town's ordinance. In sum, defendants have not shown a pattern of oppression against them.

7. The motives of the town's officials, in instituting this suit, are irrelevant. Long-continued inaction of public officials cannot constitute a waiver by the public.

8. Ex post facto is not a defense; the town is not prosecuting defendants criminally, but is only pursuing its civil remedy of injunction ( Town Law, § 135).

 

2532 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Board of Education v. Allen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


17 Misc. 2d 1080; 192 N.Y.S.2d 186; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3330



July 9, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the petitions are dismissed, without costs.

Submit orders accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, petitioners, school districts and towns, challenged the legality and constitutionality of orders of respondent, the Commissioner of Education of the State of New York, requiring that public funds be expended for the transportation of pupils to parochial schools.


OVERVIEW: The school districts and towns contended that the Commissioner's orders were not final and conclusive and were violative of the state and federal constitutions. They also asserted that the Commissioner did not have the power to order such transportation to central school districts and to transportation to schools outside of such district. The court rejected the arguments of the school districts and towns and held that the Commissioner's orders were final and conclusive under N.Y. Educ. Law § 310 because the orders were not purely arbitrary. The court also held that the Commissioner had the statutory power to order the transportation under N.Y. Educ. Law § 3635. Finally, the court concluded that orders did not violate the state constitution, which permitted the state legislature to provide for the expenditure of public funds for the transportation of children to and from any school, and the use of public funds for transportation to nonpublic schools under case law was a constitutional expenditure which did not violate the First and Fourteenth Amendments to the federal constitution.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petitions filed by the school districts and towns.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- transportation of pupils to parochial school -- court sustains orders of State Commissioner of Education directing central school district to provide transportation to nearest available parochial school if more than two miles and less than eight miles from pupils' residences (Education Law, §§ 310, 3635; N. Y. Const., art. XI, § 4).

1. Orders of the State Commissioner of Education, directing the board of education of a school district "to provide transportation for the appellants' children to the school they legally attend, provided such children are attending the nearest available parochial school of their denomination, and provided further that such school is located more than two and less than eight miles from their residences, and pay the reasonable cost thereof out of any moneys of the district which are available for such purpose", are sustained. (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78; Education Law, §§ 310, 1807, 3635; N. Y. Const., art. XI, § 4; cf. U.S. Const., 1st and 14th Amdts.)

2. Orders of the State Commissioner of Education under section 310 of the Education Law are final [***2] and conclusive, regardless of which party initiated the appeal to him.

 

2533 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Daniman v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


23 Misc. 2d 664; 190 N.Y.S.2d 225; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3336



July 8, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, in order that there may be a final termination to this litigation, the motion of Blau is denied, with leave, however, to renew, or to move for reconsideration or reargument thereof, in the event that within any reasonable time from the date hereof, the Commissioner of Education indicates in writing his change in position to the effect that he is willing to consider the appeal of the present moving party. The cross motion to dismiss is denied. Settle order on notice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding under N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act art. 78, petitioners, a group of school teachers, against respondent, the Board of Education of New York, the movant sought an order relieving him from the terms of a stipulation, and further requested that the stipulation be vacated insofar as it applied to him. By cross motion, the Board of Education sought to have the movant be bound by an order previously entered in the proceeding.


OVERVIEW: A group of teachers were terminated under the provisions of New York City, N.Y., Charter § 903 because they refused to answer questions about their affiliation with the Communist party posed by the Committee on Judiciary of the United States Senate. There was also pending a separate proceeding involving college personnel. During the pendency of the proceedings, the movant and five others were terminated for the same reasons. These individuals entered into a stipulation by which they agreed to be bound by the outcome of the pending litigation. Meanwhile, one individual's case had been severed when he chose to retain different counsel. In this individual's case, the United State's Supreme Court declared that § 903 was unconstitutional. During the stipulants' appeal to the Commissioner of Education, the movant's appeal was severed to permit a substitution of counsel. The Commissioner refused to accept jurisdiction because the stipulants had elected their remedy and had chosen the court's as their forum. The court denied the motion because setting aside the stipulation would not have permitted the movant's appeal to go forward considering the Commissioner's decision.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion with leave, however, to renew, or to move for reconsideration or reargument thereof, in the event that within any reasonable time the Commissioner of Education indicated in writing his change in position to the effect that he was willing to consider the appeal of the moving party. The cross motion to dismiss was denied.


HEADNOTES

Stipulations -- motion to be relieved from stipulation -- schoolteacher's motion denied, with leave to renew if State Commissioner of Education will reconsider his refusal to accept jurisdiction (Education Law, § 310).

Although the United States Supreme Court has held, on an appeal to it by one New York City schoolteacher, that a discharge pursuant to section 903 of the New York City Charter is unconstitutional and invalid, said court has also refused to review a denial by the New York Court of Appeals of a motion by a group of other schoolteachers for a reversal by the Court of Appeals of its earlier contrary decision in their cases (350 U. S. 551; 1 N Y 2d 855; 352 U. S. 950). This denial [***2] by the Court of Appeals included still another group of schoolteachers who had stipulated to be bound by the result of that group decision. Thereafter, the State Commissioner of Education refused to accept jurisdiction of an appeal (Education Law, § 310) by one of said stipulants for reinstatement in his position. The New York Supreme Court now denies a motion by said stipulant for an order relieving him of his stipulation; however, if within a reasonable time the Commissioner of Education indicates in writing that he is willing to reconsider this stipulant's appeal, then this stipulant may renew his motion.

 

2534 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Piantoni v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


18 Misc. 2d 1030; 189 N.Y.S.2d 804; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3379



June 30, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is, accordingly, denied. Submit order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought to declare 1959 N.Y. Laws ch. 369, § 5, and New York City, N.Y., Local Law No. 343 (1959) unconstitutional insofar as said laws purported to empower defendant, the City of New York, to impose and collect a taxicab trip tax. The taxpayer filed a motion for a temporary injunction restraining the City, and defendants, the Board of Estimate of the City of New York and the treasurer from imposing and collecting said tax.


OVERVIEW: The court held that upon considering the various grounds urged for declaring the enactment invalid, the court reached the conclusion that the taxpayer had not shown beyond reasonable doubt that it conflicted with the fundamental law. Legislation would not be declared unconstitutional unless it clearly appeared to be so; all doubts being resolved in favor of the constitutionality of a law. The wisdom of legislation was not for the court to determine. The foregoing applied particularly to a situation where, as here, a court of original jurisdiction was called upon to declare a legislative enactment invalid by way of the drastic remedy of a temporary injunction where the invalidity asserted was not plain and patent.


OUTCOME: The motion was denied.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- taxicab tax -- temporary injunction -- temporary injunction denied in action to declare unconstitutional laws empowering City of New York to impose tax of 10 cents on each trip or use of taxicab (L. 1959, ch. 369, § 5; Local Laws of City of New York, No. 343 of 1959) -- not shown beyond reasonable doubt to conflict with fundamental law.

A temporary injunction will not be granted in a taxpayer's action to declare unconstitutional section 5 of chapter 369 of the Laws of 1959 and Local Law No. 343 of 1959 of the City of New York, insofar as they purport to empower the City of New York to impose and collect a tax of 10 cents on each trip or use of the taxicab. Plaintiff has not shown beyond reasonable doubt that these laws conflict with fundamental law.

 

2535 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Camp v. Camp


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, Nassau County


21 Misc. 2d 908; 189 N.Y.S.2d 561; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3389



June 26, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife filed an action for separation against defendant husband. The husband contended that a divorce had been granted in Florida and the wife amended her complaint and added a second cause of action for a judgment declaring the invalidity of the Florida divorce.


OVERVIEW: The husband contended that Florida divorce was valid, alleging that his domicile was in Florida. The court disagreed, finding that the parties had lived in New York and spent a few months each year in Florida, and that the husband started to build homes in Florida. The court found that the testimony failed to show the husband's residence in Florida for six months preceding the filing of the bill of complaint in the Florida proceeding. Thus the Florida court did not have jurisdiction over the subject matter. The wife then contended that she was entitled to a separation on the grounds of abandonment and nonsupport. The court agreed, finding that the wife had been in Florida with the husband and with his permission and consent she returned to New York and that the husband failed to furnish her with any funds or to communicate with her. The court further found that the husband's subsequent commencement of Florida divorce proceedings without notifying the wife was evidence of abandonment. Thus the court granted the wife a judgment of separation, alimony, and counsel fees, however, counsel fee for a Florida attorney was denied.


OUTCOME: The court granted the wife a judgment of separation, and awarded her alimony and counsel fees for her New York attorney.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Husband and wife -- Florida divorce void, since short of six months' domicile -- judgment of separation awarded, on ground of abandonment -- alimony and counsel fee.

1. A judgment of separation is conclusive that a valid marriage exists, and hence such a judgment makes it unnecessary to render a declaratory judgment as to the invalidity of a prior foreign divorce.

2. The obtaining of an ex parte foreign divorce is not cruelty, and, where the parties have previously been living apart, is not abandonment warranting a separation.

3. Therefore, a plaintiff may properly plead and prove two causes of action: one for separation on the grounds of abandonment and nonsupport, and one for judgment declaring defendant's ex parte foreign divorce void. However, if the trial court finds the foreign divorce void, and also finds that plaintiff is entitled to a separation on other grounds, the court should (1) decree separation and (2) dismiss the declaratory judgment cause of action as unnecessary.

4. This husband was domiciled in Florida when he commenced suit there for divorce and when that summons for divorce was mailed to his wife; but this New York court finds that his domicile there [***2] had commenced only three days before he commenced suit, and not, as required by the Florida Annotated Statutes (§ 65.02), six months immediately prior to commencement of suit.

5. Florida decisional law allows a defendant in an ex parte proceeding to have a decree set aside at any time where the record does not contain corroborated proof of domicile, not merely residence, for the required period. The full faith and credit clause of the United States Constitution (art. IV, § 1) and section 1738 of title 28 of the United States Code, enacted in pursuance thereof, permit collateral attack in another State if such attack would be permitted in the rendering State. No principle of res judicata or rule of comity mandates recognition of such a decree by the courts of New York. Since New York will permit collateral attack upon its own divorce judgments, whether voidable only or absolutely void, no unconstitutional discrimination (U. S. Const., art. IV, § 2) occurs when New York permits such a Florida decree to be collaterally attacked.

6. Furthermore, the uncontested Florida decree in this case did not contain any express finding of residence; and this New York court finds that the [***3] transcript of the testimony on which the decree was rendered fails to establish that the husband's domicile had been established in Florida for at least six months prior to the commencement of suit (Florida Ann. Stat., § 65.02). The Florida decree is therefore without jurisdiction; it is invalid; and it is not a bar to the wife's cause of action in New York for a judgment of separation.

7. Concomitantly with his Florida suit, the husband abandoned his wife and failed to support her. The evidence supports her contention that her return to New York from Florida was with his acquiescence. He has not shown any misconduct on her part sufficiently grave to justify him in abandoning and not supporting her (Civ. Prac. Act, § 1163). She is granted a judgment of separation on the grounds of abandonment and nonsupport.

8. He was 69, she 55, when they married. Each had been previously married. She had long been used to working for her living. This marriage lasted 4 1/2 years, when he abandoned and stopped supporting her and commenced suit in Florida. He had been giving her $ 50 a week for the table, plus additional moneys when needed. He owns real property and a 1954 Cadillac car [***4] and is in the building construction business. His Federal tax returns during the years of their marriage showed adjusted gross incomes of $ 14,300, $ 12,575.26, $ 5,125, $ 3,912.83, and $ 380.68. Taking into consideration the age of the parties, the length of their marriage, their standard of living, the fact that defendant has been drawing on capital, and the present physical condition and requirements of both parties, the trial court fixes alimony in the amount of $ 100 a week, and directs that such payments commence on the return date of the motion for temporary alimony and counsel fees which had been referred to this trial court.

9. For the services of plaintiff's counsel, including his out-of-pocket expenses, in investigating the facts and the Florida law, in preparing the complaint and amended complaint, in preparing and arguing the motions for alimony, injunction, sequestration and to amend the complaint, in arguing an appeal, and in the preparation and six-day trial of the instant action, counsel fee is fixed at $ 2,500.

10. Plaintiff's request that a separate fee be allowed for a Florida attorney is denied. Although the Civil Practice Act ( § 1169-a) authorizes a separate [***5] allowance for the making of a factual investigation with respect to the Florida divorce or for an expert witness on Florida law, under the head of "sums of money necessary to enable the wife, to carry on * * * the action", the Florida attorney did not testify as an expert and there is nothing in the record to show what services he rendered in investigating the facts.

 

2536 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Connell v. Granby


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Oswego County


17 Misc. 2d 812; 187 N.Y.S.2d 672; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3421



June 22, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners sought a ruling in their action against defendants, the Town of Granby, N.Y., and others, seeking a declaratory judgment that a zoning ordinance was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The owners bought a parcel in the zoned area, and operated a dry cleaning business in clear violation of a zoning ordinance. After the neighbors tried to restrain the business, the owners sued for a declaratory judgment that the zoning ordinance was unconstitutional and invalid. The owners argued that because the zoning ordinance only applied to a portion of the Town, it was not part of a comprehensive plan as required by N.Y. Town Law §§ 260-284. The court entered judgment in favor of defendants. A decision to zone part of the Town and not the rest of it was in effect a comprehensive plan. Because it was stipulated that the zoning ordinance was adopted in a proper manner and there was no evidence that the zoning ordinance was unreasonable or arbitrary, it was valid.


OUTCOME: The court entered declaratory judgment in favor of defendants.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- comprehensive plan -- zoning of substantial portion of town leaving remainder unzoned complies with requirement of comprehensive plan and is not invalid as spot zoning (Town Law, § 263).

A Zoning Ordinance of the Town of Granby, adopted in 1938, limited the use of an area about a mile long and a half mile in depth to residential and agricultural purposes. The town is about 10 miles long and about 8 miles wide. The requirement of section 263 of the Town Law that zoning regulations "shall be made in accordance with a comprehensive plan" was not violated. The ordinance declared a comprehensive zoning plan and was not illegal "spot zoning". Absent a showing that the remainder of the town should be zoned or that the ordinance is unreasonable or arbitrary, it is valid.

 

2537 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Cohen v. Valley Stream


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


23 Misc. 2d 1017; 189 N.Y.S.2d 110; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3562



June 3, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment is granted to the defendants dismissing the complaint, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff oil company brought an action seeking to declare certain amendments to the Building Zone Ordinance of defendant Incorporated Village of Valley Stream ineffective, unconstitutional, and void as to the use of the company's property. The oil company sought an order adjudging that it was entitled to a permit for the erection, maintenance, and operation of a gasoline service station.


OVERVIEW: The company entered into a lease of the premises conditioned upon the obtaining of a special use permit. Defendant Board of Trustees amended the ordinance by repealing and eliminating in a C-I district the granting of a special permit for gasoline stations and by adding to permitted uses in an industrial district, the use of gasoline service stations. The Board denied the application of the company for a special use permit. The court determined that Valley Stream, N.Y., Building Zone Ordinance § 12-a required no notice to the company of the proposed amendment. The court explained that N.Y. Village Law § 95 did not require personal service of the amendment to validate the same. The court noted that N.Y. Village Law § 175 gave the Board the power to regulate and restrict the location and use of buildings, structures, and land for trade, industry, residence, or other purposes. The court concluded that the actions of the Board were a reasonable exercise of the powers granted under the Village Law and were not arbitrary, discriminatory, or confiscatory.


OUTCOME: The court granted judgment to defendants dismissing the complaint with costs.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- amendment to village zoning ordinance requiring special use permits for gasoline service stations in commercial districts not unconstitutional for failing to provide standards or safeguards on which to base granting or denial of applications -- plaintiffs not entitled to notice of proposed amendment limiting such stations to industrial districts, nor to personal service of copy of amendment (Village Law, § 95) -- village has authority to enact zoning legislation (Village Law, § 175) -- study of zoning map indicates orderly arrangement of use districts -- legality of ordinance not affected by fact that greater return might be realized by operator of gasoline service station than is now realized -- actions of Village Board were reasonable exercise of its powers and were not arbitrary, discriminatory or confiscatory -- complaint dismissed.

1. An amendment to the Building Zone Ordinance of the Village of Valley Stream requiring permits for gasoline service stations as a special use in commercial districts was not unconstitutional for failure to provide standards [***2] or safeguards on which to base the granting or denial of applications.

2. A subsequent amendment limiting gasoline service stations to industrial districts was not invalid for failure of the Board of Trustees to give plaintiffs notice of the proposed amendment. Notice is required only as to change of classification of a particular parcel of land, rather than to a change of the uses in a given district, and to owners of property outside, rather than within, the area of proposed change.

3. Although action on plaintiffs' application for a permit was reserved until after adoption of the latter amendment, even if it had been granted, adoption of the amendment before actual investment by plaintiffs in construction would have prevented the use.

4. Personal service of amendments is only required to accelerate the effective date (Village Law, § 95).

5. The challenged amendments are not unconstitutional. The right of a municipality to enact zoning legislation may not be interfered with by a court unless it is exercised in an arbitrary, unreasonable, discriminatory or confiscatory manner. A study of the zoning map of defendant village indicates an orderly arrangement of use districts [***3] which, defendant claims, were adopted after considerable study and are the result of a valid dedication of all the areas in the village to the most appropriate use of the land. The fact that a greater return could be realized by the operator of a gasoline service station than is now realized does not affect the legality of the ordinance (Village Law, § 175).

6. The actions of the Village Board were a reasonable exercise of its powers and were not arbitrary, discriminatory or confiscatory. The complaint is dismissed.

 

2538 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Application of Hehir v. New York City Transit Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


18 Misc. 2d 244; 189 N.Y.S.2d 1004; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3563



June 2, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the reasons herein indicated, the petition is dismissed. Settle order on notice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee filed an application pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 to review the determination of respondent commission, which affirmed a finding by the transit authority that the employee was a person of doubtful trust and reliability within the meaning of N.Y. Security Risk Law § 233.


OVERVIEW: The employee was discharged by the transit authority after it was determined that he had been a member of the Communist party and, as such, was a person of doubtful trust and reliability. The employee refused to admit that he was ever a member of the Communist party. The employee appealed but failed to testify. The commission affirmed the transit authority's action. The employee filed an application pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 to review the determination of the commission in affirming the transit authority's decision. On appeal, the employee argued that the administrative finding of reasonable grounds for belief, concerning his doubtful trust and reliability, offended due process. However, the court determined that it was the employee's lack of candor and his refusal to respond to questioning that provided the evidence of his doubtful trust and reliability. Further, the court held that there was no factual basis for the employee's claim that he was at any time charged by the transit authority with having been a member of the Communist party or that he was discharged for that reason. Accordingly, the employee's petition was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The employee's petition was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- Security Risk Law -- Security Risk Law (L. 1951, ch. 233) is constitutional -- New York City Transit Authority towerman who refused to offer evidence or to answer questions except to say "I am not now a member of the Communist party" was properly discharged.

1. Confidential information having been received by the New York City Transit Authority, a duly designated security agency under the Security Risk Law (L. 1951, ch. 233, as amd.), that a towerman, a uniformed civil service employee whose duties involved the care and operation of interlocking levers and emergency devices of the signal system, was a member or had been a member of the Communist party, and said employee having refused to offer any evidence or to answer relevant questions of the city's Commissioner of Investigation except to say "I am not now a member of the Communist party", and the Transit Authority having determined that his failure to answer questions as to his past membership in the Communist party afforded reasonable ground for belief that he was of doubtful trust and reliability, and the Authority [***2] having therefore discharged him from his civil service position, and his appeal to the State Civil Service Commission having resulted in an affirmance of the determination, his review proceeding (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78) is dismissed.

2. The Security Risk Law (L. 1951, ch. 233, as amd.) affords constitutional due process to a civil service employee.

 

2539 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Nat'l Psychological Ass'n for Psychoanalysis, Inc. v. Univ. of N.Y.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


18 Misc. 2d 722; 188 N.Y.S.2d 151; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3629



May 25, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Pursuant to the provisions of rule 113 of the Rules of Civil Practice, it appearing that no triable issues of fact are presented and that defendant is entitled to judgment, the motion for summary judgment is granted to the extent of directing judgment declaring that article 153 of the Education Law is not unconstitutional; and is otherwise denied. Defendant's cross motion to dismiss is denied.

Settle order and judgment accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a psychological association and individual members, filed a declaratory judgment action against defendant state university seeking an adjudication that N.Y. Educ. Law § 7601 et seq. (1956) was unconstitutional. Plaintiffs filed a motion for summary judgment. The university filed a cross motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The association operated a training program to prepare psychologists and other qualified persons to practice or teach psychoanalysis. All four of the individual members fell into a small group of psychologists who, by reason of circumstances beyond their control, were unable to produce documentary evidence of their training abroad, as was required by the university for certification. Plaintiffs contended that the statute violated due process and equal protection principles. The court declared that the statute was constitutional. By the terms of the statute, the individual members were prohibited from representing themselves as psychologists. In its decision, the court held that the State had the power to regulate psychoanalysis and psychotherapy because they were occupations that affected the public health or welfare. Further, plaintiffs had not overcome the presumption of constitutionality of the statute. In addition, the fact that the statute did not define the term "psychology" had no effect on its validity because it was immaterial whether a person was a psychologist, as the relevant test was whether a person was holding himself out to the public as a psychologist.


OUTCOME: The motion for summary judgment was granted to the extent of directing judgment declaring that the statute was not unconstitutional. The university's cross motion to dismiss was denied.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- certified psychologists -- statute prohibiting anyone from representing himself to be "psychologist" unless so certified by board of examiners (Education Law §§ 7601-7614) is constitutional -- persons unable to produce credentials may have judicial review of refusal to certify them (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78).

1. Article 153 (§§ 7601-7614) of the Education Law is constitutional. It prohibits anyone from representing himself to be a "psychologist" unless he is registered and certified by the Regents-appointed Board of Examiners of Psychologists as having met their standards of education, training, experience, character, age and citizenship. It also provides for suspension and revocation of certificates, and for judicial [***2] review of such action and of refusal to issue or renew certificates. It also provides for confidential communications between registered psychologist and client. The statute is designed for the protection of the public from charlatans. The statute does not attempt to define the broad term "psychology"; it does not prohibit anyone from practicing "psychology"; it merely prohibits unqualified persons from representing themselves to be "psychologists". In this respect, it is similar to article 149 of the Education Law, which does not prohibit anyone from practicing "accountancy", but does prohibit unqualified persons from using the title "C. P. A." Somewhat similar is article 131, which regulates "osteopathy" under the supervision of the Regents, without attempting to define the term. The power of the Regents and of the Board of Examiners of Psychologists to make rules and regulations (§§ 7603, 7613) is necessarily subject to the standards set forth in article 153 (§ 7605 et seq.); and the article provides for an advisory council to be broadly representative of the whole field of psychology (§ 7604).

2. Three of the plaintiffs, who are distinguished practitioners of psychology [***3] but are unable to produce their European university credentials, may bring a proceeding under article 78 of the Civil Practice Act to review administrative refusal to certify them. The statute itself is constitutional.

 

2540 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Schildhaus


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Special Sessions of the City of New York


17 Misc. 2d 825; 186 N.Y.S.2d 68; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3682



May 19, 1959 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, etc.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from Court of Special Sessions of the City of New York, Borough of Manhattan (New York), which convicted him of violating N.Y. Mullet. Dwell. Law §§ 3, 365 and 366 and Administrative Code of the City of New York §§ D26-3.1 and D26-3.2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant acted as his own trial counsel and often engaged the trial judge in argument that provoked the trial judge into making statements that raised a suspicion that he did not receive an impartial trial. The court also held: (1) the trial court had jurisdiction over defendant because he appeared in the proceeding and answered that he was ready for trial without raising a jurisdictional argument; (2) N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. §§ 321 and 323 did not permit a demurred to the information; (3) it was error under N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 392-ato admit, in this criminal action, pleadings from a civil action as proof of a fact admitted therein.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction ordered a new trial.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- right to impartial trial -- jurisdiction over offenses -- Magistrates' Court has jurisdiction over offenses under sections D26-3.1 and D26-3.2 of Administrative Code of City of New York and sections 62 and 80 of Multiple Dwelling Law -- court had jurisdiction over defendant though information and deposition contained in one instrument -- demurrer to complaint properly refused by Magistrate -- section D26-3.1 of Administrative Code of City of New York is constitutional -- undue tension created by provocation of defendant, who acted as own attorney, impaired right to impartial trial.

1. The Municipal Term of the Magistrates' Court had jurisdiction over offenses under sections 62 and 80 of the Multiple Dwelling Law and sections D26-3.1 and D26-3.2 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York [***2] ( N. Y. City Crim. Cts. Act, § 100).

2. The information and deposition, though in one instrument, contained sufficient sworn facts. Defendant appeared, pleaded, and answered "ready" for trial. Therefore, the court acquired jurisdiction of the defendant.

3. Sections 321 and 323 of the Code of Criminal Procedure permit a demurrer only to an indictment or to an information triable in the Court of Special Sessions. Therefore the Magistrate properly refused to entertain a demurrer to the complaint.

4. Section D26-3.1 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York is constitutional as a protection of the public health, safety and welfare.

5. Error was committed in receiving pleadings in a civil action over defendant's objection in this action (Code Crim. Pro., § 392-a).

6. The defendant, who acted as his own attorney, provoked the Magistrate, creating undue tension which may have impaired the defendant's right to an impartial trial. The judgment is reversed and a new trial ordered.

 

2541 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gilmore


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Columbia County


17 Misc. 2d 14; 186 N.Y.S.2d 161; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3686



May 18, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant brought an application in the form of a writ of error coram nobis to review his sentence under N.Y. Penal Law § 1048 for murder in the second degree for shooting another man during an altercation between them.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who had been imprisoned for 21 years, argued that the sentence imposed, 55 years to life, was so grossly excessive that it constituted an illegal and unconstitutional sentence. The State contended that the writ of error coram nobis was not available and that defendant's remedy was to apply for executive clemency. The court imposed a new sentence. The court noted that the punishment for murder in the second degree was an indeterminate sentence, the minimum not less than 20 years and the maximum not more than life. The court stated that under N.Y. Penal Law § 1048 it was mandatory that the sentence be not fixed or predetermined and not lead to a definite end or result. The court observed that the sentence imposed was just as effective in confining defendant for the remainder of his life as though the minimum had been 100 or 200 years. The court stated that a clear injustice had been perpetrated and that the courts could not claim to be courts of justice if the only remedy was holding the court powerless and surrendering its mistake to the executive branch of government. The court pointed out that a pardon or a reprieve was based upon mercy, not upon justice.


OUTCOME: The court imposed a new sentence that defendant be confined for an indeterminate sentence, the minimum of which should be 25 years and the maximum of which should be for his natural life.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- coram nobis proceeding -- sentence, without any investigation, of 29-year-old defendant to 55 years to life, was not "indeterminate" (Penal Law, § 1048), since his life expectancy was only 35 years; such sentence is vacated and new sentence is imposed, of 25 years to life.

1. Twenty-one years ago defendant, then 29 years old and without criminal record, got into an argument with his rooming companion after drinking on Independence Day and shot and killed him. After trial defendant was convicted of murder in the second degree. The permissible sentence is "an indeterminate sentence" of 20 years to life (Penal Law, § 1048). The court, without any presentence investigation or questioning, sentenced him to 55 years to life. But defendant's expectation of life, according to actuarial tables, was only 35.15 years. In effect it was a straight life sentence, contrary to the legislative intent. Defendant's coram nobis application is granted and he is resentenced to an indeterminate sentence of 25 years to life.

2. Defendant lacked the means to appeal to the Appellate Division for a reduction of sentence. Executive clemency cannot now be his sole recourse against [***2] this unjust and excessive punishment. The judicial system which devised the remedy of coram nobis has the inherent power to extend that remedy to this cause. This is a matter which should be passed upon by the Appellate Division or the Court of Appeals.

People v. Salerno


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Special Sessions of the City of New York


17 Misc. 2d 535; 185 N.Y.S.2d 169; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3842



April 27, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion denied, etc.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss a two-count information, which charged him with illegal possession of narcotic drugs and illegal possession of a hypodermic syringe and a hypodermic needle. Defendant alleged that N.Y. Penal Law §§ 1751-a and 1747-d(3) were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that N.Y. Penal Law §§ 1751-a, which makes it a misdemeanor to illegally possess narcotic drugs, and 1747-d(3), which makes it a misdemeanor to illegally possess narcotic implements, were unconstitutional. As to the count alleging illegal possession of narcotic drugs, the court found that no constitutional question was presented as to that count. In considering the challenge to constitutionality of § 1747-d(3), the court found that the statute had a definite relation between the narcotic evil and the purported cure or prevention offered by the statute. The legislature was within its power in making possession of narcotic implements without a prescription a crime. Further, the legislature also possessed the power to declare that on and after April 16, 1956, such possession was illegal. Finally, the court concluded that because the legislature had cause to become alarmed at the increased number of narcotic addicts and the effect of such addiction on the public health and welfare, § 1747-d(3) was part of the police power of the State. Thus, § 1747-d(3) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- narcotics -- possession of hypodermic syringe or hypodermic needle, without doctor's prescription, is misdemeanor (Penal Law, § 1747-d, subd. 3); statute constitutional -- count alleging illegal possession of narcotic drugs (Penal Law, § 1751-a) cannot be dismissed, without trial, on affidavit that it was merely trace of heroin.

1. Subdivision 3 of section 1747-d of the Penal Law, making it a misdemeanor to possess a hypodermic syringe or a hypodermic needle unless one is a physician, etc., or unless one has a prescription therefor which is less than a year old, is constitutional.

2. The second count of the above information, charging illegal possession of narcotic drugs (Penal Law, § 1751-a), cannot be dismissed in advance of trial, on an affidavit asserting that the evidence against defendant consists only of a wad of cotton containing a trace of heroin.

 

2543 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Costello v. Sheldon


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Oneida County


16 Misc. 2d 518; 190 N.Y.S.2d 161; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3854



April 23, 1959 



DISPOSITION: Since, therefore, section 95-d at the time of the accident and trial herein was unenforcible because the statute did not set up a sufficiently definite standard of conduct and was not sufficiently explicit to inform those who may become subject to its penalty as to what conduct on their part would not be an "interference with" or an "endangering of traffic" ( People v. Grogan, 260 N. Y. 138), the conviction is reversed, the fine remitted and the information is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the City Court of Rome, Oneida County (New York) upon defendant's conviction of violating N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 95-d for failure to proceed safely after stopping at a stop sign.


OVERVIEW: The information filed against defendant charged him with violating the since repealed N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 95-d. That section required that a person having stopped as directed by a stop sign proceed with caution so as not to interfere with or endanger traffic. After trial, the trial court found that defendant did stop, but did not thereafter proceed with caution so as not to interfere with or endanger traffic. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction, remitted the fine, and dismissed the information. The court held that § 95-d was vague and indefinite, as it did not set up a sufficiently definite standard of conduct and was not sufficiently explicit to inform those who may become subject to its penalty as to what conduct on their part would not be an interference with or an endangering of traffic. The court noted that a new statute, N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1172, set up a definite standard of conduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction, remitted the fine, and dismissed the information.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- "stop" sign at intersection -- former section 95-d of Vehicle and Traffic Law, insofar as it required "proceed with caution", was vague, unenforcible and unconstitutional, and has since been replaced by specific rules of road and rights of way (Vehicle and Traffic Law, §§ 1142, 1172, eff. July 1, 1958).

Former section 95-d of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, insofar as it required the driver of a vehicle, after stopping at a "stop" sign at an intersection, to "proceed with caution [***2] so as not to interfere with or endanger traffic", was too vague to be enforcible and hence was unconstitutional. Conviction is reversed, fine remitted, and information dismissed. The new rules of the road, effective July 1, 1958 (Vehicle and Traffic Law, §§ 1142, 1172) will specify the rights of way in such a situation.

Sylvander v. Taber


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Onondaga County

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff stockholders brought a declaratory action in the Supreme Court of New York, Onondaga County, contending that N.Y. Ins. Law § 199 was unconstitutional because it impaired upon the obligation of their contract as shareholders with defendant insurance company.


OVERVIEW: The stockholders brought an action for a declaratory judgment that N.Y. Ins. Law § 199, insofar as it sought to be applied to the stockholders of the insurance company, was unconstitutional. A voting trust agreement was entered into between some of the present insurance company officials for the purpose of soliciting stockholders of the company to endeavor to convert the corporation from a stock company to a mutual life insurance company pursuant to § 199. The court declared that the insurance company officials were within their rights in proceeding to mutualize the insurance company and that § 199, authorizing a plan of mutualization did not violate that portion of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, which provided no state shall pass any law impairing the obligations of contracts.


OUTCOME: The court held that the plan of mutualization did not violate the Constitution by impairing on the obligations of contracts.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Insurance -- mutualization of stock life insurance corporation -- constitutional law -- declaratory judgments -- mutualization of stock life insurance corporation is valid and constitutional (Insurance Law, § 199, subds. 2, 3; N. Y. Const., art. I, § 6; art. X, § 1; U. S. Const., art. I, § 10; 14th Amdt.).

Mutualization of a stock life insurance corporation so as to convert the corporation into one issuing participating policies, upon authorization of such conversion by a majority of the outstanding stock and a majority of the eligible policyholders and a majority of the board of directors and the approval of the State Superintendent of Insurance (Insurance Law, § 199, subds. 2, 3) is not ultra vires but is valid and constitutional (N. Y. Const., art. I, § 6; art. X, § 1; General Corporation Law, § 5; U. S. Const., art. I, § 10; 14th Amdt.), as applied to a stock life insurance corporation which was incorporated in 1912, and as applied to dissenting minority stockholders thereof whose stock was issued by the corporation either about the year 1912 or after the certificate of incorporation was amended in 1922 to authorize the issuance of additional stock, at all [***2] of which times the above constitutional provisions already existed and the above statutory provisions or their prototypes already existed (N. Y. Const. of 1894, art. I, § 6; art. VIII, § 1; U. S. Const., above-cited; Insurance Law of 1909, § 95, as amd. by L. 1911, ch. 150; Insurance Law of 1909, § 16, as amd. by L. 1911, ch. 150, L. 1917, ch. 301; General Corporation Law of 1909, § 320).

 

2545 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Ward v. New Rochelle


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


20 Misc. 2d 122; 197 N.Y.S.2d 64; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3956



April 8, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner filed suit against defendants, a city and city officials, to declare an amendment to a city zoning ordinance unconstitutional as it affected plaintiff's property. Plaintiff also sought a declaration that she had a vested right to develop her property in accordance with the provisions of the R-1A district zone of the city zoning ordinance. Plaintiff also sought injunctive relief. The matter was referred to a referee.


OVERVIEW: After extensive study, the city adopted a comprehensive zoning ordinance, in which plaintiff's property was placed in an R-1A district, the highest residence district at that time. The school district requested plaintiff to give it 13 acres of her property to be used for the erection of an elementary school, with its surrounding recreational area. Plaintiff was willing to make the gift of land on condition that the school parcel conform to the overall development of her property, which could only mean a development in accordance with the zoning ordinance as it then existed. By reason of the city's approval of plaintiff's plat plan, when she completed the conveyance to the school district, plaintiff had a vested right to develop her remaining land in accordance with her plan, as approved by the planning board. The vested right thus acquired gave plaintiff the right to make and develop the subdivision in accordance with the approved plat plan and the zoning ordinance that was in effect at the time of the conveyance. Having the vested right, the referee ruled that the upzoning of her premises by the city council was illegal and without effect as applied to plaintiff's property.


OUTCOME: The referee entered judgment in favor of plaintiff.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- at request of School District, plaintiff agreed to make gift of 13.3 acres of her land, constituting 20% of her property and worth $ 140,000, for school purpose provided school parcel conformed to development of her remaining property according to plan incorporating then applicable Zoning Ordinance -- City Planning Board approved such plan but, after plaintiff conveyed property to city, said board disapproved plan and recommended that plaintiff's property be upzoned -- ordinance adopted to carry out such recommendation not applicable to plaintiff's property -- City Planning Board without power to disapprove plan once approved.

In 1955 the City of New Rochelle adopted a Zoning Ordinance by which plaintiff's property was placed in a residence district which provided that lots must contain 10,000 square feet, with a 100-foot frontage at the building line. In 1956 the New Rochelle City School District requested plaintiff to give it 13.3 acres of her property, to be used for the erection of an elementary school, with its surrounding recreational area. Plaintiff was willing to make this gift of land, constituting more than 20% of her property [***2] and admittedly worth $ 140,000, on condition that the school parcel conform to the overall development of her property, which could only mean a development in accord with the Zoning Ordinance as it then existed. Plaintiff had a plat plan of her entire property prepared. At a meeting of the City Planning Board held on December 10, 1956, the board approved the subdivision as shown on plaintiff's plan upon certain stated conditions, all of which were met. The plat plan provided a benefit to the city in that no lots faced on two important highways, and, further, that land was provided for the widening and straightening of those roads without cost to the city. Plaintiff was notified in writing by the Planning Board of the approval of the subdivision map and of the conditions imposed. By deeds dated December 29, 1956 and January 8, 1957, plaintiff conveyed the school site to the Board of Education. The Planning Board met on January 14, 1957, after plaintiff had delivered her deeds, and at this meeting the board deleted one of the conditions, disapproved the subdivision map, and recommended to the Common Council that the Zoning Ordinance be amended by placing the undeveloped areas of [***3] the city in a new district, where 20,000-square-foot lots, with a width of 150 feet at the building line, would be required. By ordinances dated May 15, 1957, August 19, 1957 and September 11, 1957, the Common Council followed this recommendation to upzone, with the result that plaintiff's property was placed in the new district. There is no statutory authority for a planning board, having once approved a plat plan, later to disapprove it. When plaintiff completed the conveyance, she had a vested right to develop her remaining land in accord with her plan as approved by the Planning Board. The upzoning of her premises was illegal and without effect. The zoning amendment should not be set aside as wholly invalid, but it is not applicable to the plaintiff's property.

Gail Turner Nurses Agency, Inc. v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, New York County


17 Misc. 2d 273; 190 N.Y.S.2d 720; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 4195



March 4, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action before the Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, New York County, plaintiff employment agency requested injunctive relief preventing the state from enforcing N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 185(9)(1), which reduced the percentage that an agency could charge an employer. The employment agency claimed this newly enacted provision was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The employment agency sought a declaratory judgment determining that the particular provisions of § 185 which reduced fees which could be charged by nurses' registries for private duty placement of was unconstitutional and void. The issue, thus, was whether a statute limiting fees chargeable by employment agencies for placing nurses in private duty to five percent of the salary or wages received each week by the nurse (for the first 10 weeks of employment) was unreasonable and invalid. The court held that such a limitation was completely proper where closely related to the protection of state citizens. Because the legislature's valid exercise of police power was deemed valid, the court dismissed the employment agency's action.


OUTCOME: The court rendered judgment is rendered in favor the state and thereby dismissed the employment agency's challenge to recently enacted state legislation.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- employment agencies' fees -- private nurses' employment agencies' fees validly reduced (General Business Law, § 185, subd. 9, par. [1]) -- police power valid, though some members of group may be unable to stay in business.

1. The Employment Agency Act (General Business Law, art. 11), as amended (L. 1958, ch. 893), insofar as it reduces the fees which may be charged by employment agencies or registries for placing nurses in private duty (General Business Law, § 185, subd. 9, par. [1]) is a constitutional and valid exercise of the police power.

2. The fact that the enactment of a statute results in reduced income, or diminishes property value, or makes it impossible for some people to continue in business, does not establish a denial of constitutional due process or equal protection under the law. Public welfare is a broad and inclusive concept. Legislation regulating an entire group is valid even though some members of the group may suffer economic losses not shared by others of the group. Courts may not sit as superlegislatures to weigh the wisdom of each enactment or to decide whether the legislative policy offends the welfare of a particular [***2] group.

 

2547 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bell


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Schenectady County


15 Misc. 2d 562; 183 N.Y.S.2d 190; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 4216



March 2, 1959 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Police Court of the City of Schenectady, Schenectady County (New York) entered a judgment convicting defendant of violating N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1214. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1214, which prohibited the sudden opening of a car door or leaving a car door open on the side available to moving traffic. Defendant was fined. Defendant appealed. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction and remitted the fine to defendant. The court held that the weight of the evidence favored the finding of innocence and that the benefit of the doubt should have been resolved in defendant's favor. According to the court, there was a sharp conflict in the testimony of the complainant and defendant, and a disinterested witness testified that there was no traffic moving at the time of the accident. In addition, the court also declared § 1214 unconstitutional. According to the court, the law left many questions of interpretation open and susceptible to extensive variations of understanding. The court concluded that the law was too vague and indefinite in its wording to guide operators of motor vehicles and enforcement officers and that it lacked clarity and definition for courts in interpreting and carrying out its provisions.


OUTCOME: The court set aside defendant's conviction and remitted the fine to him.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- opening door of motor vehicle -- section 1214 of Vehicle and Traffic Law which provides that no person shall open door of motor vehicle on side available to moving traffic unless reasonably safe to do so, nor leave door open longer than necessary to load or unload passengers, is unconstitutional -- statute fails to establish standards for enforcement officers and courts, and is vague and impossible to enforce -- moreover, verdict contrary to weight of evidence.

1. Section 1214 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law provides that: "No person shall open the door of a motor vehicle on the side available to moving traffic unless and until it is reasonably safe to do so, nor shall any person leave a door open on the side of a vehicle available to moving traffic for a period of time longer than necessary to load or unload passengers." It fails to set forth standards and guideposts for enforcement officers, as well as courts. It is too vague [***2] in its meaning and, by reason thereof, becomes impossible to enforce. The law leaves many questions of interpretation open and susceptible to extensive variations of understanding. Section 1214 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law is unconstitutional.

2. Moreover, the verdict is contrary to the weight of evidence. The prosecution has failed to meet its burden of proving the defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.
