People v. Hammond


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Steuben County


15 Misc. 2d 724; 182 N.Y.S.2d 859; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 4237



February 26, 1959 



DISPOSITION: The order of the City Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an order from the City Court of the City of Corning, Steuben County (New York), which granted defendant's motion to release him and dismiss the charge of violating N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1210, subd. (a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant got out of his car without turning off the motor or removing the key from the ignition. A police officer saw him do it and drove the vehicle to the police station. When defendant arrived to claim it, he was arrested for violating § 1210, subd. a. The trial court dismissed the charge against defendant because § 1210, subd. a was unconstitutionally vague. Section 1210, subd. a provided that no person driving or in charge of a motor vehicle leave it unattended without first stopping the engine, locking the ignition, removing the key, and effectively setting the brake. The court found that the provision "removing the key" was vague because its only direction was removing the key from the ignition. It did not provide enough information to warn a person in advance whether his act was criminal or not. The court stated that if the statute was intended to require a person to completely remove the key from the vehicle, it should have so stated. The court concluded that § 1210, subd. a was too vague to be legally enforced.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which granted defendant's motion to release him and dismissed the charges against him.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- leaving key in ignition -- Vehicle and Traffic Law ( § 1210, subd. [a]), insofar as it makes it traffic infraction to leave key in ignition of unattended car, is unconstitutional.

Subdivision (a) of section 1210 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, insofar as it makes it a traffic infraction to leave the key in the ignition of an unattended motor vehicle, is too vague to be legally enforced and is therefore unconstitutional. Defendant is discharged.

People v. Wilson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Queens County


15 Misc. 2d 858; 182 N.Y.S.2d 842; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 4238



February 26, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly the motion to dismiss the indictment herein is denied. Order entered accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss his criminal indictment on the grounds that he was denied a speedy trial. Defendant asserted that N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 673, the statute that formed the basis for his indictment, unconstitutionally deprived him of his right to a speedy trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted on criminal charges. His original indictment was dismissed on the grounds that prejudicial delay had denied defendant his right to a speedy trial. The state then reindicted defendant for the same crimes pursuant to N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 673. The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss his reindictment. Although the court expressed doubts as to the wisdom of the statutory scheme created by § 673, it felt constrained to abide by state law, which dictated that undue delay was measured from the time that the indictment to which the motion of dismissal was addressed was found.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss the indictment.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- failure to prosecute -- effect of new indictment -- original indictment dismissed for failure to prosecute (Code Crim. Pro., § 668) -- subsequently defendant again indicted (Code Crim. Pro., § 673) -- undue delay not measured in such case from time of original indictment -- dismissal of original indictment does not bar new indictment under section 673 of Code of Criminal Procedure where offense charged is felony.

The defendant originally was indicted by an indictment filed January 7, 1955. The Appellate Division dismissed the indictment for failure to prosecute (Code Crim. Pro., § 668) without prejudice to the right of the District Attorney to proceed as permitted in section 673 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. The District Attorney thereafter did so proceed and defendant was indicted by indictment filed November 3, 1958. A motion by defendant for an order dismissing the indictment on the grounds that he has been denied a speedy trial is denied. The law of this State measures the undue delay in such a case from the time the particular indictment to which the [***2] motion is addressed was found. Such a dismissal does not bar the District Attorney from proceeding to obtain a new indictment under section 673 of the Code of Criminal Procedure if the offense charged, as in this case, be a felony. Because of the statutory provisions, the court may not consider on this motion the delay which was found by the Appellate Division to be fatal to the first indictment. There is no claim here by the defendant that he has been denied a speedy trial since the new indictment was found.

People v. Pavia


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Schenectady County


15 Misc. 2d 861; 182 N.Y.S.2d 915; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 4239



February 26, 1959 



DISPOSITION: The convictions herein are affirmed. Submit order accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Police Court of the City of Schenectady (New York), which convicted him of conducting a gambling business.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the search warrant used by officers was improper and incompetent. The court affirmed and found that the proof amply substantiated the finding that the defendant was conducting a gambling operation as a business. Defendant personally handed papers to police officers containing notations of bets and other numerical listings allegedly connected with policy numbers. The actual exhibits were not submitted to the court for examination. The court found testimony describing defendant's activities convincing. The court rejected defendant's objection to a telephone tap and held that the information received by the tap could be used against defendant even though obtained in the course of intercepting another's phone. Defendant was tied to the conversations by the identification of his voice. Thus defendant was present in effect and the calls were binding upon him. The court found no reason to exclude a tape recording because although somewhat muted, it appeared that defendant's voice was recorded and satisfactorily identified. The court held that there was no double punishment for a single crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- book-making -- policy -- defendant properly convicted of violation of Penal Law ( §§ 974, 986) -- information could be used against defendant although obtained in course of intercepting another's telephone -- not necessary that intercepted telephone be manned at all times and conversations manually recorded -- convictions and sentences under both statutes did not amount to double punishment for single crime.

1. Defendant was properly convicted of a violation of section 986 of the Penal Law.

2. Information could be used against this defendant even though obtained in the course of intercepting another's telephone. Defendant was tied to the conversations by the identification of his voice. He was thus present in effect and the calls were binding upon him.

3. The use of a tape recorder attached to the intercepted telephone is merely an extension of the authorization permitted in the interception [***2] order. It is not necessary for the intercepted telephone to be manned by a police officer at all times and conversations manually recorded.

4. Defendant was charged with separate crimes of keeping a place for the game of policy and book-making in violation of sections 974 and 986 of the Penal Law. The proof shows that defendant's acts related to both policy and horse bets. The separate convictions and the imposing of separate sentences did not amount to double punishment for a single crime.

Baldwin v. Buffalo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


15 Misc. 2d 607; 185 N.Y.S.2d 996; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 4270



February 19, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motions to dismiss the complaint and the petition are denied.

Submit orders accordingly, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual and petitioner individual instituted actions against defendant/respondent city and others asking for a judgment declaring a local law ineffective to change the ward boundaries of the city and seeking an order to compel the city to submit the local law to a referendum vote. The city and other respondents made a motion to dismiss the complaint on the ground that it failed to state a cause of action.


OVERVIEW: The individuals maintained that the city had no power to enact the local laws in question under the constitutional and statutory grants of power to a city to enact local laws relating to its "property, affairs or government," while the city and other respondents firmly asserted the contrary. The court held that the issue presented was whether the change of the ward boundaries by Local Law No. 1 (1959) was a "mode of selection" in relation to the election of ward supervisors who were elected members of the board of supervisors. The court concluded that the changes made by Local Law No. 1 (1959) in the boundaries of the wards of the city clearly changed the mode of selection or methods of nominating and electing ward supervisors of the city, in violation of the constitutional and statutory prohibitions. The court also concluded that Local Law No. 2 also failed because the council district boundaries were based on assumed but nonexisting ward boundary lines. Accordingly, the court denied the motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court denied the city and other respondents' motion to dismiss the individuals' actions asking for a judgment declaring a local law ineffective to change the ward boundaries of the city.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- city home rule -- in action for judgment declaring that Buffalo City Council cannot validly, since city is wholly within county, enact local law changing boundaries of wards and council districts, and in proceeding to compel referendum thereon if adjudged validly enacted (N. Y. Const., art. IX, § 12; City Home Rule Law, § 11, subd. 1), motions to dismiss complaint and petition are denied.

1. The ward boundaries and council districts of the City of Buffalo (Charter of City of Buffalo, enacted by Local Law No. 4 of 1927 of City of Buffalo, published in Local Laws of 1932, p. 21) were purportedly changed by the City Council of the City of Buffalo by Local Laws Nos. 1 and 2 of 1959. In this action for a judgment declaring Local Law No. 1 of 1959 unconstitutional and void, and in this mandamus proceeding to compel a referendum on said Local Laws Nos. 1 and 2 of 1959 if they are adjudged to be validly enacted (City Home Rule Law, § 15, subd. 4), motions to dismiss the complaint and the petition as insufficient in law are denied.

2. The City [***2] of Buffalo is wholly contained within the County of Erie. A city cannot validly enact a local law relating to the "mode of selection" of those of its officers who are "members of the governing elective body of the county in which such city is wholly contained" (N. Y. Const., art. IX, § 12) or of those of its officers "who perform no functions for the city except as members of the governing elective body of a county in which such city is wholly contained" (City Home Rule Law, § 11, subd. 1). (See, also, N. Y. Const., art. IX, § 1; County Law, § 150; Buffalo City Charter, § 425.)

3. If a motion to dismiss a complaint for legal insufficiency is not addressed to any specific cause of action in the complaint, the motion must be denied if any cause is sufficient. The first cause of action here is sufficient; hence it is unnecessary to decide whether the second and third causes of action are sufficient.

 

2552 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Gordon v. Gerosa


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


16 Misc. 2d 710; 185 N.Y.S.2d 329; 1959 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 4272



February 19, 1959 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff poultry agents' declaratory judgment action against defendant city fiscal officers for an injunction against sales tax collection, the fiscal officers sought to dismiss the agents' complaint on various grounds.


OVERVIEW: The agents bought chicken coops which were not returned to them by the purchasers. The fiscal officers imposed a sales tax on the purchase price of the coops, contending that the agents rented the coops and that in some way they were returned to the lessor. The agents sought a declaratory judgment to the effect that sales taxes were improperly imposed and an injunction prohibiting the tax collection and further hearings regarding it. The agents contended that relegating them to appeal from an adverse administrative finding by way of N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 would involve a hardship because they would have to post a bond in the amount of the tax assessed, and that the fiscal officers should be estopped from imposing the tax. The court granted the fiscal officers' motion to dismiss, finding that the agents had not shown that the amount of the tax was confiscatory, and that the fact that the agents' books had been periodically audited by the city authorities without any tax being assessed did not create an estoppel. Thus, the court concluded that the agents should be relegated to the usual procedure in tax matters and discretion should not be exercised to entertain the action.


OUTCOME: The court granted the fiscal officers' motion to dismiss the agents' action against them.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- declaratory judgments -- despite tax statute's provision that review proceeding (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78) is exclusive remedy (Administrative Code of City of New York, § N41-7.0), action for declaratory judgment is proper in case of wide public interest or to declare unconstitutionality or inapplicability -- tax statute's requirement for bond in amount of tax in order to institute review proceeding (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78) is not inequitable unless confiscatory -- city is not estopped to impose sales tax for past years merely because of its past years' audits of taxpayer's books -- if questions of fact are involved, remedy is administrative hearings rather than court hearings -- taxpayers claim that chicken coops are used up in sales of live poultry, whereas city claims that coops are sales-taxable; administrative hearings have already consumed 300 pages; action for declaratory judgment and injunction dismissed (Rules Civ. Prac., rule 212).

1. Despite a tax statute's provision (Administrative Code of City of New York, § N41-7.0) that the exclusive method of review is a proceeding under article 78 of the Civil Practice Act, an action for a [***2] declaratory judgment may be proper (1) where the constitutionality of the taxing statute is questioned, or (2) where imposition of the tax is claimed to be inapplicable to the situation, or (3) where the decision will affect a great many other people.

2. A tax statute's provision that, in order to obtain review by a proceeding under article 78 of the Civil Practice Act, the taxpayer must post a bond in the amount of the tax assessed, is not an inequitable hardship, unless the amount of the tax is confiscatory or so substantial as to preclude the possibility of advantage from such right of review.

3. Where a tax review involves substantial questions of fact, such questions should be resolved in administrative hearings, rather than in court.

4. The city is not estopped to impose a sales tax for past years merely because, in the past, it periodically audited the taxpayer's books and did not impose a tax on this particular kind of sale, so that now, asserts the taxpayer, it would be a hardship to pay a tax on sales on which no tax was originally collected by the seller. He does not allege that any departmental ruling or interpretation was ever made on which he relied.

5. The taxpayers [***3] are poultry agents, who put the live birds in coops and sell the birds to slaughterhouses. The taxpayers claim that the coops are practically used up in delivery, whereas the city claims that the taxpayers rent the coops and that in some way the coops are returned to the lessors and that a sales tax is payable thereon. Administrative hearings are pending, and over 300 pages have already been devoted to the city auditors' procedures. Clearly, the question of estoppel involves disputed issues of fact. Accordingly, the taxpayers should be relegated to the usual procedure and review in tax matters. The court declines to entertain this action for a declaratory judgment and injunction, and dismisses the complaint (Rules Civ. Prac., rule 212).
