Western New York Medical Plan, Inc. v. Winkler


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


15 Misc. 2d 277; 178 N.Y.S.2d 981; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2554



October 9, 1958 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff medical plan instituted an action against defendant New York Superintendent of Insurance seeking a judgment declaring that N.Y. Ins. Law § 250(1), as amended by 1957 N.Y. Laws 621, did not make it mandatory for it to reimburse subscriber contract holders for services performed by licensed podiatrists. Intervenor podiatry society, together with the Superintendent, moved for a summary judgment pursuant to N.Y. R. Civ. Prac. 113(9).


OVERVIEW: In their motion, the Superintendent and the podiatry society sought a judgment that the medical plan was required to reimburse contract holders for covered services that were recognized as common to both the medical and podiatrical professions, regardless of whether such service was performed by the podiatrist or the physician. N.Y. Ins. Law § 250(1) (1957) provided that medical expense indemnity consisted of reimbursement for medical care provided through duly licensed physicians, dental care provided through duly licensed dentists, podiatrical care provided through duly licensed podiatrists, nursing service, and of furnishing necessary appliances, drugs, medicines, and supplies. It also consisted of reimbursement for bio-analytical or clinical laboratory examinations and reports thereof reported to a physician, osteopath, dentist, or podiatrist made by any privately operated bio-analytical or clinical laboratory. Therefore, where a medical expense indemnity contract covered service of a kind recognized as common to both the physician and the podiatrist, a subscriber was entitled to reimbursement for such service whether performed by a physician or a podiatrist.


OUTCOME: The motion for summary judgment was granted.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Insurance -- nonprofit medical expense indemnity contracts -- under amendment (L. 1957, ch. 621) to Insurance Law (§ 250, subd. 1) providing that medical expense indemnity should include reimbursement for podiatrical care by duly licensed podiatrists, subscriber to medical expense indemnity contract covering service of kind common to both physician and podiatrist was entitled to reimbursement for such service whether performed by physician or by podiatrist (Matter of United Med. Serv. v. Holz, 5 Misc 2d 999, held controlling).

Subdivision 1 of section 250 of the Insurance Law (as amd. by L. 1954, ch. 474), which had provided that medical expense indemnity "may" consist of reimbursement for podiatrical care provided through duly licensed podiatrists, was amended (L. 1957, ch. 621) to provide that such medical expense indemnity "shall", among other things, consist of reimbursement for such "podiatrical care provided through duly licensed podiatrists." In a proceeding previously brought concerning a similar statutory provision with respect to dental care (Matter of United Med. Serv. v. Holz, 5 Misc 2d 999) the courts, in deciding virtually identical claims, held that [***2] the medical indemnity corporations' rights had not been abrogated; that the requirement of reimbursement was applicable to covered services performed by dentists; that the statute was not unconstitutional, and that no retroactive liability was imposed. The principles so determined applied equally to podiatric care and, accordingly, where a medical expense indemnity contract covered service of a kind common to both physicians and podiatrists, a subscriber contract holder was entitled to reimbursement for such service whether performed by a physician or a podiatrist.

New York v. Windsor Madison Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, New York County


14 Misc. 2d 674; 179 N.Y.S.2d 734; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2574



October 7, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The application is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This matter came to the court by way of an application that plaintiff, City of New York, filed under New York City, N. Y., Admin. Code ch. 32, tit. B. art. 28, in order to permanently restrain defendant corporation from advertising in such a manner as to suggest that it would close upon disposal of its stock. The corporation filed for a declaratory judgment stating that ch. 32, tit. B, art. 28 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The City of New York instituted an action under New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code ch. 32, tit. B. art. 28, seeking to permanently restrain a corporation from advertising in a manner suggesting that it would close down upon disposing of its stock. The court granted the city's application and restrained the corporation in the desired manner. The court found that ch. 32, tit. B. art. 28 was constitutional in that it represented a lawful exercise of police power. Statutory laws that regulated business to protect the public welfare and penalized refusals to comply thereto were constitutional. In its decision, the court noted that the corporation's advertisements were deceptive in the sense that they tended to cause the public to draw false conclusions.


OUTCOME: The court granted the application and prevented the corporation from making the sale in a manner that could have led the public to believe that it was a closing sale.


HEADNOTES

Injuctions -- municipal licensing violation -- store which was licensed to conduct forced-out-of-business sale (Administrative Code of City of New York, § B32-205.0) applied again for such license three years later and was refused but nevertheless continues to advertise and conduct such "sale"; Magistrates' Courts summonses have in some cases brought fines and in some cases dismissals; in civil suit by city, permanent injunction issued against such "sales".

A corporation which conducted a men's retail haberdashery was granted a license to conduct for 30 days a so-called "forced-out-of-business sale" (Administrative Code of City of New York, § B32-205.0). After such sale, it merely changed the business name of the store and reopened for business. Three years later, it applied for another such license. Application was rejected. The corporation's review proceeding (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78) and its action for a judgment declaring the law unconstitutional were dismissed. Nevertheless it persisted in advertising and placarding a "forced-out-of-business" or "close-out" or "final" or "loss of lease" sale. In the last 10 months, the City of New [***2] York has served approximately 76 Magistrates' Courts summonses therefor on defendant. In some cases the defendant was fined, and in some instances the summons was dismissed. In the instant civil suit, the city is granted a permanent injunction against defendant's purported "sales".

 

2573 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Berkowitz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Kings County


14 Misc. 2d 384; 178 N.Y.S.2d 119; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2670



September 19, 1958 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant demurred to an indictment charging him and four others with one count of obscene prints and articles, pursuant to N.Y. Penal Law § 1141, and one count of conspiracy, pursuant to N.Y. Penal Law § 850. The indictment was drafted pursuant to N.Y. Code of Crim. Proc. §§ 295-a to 295-l (1929 N.Y. Laws 176), which governed simplified forms of indictment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and others were charged with one count of obscene prints and articles, pursuant to N.Y. Penal Law § 1141, and one count of conspiracy, pursuant to N.Y. Penal Law § 850. Defendant demurred to the simplified indictment, and the court allowed the demurrer, holding that the indictment could not be sustained under N.Y. Code of Crim. Proc. § 275 because defendant was neither advised of the nature of the charges against him nor of the facts which might have been proved at trial, and the indictment failed to recite the time, date, or place of the commission of the crimes charged. The court found that N.Y. Code of Crim. Proc. §§ 295-a to 295-l intended that after an indictment, the People would supply by a bill of particulars the information required in long-form indictments by N.Y. Code of Crim. Proc. § 275, but that even if defendant had demanded such a bill, it could not have met the requirements of procedural due process because there was no certainty that the crime described in the indictment was the same crime for which the grand jury indicted defendant. The court concluded, however, that the objections on which the demurrer was allowed could be avoided on a new indictment.


OUTCOME: The court allowed defendant's demurrer to the indictment in all respects and found that the objections on which the demurrer was allowed could be avoided on a new indictment. The court directed the district attorney to resubmit to the same or another grand jury.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- simplified indictment -- demurrer allowed to simplified indictment for obscenity and conspiracy; District Attorney is directed to resubmit matter to Grand Jury ( Penal Law, §§ 1141, 580; Code Crim. Pro., §§ 295-a to 295-1, 323, 327; N. Y. Const., art. I, § 6) -- if criminal statute may be violated in several ways, and evidence before Grand Jury supports more than one way, simplified indictment cannot be used constitutionally.

1. A demurrer is allowed to the following simplified form of indictment (Code Crim. Pro., §§ 295-a to 295-1), and the District Attorney is directed to resubmit the matter to the same Grand Jury or to another Grand Jury (Code Crim. Pro., §§ 323, 327): "First Count. The Grand Jury * * * accuse the defendants, each aiding and abetting the other, of the crime of obscene prints and articles, contrary to Penal Law section 1141. Second Count. The Grand Jury * * * accuse the defendants of the crime of conspiracy, contrary to Penal Law section 580."

2. The statute authorizing simplified indictments (Code Crim. Pro., §§ 295-a to 295-1) requires the People to furnish a bill of particulars as to dates, times and places of commission of crimes, and as [***2] to the nature of defendant's violation of the provisions of criminal statute, and as to the facts which constitute such a violation or violations. But only a Grand Jury can indict (N. Y. Const., art. I, § 6); and a Grand Jury's indictment must fulfill the constitutional requirements of due process, by sufficiently informing the defendant of the nature of the charge against him so as to enable him to prepare his defense and to protect him adequately against possible double jeopardy. A District Attorney cannot indict by drawing a bill of particulars; that is, a defendant cannot constitutionally be subjected, by means of a District Attorney's bill of particulars, to danger of trial on a charge on which he was not indicted. A simplified indictment is constitutional in a situation where the court can be certain that a bill of particulars of the indictment will describe the same crime as charged in the indictment. Where a statute defines a crime which may be charged in several different ways, and the evidence presented before the Grand Jury can support more than one of the charges, the simplified form should not be used. When a simplified indictment is used in such a situation, the [***3] trial court finds it difficult to charge the trial jury intelligently, and the same difficulty confronts the District Attorney in his summation to the jury, and the constitutional question can be raised during the trial and will then survive a judgment of conviction and will be ground for an appeal; so, in the interest of finality of judgment, the simplified form of indictment should not be used in such a situation.

3. In this case, on the argument of the demurrer, sufficient facts were presented to convince the court that, even if the court were to direct the District Attorney to furnish the court with the Grand Jury minutes and with the District Attorney's proposed bill of particulars, still the court would be unable to determine (1) whether the Grand Jury indicted the defendants (under Penal Law, § 1141) (a) for distribution or for possession with intent to sell or for mere possession, and (b) whether, of the many articles introduced in evidence, the Grand Jury deemed books or magazines or newspapers or photographs or motion pictures or recordings or paintings to be obscene, and (2) whether the Grand Jury indicted the defendants (under Penal Law, § 580) (a) for conspiracy to [***4] commit the substantive crimes of publishing, or printing, or selling, or possessing ( Penal Law, § 580, subd. 1) or (b) for conspiracy to commit an act injurious to public morals ( Penal Law, § 580, subd. 6). Therefore, demurrer is allowed.

Bieck v. Radmin


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


14 Misc. 2d 416; 178 N.Y.S.2d 983; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2682



September 17, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] It is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a Florida corporation and New York residents, moved for dismissal of a complaint brought upon a Florida judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that Fla. Stat. ch. 47.16, 47.30, pursuant to which service in the prior action was effected and jurisdiction in the Florida court that rendered the judgment rested, exceeded the permissible limits of jurisdiction by substituted service of summons on nonresidents. In denying defendants' motion to dismiss, the court held that the duly authenticated record of the judgment was entitled to the enforcement it would receive in Florida when the complaint attached the record satisfactorily establishing jurisdiction. Fla. Stat. ch. 47.16, 47.30 had been declared constitutional in Florida. The provisions of the Florida statute and the findings contained in the record of the judgment afforded the required due process by virtue of defendants' contacts with the forum state; maintenance of the suit there did not offend traditional notions of fair play and substantial justice.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motions to dismiss.


HEADNOTES

Judgments -- foreign judgment -- in action upon Florida judgment, motion by defendant Florida corporation and remaining defendants, who are residents of this State, to dismiss complaint denied -- provisions of Florida statute upon which jurisdiction rested and findings in record afford required due process.

In an action upon a Florida judgment, a motion by defendant Florida corporation and the remaining defendants, who are residents of this State, to dismiss the complaint is denied. The Florida statute pursuant to which service was effected and jurisdiction rested ( Florida Stats., §§ 47.16, 47.30) has been declared constitutional in that State and is similar to section 229-b of the Civil Practice Act. The provisions of the Florida statute and the findings in the record of the judgment afford the required due process by virtue of defendants' contacts with the forum State. Maintenance of the suit would not offend against fair play and substantial justice.

 

2575 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Brunacini v. Loomis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


13 Misc. 2d 884; 177 N.Y.S.2d 954; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2767



September 3, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petitioner's motion is granted to the extent of declaring section 2 of article 2 of said ordinance as unconstitutional, and directing said Town Clerk to consider and pass upon petitioner's request for junk dealer's license, and to that extent only; in all other respects the motion is denied, without costs to either party.

Prepare and submit order accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner junk dealer initiated an action under N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act art. 78 seeking an order to compel respondent town supervisor to issue him a license to engage in a junk business and to disregard an allegedly unconstitutional ordinance regulating junk dealers. The dealer also sought an order restraining respondent town board from enacting any legislation that prevented the dealer from using his property as junk business.


OVERVIEW: The dealer applied to the town clerk for a license to operate a used car parts and junk business on his property. The clerk refused to issue the license because the dealer failed to obtain the consent of each and every taxpayer within a radius of 500 yards of his place of business, as required by a town ordinance. The town supervisor also refused to issue the license. The dealer filed an action against the supervisor seeking, among other things, an order to compel the supervisor to issue the license and to disregard the ordinance, which allegedly violated N.Y. Const. art. I, § 6 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court entered an order granting the dealer's motion declaring the unconstitutionality of the ordinance's "consent requirement," and it directed the town clerk to consider and pass upon the dealer's request for a junk operator's license; the motion was otherwise denied. The court held that (1) because the town board was unable to decide the constitutionality of an ordinance, it was proper for the court to assume jurisdiction; and (2) the consent provisions in the ordinances was clearly unreasonable and oppressivebecause it gave one taxpayer absolute power to void the license.


OUTCOME: The court granted the dealer's motion declaring the unconstitutionality of the ordinance's consent requirement, and it directed the town clerk to consider and decide the dealer's application for a junk dealer's license. In other respects, the dealer's motion was denied.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- license conditioned upon consents of all nearby taxpayers -- refusal of Town Clerk to issue junk dealer's license because applicant could not obtain written consent of each taxpayer within radius of 500 yards of place of business, as required by town ordinance regulating junk dealers, reviewable by Supreme Court in article 78 proceeding (Civ. Prac. Act, § 1285, subd. 4) -- applicant adversely affected by ordinance in such specific manner as to entitle him to contest constitutionality thereof -- that part of ordinance conditioning grant of licenses on consent of all taxpayers within specified radius unconstitutional.

1. The refusal of a Town Clerk to issue a junk dealer's license because the applicant could not obtain the written consent of each taxpayer within a radius of 500 yards of the [***2] place of business, as required by a town ordinance regulating junk dealers, was not a determination as to which "adequate" relief could be obtained from the Town Board, since the Town Board could not hear and determine the constitutionality of the ordinance, and the Supreme Court was empowered, therefore, in a proceeding under article 78 of the Civil Practice Act, to assume jurisdiction and decide the entire controversy (Civ. Prac. Act, § 1285, subd. 4).

2. The applicant was adversely affected by the ordinance in such specific manner as to be entitled to contest the constitutionality thereof, especially where he could not obtain the required consents of nearby taxpayers.

3. That part of the ordinance conditioning the grant of licenses on the consent of all taxpayers within a radius of 500 yards of the place of business was unconstitutional in that it conferred upon one taxpayer the absolute power to void the license, and to that extent the ordinance was clearly unreasonable and oppressive (N. Y. Const., art. I, § 6; U. S. Const., 14th Amendt.). Relief was granted to the applicant to the extent of directing the Town Clerk to consider and pass upon his request for a junk dealer's [***3] license.

 

2576 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Gayle v. Samuel Adler, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Magistrates' Courts of New York, Borough of Brooklyn


13 Misc. 2d 497; 177 N.Y.S.2d 361; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2808



August 20, 1958 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with violating the milk-dating regulations promulgated under the authority contained in New York City, N.Y., Charter § 551 et seq. and New York City, N.Y., Charter § 885.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with violating the milk-dating regulations. It had in its possession a quantity of milk in quart size containers that was improperly labeled in violation of regulation 155 (subd. 4) of section 156 of the Sanitary Code of the City of New York. Additionally, defendant had in its possession heavy cream in half-pint containers, which were not labeled with the date on which distribution might begin. Defendant committed the acts with which it was charged, as established by the evidence and concessions. Defendant raised constitutional questions regarding the validity of the regulations. The court concluded defendant was guilty. The court acknowledged that there was evidence that there was evidence that the regulations did not serve the health purpose for which they were established. The court found, however, that the regulations could be based on common beliefs. The court concluded that it could only strike down the legislation and the regulations if there was no rational basis for them. The court noted that the existence of another factor, refrigeration, affecting the quality of milk did not negate the regulation of the age factor.


OUTCOME: The court found that defendant was guilty of violating the milk-dating regulations and that the regulations were constitutional.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Food -- milk -- milk-dating requirements of New York City Sanitary Code, which in effect prohibit sale of milk to consumer more than 90 hours after pasteurization, are constitutional, in spite of recent advances in methods of refrigeration for longer periods -- provision that such dating requirements do not apply to one-half pints or one-third quarts in automatic dispensing machines, is not unreasonably discriminatory against stores.

1. The mandatory milk-dating regulations of the Sanitary Code of the City of New York (§ 156, regulations 51, 154, 155), which in effect prohibit the sale of milk to a consumer more than 90 hours after pasteurization and of cream more than 108 hours after pasteurization, are valid and constitutional, even though recent advances in methods of refrigeration may keep milk and cream wholesome for longer periods.

2. The Sanitary Code provisions, that the dating requirements "shall not apply to one-third quart or one-half pint containers or bottles when such containers or bottles are dispensed through mechanically operated dispensing machines" (§ 156, reg. 155, subd. 8), do not unconstitutionally discriminate against stores and in favor of automatic [***2] vending machines. The legislative body was rationally impressed with the continuous refrigeration provided by the automatic vending machines; and at the same time the legislative body rationally saw fit to limit the machines' advantage to small sizes, since larger quantities in the hands of a consumer would be likely to deteriorate during the longer period of consumption.

Welton v. Lockport


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Niagara County


13 Misc. 2d 341; 177 N.Y.S.2d 438; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2812



August 19, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion granted, without costs. Prepare and submit order accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town board supervisor filed a motion for an order restraining defendant city from discontinuing water service or the furnishing of water in accordance with agreements in force between the parties in the supervisor's action for a declaratory judgment regarding the rates charged for the water.


OVERVIEW: At a regular meeting of the city's common council, the city adopted a resolution retroactively raising its water rates for water districts outside the city's limits. The town filed sought a declaratory judgment against the city and sought to restrain the city from discontinuing water service during the pendency of the action. Granting the motion, the court held that it would have been in the nature of a public calamity to have the water service discontinued during the time that might have been necessary to adjust the situation. The court ordered that the higher rates were to be paid during the pendency of the action without prejudice to either party.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion with the order that the higher rate was to be paid without prejudice to either party.


HEADNOTES

Injunctions -- furnishing of water -- plaintiff town alleges that defendant city threatens to discontinue water service being provided under contract unless new and higher rates are paid -- motion by plaintiff for order restraining city, during pendency of present action, from discontinuing water service granted, provided higher rates are paid, without prejudice to either party.

Contracts were executed by the Town Board of the Town of Lockport with the City of Lockport in behalf of two water districts, and payment has been made to defendant City of Lockport for said water districts at 40 cents a 100 cubic feet in accord with the contract. Defendant city claims to be entitled to 60 cents a 100 cubic feet on the basis of a change of rates. Plaintiff Town Board of the Town of Lockport claims that the change in rates violated the prior agreements and was discriminating and confiscatory, and alleges that defendant threatens to discontinue the water service unless the new rates are paid. A motion by plaintiff for an order restraining defendant city, during the pendency of the present action for a declaratory [***2] judgment, from discontinuing water service is granted, provided that the water rates of 60 cents a 100 cubic feet be paid, the payment to be without prejudice to either party. It would be in the nature of a public calamity to have the water service discontinued, and the granting of such a temporary injunction is within the discretion of the court.

Ballou v. Kelly


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Onondaga County


12 Misc. 2d 178; 176 N.Y.S.2d 1005; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2859



August 4, 1958 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner licensee, who had been arrested and charged with operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated and refused to submit to a chemical test, brought a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act. art. 78 that sought review of an order from respondent, the commissioner of motor vehicles, which temporarily suspended his operator's license.


OVERVIEW: The licensee was arrested and charged with operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, and he refused to submit to a chemical test. The commissioner of motor vehicles temporarily suspended his operator's license pending a hearing to revoke. The licensee sought review of the order, arguing that N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 71-a was unconstitutional. The previous version of the statute had been found unconstitutional because it permitted revocation of a license without providing for a lawful arrest and because it failed to afford the licensee an opportunity to be heard. The court dismissed the petition, holding that the amended version of the statute required a lawful arrest and provided an opportunity to be heard and therefore that it was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition for review.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Licenses -- operator's license -- temporary revocation -- Vehicle and Traffic Law ( § 71-a), which provides that, where Commissioner of Motor Vehicles acts on sworn report of police officer that he had reasonable grounds for believing operator of automobile was driving while intoxicated and police officer requested operator to submit to test to determine alcoholic content of blood after arrest and operator refused to submit, commissioner may temporarily revoke operator's license pending hearing to revoke it, not unconstitutional.

Petitioner was arrested and charged with operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 70, subd. 5). The arresting officer requested him to submit to a test to determine the alcoholic content of his blood, but petitioner refused to submit. The Commissioner of Motor Vehicles properly temporarily suspended petitioner's operator's license pending a hearing to revoke it. Section 71-a of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, which permits such temporary revocation, does not violate any constitutional guarantees. It provides for temporary revocation only where the test is demanded after a driver has been arrested, where the commissioner [***2] acts on a sworn report of the officer making the demand that he had reasonable grounds for believing petitioner was driving while intoxicated, and provides that the driver may have a hearing.

People v. Sisson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Schenectady County


12 Misc. 2d 18; 176 N.Y.S.2d 785; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2862



August 1, 1958 



DISPOSITION: Based upon the above findings, this court reverses the conviction of this defendant dated May 21, 1958, remits the fines imposed and directs that the convictions be expunged from the records of the Bureau of Motor Vehicles of the State of New York.

Submit order accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Court of Special Sessions of the Town of Glenville, County of Schenectady (New York), which convicted him of violation of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 15(1), having an inadequate muffler, and a violation of § 95-b, crossing white solid line or lines.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violation of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 15(1), having an inadequate muffler on his car and a violation of § 95-b, crossing white solid line or lines. At trial, the only testimony of inadequacy of the muffler was the statement of the state trooper that the noise from the exhaust of defendant's car was loud or excessively loud. There was no proof that the muffler was not in proper working order, that it was defective, or that it used a "cutout." The court reversed the conviction, holding that § 15(1) was unconstitutional because it set up no standards sufficient to define a violation thereof. The court further held that the information charging a violation of § 95-b was vague, indefinite, and defective in that from a reading of the text, defendant could not determine whether he was charged with the crossing of a single solid white line, double solid white lines, a solid white line and a broken white line, or a combination of the foregoing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction, remitted the fines imposed, and directed that the convictions be expunged from the records of the state bureau of motor vehicles.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- muffler -- Vehicle and Traffic Law ( § 15, subd. 1) under which defendant was charged with operating motor vehicle with inadequate muffler is unconstitutional in that it fails to set up standard sufficient to define violation thereof -- information charging violation of section 95-b of Vehicle and Traffic Law too vague and indefinite since defendant could not determine whether he was charged with crossing single solid white line, double solid white lines, solid white line and broken white line, or combination -- guilt beyond reasonable doubt not established.

1. Defendant was charged with a violation [***2] of subdivision 1 of section 15 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law in that he had an inadequate muffler. The only testimony of inadequacy was the statement of the State trooper that the noise from the exhaust from defendant's car was loud or excessively loud. The statute is unconstitutional in that it fails to set up any standard sufficient to define a violation thereof.

2. Defendant was charged with a violation of section 95-b of the Vehicle and Traffic Law (crossing white solid line or lines). The evidence failed to prove defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt and the information was vague, indefinite and defective. The testimony as to the crossing of the solid line or lines was rebutted to an extent that a reasonable doubt was raised. From a reading of the information, defendant could not determine whether he was charged with the crossing of a single solid white line, double solid white lines, a solid white line and a broken white line, or a combination thereof.

 

2580 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


New York Mobile Homes Asso. v. Steckel


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Equity Term, Monroe County


12 Misc. 2d 761; 176 N.Y.S.2d 482; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2896



July 24, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The complaint is dismissed with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town officers filed a motion to dismiss the complaint of plaintiffs, owners of trailer camps and landowners, which sought to declare unconstitutional 1954 N.Y. Laws 726, which amended N.Y. Tax Law § 2 by adding § 2(6-a).


OVERVIEW: The legislature passed a law that permitted the taxation of mobile homes and trailers. Plaintiffs filed an action to declare the taxation statute unconstitutional. Up to the time that the 1954 statute was passed, there was no tax. The statute was an attempt by the legislature to require, indirectly, the occupants of these homes to contribute to the expense of the privileges that everyone in their tax district enjoyed. The officers filed a motion to dismiss. The court dismissed the complaint. The court held that the owners were not permitted to maintain the action when their objection to it necessarily was that it could affect someone else. The owners owned trailer camps within the state, but neither of them demonstrated any financial interest in any property within the town. The court found that plaintiffs had no standing to attack the constitutionality of the statute because they did not prove that they sustained or were even threatened with any damage or loss by reason of it. The court concluded that the statute was constitutional and reasonable and should be upheld.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the complaint.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- trailers -- constitutional law -- subdivision 6-a of section 2 of Tax Law (added by L. 1954, ch. 726) defining real property as including trailers and providing for assessment of trailers to owners of real property on which they are located not unconstitutional -- trailers are as much real estate as are conventional homes and should be taxed accordingly -- corporate plaintiffs have no financial interest in property in town and complaint is dismissed -- neither remaining plaintiff, owner of land within town, nor corporate plaintiffs have suffered loss, damage or inconvenience from enforcement of statute and have no standing to attack the constitutionality of statute.

1. Chapter 726 of the Laws of 1954 amended section 2 of the Tax Law by adding thereto subdivision 6-a which reads as follows: "6-a. a. In addition to their meaning as provided in subdivision six, the terms, 'land,' 'real estate,' and 'real property,' as used in this chapter, include all the forms of housing which are adaptable to motivation by a power connected thereto or which may be propelled by a power within themselves and which are or can be used as a [***2] house or living abode or habitation of one or more persons, or for business, commercial or office purposes, either temporarily or permanently, and commonly called and hereafter referred to as 'trailers'; except (1) transient trailers which have been located within the boundaries of a tax district for less than sixty days and (2) trailers which are for sale and which are not occupied. b. Trailers shall be assessed to the owners of the real property on which they are located." The statute is not unconstitutional. Trailers for practical purposes are homes and are just as much a piece of real estate as the conventional home and should be taxed accordingly.

2. The two corporate plaintiffs, composed of owners of trailer camps, have not demonstrated any financial interest in any property within the town and the complaint is dismissed.

3. Neither the remaining plaintiff, owner of land within defendant town upon which are located sites for trailers, nor either of the corporations named as plaintiffs has suffered any loss, damage or inconvenience by reason of the administration or enforcement of the statute other than the necessity of payment by the owner of the land of increased taxes by [***3] reason of the fact that his land is occupied by trailers. Under the circumstances, plaintiffs have no standing to attack the constitutionality of the statute.

 

2581 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


North Hempstead v. Colonial Sand & Gravel Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


14 Misc. 2d 727; 178 N.Y.S.2d 579; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2923



July 17, 1958 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, three sand and gravel companies, motioned for summary judgment on their counterclaims and for judgment dismissing the complaint of plaintiff Town of North Hempstead (town), which had instituted an action against defendants who had been engaged in mining sand and gravel within the unincorporated area of the town. The town sought to enjoin defendants from further mining until they had obtained from the town a permit.


OVERVIEW: After the town instituted an action against defendants to enjoin them from conducting sand mining or excavation until they had obtained from the town a permit as required by its recently enacted ordinance. Town of Hempstead, N.Y., Ordinance Relating to Sand Bank and Pit, Topsoil Removal and Other Excavations (Jan. 8, 1946). Upon review, the court held that as a regulatory measure the town's license fee was restricted to an amount which would have compensated for having issued and having recorded the license and for having paid for inspection to see to the enforcing of the license provisions. Thus, as defendants appeared to be the only operators in the unincorporated area of the town, the town ordinance's levy of a charge of one cent on every cubic yard of sand or gravel removed was arbitrary, unreasonable, exorbitant and invalid. The court held that judgment on defendants' counterclaim was limited to the declaration that only that section that levied such charges was invalid and unenforceable as to defendants because the fee fixed therein was grossly excessive. The remainder of the ordinance was unaffected and was binding upon defendants.


OUTCOME: The court held that judgment on defendants' counterclaim was limited to the declaration that only that section that levied such charges was invalid and unenforceable as to defendants because the fee fixed therein was grossly excessive. The remainder of the ordinance was unaffected and was binding upon defendants.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- ordinance requiring license for excavations -- town validly enacted ordinance requiring license for excavations other than for buildings ( Town Law, § 130, subd. 23) -- sand and gravel mining corporations enjoined -- but excessive fee for license is invalid; however, this void part of ordinance can be excised -- defendants' prior uses, and town's grant of variance as to one property, immaterial; this is not zoning ordinance -- though action for injunction is not listed in rule 113 (Rules Civ. Prac.), and plaintiff has not moved for summary judgment, court grants summary judgment on defendants' counterclaim to extent of invalidating license fee, and awards to town summary judgment enjoining defendants from excavating without license.

1. Under the Town Law ( § 130, subd. 23; cf. Village Law, § 89, subd. 67) the Town of North Hempstead in Nassau County validly enacted the following ordinance: § 1. "It is hereby declared to be the policy of the Town * * * to prevent * * * excavations which create pits, holes or hollows in the earth, leaving it in a hazardous or dangerous state, or cause soil erosion which depletes the land of its natural vegetative cover [***2] and supply of organic material, renders such land unproductive and unsuitable for agricultural purposes and undesirable for building homes, resulting in lower land values * * * danger of health and life * * * damage to agricultural crops through dust storms * * * wind action, and * * * pools of water, which ordinance will promote the safety, health and general welfare of the people of the Town." § 2. "No excavation for purposes other than the construction of a wall, driveway, sidewalk, building or part thereof * * * shall be commenced except in conformity with the provisions of this article." § 3. "Before any excavation be commenced * * * the owner, lessee or agent of the premises shall obtain a written permit therefor from the Town Board." § 4. "No such excavation shall be made: (a) Within Twenty (20) feet of any property line and must not be greater than 10 feet below the established grade, unless the sidewalls remain at an incline of at least 45 degrees or are supported by retaining equipment equal to that spcified for building excavations, except in the case of bank excavations same may begin at the property line."

2. The town is granted summary judgment enjoining the three [***3] corporate defendants, who appear to be the only sand and gravel mining operators in the unincorporated area of the town, from continuing their operations unless they obtain a permit from the Town Board.

3. But section 7 of the ordinance, which imposes a license fee of "$ 200 for an excavation volume not to exceed 20,000 cu. yds. * * * plus one cent for each additional cu. yd.", is exorbitant and invalid. The affidavits and the pretrial examination of the town supervisor show that the license fee was intended, not as a tax, but as compensation for the town's expense of inspections and administration. The town estimates such expense at $ 6,100 a year; the defendants estimate it at $ 1,500 a year. At one cent a cubic yard on defendants' average yearly operations, the license fees would amount to about $ 34,000. As a regulatory measure, a license fee must be limited to an amount which will compensate for issuing, inspecting and enforcing.

4. However, the invalid section can be excised without affecting the valid sections.

5. It is immaterial that the defendants have been operating in this town for years before the enactment of the ordinance and assertedly have made no excavations [***4] which violate section 4 of the ordinance. They must get a permit for any further excavations, including bank excavations.

6. Likewise immaterial is the fact that the town's Board of Appeals, after the enactment of this ordinance, granted to defendants' predecessor a variance for the mining of sand and gravel on certain premises for 15 years. The ordinance in suit is not a zoning ordinance (under Town Law, § 261) but a regulatory ordinance (under § 130, subd. 23).

7. On defendants' motion for summary judgment under rule 113 of the Rules of Civil Practice the court may and does grant summary judgment to plaintiff even without a cross motion therefor. Although an action for an injunction is not one of those actions enumerated in rule 113, such procedure in this instance is allowable. The town is granted summary judgment of injunction, and the defendants are granted summary judgment on their counterclaim, declaring the invalidity of section 7.

 

2582 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lewis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Orange County


12 Misc. 2d 266; 176 N.Y.S.2d 136; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2962



July 8, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The other relief applied for is hereby denied.

Submit order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of manslaughter on the first degree, applied for an order directing the delivery to him of a copy of the stenographic minutes of his trial without cost for use in his appeal. The appeals court had granted defendant leave to appeal as a poor person.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been granted leave to appeal his manslaughter conviction as a poor person, and he sought a free transcript of his proceedings. The transcript had also been filed in the office of the county clerk. Defendant's attorney had not been paid and had expended substantial out-of-pocket sums, and obtaining the recorded transcript would impose an additional burden because the county clerk was 40 miles away. The court held that it had the discretionary authority to order that a transcript be provided to indigent defendants at public expense. However, the court held that such power was only to be exercised where there was satisfactory proof that defendant was completely without funds, that defendant's attorney had not been and would not be compensated in any way for the services that he rendered, and that the appeals court had granted leave to defendant to appeal as a poor person.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's application.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- right to minutes of trial without cost -- defendant, who was convicted of manslaughter in first degree and has been granted leave to appeal to Appellate Division as poor person, is entitled to receive copy of stenographic minutes without cost -- original minutes were filed and right of defendant to appeal has not been defeated but, unless minutes are furnished free of cost, defendant would be unable to make effective use of right to appeal -- court has inherent power to grant relief -- power should be exercised where defendant is without funds, his attorney will not be compensated, Appellate Division has granted leave to appeal as poor person, and substantial questions are involved.

1. Defendant was convicted of manslaughter in the first degree and is now serving an indeterminate term in prison. From the conviction and sentence he has been granted leave to appeal by the Appellate Division as a poor person. His present attorney has received no compensation and is regarded as if he were an assigned counsel. A motion by defendant for an order directing the delivery to him of a copy of the stenographic [***2] minutes of the trial without cost is granted.

2. The original minutes of the trial had been filed in the County Clerk's office, and the right of defendant to appeal has not been defeated by the failure to file the record. Accordingly, Griffin v. Illinois (351 U.S. 12) and People v. Pride (3 N Y 2d 545) do not require the granting of the requested relief.

3. On the other hand, unless defendant is furnished the minutes free, defendant will be unable to make effective use of the right to appeal. Defendant has no funds and is at present in prison and unable personally to inspect the minutes. It would be a great hardship on his attorney to undertake the task of making copies of the minutes. The court has inherent power to grant the relief sought in a proper case as an incident to the duty of the court to provide defendant in a criminal case with effective means to obtain ultimate justice. The provisions in section 308 of the Code of Criminal Procedure making the exercise of this power mandatory in a first degree murder case do not deprive the courts of their inherent powers in other cases.

4. The exercise of this power should be limited to a case where there is proof [***3] that defendant is without funds, that defendant's attorney was not, has not been and will not be compensated for the services which he has rendered, and that the Appellate Division shall have granted leave to defendant to appeal as a poor person. It should also appear that there are substantial questions involved in the appeal, and that the record cannot be made available to defendant except at public expense. The present application meets that test.

 

2583 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Mallinson v. Tarrytown


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Westchester County


14 Misc. 2d 5; 177 N.Y.S.2d 384; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2967



July 7, 1958 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners brought a declaratory judgment against defendants, a village and other interested parties, seeking to declare the village's zoning unconstitutional to the extent that it zoned the landowners' property residential.


OVERVIEW: The landowners' had historically used their property at the intersection of two roads as a hotel and a gasoline station. However, the village, over the objections of the landowners, zoned their property as residential. Property near that owned by the landowners was both residential and commercial. The landowners claimed that their property could not be used as an apartment house and that the residential zoning decreased the value of their property by over 90 percent. The court dismissed the landowners' complaint. It held that zoning regulations were permitted to decrease the value of property. The court ruled that the landowners were factually wrong when they claimed that they could not construct an apartment building under the residential zoning because the setback that governed the landowners' parcel did enable the landowners to construct an apartment. Thus, the landowners had failed to establish by a fair preponderance of the credible evidence that the zoning determination of the village was arbitrary, capricious or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the landowners' declaratory judgment complaint.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- plaintiffs failed to establish that their land could not reasonably and profitably be used in conformity with village zoning ordinance placing property in residence district; in action for judgment declaring ordinance unconstitutional as applied to plaintiffs' property, complaint dismissed.

1. Plaintiffs failed to demonstrate by credible evidence that their land could not reasonably and profitably be used in conformity with a village zoning ordinance placing their property in a "Residence C" district, and in plaintiffs' action for a judgment declaring the statute unconstitutional and void insofar as it restricted their property to the uses allowed in such a district, the complaint was dismissed.

2. Zoning is a legislative function and a zoning ordinance or an amendment thereto is presumed to be valid. The burden of proving the invalidity of a zoning ordinance or an amendment thereto is upon the party who assails its validity, and that party must show by a fair preponderance of the credible evidence that the zoning determination of the legislative body was arbitrary, capricious or unreasonable. If the validity of the legislative classification [***2] for zoning purposes is fairly debatable, the judgment of the legislative body is conclusive and beyond interference by the courts.

3. A municipality is not required to zone property so as to produce the highest return for the owner. Evidence that property zoned for residential use would be worth a great deal more if zoned for business did not establish the unreasonableness of the zoning ordinance. All zoning regulations may depreciate property values.

 

2584 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Gardner v. Le Boeuf


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


14 Misc. 2d 98; 177 N.Y.S.2d 643; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3055



June 20, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, since the facts stated are insufficient to constitute a cause of action both as to the unreasonableness of the zoning and the unavailability or the exhaustion of administrative remedies, the motion is granted with leave to serve an amended complaint within 20 days after service of a copy of the order entered hereon.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant village board of trustees filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff property owner's complaint on the ground that the property owner failed to state facts sufficient to state a cause of action. The property owner instituted an action seeking a declaration that a village ordinance restricting the use of her property to detached single-family residences was null and void.


OVERVIEW: The property owner alleged that due to heavy traffic on the highways bordering her property and the existence of business uses near her property, her property was no longer suitable to one-acre residential use. The board filed a motion to dismiss asserting that the property owner failed to allege facts supporting her claim that the ordinance was confiscatory and that the property owner's complaint failed to allege the exhaustion of administrative remedies. The court held that the facts stated in the complaint were insufficient to constitute a cause of action as to the reasonableness of the zoning ordinance. The court found that the property owner failed to allege facts showing that the property could not be reasonably used for residential purposes or that the property could not be successfully sold as residential property. The property owner also failed to set forth facts as to the property's value. The court also held that the property owner failed to allege the exhaustion of administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court granted the board's motion with leave for the property owner to serve an amended complaint.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- complaint seeking declaration of present unsuitability and unconstitutionality of 32-year-old zone classification restricting any buildings to one-family residences on acre plots, on asserted grounds of present heavy and increasing traffic on arterial highways and increasing business uses in neighborhood, must allege facts as to attempts to sell or as to comparative values for residential and business purposes or as to other residences in zone or other facts to support plaintiff's burden of proving present unconstitutionality beyond reasonable doubt -- complaint must also allege that application for variance was denied; not enough to allege application for reclassification.

1. In an action for a judgment annulling a zoning ordinance enacted 32 years ago which restricts any buildings in a certain zone to one-family [***2] residences on plots of at least one acre, as now being utterly unsuitable, confiscatory and unconstitutional, on the grounds that heavy and increasing traffic on three arterial highways bordering plaintiff's 16 1/2-acre property causes noise, dirt, congestion and air-pollution and that businesses and high-density zoning have been established in the adjoining neighborhoods, the complaint must at least allege facts showing unsuccessful attempts to sell all or part of plaintiff's property for residential purposes, or facts showing that experts in the home development field have advised plaintiff that any residences erected on her property could not be sold with a reasonable profit, or facts showing the value of her property as now zoned and its value if zoned for business, or facts showing that residences have not been built recently along these highways on other parcels in this zone, or that old dwellings on other parcels in this zone have been abandoned for residential use, or other factual criteria which would tend to support plaintiff's burden of proving unconstitutionality beyond a reasonable doubt.

2. The complaint must also allege that plaintiff has applied for, and has been denied,  [***3] a hardship variance as to use. It is not enough that plaintiff has applied for a rezoning and that the board has taken no action thereon.

 

2585 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brooklyn News Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Kings County


12 Misc. 2d 768; 174 N.Y.S.2d 813; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3177



June 4, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The verdict is not guilty.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were indicted for publishing and distributing an obscene magazine in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 1141.


OVERVIEW: Defendants published and distributed a magazine called "Gent," which contained art and stories. Defendants were indicted for publishing and distributing obscene material in violation of § 1141. Upon review, the court entered a verdict holding that defendants were not guilty of obscenity pursuant to § 1141. The court ruled that § 1141 required proof that the publisher, printer, distributor, or seller of a publication knew that the publication was obscene. The court determined that there was insufficient proof to establish that defendants knew that the magazine was obscene. The court held that the test for obscenity was whether to the average person, applying contemporary community standards, the dominant theme of the material taken as a whole appealed to prurient interests. The court ruled that only smut or pornography was punishable by § 1141, and that smut or pornography was material with a dominant purpose of inciting sexual desire. The court determined that the art and stories in the magazine were not obscene within the meaning of § 1141.


OUTCOME: The court entered a verdict holding that defendants were not guilty of publishing and distributing an obscene magazine.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- obscenity -- defendants not guilty of charge that in publishing magazine "Gent" they violated section 1141 of Penal Law which provides for punishment for printing, publishing, possession with intent to distribute or sell, distributing and selling any "obscene, lewd, lascivious, filthy, indecent, sadistic, masochistic or disgusting" magazines -- insufficient proof that individual officers of publishing or distributing corporation knew contents of magazine -- words in statute synonymous with "obscene" -- only sexual impure (smut or pornography) punishable under statute -- smut or pornography is writing whose purpose and actual effect is incitement to sexual desire -- magazine not obscene in art or stories -- knowledge of obscene contents must be proved -- book reviews may be received in evidence -- evidence of expert witnesses proper -- comparison with similar material previously adjudicated is proper.

1. Defendants are found not guilty upon a charge that in publishing a magazine "Gent" they violated section 1141 of the Penal Law. The statute provides for punishment for printing, publishing, possession with intent to distribute or sell,  [***2] distributing and selling any "obscene, lewd, lascivious, filthy, indecent, sadistic, masochistic or disgusting" magazines.

2. There is insufficient proof to establish that the individual officers of the publishing or distributing corporation knew the contents of the magazine.

3. The words in the statute are synonymous with "obscene".

4. Only the sexual impure -- smut or pornography -- can be punished under the statute.

5. Smut and pornography is defined as any writing whose purpose and actual effect is incitement to sexual desire. If its purpose is to reflect life with reasonable accuracy and balance, it is not obscenity.

6. The magazine judged by the applicable standards is not obscene in its art or its stories.

7. Knowledge of the obscene contents of the writing must be proved.

8. Book reviews may be received in evidence.

9. Evidence of expert witnesses is proper.

10. Comparison of the material with other similar material previously adjudicated is proper.

 

2586 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Hempstead T-W Corp. v. Hempstead


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, Nassau County


13 Misc. 2d 1054; 177 N.Y.S.2d 445; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3233



May 27, 1958 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tow car operators filed an action against defendant town to have a town ordinance governing the operation of tow cars declared unconstitutional and void and for an injunction to prohibit enforcement of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The tow car operators argued that an ordinance that prevented them from going to the scene of an accident to solicit business was unconstitutional. The court disagreed. The court held that the ordinance did not prohibit the use of public streets to tow cars nor did it prohibit all solicitation of towing work. It prohibited unregulated solicitation that interfered with the free choice by the damaged car owner to properly protect himself from tow car operators racing to the scene of an accident to solicit business and the resultant interference traffic and police investigations. The court rejected the tow car operators' claim of unconstitutionality to portions of the ordinance that did not affect them. They were not aggrieved. The provision prohibiting transfer of the tow car operators' licenses was constitutional because the city had the right to know and to determine who the licensees would be. Provisions requiring disclosure of convictions were valid because a mechanism for due process was included in the ordinance. The tow car operators' attacks on other provisions of the ordinance were likewise rejected. The court held that the ordinance was valid and constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court held that the tow car operators failed to sustain their burden of proof to show that a town ordinance governing tow car operators was unconstitutional and invalid. The court sustained the ordinance as reasonable and constitutional.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Motor vehicles -- constitutionality of ordinance licensing and regulating tow-car business -- town ordinance requiring tow-car operators to apply for licenses and to report summonses, arrests and convictions, and to file schedule of fees, and prohibiting them from refusing request to tow at those fees, and forbidding them to solicit business at scene of accident, or to make immediate agreement for repair of vehicle of hospitalized owner, or to remove vehicle unless so authorized on prescribed form by owner or person in charge, or to remove vehicle in which death or injury occurred unless police authorize removal, and prohibiting transfers of licenses and requiring surrender of license if tow car is disposed of, all constitutional.

1. An ordinance is presumed to be supported by facts known to the legislative body, as is any legislation. The legislation must be reasonably related to some reasonably apprehended evil, but any unconstitutionality must be demonstrated beyond a reasonable doubt, and a court will strike down a legislative enactment only as a last resort.

2. Plaintiffs are licensed tow-car owners and operators in the Town of Hempstead, Nassau County. On the average [***2] in Hempstead, five or six competing tow cars arrive at the scene of an accident, each with a crew of two or three men. Sometimes 15 operators mill around the scene and try to solicit the dazed or emotionally upset motorist who has just suffered an accident. They interfere with the policeman who is trying to gather the evidence at the scene. They often race to the scene and violate speed laws, and often interfere with traffic at the scene. Plaintiffs concede that legislative regulation is needed. The town has enacted Ordinance No. 40, which declares the background facts (§ 1.0) and which validly and reasonably provides as follows: (§ 12.0) "It shall be unlawful for any person to drive along any street or bridge in the Town of Hempstead and solicit towing work. Solicitation of towing work by the operator or other occupant of a tow car while parked on any street or bridge is also prohibited. A tow car operator shall not proceed to the scene of a disabled motor vehicle without having been requested or notified to do so by the owner or his authorized representative or the Police. Responding to a call, merely upon notification from gas station attendants, taxicab drivers or other [***3] unauthorized persons shall be considered in violation of this provision"; and (§ 12.1) "The owner or driver of any disabled motor vehicle shall have the right to require the services of any available tow car and it shall be unlawful for any owner or driver, or helper of any tow car to refuse to render such services if such owner or driver of such disabled motor vehicle is able and willing to pay the fee prescribed in the schedule of prices filed by the owner of such tow car with the Town Clerk provided, however, that it is physically possible for such tow car to tow such disabled motor vehicle and that such tow car is not already going to or returning from a job."

3. Of course, ordinances of the town do not apply to the incorporated villages or to the cities; but that does not render this ordinance discriminatory and unconstitutional.

4. The fact that a better ordinance could have been drafted does not render the one enacted unconstitutional.

5. Similar ordinances in cities of Texas and Tennessee have been held constitutional by the highest courts of those States.

6. The licensing requirements of the ordinance (§§ 3.2, 3.5, 3.6, 3.8, 3.9, 4.2, 4.4, 5.0) and the provisions for [***4] suspension or revocation (§§ 9.0, 9.1) and the requirement that summonses and arrests be reported to the town clerk (§ 11.2) are reasonable, constitutional, and authorized by the Town Law ( § 137), which empowers a town clerk to refuse to issue a license to a person who has been convicted of felony or misdemeanor or whom he deems undesirable or incapable to carry on the licensed business, and provides for a hearing and review of such refusal by the town board and then for review by the court by a proceeding under article 78 of the Civil Practice Act.

7. The ordinance (§ 3.13), like the Town Law ( § 137), validly makes a license nontransferable.

8. The ordinance (§ 10.5) validly requires that the license for each tow car be surrendered within 24 hours after that tow car is disposed of.

9. The ordinance (§ 12.5) properly makes it unlawful for anyone to enter into an agreement for the repair or estimate of repairs of a vehicle when the owner is to be hospitalized, until 24 hours after the accident, unless the injured person has been discharged from the hospital in the meantime.

10. The ordinance (§ 11.1) validly prohibits tow cars from removing a vehicle which has been damaged [***5] in an accident in which a person has been killed or injured, until such removal has been allowed by the Nassau County Police Department.

11. The ordinance (§§ 11.1, 12.6) validly prohibits the removal of vehicles disabled in an accident, unless authorized on a prescribed form by the owner or party in charge. Of course, the police could nevertheless validly order the removal of a damaged vehicle.

 

2587 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Merry


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Justice Court of New York, Town of Lowville, Lewis County


12 Misc. 2d 20; 178 N.Y.S.2d 454; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3226



May 27, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Defendant's motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for the dismissal of the information after he was charged with a violation of the Muffler Law found in N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 15(1). Defendant asserted that the relevant statute violated the Due Process Clause of the Constitution for vagueness of standard of conduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with a violation of the Muffler Law, which provided that every motor vehicle should have a suitable muffler or device to prevent unnecessary noise from exhaust gases. Defendant filed a motion for the dismissal of the information on the ground that the relevant statute violated the Due Process Clause of the Constitution for vagueness of standard of conduct. The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss and held that the Muffler Law did not violate the Due Process Clause of the Constitution because the term "unnecessary noise" was not improperly vague, as it could be defined as that noise which was not required by the usual circumstances. The court further found that it was for the trier of facts to determine whether or not the noise in question was usual after all circumstances had been considered.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion for the dismissal of the information after he was charged with a violation of the Muffler Law on the ground that the relevant statute violated the Due Process Clause of the Constitution for vagueness of standard of conduct.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- muffler -- statute (Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 15, subd. 1) which provides that "Every such motor vehicle, also, shall have a suitable muffler or device to prevent unnecessary noise from exhaust gases" not unconstitutional -- word "unnecessary" provides sufficient standard of conduct.

A motion by defendant to dismiss the information which charges defendant with a violation of the Vehicle and Traffic Law ( § 15, subd. 1) which provides that "Every such motor vehicle, also, shall have a suitable muffler or device to prevent unnecessary noise from exhaust gases" on the ground that the statute violates the Due Process Clause of the Constitution for vagueness of the standard of conduct is denied. The statute is constitutional. The word "unnecessary" is used in a great number of statutes and is a sufficient standard of conduct.

 

2588 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bowen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Special Sessions of the City of New York, Appellate Part, First Department


11 Misc. 2d 462; 175 N.Y.S.2d 125; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3282



May 21, 1958 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of judgments of the Manhattan District Magistrates' Courts of the City of New York (New York), which convicted them of acting as sightseeing guides without being licensed as such by the commissioner of licenses of the City of New York.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were Pennsylvania residents who worked for a Pennsylvania tour company. During a trip that started and ended in Pennsylvania, defendants conducted a tour in New York City without a license. Defendants were convicted of acting as sightseeing guides without being licensed by the City, and the court reversed their convictions. The court held that New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code art. 12, ch. 32, §§ B32-75.0, -76.0, -77.0, did not constitute an undue burden on interstate commerce because the interstate character of the tour was interrupted by the purely local side trip. The court found that the local regulation was not preempted by federal legislation. The court held that the licensing of sightseeing guides fell within the police powers of the local government. The court concluded that the City had the power to license the guides and to prescribe reasonable standards and qualifications as prerequisites to the granting of the licenses. The court held that the two-year residence requirement of § B32-77.0 was invalid because it discriminated against nonresidents of the City and residence had little relationship to a detailed knowledge of local physical and historical geography.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial courts' judgments.


HEADNOTES

Licenses -- sightseeing guides -- provisions of New York City Administrative Code regulating licensing of sightseeing guides not undue burden on interstate commerce as applied to defendants, Pennsylvania residents who guided in New York City passengers transported in busses operated by Federally authorized transportation company on round-trip tour which originated in Philadelphia -- licensing and regulation of sightseeing guides within police power of City of New York -- requirement that applicant for licensing as sightseeing guide be resident of City of New York for two years, invalid -- conviction of defendants for acting as sightseeing guides without license reversed, fines remitted and complaints dismissed.

1. Provisions of the New York City Administrative Code (ch. 32, art. 12) regulating the qualifications and licensing of sightseeing guides [***2] did not constitute an undue burden on interstate commerce as applied to defendants, Pennsylvania residents employed by a Pennsylvania corporation licensed by the Interstate Commerce Commission, who guided in Battery Park, New York City, though not licensed by New York City as guides, a tour of passengers transported in busses operated by a Federally authorized transportation company on a round-trip tour which originated and terminated in Philadelphia. The interstate character of the tour was interrupted upon its arrival at Battery Park, where passengers left the busses to view local points of interest, and in any event the requirement that all sightseeing guides in New York City be licensed was not an undue interference with interstate commerce. The field was not one pre-empted by Federal legislation so that local regulation was excluded.

2. The licensing of sightseeing guides in a large metropolis falls within the police powers of the local government. The City of New York had the power to license guides and to prescribe reasonable standards and qualifications as prerequisites to the granting of licenses.

3. A requirement of the Administrative Code that applicants for licensing [***3] as sightseeing guides be residents of the City of New York for two years, as applied to defendants, was invalid. Unless residence within the city presents a clear-cut reasonable basis for distinction between persons seeking to pursue the same occupation within the city, a requirement of residence as a prerequisite to practising such occupation must fail.

4. Judgment of conviction of defendants for acting as sightseeing guides without the license required by the Administrative Code was reversed, the fine remitted to each defendant and each complaint dismissed.

 

2589 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Caliendo v. McFarland


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, New York County


13 Misc. 2d 183; 175 N.Y.S.2d 869; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3292; 42 L.R.R.M. 2235



May 20, 1958 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff union shop stewards brought an action that sought to permanently restrain defendants, the union, its executive board, and other union members, from permitting a special meeting for the purpose of electing new shop stewards on a company-wide basis because it contravened the union's constitution and by-laws. Several union members had proposed the special meeting and the executive board had implicitly condoned it.


OVERVIEW: The union's constitution and by-laws provided that there must be a steward for each barn within the company and that said steward was to be appointed by the union. Prior to the dispute, the union's practice had always been to elect each barn's shop steward from the union employees that worked in that barn. On review, the court held for the union shop stewards and restrained defendants from the company-wide elections. The court found that the threatened company-wide elections were a change in constitutional practice which required an amendment to the constitution that had not been accomplished. The court held that it would look to the union and its members' conduct with regard to the election procedures because the constitution did not contain specific procedures or requirements for elections. The court found that the practice was clearly to elect the shop stewards from the barn which they represented, and not to have company-wide elections. The court also held that the union shop stewards were not required to exhaust all remedies within the union before seeking equitable relief because the union had not acted within the scope of its powers under the union constitution and by-laws.


OUTCOME: The court found for the union shop stewards and permanently restrained defendants from having company-wide elections unless and until appropriate amendment was made to the union constitution.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Labor unions -- rights of members under union's constitution -- union's constitution is contract equitably enforcible by member -- union's constitution provides for "steward for each barn" of any employer and that stewards have seniority in case of layoffs; practical construction for many years has been for executive board to appoint 18 shop stewards, one from among each of employer's 18 barns, and to require seniority provision for them in union's collective bargaining agreement with employer; bargaining committee, with acquiescence of executive board, is calling special meeting of all union members to elect shop stewards on company-wide basis; 4 present shop stewards, plaintiffs, are granted permanent injunction against such violation of union's constitution, unless and until such constitution is properly amended.

1. The constitution and by-laws of an unincorporated labor union are a binding contract between the union and its members and among its members, and members of the union may seek a decree in equity against the union or against other members so as to enforce their rights under such constitution and by-laws.

2. The constitution and by-laws of defendant local union [***2] provide that "there must be a steward for each barn [of an employer], said steward to be appointed by the local Union". The document is silent as to the manner of appointment. But its practical construction is shown by the uniform course of conduct of the union for many years. The local union's executive board has always appointed a shop steward for each of the employer's separate barns, and, in each case, from the ranks of the employees in the particular barn. The union constitution provides that the "steward shall be the last man to be laid off"; and this seniority is reaffirmed in the union's collective bargaining agreement with the employer. The constitution further empowers only the executive board to call special meetings of the union's members, and to transact all necessary union business between meetings. Nevertheless, the individual defendants, who are not on the executive board but who merely comprise a collective bargaining negotiating committee, recently posted in all the barns a notice calling for a special meeting of the union's members employed by a certain employer, for the purpose of electing shop stewards on a company-wide basis, instead of, as heretofore,  [***3] a steward in and for each of this employer's 18 barns. Plaintiffs are 4 of the present 18 stewards, and they sue individually and on behalf of all others similarly situated, for an injunction against any such special meeting or election. After trial, plaintiffs are granted such a permanent injunction, unless and until the union's constitution is amended by the amendment procedures therein provided so as to allow such company-wide election of shop stewards.

3. It is not necessary for a union member first to exhaust his remedies within the union, if the union is acting in violation of its own constitution. However, plaintiffs did protest orally and in writing to the local union's executive board and to the president of the union's joint council and to the vice-president of the international union, but received only noncommittal answers and the information that the union was paying for this meeting hall and that similar notices had been posted in the barns of other employers with whom the union had contracts, and that company-wide stewards had already been elected in such other companies in place of the former separate stewards for each separate barn. It appears further that the [***4] present notice falsely states that a recently concluded contract with this employer requires that shop stewards be elected on a company-wide basis. It is evident that plaintiffs have exhausted all reasonable efforts and that further appeals to defendant union's officials would be fruitless.

4. Plaintiffs have a property right for which they have no adequate remedy at law. Only an injunction in equity will prevent irreparable injury to their right.

5. This intra-union dispute is not a labor dispute within section 876-a of the Civil Practice Act.

 

2590 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Windsor Madison Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Magistrates' Court of New York, Borough of Manhattan
