12 Misc. 2d 446; 173 N.Y.S.2d 964; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3406



May 5, 1958 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged under New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § B32-207.0 with publicizing and conducting a "forced out of business sale" without a license. Though he had applied for a license, it was denied, and the denial was upheld on appeal. In defense, he claimed that § B32-207.0 was an improper exercise of police power, violated his constitutional rights to free speech, equal protection, and due process, and violated N.Y. Const. art. I, § 6.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was denied a license for a "forced out of business sale," and after the supreme court rejected an appeal of the denial, defendant proceeded to advertise and hold the sale anyway. When cited with nine violations of Admin. Code § B32-207.0, he sought dismissal of the charges on claims that § B32-207.0 was unconstitutional under federal and state constitutions. The court rejected all of his arguments and entered convictions on eight of the nine citations, dismissing the ninth for lack of sufficient evidence. The court held that the regulation constituted a valid exercise of the city's police power because its object was the prevention of fraud on the public. Because it was a valid exercise of police power, it followed that its enforcement did not deprive defendant of any constitutionally cognizable property interest and therefore did not violate state or federal due process clauses. The court also rejected claims that defendant was denied equal protection because all persons except those acting under court orders and auctioneers (who were subject to special licensing) were covered. Defendant's freedom of speech claim was given short shrift and rejected as well.


OUTCOME: The court convicted defendant of eight violations of the regulation. As to the ninth claimed violation, the court found that there was insufficient evidence of defendant's guilt thereon and discharged defendant on that citation.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- conducting sale without license -- defendant was convicted on seven of eight summonses of violating section B32-207.0 of Administrative Code of City of New York in that it unlawfully published and conducted "forced out of business sale" without license -- proof as to eighth summons insufficient -- statute not unconstitutional.

1. Defendant is convicted on seven of eight summonses of violating section B32-207.0 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York in that it unlawfully published and conducted a "forced out of business sale" without a license.

2. The proof on the eighth summons consisted of testimony that an advertisement had appeared in a New York newspaper bearing the name and address of the defendant, and advertising a "forced out of business sale". No proof was offered as to who placed the advertisement or who paid for it. The proof on this violation was insufficient.

3. The statute is not unconstitutional. It was the intention of the statute to protect the public from the consequences of fraud, by requiring merchants who represent that they intend to dispose of their entire stock of merchandise and go out of business thereafter to submit proof [***2] as to the truth of the representations. The license fee imposed was a reasonable charge for the cost of investigation. The statute does not interfere with defendant's right to sell its goods nor does it impair its freedom to determine the price at which it will sell them. Defendant is not deprived of the equal protection of the laws. The statute does not deny defendant its right to freedom of speech and freedom of the press.

 

2591 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Adlerstein v. New York, Dep't of Water Supply, Gas & Electricity


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


11 Misc. 2d 754; 174 N.Y.S.2d 610; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3439



April 29, 1958 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff electricians brought an action against defendant city seeking an injunction and a declaration that New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § B30-14.10 be declared unconstitutional. Both parties moved for judgment on the pleadings.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § B30-14 that charged a licensing fee to electricians. The fee was to compensate the licensing authority for issuing and recording the license and pay for inspections to see to the enforcing of the license provisions. A group of electricians sought a declaration that the statute was unconstitutional and sought an injunction. Both parties moved for judgment on the pleadings. The court found that the statute was unconstitutional but dismissed that portion of the complaint seeking an injunction. The court found that the inspections referred to had nothing to do with licensing. The inspections were for the purpose of protecting the city's inhabitants from inferior workmanship. The court found that this expense would have been precisely the same whether the artisans doing the work were licensed or not. The court found that an electrical contractor with business in the millions paid exactly the same for the inspection of his work as a shop proprietor who grossed a few thousands. The court held that there was no constitutional warrant for putting the expense of regulating the business of electricians in the guise of a license fee.


OUTCOME: The court found the statute unconstitutional but the portion of the complaint seeking an injunction was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- licensing of electricians -- constitutional law -- Local Law No. 3 of 1957 of City of New York, providing for licensing of electricians and for fee of $ 250, is unconstitutional -- no constitutional warrant for putting expense of regulating business of electricians in guise of license fee.

1. Plaintiffs seek a declaration of unconstitutionality of Local Law No. 3 of 1957 of the City of New York, which provides for the licensing of electricians and for a fee of $ 250, and of the prior section which provides a fee of $ 100. This is not a revenue statute. The fee which may be charged for the issuance of a license is such as will compensate the licensing authority for issuing and recording the license and pay for inspection to see to the enforcing of the license provisions. The cost in 1956 for the inspection of all electrical installments was $ 892,365.50, while the license revenue was $ 234,600. Under the $ 250 fee the return would still be less than the cost, but these figures are irrelevant. The inspections are for the purpose of protecting the city's inhabitants from the dangers of inferior workmanship. This expense would be the same and equally [***2] necessary whether the electricians were licensed or not. A large electrical contractor pays exactly the same for the inspection of his work as a small contractor. There is no constitutional warrant for putting the expense of regulating the business of electricians in the guise of a license fee. The statute is unconstitutional.

2. The court will not fix the fee or limit the Legislature in advance. When a fee is fixed, if challenged, it must be passed on but in advance there is no judicial authority.

3. Plantiffs' motion is granted but only to the extent that it seeks a declaration. The portion of the complaint which seeks an injunction is dismissed.

 

2592 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wright


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Special Sessions of the City of New York, New York County


12 Misc. 2d 961; 173 N.Y.S.2d 160; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3473



April 22, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly the demurrer is disallowed in its entirety and the defendant's motion is in all respects denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in a seven-count information with violating N.Y. Penal Law § 964-a and with making a false statement in writing for the purpose of procuring property and credit. He demurred to the charges, seeking their dismissal on various grounds, including on the grounds that § 964-a violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, U.S Const. amend XIV, and N.Y. Const. art. I, § 11, art. III, § 1, and art. III, § 17.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with having held himself out as an employee of the United Nations in connection with a credit purchase of an encyclopedia. He sought dismissal, claiming that N.Y. Penal Law § 964-a violated sundry state and federal constitutional provisions. Applying the rule that an inferior court was not to declare a statute unconstitutional unless its flaws were clear, the court rejected the attacks on §964-a and held that it was constitutional. In specific, the court found no violation of the federal constitutional treaty provision because the statute did not require the State to enter into an agreement with a foreign power. Nor was there any basis to the claim that it violated the federal or state constitution due process or equal protection clauses. The court rejected a defense claim that the legislature had unlawfully delegated authority to the Secretary General of the United Nations for the use of the name "United Nations" or that it had granted an exclusive privilege or franchise to a private individual. The court also found that the language of the seventh count was perfectly adequate because it followed the specific language of N.Y. Penal Law § 1293-b, subd. 1.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss all seven charges brought against him in connection with his use of the name of the "United Nations" in connection with a commercial undertaking.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- unauthorized use of name of "United Nations" -- Penal Law ( § 964-a) which makes it misdemeanor to use name "United Nations" without authority of Secretary General thereof is constitutional.

1. Section 964-a of the Penal Law, which makes it a misdemeanor to adopt and use the name "United Nations" or any abbreviation thereof without express authority from the Secretary General of the United Nations is constitutional. There is nothing in section 964-a which requires the making of any agreement or treaty between the State of New York and the United Nations, and, therefore, the consent of the Congress was unnecessary. Defendant, who was charged with violating the section, was not denied the equal protection of the laws or deprived of his property without due process of law. That the statute requires that authority for the use of the name "United Nations" be obtained from the Secretary General of that body, does not constitute delegation of legislative power to him. It is the statute, enacted by the Legislature, which defines the unauthorized use of the [***2] name as a misdemeanor. Accordingly, defendant's motion to dismiss the first six counts of the information which charged him with violating section 964-a was denied.

2. The seventh count charged defendant with having falsely represented that he was employed by the Secretary General of the United Nations when in fact he was not so employed and obtained credit by such false statement. Such count followed the specific language of subdivision 1 of section 1293-b of the Penal Law. It was not necessary that the information set forth each and every element of the crime charged. It was sufficient to follow the statutory language if it contained all that was essential to constitute the crime and apprise the accused of the nature of the crime so that his conviction or acquittal would prevent a subsequent charge for the same offense. The motion to dismiss the seventh count of the information was also denied.

 

2593 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Carey v. Instantwhip Schenectady, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Albany County


10 Misc. 2d 113; 173 N.Y.S.2d 63; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3509



April 15, 1958 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Commissioner of Agriculture and Markets of the State of New York instituted an action against defendants, a manufacturer and two of its officers, seeking to enjoin the manufacture and sale of a product known as Instantwhip topping on the theory that it was a violation of N.Y. Agric. & Mkts. Law § 68-a.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner's action was based on the fact that in the manufacture of such topping defendant used dry buttermilk powder that was a dairy product. Thus, the Commissioner was seeking to restrain the manufacture, not because the topping was in semblance of or in imitation of instant whipped cream, but because a certain percentage of its total ingredients was a dairy product. The court dismissed the action. The burden was upon the Commissioner to prove that defendants in manufacturing and selling Instantwhip topping, were guilty of a designed and intentional imitation or resemblance of instant whipped cream, which did not result from the inherent characteristics of the ingredients used. By statutory definition whipped cream contained nothing but cream, sugar, and flavoring and must have been aerated by whipping. Defendants' product contained not only cream, sugar, and flavoring but also skimmed milk, whole milk and a stabilizer. Thus the ingredients of Instantwhip and whipped cream were different, and Instantwhip was a frozen dessert and not a milk or dairy product. Thus, the Commissioner failed to sustain its burden of proof.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the Commissioner's complaint with costs.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Food -- instant whipped cream -- inherent characteristic of combination of vegetable fat and buttermilk powder that it can be aerated to resemble whipped cream, hence such imitation is not intentional, and hence statute against "imitation of instant whipped cream manufactured by any process by which fat * * * has been * * * blended with a dairy product" (Agriculture and Markets Law, § 68-a) is not violated.

1. The Agriculture and Markets Law ( § 46) defines whipped cream as cream "which has been aerated by whipping. There may be added thereto only sugar or flavoring, or both." Section 68-a of said law, in five unnumbered paragraphs, regulates the sale of instant whipped cream. Unnumbered paragraphs 3 and 4 of said section 68-a permit certain substitutes for instant whipped cream; and unnumbered paragraph 2 prohibits any "imitation of instant whipped cream manufactured by any process by which fat or oil other than that of milk has been added to or mixed or blended with a dairy product in such a manner that the resultant product is an imitation of or resembles instant whipped cream." Defendant corporation manufactures two products: "Instantwhip", principally from cream; and [***2] "Instantwhip Topping", principally from vegetable fat, but with dry buttermilk powder added. It sells said "Topping" in two separate forms: one under gas pressure which, when dispensed from the pressurized container, as is Instantwhip, resembles whipped cream; and another form not under gas pressure, sold to bakers and confectioners in bulk form, having no resemblance to whipped cream, and which is whipped or gassed by the baker or confectioner. It is quite possible that this "Topping" is not a "dairy product" at all (within the meaning of Agriculture and Markets Law, art. 4, § 68-a) but is merely a "frozen dessert" (under art. 4-a). In any event, it is an inherent characteristic of the ingredients of this "Topping" that they can be aerated ("whipped") into a fluffy white texture resembling whipped cream. It cannot be said that such a resemblance is a designed or intentional imitation; and therefore this action by the State Commissioner of Agriculture and Markets to enjoin the manufacture and sale of "Instantwhip Topping" is dismissed.

2. The commissioner failed to sustain the burden of proving a designed, intentional imitation not resulting from the inherent characteristics [***3] of the ingredients.

 

2594 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Langan v. Syracuse


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Onondaga County


12 Misc. 2d 392; 175 N.Y.S.2d 268; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3555



April 5, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion of the defendants for judgment on the pleadings is, therefore, granted with $ 10 costs. Order accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners brought an action for a declaratory judgment determining that an assessment made by the commissioner of finance of defendant city against the landowner's real property was null and void and unenforceable. The city filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings.


OVERVIEW: The landowners made an application to the city water department for the necessary supply of water for the operation of its commercial laundry. No notice was ever issued to the landowners that they had defaulted in payment of the water bills. The unpaid water bills owed by the landowner's tenant were assessed as part of the general city tax upon the premises of the landowner. The landowner sought a declaratory judgment that the assessment was null and void. The city filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings. In granting the motion, the court held that it would not invoke the right to grant special dispensation through the equitable relief of a declaratory judgment when an adequate remedy to the taxpayer was granted by statute. Where an adequate remedy at law was provided, the reason for granting equitable relief disappeared. Because the landowner had an adequate remedy at law against the tenant, the court refused to grant the landowner's request for equitable relief.


OUTCOME: The motion of the city for judgment on the pleadings was granted.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- declaratory judgment -- motion by defendants for judgment on pleadings granted in action for declaratory judgment determining that assessment covering unpaid water taxes or rents incurred by tenant, made against plaintiffs' property as part of general city tax against property, is invalid -- plaintiffs have adequate remedy at law under statutes and city charter provisions under which assessment was made -- since plaintiffs have adequate remedy at law, statutes and charter could not deprive them of property without due process of law.

1. An assessment was made pursuant to the provisions of sections 94 and 95 of the Second Class Cities Law and section 117 of the City Charter of the City of Syracuse (Local Laws, 1935, No. 7, as amd. by Local Laws, 1938, No. 11) covering unpaid water taxes or rents incurred by a tenant of plaintiffs. The assessment was made against the property as part of the general city tax against the property. In an action for a declaratory judgment determining that the assessment was null and void and unenforcible, a motion [***2] by defendants for judgment on the pleadings is granted. Plaintiffs have an adequate remedy at law to test the propriety, correctness, legality and constitutionality of the assessment, and the jurisdiction of the city to make the assessment under section 2 of chapter 75 of the Laws of 1906 as amended by chapter 304 of the Laws of 1923, and are relegated to the form of relief therein provided.

2. Since plaintiffs have an adequate remedy at law the statutes and the charter under which the assessments were made could not be unconstitutional as depriving plaintiffs of property without due process of law.

 

2595 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Farrall v. Bragalini


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Oneida County


11 Misc. 2d 1075; 178 N.Y.S.2d 850; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3558



April 4, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, defendants' motion for judgment on the pleadings is granted. The cross motion is denied.

Settle order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State Tax Commissioners and the Commissioner of Motor Vehicles, filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings, and plaintiff owner filed a cross motion for summary judgment in the owner's action for a judgment declaring invalid N.Y. Veh. & Traf. §§ 11(7) and 11(5).


OVERVIEW: The owner's station wagon was a private passenger motor vehicle bought and used for such purposes. The owner alleged that he applied for renewal of registration and tendered $ 17 as provided by the rate set forth in N.Y. Veh. & Traf. § 11(6). When the Commissioner of Motor Vehicles rejected the application and informed the owner that the fee for renewal would be $ 25.50, the owner resubmitted his application and paid under protest the fee of $ 25.50. He argued that the law unfairly and arbitrarily discriminated and was unconstitutional and void: § 11(7), in prescribing a higher rate for station wagons than for private passenger vehicles and § 11(5), in providing a shorter period of time for registering and re-registering station wagons. The court disagreed. The court found that there was a substantial distinction, clearly cognizable, between a station wagon and a passenger motor vehicle and that these vehicles were capable of a special and extraordinary use. The court found that the distinction in the statute, which seemed initially a matter of identification, was logically based upon conservation and safety.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion for judgment on the pleadings and denied the owner's cross motion.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- discrimination against station wagons in fees and registration -- provisions of Vehicle and Traffic Law providing higher registration fees for station wagons than for private passenger vehicles and shorter period of time for registering and re-registering station wagons, not confiscatory or discriminatory, nor do they deprive owner of station wagon of equal protection of laws.

Provisions of the Vehicle and Traffic Law which prescribe higher registration fees for station wagons than for private passenger motor vehicles, and a shorter period of time for registering and re-registering station wagons, are not unreasonable, confiscatory and discriminatory as to one who operates his station wagon as a private passenger vehicle, nor do those provisions deprive such an owner of equal protection of the laws (Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 11, subds. 5, 7). In an action for a judgment declaring the invalidity, on constitutional grounds, of such provisions, defendants' motion for judgment on the pleadings was granted.

 

2596 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Petition of Mundorf


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


10 Misc. 2d 593; 172 N.Y.S.2d 493; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3616



March 28, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] This proceeding is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a rooming house owner, sought an order declaring N.Y. Mult. Dwell. Law § 194 (1956) unconstitutional. In the alternative, the owner sought an order annulling the regulations, promulgated by respondent, the Commissioner of the Department of Buildings of the City of New York, pursuant to § 194.


OVERVIEW: The owner maintained a rooming house of 19 separate units in a building that was once a single family dwelling. Section 194 required the owner and others like him to maintain sprinkler heads in every room of a non-fireproof converted dwelling. The owner alleged that the law was unconstitutional. In dismissing the petition, the court stated that it would have been loath to condemn as unconstitutional any statute, enacted for the protection of life, unless its invalidity was so manifest that the court had no alternative. The court noted that housing accommodations for low, moderate, and middle income groups in New York City were woefully inadequate. The court also noted that there had been a wave of serious fires in rooming houses in recent years due to overcrowding. The court stated that if the public could not invest the dwelling places of the underprivileged with dignity, it could at least insist by statute and public opinion, that they be kept secure. The court held that until the Commission made a determination that the owner's premises violated the statute, the court could not determine whether such action was arbitrary or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition and the proceedings.


HEADNOTES

Multiple dwellings -- automatic sprinkler system -- Multiple Dwelling Law ( § 194) requiring every room in rooming house to contain one or more fire sprinkler heads, not unconstitutional -- respondent commissioner had power to make rules.

1. Petitioner, owner of a five-story building which was originally erected as a one-family private dwelling and is now converted into a rooming house of 19 separate units, seeks an order declaring section 194 of the Multiple Dwelling Law unconstitutional, or, in the alternative, annulling the regulations, promulgated by respondent, commissioner of the department of buildings of New York City, pursuant to the section. Section 194 provides that "in every room in a class B non-fireproof converted dwelling * * * there shall be one or more sprinkler heads." The statute is not unconstitutional.

2. Respondent had power to adopt the regulations implementing the statute. The section specifically states that the sprinkler heads are to be installed "in accordance with the supplementary rules and regulations of the department." The Multiple Dwelling Law ( § 4, subd. 3) states: "The term 'department' shall mean the [***2] department, bureau, division or other agency charged with the enforcement of this chapter."

3. Respondent has not issued a violation order or made any determination with reference to the premises of the petitioner. Until the respondent acts or makes a determination that the petitioner's premises violate the section, there is nothing to review.

 

2597 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Scott v. McCaffrey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Bronx County


12 Misc. 2d 671; 172 N.Y.S.2d 954; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3636



March 25, 1958 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a proceeding for a joint writ of prohibition and mandamus under N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act art. 78 against respondent, a county court judge, who denied defendant's request for a waiver of a trial by jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 16-year-old, sought to waive his right for a trial by jury after a county court denied his application for severance of his criminal trial from the trial of five other co-defendants for first-degree assault, several counts of second-degree assault, and a violation of the Sullivan Law, N.Y. Penal Law § 1897, which arose from an incident where a victim was shot. At the time of the incident, defendant was a block away and was departing the scene. The other co-defendants were also separately indicted for other offenses that arose from a separate incident. The county court denied defendant's motion on the ground that it would have accomplished a severance of trial indirectly what that court had previously denied on defendant's direct motion. The court held that: (1) defendant should be aided in the proceeding by a guardian ad litem or a special guardian and that the court would make an appointment nunc pro tunc without prejudice upon an application; and (2) approval of a waiver of a jury trial was to follow where a judge has ascertained that defendant was fully aware of the nature and consequence of the request and defendant signed a written statement in open court.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition but only to the extent of a remand to the judge for a determination as to whether defendant knew the meaning and consequence of a waiver or whether the judge came to a conclusion that the defendant did not know.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Jury -- waiver in criminal case -- constitutional right of defendant in criminal case to waive jury trial (N. Y. Const., art. I, § 2) is subject to court's approval merely as to whether defendant understands what he is signing; court has no right or discretion to withhold approval on ground that defendant is really seeking severance of his trial and that such motion for severance had been previously denied -- matter of such waiver by 16-year-old defendant is remitted to County Court, which may wish to confer with defendant's relatives, counsel and guardian to be appointed in this proceeding in nature of prohibition and mandamus (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78).

1. The New York State Constitution (art. I, § 2, as amd. in 1938) provides: "Trial by jury in all cases in which it has heretofore been guaranteed by constitutional provision shall remain inviolate forever * * *. A jury trial may be waived by the defendant in all criminal cases, except those in which the crime charged may be punishable by death, by a written instrument signed by the defendant in person in open court before and with the approval of a judge or justice of a court having jurisdiction to try the offense. The [***2] legislature may enact laws, not inconsistent herewith, governing the form, content, manner and time of presentation of the instrument effectuating such waiver." As shown by the proceedings of the 1938 Constitutional Convention, the intent was to give a defendant an absolute right to waive a jury trial, and the only function of the court is to make sure that the defendant is aware of the nature and consequences of his waiver. The court does not have discretionary power to refuse to approve the waiver. Here, indictments against this defendant and five other defendants were directed by the County Court to be tried jointly. Then this defendant moved for a severance and separate trial, and his motion was denied. Then this defendant sought, by a written instrument in open court, to waive jury trial. The County Court denied his application, solely on the ground that a waiver would accomplish indirectly the very severance which defendant had been denied. This was error. The judge may withhold approval only if he determines that the defendant does not adequately understand the nature and consequences of his waiver.

2. In this proceeding in the Supreme Court under article 78 of the Civil [***3] Practice Act in the nature of a joint writ of prohibition and mandamus, the court remands the matter to the County Court so that that court may ascertain whether the defendant is fully aware of the nature and consequences of his waiver. The County Court may wish to confer with the defendant, who is 16 years old, and with, among others, his parents or nearest relatives, and his counsel, and his guardian ad litem or special guardian to be appointed in this proceeding.

3. Application should be made, in this article 78 proceeding, for the appointment of a guardian ad litem or special guardian for this infant (Civ. Prac. Act, §§ 202, 207), and such an appointment will be made nunc pro tunc.

4. This special proceeding in the nature both of prohibition and of mandamus (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78) is an appropriate remedy. It is not in the nature of a writ of certiorari; nor is it intended "to review a determination" "made in a criminal matter" (Civ. Prac. Act, § 1285, subd. 2) nor, since petitioner cannot raise bail, is the determination one which can be "adequately" reviewed by an appeal (Civ. Prac. Act, § 1285, subd. 4).

 

2598 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Stewart v. Strauss


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Municipal Court of the City of New York, Borough of Manhattan


11 Misc. 2d 433; 177 N.Y.S.2d 863; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3635



March 25, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For all of the foregoing, the court finds that the petition is insufficient and is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was the motion to dismiss filed by defendants, statutory tenant, State Rent Administrator, and Attorney General, in an action brought by plaintiff landlord under N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act art. 83 to evict the statutory tenant from the apartment in order to secure possession for the landlord's use.


OVERVIEW: Before attempting to exhaust his administrative remedies, the landlord commenced an eviction action against the statutory tenant. The landlord alleged that the N.Y. State Residential Rent Law ch. 755 was unconstitutional in that no emergency existed to justify it. The landlord argued that he did not have to exhaust the administrative remedies available before challenging the constitutionality of the N.Y. State Residential Rent Law ch. 755. The State Rent Administrator was authorized to intervene by stipulation of the landlord and the tenant. Under N.Y. Exec. Law § 71 the Attorney General was required to appear in support of the constitutionality of the emergency housing rent control laws. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss the landlord's petition. The court found that the landlord's petition was insufficient and dismissed it. The court determined that defendant had to exhaust his administrative remedies and could not by-pass or circumvent the rent control law. The court concluded that prior to exhausting his administrative remedies the landlord was not an aggrieved person, and thus was not in a position to attack the constitutionality of N.Y. State Residential Rent Law ch. 755.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the landlord's petition was insufficient and dismissed the petition.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- rent regulation -- State Residential Rent Law, as extended to June 30, 1959 (L. 1957, ch. 755) is constitutional -- in any event landlord must first apply for certificate of eviction (State Rent and Eviction Regulations, § 54) before he can challenge constitutionality of statute as aggrieved person.

1. The State Residential Rent Law (L. 1946, ch. 274, as last amd. by L. 1957, ch. 755 and extended to June 30, 1959) is constitutional and valid.

2. In any event, this summary dispossess proceeding in the Municipal Court is not the proper forum for a declaratory judgment; furthermore, a court of limited jurisdiction should not treat a statute as null and void unless the statute is obviously so.

3. Furthermore, this landlord is not an aggrieved party, since he has not exhausted his administrative remedies for obtaining a certificate authorizing eviction under section 54 of the State Rent and Eviction Regulations in cases where "the requested removal or eviction is not inconsistent with the purposes of the Act or these Regulations and would not be likely to result [***2] in the circumvention or evasion thereof." Landlord alleges, merely on the asserted statement of an unnamed representative of the State Rent Administrator, that it would be futile to apply for such a certificate. However, it appears that the tenant now owns a residential cooperative apartment which is comparable in all respects with the premises involved in this dispossess proceeding, and hence it may very well be that the State Rent Administrator would issue a certificate of eviction if the landlord made application therefor under section 54 of the regulations (see Administrator's Opinion No. 118; see, also, provisions for decontrol set forth in L. 1957, ch. 755).

4. Accordingly, this summary dispossess proceeding is dismissed.

 

2599 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bantam Books, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


9 Misc. 2d 1064; 172 N.Y.S.2d 515; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3653



March 22, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motions are granted. Submit orders to Troy on three days' notice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants moved to inspect the minutes of an indictment that charged one defendant with conspiracy in publishing and distributing a book and that charged the other defendant with distributing the book. The application of N.Y. Penal Law § 1141 was central to the dispute among the parties.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' affidavits established that only isolated passages of the book were submitted to the grand jury. The court granted the motions to inspect the grand jury minutes. It held that in order to be convicted of publishing or distributing obscene material pursuant to § 1141, the publication as a whole, as opposed to isolated passages, had to be considered. The court ruled that the test for determining whether a publication was obscene was whether to the average person, applying contemporary community standards, the dominant theme of the material taken as a whole appealed to a prurient interest. The court also held that a motion to inspect the grand jury's minutes could be granted if the facts shown demonstrated that there was a reason to believe that the evidence before the grand jury was insufficient or illegal.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motions to inspect the grand jury minutes.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- obscene books -- Special Term read minutes of Grand Jury on indictments against publisher and distributor of allegedly obscene novel (Penal Law, § 1141; Code Crim. Pro., § 251) and, finding that only excerpts were submitted to Grand Jury, granted defendants' motions for inspection of Grand Jury minutes.

Indictments against the distributor and the publisher of an allegedly obscene novel must be dismissed if the Grand Jury minutes show that the only proofs submitted to the Grand Jury were isolated passages from the book (Penal Law, § 1141; Code Crim. Pro., § 251). The test is not the effect of isolated passages on susceptible persons, but the character of the work as a whole. Consideration must be given to the estimation of approved critics. Legitimate works of literature must not be interfered with. On these motions by the publisher and by the distributor of the novel "Ten North Frederick", to inspect the Grand Jury minutes, Special Term has read the Grand Jury minutes and now grants the motions for inspection.

 

2600 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Application of Coates


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Monroe County


14 Misc. 2d 89; 181 N.Y.S.2d 599; 1958 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3658



March 20, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is denied. Submit order accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On the ground that N.Y. Mental Hyg. Law § 74 was unconstitutional and violated the due process provisions of the federal and state constitutions, plaintiff patient filed a motion to vacate the order of certification in the Monroe County Court (New York), which admitted her to the state hospital for treatment of mental illness. She also sought to vacate the subsequent certificate of the medical officer that she remain admitted in the hospital.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to N.Y Mental Hyg. Law § 74, the patient, by order of certification of a county court, was admitted to a state hospital for observation and treatment for specified period. Before the expiration of the period a medical officer of the institution executed a certificate that he considered the patient to be in need of continued care and treatment. The order of certification automatically became a final order in accordance with § 74 upon the filing of the certificate. The patient filed a motion to vacate the order of certification and the certificate of the medical officer on the ground that the § 74 was unconstitutional and violative of the constitutional due process provisions. The court denied her motion. The findings of the medical officer did not constitute a "judicial proceeding," and there was no statutory right to notice at that stage of the proceedings. The court concluded that the rights to hearing, review, and habeas corpus contained in N.Y. Mental Hyg. Law §§ 74, 76, 204 adequately protected the patient. Thus, her constitutional rights were not violated.


OUTCOME: The court denied the patient's motion.


HEADNOTES

Insane and other incompetent persons -- commitment procedure -- constitutionality of provision for keeping patient in institution on medical certificate that patient needs continued treatment -- patient's application for jury trial of issue of her mental illness was denied since made more than 30 days after State hospital had filed certificate that she needed continued care and treatment (Mental Hygiene Law, § 74); said statute affords due process and is constitutional.

By an order of a County Judge or other court of record, notice to an alleged mentally ill person of an application to certify her for admission to an authorized institution may be dispensed with, and the court may make an order certifying that such patient be admitted to such institution for observation and treatment for a period not exceeding 60 days (Mental Hygiene Law, § 74). Nevertheless, if the director of the institution believes that the patient is not mentally ill, he may refuse to receive the patient or he may discharge the patient (§ 74, subd. 8). Or, the judge, on his own motion or on demand of a relative or friend of the patient, may hold [***2] a hearing (§ 74, subd. 5). Or, within 60 days after the date of the order of certification, the superintendent or other duly designated medical officer of the institution may file in the County Clerk's office his certificate that the patient needs continued care and treatment; and such filing makes the order of certification a final order (§ 74, subd. 7). Within 30 days after such final order, the patient or any relative or friend may petition a Justice of the Supreme Court, who shall order a jury trial of the issue of mental illness (§ 76). Or a writ of habeas corpus may be sued out (§ 204). Taken together, these provisions afford due process. In this case, the court's orders certifying the patient and dispensing with notice were dated April 17, 1957, and the medical officer's certificate of the patient's need for continued treatment was filed on May 3, 1957; hence the patient's petition on June 17, 1957 for a jury trial was too late and was therefore denied. The patient's present petition, to vacate the orders and certificate on the ground that section 74 is unconstitutional, is denied.
